# Findings — 10-bughunt (appended per batch; raw JSON in 10-bughunt-raw/)

## Batch B1-estimation

### unit: estimation-kf (4 findings)

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** Track initiation treats RangeBearing2D polar values as ENU Cartesian position
  - `core/estimation/EkfEstimator.cpp:82` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: canInitiateTrack (core/estimation/MeasurementModels.hpp:29-31) whitelists RangeBearing2D as birth-capable ('active sensors ... do', citing Helgesen 2022), and every tracker birth path calls estimator initiate() with the raw measurement (Tracker.cpp:176-178 and 313-315, MhtTracker.cpp:350->38, PmbmTracker.cpp:441->484 and 1411->1453). But EkfEstimator::initiate does x(0)=z.value(0), x(1)=z.value(1) and copies z.covariance's 2x2 block into the position covariance — it assumes the value vector is ENU [px,py]. For RangeBearing2D the value is (range_m, bearing_rad), so the polar pair is planted verbatim as a Cartesian position, sensor_position_enu is ignored entirely, and the position covariance mixes m^2 and rad^2 units (a sigma_b=0.01 rad default becomes sigma_py=0.01 m, absurdly overconfident). The same pattern exists in ImmEstimator::initiate (ImmEstimator.cpp:449-461) and UkfEstimator::initiate (UkfEstimator.cpp:122-136). RangeBearing2D is a first-class supported input: SensorDefaults.cpp:39-44 ships default covariances for ArpaTtm+RangeBearing2D and EoIr+RangeBearing2D, so a consumer feeding radar/EO-IR as range-bearing (a documented Measurement model) hits this on any unassociated measurement. No test pins initiate-from-RangeBearing2D (tests/estimation/test_ekf_estimator.cpp initiates only from Position2D); the sim builder buildRangeBearingPassScenario deliberately works around it by seeding each scenario with one Position2D measurement first (Builders.hpp:69-75, evaluation-log.md:5399), which is why the scenario tests stay green.
  - failure_scenario: Consumer feeds ARPA TTM as RangeBearing2D per SensorDefaults: first-ever measurement z.value=(3000 m, 2.0 rad), z.covariance=diag(625 m^2, 1e-4 rad^2). No track gates, so Tracker.cpp:177 calls initiate(z): a track is born at ENU (3000 m E, 2.0 m N) instead of the true (~-1248, ~2728), with sigma_py=0.01 m. Subsequent range-bearing measurements of the real target cannot gate to this track (bearing residual ~2 rad against a mrad-scale S), so every scan births another garbage track while the real target never acquires a valid one — silent wrong tracks plus phantom-track proliferation, violating the presence-over-classification goal for that sensor configuration.
  - evidence: EkfEstimator.cpp:81-98 (x(0)=z.value(0); x(1)=z.value(1); p block from z.covariance; sensor_position_enu unused); MeasurementModels.hpp:29-31 (canInitiateTrack returns true for RangeBearing2D); Tracker.cpp:176-178; PmbmTracker.cpp:441,484; MhtTracker.cpp:350; SensorDefaults.cpp:39-44 (ArpaTtm/EoIr RangeBearing2D defaults); docs/algorithms/estimation.md:78 documents one-point initiation as x=[zx,zy,0,0] i.e. Cartesian only.
  - suggested_fix: Either perform the polar-to-Cartesian conversion in initiate (px = sx + r*cos(beta), py = sy + r*sin(beta), with linearized/unscented covariance conversion of diag(sigma_r^2, sigma_b^2)), or make canInitiateTrack(RangeBearing2D) return false until such a conversion exists so unassociated range-bearing measurements are dropped like Bearing2D instead of seeding garbage.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full failing path. (1) EkfEstimator.cpp:81-98 plants z.value(0)/z.value(1) as ENU px/py and copies z.covariance's 2x2 into the position covariance with no model branch and no use of sensor_position_enu; identical pattern in ImmEstimator.cpp:448-461, UkfEstimator.cpp:122-136, and also ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:127-140 (one more than claimed). (2) canInitiateTrack (MeasurementModels.hpp:29-31) whitelists RangeBearing2D, and every birth path calls initiate with the raw measurement: Tracker.cpp:175-178 and 312-314, MhtTracker.cpp:38/349, PmbmTracker.cpp:441/484 and 1452/1494 — no conversion anywhere. (3) The path is a documented consumer contract: docs/integration-guide.md:218-227 table says RangeBearing2D value=[range_m, bearing_rad] and "can start a track? yes"; SensorDefaults.cpp:39-44 ships ArpaTtm/EoIr RangeBearing2D defaults. Hand-executed z=(3000 m, 2.0 rad), R=diag(625, 6.9e-4): track born at ENU (3000, 2.0) m with ~0.026 m north sigma; subsequent looks at the real target have ~2 rad bearing residual vs S_bb~6.9e-4 rad^2 (Mahalanobis ~5800), so nothing gates and each scan births another garbage track. (4) No guard or test contradicts: all shipped adapters emit Position2D/PositionVelocity2D/Bearing2D; the canonical builders project range/bearing to Position2D; the only in-repo RangeBearing2D producer, buildRangeBearingPassScenario, deliberately seeds each run with one Position2D first (Builders.hpp:68-74 says "to seed the track"), which is exactly why scenario tests stay green; test_ekf_estimator.cpp initiates only from Position2D. Refutation attempt via IEstimator.hpp:44 ("seeded from a position-type measurement") fails because the core's own birth gate (canInitiateTrack) admits RangeBearing2D and the consumer guide promises it births. Minor errata: the cited evaluation-log.md:5399 path does not exist, and the same Cartesian assumption additionally appears in the coverage/occupancy feed at PmbmTracker.cpp:1797-1798 — neither affects the verdict.
  - verifier corrected details: Track initiation from RangeBearing2D measurements plants the polar pair (range_m, bearing_rad) verbatim as ENU Cartesian position and mixes m^2/rad^2 units in the birth covariance, in all four estimators: EkfEstimator.cpp:81-98, ImmEstimator.cpp:448-461, UkfEstimator.cpp:122-136, and ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:127-140 (the claim missed the PF). sensor_position_enu is ignored at birth even though update() correctly uses it via predictMeasurement. Every tracker birth path (Tracker.cpp:175-178/312-314, MhtTracker.cpp:38/349, PmbmTracker.cpp:441/484, 1452/1494) feeds the raw measurement because canInitiateTrack (MeasurementModels.hpp:29-31) whitelists RangeBearing2D. The integration guide (docs/integration-guide.md:218-227) explicitly documents RangeBearing2D as able to start a track, and SensorDefaults.cpp:39-44 ships ArpaTtm/EoIr defaults for it, so a consumer following the guide silently gets wrongly-placed, absurdly overconfident tracks plus per-scan phantom-track proliferation while the real target never acquires a valid track. Mitigating scope (why not critical): no shipped adapter or canonical builder ever emits RangeBearing2D (they all project to Position2D), and the in-repo scenario builder works around it by seeding with a Position2D measurement — the bug fires only for consumers constructing RangeBearing2D Measurements directly, which is nonetheless the documented contract. Related latent instance: PmbmTracker.cpp:1797-1798 also treats value(0)/value(1) of any initiable model as ENU position when feeding coverage/occupancy. Fix options: convert polar to ENU (using sensor_position_enu) inside initiate with unscented/linearized covariance transform, or make canInitiateTrack exclude RangeBearing2D until birth conversion exists; either way add an initiate-from-RangeBearing2D test.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** isMeasurementCovariancePsd never validates R's dimension against the measurement, despite claiming to reject 'wrong shape'
  - `core/estimation/MeasurementModels.hpp:81` (input-validation, confidence high)
  - description: The guard's contract comment (MeasurementModels.hpp:68-79) says it rejects covariance that is 'non-finite (NaN/Inf), the wrong shape, or not strictly positive-definite' and exists so 'one bad NMEA frame' cannot poison a track. The implementation only checks non-empty, square (rows==cols), finite, and LDLT-positive — it never compares R's size to the measurement's value/model dimension (the function does not even receive the measurement). A square-but-wrong-size R (e.g. a 1x1 scalar variance attached to a 2-dim Position2D value, or a 2x2 position-only R on a 4-dim PositionVelocity2D value) passes every guard, then flows into S = H*P*H' + z.covariance where the operand sizes disagree. Eigen's dimension check on operator+ is an eigen_assert: abort in debug builds, disabled under NDEBUG in release where the mismatched CwiseBinaryOp reads out of bounds — garbage S, nondeterministic gate/likelihood, or memory-corruption-grade UB. The crash site is IEstimator::gate (EstimatorDefaults.cpp:34) or EkfEstimator::update (EkfEstimator.cpp:47), i.e. inside the very estimator entry the guard claims to protect; there is no other dimension validation anywhere between Measurement construction and the estimator (applyDefaultsIfEmpty only fills empty covariance). Consumers constructing Measurements directly are the documented canonical integration path, so a units/shape mistake in consumer code is exactly the threat this guard was added for.
  - failure_scenario: A consumer builds a Position2D measurement with value=Vector2d(e,n) but covariance = 1x1 matrix (sigma^2 scalar, a plausible mistake for a bearing-style sensor wrapper). isMeasurementCovariancePsd passes (1x1, finite, positive). The associator calls IEstimator::gate, which computes the 2x2 H*P*H' plus the 1x1 R: assert-abort of the whole process in a debug build; in a release (NDEBUG) build an out-of-bounds read produces a garbage innovation covariance and a nondeterministic gate decision, silently corrupting association for that scan.
  - evidence: MeasurementModels.hpp:81-92 checks only rows()==cols(), allFinite, and LDLT positivity; EstimatorDefaults.cpp:28-36 and EkfEstimator.cpp:37-50 rely on it and then form H*P*H^T + z.covariance with H sized from the model, R sized by the caller; grep shows no other value-vs-covariance dimension check in core/ or adapters/.
  - suggested_fix: Give the guard (or a wrapper used at estimator entry) the expected measurement dimension — e.g. isMeasurementCovarianceValid(const Measurement& z) checking z.covariance.rows() == z.value.size() and z.value.size() == dimensionFor(z.model) — and use it at the same call sites.

- **[LOW/unverified]** softUpdate bypasses the bearing-range guard that update() applies, so JPDA/PDAF bearing-only updates are unclamped even when the guard is enabled
  - `core/estimation/EkfEstimator.cpp:120` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: EkfEstimator's constructor doc (EkfEstimator.hpp:26-27) says bearing_range_guard 'enables the along-LOS variance non-decrease clamp for bearing-only updates'. update() honors it (EkfEstimator.cpp:60-63), but softUpdate() — the PDAF/JPDA path that folds gated Bearing2D clusters — never calls applyBearingRangeGuard, so its posterior covariance (lines 163-170) can drive the along-line-of-sight position variance below the predicted value through the kinematic cross-correlations, which is exactly the bearings-only-tracking pathology the guard was built for (BearingRangeGuard.hpp:8-15, motivated by the AutoFerry sc5 NEES data). ImmEstimator has the identical asymmetry (guard in update() at ImmEstimator.cpp:246-251, absent from softUpdate — noted, out of this unit's scope). A deployment that pairs a bearing-only sensor with JpdaAssociator and requests the guard gets the documented protection only on hard-match updates; the bench matrix already contains both a guard-enabled estimator config (core/benchmark/Config.cpp:155) and JPDA associators (Config.cpp:212-224), so estimator-vs-guard A/B comparisons run through JPDA are silently diluted.
  - failure_scenario: Guard-enabled estimator + JpdaAssociator + EO-IR Bearing2D stream on a closing target: each scan's gated bearings enter softUpdate, whose combined-gain covariance update reduces along-LOS position variance below the prediction with no clamp; over tens of scans the filter becomes overconfident in a range it never measured — the NEES blow-up and overconfident CPA geometry the guard flag promises to prevent, while the operator believes the guard is active.
  - evidence: EkfEstimator.cpp:33-65 (update: guard applied when bearing_range_guard_ && model==Bearing2D) vs EkfEstimator.cpp:120-172 (softUpdate: no applyBearingRangeGuard call, no bearing_range_guard_ reference); EkfEstimator.hpp:26-27 documents the flag as covering 'bearing-only updates' without excluding the soft path.
  - suggested_fix: In softUpdate, when bearing_range_guard_ && z0.model==Bearing2D, capture the pre-update covariance and apply applyBearingRangeGuard(P_pre, P_post, x_pre, z0.sensor_position_enu) after the combined covariance update (mirror the fix in ImmEstimator::softUpdate).

- **[LOW/unverified]** EkfEstimator::initiate hardcodes a 4-state seed while accepting any motion model, and CoordinatedTurn.hpp falsely claims the EKF predict path uses propagate()
  - `core/estimation/EkfEstimator.cpp:81` (api-contract, confidence high)
  - description: EkfEstimator's constructor accepts any IMotionModel and its class doc says 'Linear-Gaussian prediction via the supplied motion model', but initiate() always builds Eigen::Vector4d state / Matrix4d covariance (EkfEstimator.cpp:81,94) regardless of motion_->stateDim(). Wiring EkfEstimator with a 5-state model (ConstantVelocity5State or CoordinatedTurn): the first predict computes a 5x5 transitionMatrix times a 4-vector (EkfEstimator.cpp:26-28) — eigen_assert abort in debug, UB in release. Compounding this, CoordinatedTurn.hpp:32 states 'the EKF predict path uses propagate(x, dt) which reads omega from x' — false for EkfEstimator, which uses motion_->transitionMatrix(dt) (the omega=0 CV limit for CT) for both mean and covariance and never calls propagate(); only ImmEstimator (via dynamic_cast + transitionMatrixAt, ImmEstimator.cpp:147-152), UkfEstimator, and the particle filter use propagate(). So even a consumer who seeds 5-state tracks externally would silently get pure-CV behavior from an EkfEstimator+CoordinatedTurn pairing that the CT header comment presents as supported. UkfEstimator::initiate (UkfEstimator.cpp:113-146) already does this correctly by sizing from motion_->stateDim(), confirming the EKF omission is not a design constraint. All in-repo configs pair EkfEstimator only with ConstantVelocity2D (core/benchmark/Config.cpp:82-85, app/example.cpp:41), so this is latent, but both classes are public library surface and the misleading comment actively invites the broken pairing.
  - failure_scenario: A library consumer, reading CoordinatedTurn.hpp's claim that the EKF predict path reads omega from the state, constructs EkfEstimator(std::make_shared<CoordinatedTurn>(...)). The first measurement births a 4-state track; the next predict multiplies the 5x5 F by the 4-vector state: assertion abort in a debug build, undefined behavior (out-of-bounds read into state/covariance) in release.
  - evidence: EkfEstimator.cpp:81 (Eigen::Vector4d x), 94 (Eigen::Matrix4d p), 26-28 (f = motion_->transitionMatrix(dt); track.state = f * track.state — no propagate() call anywhere in the file); CoordinatedTurn.hpp:31-33 ('the EKF predict path uses propagate(x, dt)'); CoordinatedTurn::transitionMatrix (CoordinatedTurn.cpp:32-36) returns the omega=0 CV limit; UkfEstimator.cpp:117 sizes the seed from motion_->stateDim().
  - suggested_fix: Size the initiate() seed from motion_->stateDim() exactly as UkfEstimator does, use motion_->propagate(track.state, dt) for the mean in predict(), and fix the CoordinatedTurn.hpp:32 comment to name the estimators that actually call propagate() (UKF/PF/IMM), or explicitly document EkfEstimator as 4-state/linear-only and assert stateDim()==4 in its constructor.

Coverage notes (estimation-kf): Scope files read end-to-end: ConstantVelocity2D.*, ConstantVelocity5State.*, CoordinatedTurn.*, EkfEstimator.*, MeasurementModels.*, NoiseModels.hpp, GaussianScore.hpp, BearingRangeGuard.*, PolarVelocity.hpp, EstimatorDefaults.cpp; plus call-site tracing through Tracker/MhtTracker/PmbmTracker/ImmEstimator/UkfEstimator, benchmark Config.cpp wiring, AIS adapters (PolarVelocity consumers), SensorDefaults, docs/algorithms/estimation.md, and the mirror tests. Verified CLEAN: (1) GaussianScore all paths — 2x2 closed-form Mahalanobis/det algebraically identical to S.inverse() form; safeLogDet 1e-300 floor reproduces legacy guard split (raw det for Mahalanobis, guarded det for log term) on both dynamic-LU and stack paths; logLikelihood normalization -d/2*log(2pi) - 1/2*log|S| - 1/2*d2 textbook-correct in EstimatorDefaults; IMM per-mode log_lambda correctly omits the constant 2pi term (cancels in the mode softmax). (2) EKF Joseph form present and consistent in both update() (with Student-t-scaled R used consistently in gain and K*R*K') and softUpdate() (PDAF combined covariance beta0*P + (1-beta0)*P_Joseph + K*spread*K' matches Bar-Shalom exactly; spread = sum(beta*y*y') - ybar*ybar'). (3) Jacobians: RangeBearing2D/Bearing2D H match h(x)=atan2(dy,dx) convention including offset-sensor dx,dy; pinned by finite-difference tests. (4) wrapAngle boundary (-pi,pi] hand-checked at +/-pi, +/-3pi, 0; residual wrap indices correct (RB idx1, bearing idx0). (5) Q discretization: CV2D/CV5/CT all q*[[dt^3/3,dt^2/2],[dt^2/2,dt]] per axis + q_omega*dt — properly dt-scaled, matches doc. (6) CoordinatedTurn closed-form F verified against the standard CT model; omega->0 cutoff at 1e-6 gives a ~5e-7*dt^2*v discontinuity (negligible, continuity fine). (7) PolarVelocity: v=SOG*[sin,cos] and polar Jacobian correct for marine COG; both call sites (AisAdapter, AisCsvReplayAdapter) convert deg->rad correctly; nav-status suppress codes 1/5 correct; iso floor always-added is documented. (8) StudentT scale (nu+d2)/(nu+d) matches Roth 2013; >=1 clamp documented and pinned by tests. (9) BearingRangeGuard clamp is PSD-preserving (equivalent to adding a rank-1 PSD increment) and correctly uses the pre-update state for LOS. (10) update() rewinding last_update on stale input is documented and guarded by Tracker's default reject_stale=true. (11) Eigen aliasing in P = IKH*P*IKH' + ... safe (product temporaries); dt<=0 predict no-ops; empty-covariance initiate sentinel guarded at all birth call sites. OVERFLOW / OUT-OF-SCOPE observations for other units: ImmEstimator::gate and logLikelihood (imm path) skip the isMeasurementCovariancePsd guard that the IEstimator defaults apply — an empty/mismatched R asserts or is UB there instead of failing closed (same class as my finding 2); ImmEstimator::softUpdate also lacks the bearing-range guard (mirrors finding 3); ImmEstimator::initiate hardcodes 5-state and UkfEstimator/ImmEstimator initiate share the RangeBearing2D polar-as-Cartesian defect (covered inside finding 1); EkfEstimator/ImmEstimator softUpdate assert shared model+sensor pose but not shared R across the gated batch (documented assumption; silent mis-weight with mixed-accuracy same-sensor measurements, and asserts vanish under NDEBUG); app/example.cpp:41 and integration-guide.md:82 label EkfEstimator's init_speed_std argument as /*init_pos_std_m=*/ (misleads consumer tuning); docs/algorithms/estimation.md:87 still lists Joseph-form as a future improvement although implemented (stale doc).

### unit: estimation-ukf-pf (4 findings)

- **[MEDIUM/CONFIRMED]** UKF predicted bearing is a linear weighted mean across the +-pi wrap; corrupts update whenever sigma-point bearings straddle the discontinuity (except by numeric coincidence at the shipped defaults)
  - `core/estimation/UkfEstimator.cpp:80` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: UkfEstimator::update computes z_pred as a plain weighted sum of sigma-point measurement values (line 80). For Bearing2D/RangeBearing2D the bearing column comes from atan2, which is discontinuous at +-pi. When the sigma points straddle the discontinuity (target near due-west of the sensor in ENU), one or more columns differ by 2*pi from the rest, and with the scaled-UT weights (|Wm(i)| ~ 1e5-1e6 at alpha=1e-3) z_pred becomes garbage (verified: -785395 rad for a true bearing of 3.14158). At the SHIPPED defaults (alpha=1e-3, beta=2, kappa=0) the error happens to be a near-exact integer multiple of 2*pi (per-point weight 1/(2*alpha^2*(n+kappa)) is within ~1e-10 of an integer for n=4 and n=5), so the subsequent wrapAngle calls on zd (line 86-87) and on the residual (measurementResidual, line 103) cancel it almost perfectly — numerically verified residual damage ~5e-8 m. But with the constructor-documented alternative kappa = 3 - state_dim (UkfEstimator.hpp:27 'commonly 0 or 3 - state_dim') the weight is 166666.67 (frac 2/3) and the cancellation fails: numerically verified, a PERFECTLY consistent bearing measurement produces innovation y = -2.094 rad and Sxx = 17.55 rad^2 (true value 1e-4); with alpha=0.5 the innovation is -pi and the state is displaced ~2.7 m per scan. The identical code pattern is on the CANONICAL production path: ImmEstimator.cpp:210 (canonical IMM was promoted to use_ukf=true, core/benchmark/Config.cpp:115) has the same unwrapped mean, and the corrupted y/S also feed the per-mode likelihood gaussianScore, corrupting IMM mode probabilities. No test pins this region: the only UKF range-bearing test (tests/estimation/test_ukf_estimator.cpp:54) uses bearing atan2(4000,3000)=0.93 rad, and buildRangeBearingPassScenario geometries keep y=+50/+20 so bearings never cross +-pi. Stone Soup and other UT implementations use an angle-aware mean for exactly this reason.
  - failure_scenario: Consumer wires UkfEstimator (or ImmEstimator with use_ukf=true) with the header-suggested kappa = 3 - state_dim, feeds EO/IR Bearing2D measurements (live camera-bearing pipeline). An anchored vessel sits due west of own-ship, predicted bearing within ~1e-4 rad of +-pi, so sigma points straddle the wrap every scan: each perfectly consistent measurement yields a -2.09 rad innovation with S inflated 10^5x, pulling the state the wrong way and randomizing the IMM mode probabilities scan after scan; the track drifts/corrupts silently while the display keeps showing it as updated.
  - evidence: UkfEstimator.cpp:79-80 'Eigen::VectorXd z_pred = Eigen::VectorXd::Zero(nz); for (...) z_pred += sp.Wm(i) * Zsp.col(i);' with no wrap normalization; same at ImmEstimator.cpp:209-210. Numeric replication of computeSigmaPoints + update at state (-1000, 0.01) m, P=diag(100,100,4,4), Bearing2D R=(1 deg)^2: defaults give z_pred=-785395.02 rad but residual damage only 5e-8 m (integer-weight cancellation); kappa=3-n gives y_perfect=-2.094 rad, Sxx=17.55; alpha=0.5 gives y_perfect=-3.142, state correction (-2.67, -2.66) m per update.
  - suggested_fix: Compute the bearing component of z_pred with an angle-aware mean (e.g. rotate all sigma bearings into the frame of Zsp.col(0) via wrapAngle(Z_i - Z_0), average the wrapped deviations, add back and re-wrap), in UkfEstimator.cpp:80 and ImmEstimator.cpp:210.
  - verifier: Independently traced and numerically replicated the claimed failure path. (1) Code: UkfEstimator.cpp:79-80 and ImmEstimator.cpp:209-210 compute z_pred as a plain weighted sum of atan2 bearing columns with no angle-aware mean; wrapAngle is applied only afterward to zd and the residual. (2) Replication with an exact re-implementation of computeSigmaPoints + the update at state (-1000, 0.01), P=diag(100,100,4,4), Bearing2D R=(1 deg)^2: at shipped defaults (alpha=1e-3, kappa=0) sigma points straddle +-pi, raw z_pred = -785395 rad, but the per-point weight 1/(2*alpha^2*(n+kappa)) is 125000 exactly (n=4) / 100000+1.5e-11 (n=5), so the 2*pi-multiple offset cancels through the subsequent wraps (residual damage ~4e-10 rad) — defaults are masked by an integer-weight coincidence, exactly as claimed. With the header-suggested kappa=3-n (UkfEstimator.hpp:27 'commonly 0 or 3 - state_dim') the weight fraction is 2/3 and cancellation fails: a perfectly consistent measurement produces y=-2.0944 rad and Sxx=17.55 rad^2 (true ~1e-4) — replicated to 4+ digits. With alpha=0.5: state correction (-2.67,-2.66) m per update — replicated. (3) Call sites: all in-repo constructions (core/benchmark/Config.cpp:89/94/111/131/152/180/202 incl. canonical makeImmCvCt with use_ukf=true; app/mht_fusion_example.cpp:61) use default alpha/kappa; ukf_kappa is not exposed through any config struct, so no shipped config is affected — the trigger is a library consumer passing the constructor-documented kappa=3-n or larger alpha. (4) Tests: tests/estimation/test_ukf_estimator.cpp uses bearing 0.93 rad only; no test exercises bearings near +-pi. (5) Docs: docs/algorithms/estimation.md lists the assumption 'h(x) continuous over the sigma spread' and 'circular-statistics bearing mean when sigma spread is wide' under Ways-to-improve — the limitation is partially documented as known/parked, but the doc misses that kappa=3-n breaks even the narrow-spread case and that defaults are safe only by numeric coincidence. The technical claim is fully accurate.
  - verifier corrected details: Real latent correctness defect on the public constructor surface, but severity is medium, not high, for three verified reasons. (a) Every in-repo/canonical configuration uses the default alpha=1e-3, kappa=0, where the error cancels to ~4e-10 rad by the integer-weight coincidence — no shipped path is affected. (b) At the documented small alpha (even with kappa=3-n), the sigma-point bearing spread is only ~1e-5 rad, so the straddle band is centimeters wide laterally at km ranges; and when triggered, S is inflated ~1e5x so the gain is near zero — the direct state corruption is mm-scale per scan (measured 0.012 m), i.e. the update becomes near-inert rather than divergent. The concrete damage in that regime is the corrupted (y, S) pair feeding gaussianScore in ImmEstimator (wrong per-mode likelihoods -> skewed IMM mode probabilities) and effectively dropped bearing updates for a target pinned near due-west LOS. (c) Meter-scale state corruption (2.7 m/update) requires a large non-default alpha (~0.5) that neither the defaults nor the header suggest. Aggravating factors keeping it at medium rather than low: the header docstring actively recommends the failing kappa=3-n; the failure is silent; no test covers the wrap region; and docs/algorithms/estimation.md already names the fix ('circular-statistics bearing mean') under Ways-to-improve without warning that the accidental safety of the defaults is parameter-dependent. Recommended fix scope: angle-aware weighted mean (e.g. atan2 of weighted sin/cos, or unwrap columns relative to Zsp.col(0) before averaging) at UkfEstimator.cpp:80 and ImmEstimator.cpp:210, plus a regression test with predicted bearing at pi and kappa=3-n.

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** initiate() treats RangeBearing2D value [range_m, bearing_rad] as ENU [x, y]; every track born from an unassociated range-bearing measurement gets a garbage position with a rad^2 position covariance
  - `core/estimation/UkfEstimator.cpp:123` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: UkfEstimator::initiate seeds x(0)=z.value(0), x(1)=z.value(1) and p(0,0)=z.covariance(0,0), p(1,1)=z.covariance(1,1) (lines 123-136) with no model dispatch. For MeasurementModel::RangeBearing2D, value = [range_m, bearing_rad] relative to sensor_position_enu — so the track is born at ENU position (range, bearing), e.g. (5000.0, 0.9) for a target 5 km out at 0.9 rad, with py 1-sigma = sigma_bearing (~0.017 rad read as meters). canInitiateTrack(RangeBearing2D) == true (MeasurementModels.hpp:29), and all three birth paths call initiate directly with the raw measurement: Tracker.cpp:175-178, PmbmTracker.cpp:441+484 and 1411+1453, MhtTracker.cpp:38 (rootFromMeasurement). No polar-to-Cartesian conversion exists anywhere between association and initiate (grepped: none). The consumer contract explicitly promises this works: docs/integration-guide.md measurement-model table lists RangeBearing2D 'can start a track? yes'. ParticleFilterEstimator::initiate has the identical defect (ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:128-129, the whole particle cloud is drawn around (r, theta)); EkfEstimator.cpp:82-83 too (outside this review unit). Tests dodge it rather than pin it: buildRangeBearingPassScenario (core/scenario/Builders.cpp:241-244) deliberately emits the FIRST fix as Position2D so births never come from RangeBearing2D, and the shipped NMEA adapters convert range/bearing to Position2D (MeasurementBuilders.cpp:34, ArpaAdapter.cpp:81). So nothing in-repo fails, but any consumer following the guide (RangeBearing2D is otherwise fully supported: update h(x), bias correction, SensorDefaults ArpaTtm/EoIr RB2D entries) gets a silently wrong track on every first detection of a new target.
  - failure_scenario: A consumer with a radar that outputs polar plots follows the integration guide and constructs RangeBearing2D measurements (range 5000 m, bearing 0.9 rad, sigma_r=75 m, sigma_b=1.5 deg per the SensorDefaults row). A new vessel appears with no AIS: the first plot associates to nothing, Tracker births a track at ENU (5000.0, 0.9) — kilometers from the true position — with py variance 6.9e-4 m^2. Under PMBM every unassociated plot births such a Bernoulli. The phantom sits near the ENU origin (own-ship!) as a confidently-located track: wrong track output in exactly the safety-relevant near-field.
  - evidence: UkfEstimator.cpp:123-124 'x(0) = z.value(0); x(1) = z.value(1);' + 133-136 seeding p from z.covariance(0..1,0..1); MeasurementModels.hpp:29 canInitiateTrack returns true for RangeBearing2D; Tracker.cpp:175-178 'else if (canInitiateTrack(z.model) && isMeasurementCovariancePsd(z.covariance)) { Track seed = estimator_.initiate(z); ... }'; integration-guide.md table row '| RangeBearing2D | [range_m, bearing_rad] ... | yes |'; Builders.cpp:241-252 shows the i==0 Position2D dodge.
  - suggested_fix: In each estimator's initiate (or better, one shared helper), dispatch on z.model: for RangeBearing2D convert to ENU via sensor_position_enu + [r cos(b), r sin(b)] and propagate the polar covariance through the Jacobian (the projectRangeBearingToEnu math already exists in MeasurementBuilders.cpp); or make canInitiateTrack(RangeBearing2D) false until conversion exists and fix the guide table.
  - verifier: Independently traced the failing path. (1) UkfEstimator.cpp:123-124/133-136 copy z.value(0..1) and z.covariance(0..1,0..1) straight into state/covariance with no model dispatch; ImmEstimator.cpp:449-461 does the same. (2) canInitiateTrack (MeasurementModels.hpp:29-31) returns true for RangeBearing2D and its comment explicitly lists RB2D as birth-capable. (3) Every birth site passes the raw measurement: Tracker.cpp:175-178 & 312-314, PmbmTracker.cpp:441/484 & 1452/1494, MhtTracker.cpp:36-38. No polar-to-ENU conversion exists on any birth path (grepped all RangeBearing2D handling in core/). (4) Decisive proof it is an omission, not a convention: SourceTouchPopulate.hpp:45-60 performs exactly the missing conversion (sensor_position_enu + (r cos b, r sin b) with Jacobian covariance) but only for the diagnostic SourceTouch, never for the seed. (5) Consumer contract confirmed: integration-guide.md:222 says RangeBearing2D "can start a track? yes", and SensorDefaults.cpp:39-42 ships ArpaTtm/EoIr RB2D noise rows, so feeding raw RB2D is a documented first-class path. (6) No test pins RB2D birth: test_ukf_estimator.cpp:75 pins initiate only for Position2D (RB2D test at :54 only exercises update, which handles RB2D correctly via predictMeasurement), and Builders.cpp:241-252 deliberately emits the first fix as Position2D. Hand-executed: value [5000, 0.9] births a track at ENU (5000, 0.9) vs true (3110, 3917) — ~4 km error, py variance 6.85e-4 m². Follow-on RB2D measurements predict bearing ~1.8e-4 rad from that state, residual ~0.9 rad never gates, so the real target never forms a valid track and each scan births a new garbage tentative.
  - verifier corrected details: Claim is accurate with one refinement to the failure scenario: because subsequent RB2D measurements do not gate to the garbage seed (bearing residual ~0.9 rad vs sigma ~0.026 rad), the phantom generally receives no updates and stays tentative/low-existence rather than persisting as a confirmed, confidently-located track near own-ship. The dominant operational symptom is therefore a silent TOTAL MISS: a non-cooperative target seen only by a raw-RangeBearing2D sensor is never tracked at all (every scan births a fresh garbage tentative that dies), which violates the repo's core presence-over-classification invariant. The defect is latent for all in-repo configurations (shipped NMEA adapters convert range/bearing to Position2D; scenario builders dodge the first fix), but it sits on a documented consumer contract (integration-guide.md:222 "can start a track? yes" plus ArpaTtm/EoIr RB2D SensorDefaults), and SourceTouchPopulate.hpp:45-60 shows the correct polar-to-ENU seed conversion already exists in-repo but is unused at birth. Affects UkfEstimator, EkfEstimator, ImmEstimator (verified :449-461), and ParticleFilterEstimator alike, across all three trackers' birth paths. Severity high: silent, safety-relevant, on a documented path — but not critical since no shipped in-repo pipeline triggers it.

- **[LOW/unverified]** PF update lacks the measurement-covariance PSD guard every other estimator has; a malformed R silently wipes the ensemble weights to uniform instead of rejecting the measurement
  - `core/estimation/ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:79` (robustness, confidence high)
  - description: EkfEstimator::update (EkfEstimator.cpp:37), UkfEstimator::update (UkfEstimator.cpp:61) and ImmEstimator::update (ImmEstimator.cpp:170) all start with 'if (!isMeasurementCovariancePsd(z.covariance)) return;' — the Phase 8 R3 guard added because one bad frame reaching the core permanently poisons a track. ParticleFilterEstimator::update instead calls z.covariance.inverse() unguarded (line 79). For a NaN/singular R, Rinv contains NaN/inf, every log_w becomes non-finite, the normalization sum is non-finite, and the code takes the 'All particles deemed impossible' fallback (lines 94-96) which resets particle_weights to uniform and then records last_update = z.time (line 114). The fallback comment shows it was designed for the all-likelihoods-underflow case, but that case can never reach it (log-sum-exp guarantees the max entry maps to exp(0)=1, so sum >= 1); the ONLY inputs that trigger it are non-finite ones — precisely the inputs the other estimators reject while leaving the track untouched. Net effect: the accumulated importance-weight information is silently destroyed and the garbage measurement is recorded as a successful update. No NaN reaches state/covariance (projectToGaussian uses finite particles + uniform weights), so this is degradation, not corruption.
  - failure_scenario: The same malformed frame class the Phase 8 R3 guard was built for (e.g. a 2x2 R with zero determinant from a degenerate upstream covariance) reaches a PF-configured pipeline: EKF/UKF/IMM tracks skip the frame unharmed, but the PF track's weight vector is reset to uniform — a sharply peaked posterior (e.g. mid bearing-only range collapse) is silently flattened and last_update advances, so the frame also consumes the track's freshness window.
  - evidence: ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:79 'const Eigen::MatrixXd Rinv = z.covariance.inverse();' with no isMeasurementCovariancePsd call (grep confirms the guard appears in EKF/UKF/IMM update and in all three tracker birth paths, but not in PF update); lines 94-96 'if (!std::isfinite(sum) || sum <= 0.0) { w = Eigen::VectorXd::Constant(N, 1.0 / N); }'.
  - suggested_fix: Add 'if (!isMeasurementCovariancePsd(z.covariance)) return;' at the top of ParticleFilterEstimator::update, mirroring the other estimators.

- **[LOW/unverified]** PF predict skips ALL process noise when Q(dt) is merely singular (not just zero), e.g. 5-state motion with omega PSD = 0 — deterministic propagation causes particle depletion after resampling
  - `core/estimation/ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:52` (correctness, confidence medium)
  - description: predict() draws process noise only if Eigen::LLT of Q succeeds (lines 52-60); on failure it 'skip[s] the noise term entirely' (comment, line 61). Eigen's LLT reports NumericalIssue for any exactly singular PSD matrix (zero pivot), not only Q == 0. CoordinatedTurn/CV5State/PrescribedTurn all build Q with Q(4,4) = q_omega * dt (CoordinatedTurn.cpp:56); a consumer who sets q_omega = 0 (a natural choice, e.g. pairing a PF with PrescribedTurn where omega is fixed by construction and needs no noise) gets a Q whose position/velocity block is PD but whose 5th pivot is 0 — LLT fails and the ENTIRE noise injection is dropped, not just the omega component. Every particle then propagates deterministically; after each systematic resample the surviving duplicates are never re-diversified, so the ensemble collapses to a handful of unique particles, projectToGaussian covariance shrinks toward zero, and gating becomes overconfident (dropped associations, dead track). The class comment (ParticleFilterEstimator.hpp:19-21) documents the skip only for 'q == 0 / singular' without acknowledging the partial-singularity case where valid noise dimensions exist. No test covers a PF with a singular-but-nonzero Q (tests use q > 0 throughout).
  - failure_scenario: Consumer configures ParticleFilterEstimator with a 5-state model and omega_psd = 0 (fixed-rate turn assumption). Q(dt) is singular every cycle, so no process noise is ever injected. Within a few resampling events (ESS collapses because weights concentrate) the 500-particle ensemble degenerates to a few identical copies; the projected covariance collapses, subsequent measurements fall outside the gate, and the track starves and is deleted while the target is still present.
  - evidence: ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:51-62: noise stays Zero(n,N) unless llt.info() == Eigen::Success; no fallback (e.g. LDLT or eigendecomposition with clamped zeros, as SigmaPoints.cpp:30-32 does for the same problem in the UKF).
  - suggested_fix: Fall back to a PSD square root when LLT fails (mirror SigmaPoints.cpp's SelfAdjointEigenSolver + cwiseMax(0) fallback), so the non-degenerate noise subspace is still sampled.

Coverage notes (estimation-ukf-pf): Read end-to-end: SigmaPoints.{hpp,cpp}, UkfEstimator.{hpp,cpp}, ParticleFilterEstimator.{hpp,cpp}, Resampling.{hpp,cpp}, PrescribedTurn.{hpp,cpp}; supporting reads: MeasurementModels.{hpp,cpp}, CoordinatedTurn.cpp, IMotionModel.hpp, EkfEstimator.cpp, ImmEstimator.cpp (predict/update UKF paths), GaussianScore.hpp, Tracker.cpp, PmbmTracker/MhtTracker birth paths, core/benchmark/Config.cpp wiring, AisAdapter.cpp, MeasurementBuilders.cpp, Builders.cpp, and tests (test_sigma_points, test_ukf_estimator, test_particle_filter_estimator, test_resampling, test_prescribed_turn, test_filter_comparison RB2D geometries). Verified clean against the hints: (1) systematicResample off-by-one — the 'i < N-1' guard makes the last particle absorb any float-error cumsum tail; N==0 early-out; u==0 boundary is a measure-zero non-issue; pinned by tests. (2) All-weights-underflow — the log-sum-exp normalization guarantees the max weight maps to exp(0)=1 so sum>=1; divide-by-zero unreachable for finite inputs (the non-finite path is finding 3). (3) PF RNG/determinism — single mt19937_64, draw counts purely input-driven, matches DeterministicForSameSeed; ESS threshold semantics (fraction*N) correct. (4) computeSigmaPoints non-PD handling — LLT-failure fallback via SelfAdjointEigenSolver with negative eigenvalues clamped exists and is tested (rank-1 and indefinite cases); negative w0/Wc(0) at small alpha is standard scaled-UT and reconstructions behave (verified numerically); NO validation of alpha=0 or kappa<=-n (scale<=0 gives inf/NaN weights or an all-zero fallback sqrt) — misconfiguration-only, left as a one-liner. (5) PrescribedTurn 'integration vs dt' — F(dt) closed form checked against the standard CT solution (position integral (s/w, -(1-c)/w; (1-c)/w, s/w), velocity rotation, CV limit at |w|<1e-6) and Q is the exact white-accel integral (dt^3/3, dt^2/2, dt) + q_omega*dt: correct; state omega passes through F unchanged by design (prescribed omega used, state omega only for IMM mixing). Also checked clean: UKF predict adds Q after reconstruction, no Eigen aliasing anywhere in scope (all products write fresh temporaries), dt<=0 no-ops, UKF update PSD-guard + LDLT solve + resymmetrisation, PF initiate PSD guard (its particle-less fallback track is inert — cannot predict/update — but unreachable through Tracker/PMBM/MHT since all three guard PSD before initiate), initiate() ignoring PositionVelocity2D velocity components matches the deliberate backlog-#20 decision (hint-based birth velocity only) so not reported. Overflow one-liners (not reported as findings): estimator update() sets track.last_update BACKWARDS on an out-of-order measurement (UkfEstimator.cpp:110, ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:114) causing double-propagation on the next predict — reachable only if a consumer calls Tracker::setRejectStaleMeasurements(false) (default is reject=true); PmbmTracker.cpp:1756 and MhtTracker.cpp:821 read scan[j].value(0/1) as ENU positions for coverage/clutter maps, which misplaces RangeBearing2D returns (same misinterpretation class as finding 2, outside my unit); finding 1's defect also exists verbatim in ImmEstimator.cpp:210 (canonical config runs use_ukf=true) — anchored in-scope at UkfEstimator.cpp:80 but the IMM site needs the same fix. Numeric verification of finding 1 was done by replicating computeSigmaPoints + the update equations in Python (scratchpad; repo untouched).

### unit: estimation-imm (5 findings)

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** initiate() treats RangeBearing2D value as ENU position — tracks born at (range_m, bearing_rad) as meters
  - `core/estimation/ImmEstimator.cpp:449` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: ImmEstimator::initiate copies z.value(0)/z.value(1) into the ENU position states (lines 449-450) and z.covariance's top-left 2x2 into the position covariance (lines 458-461) with no model dispatch. For MeasurementModel::RangeBearing2D, value = [range_m, bearing_rad] relative to sensor_position_enu (docs/integration-guide.md line 222), so the track is seeded at ENU east=range, north=bearing, and P(1,1) becomes a bearing variance in rad^2 (~1e-4) interpreted as m^2 — an absurdly tight north covariance. Yet canInitiateTrack(RangeBearing2D) returns true (MeasurementModels.hpp:29-31, doc comment explicitly says active range-bearing sensors DO initiate), and the integration guide's model table says RangeBearing2D 'can start a track: yes'. Every birth call site (Tracker.cpp:175-177/312-314, MhtTracker.cpp:349-355, PmbmTracker.cpp:441-484/1411-1453) gates only on canInitiateTrack + PSD, so any unassociated RangeBearing2D measurement births a garbage track. Guards elsewhere: none — grep shows no polar-to-ENU conversion anywhere on the initiate path. Tests: tests/estimation/test_imm_estimator.cpp initiates only from positionMeas(); no test covers RB initiation. The bench masks it: buildRangeBearingPassScenario (core/scenario/Builders.cpp:241-252) deliberately emits the FIRST fix as Position2D and RB only afterwards, so single-target sims rarely birth from RB. Same defect exists in EkfEstimator/UkfEstimator::initiate (out of scope, noted for synthesis).
  - failure_scenario: Consumer follows the integration guide and feeds a radar as RangeBearing2D (SensorDefaults.cpp:39 even provides default R for ArpaTtm+RangeBearing2D). A new vessel appears at true range 3000 m, bearing 2.5 rad (roughly WNW): the first return gates to no track, canInitiateTrack passes, and ImmEstimator::initiate seeds all IMM modes at ENU (3000, 2.5) m — ~3 km due east of own-ship regardless of true bearing — with north sigma ~= bearing sigma in radians (~0.02 m). Subsequent returns of the same vessel never gate to this track (predicted bearing from the garbage state differs by radians against a mrad-scale gate), so each scan births another phantom while the real vessel is never correctly tracked. Silent wrong tracks in a documented-supported configuration.
  - evidence: ImmEstimator.cpp:448-461 (x(0)=z.value(0); x(1)=z.value(1); P from z.covariance top-left 2x2, no switch on z.model); MeasurementModels.hpp:22-31 (canInitiateTrack doc: RangeBearing2D 'do'); docs/integration-guide.md:222 ('can start a track? yes' for RangeBearing2D); Tracker.cpp:175-177; PmbmTracker.cpp:484; evaluation-log.md:5003 ('Synthetic radars emit RangeBearing2D').
  - suggested_fix: In initiate(), dispatch on z.model: for RangeBearing2D convert (r, beta) + sensor_position_enu to ENU (px = sx + r*cos(beta), py = sy + r*sin(beta)) and propagate the polar covariance through the Jacobian (as adapters/projectRangeBearingToEnu already does); or make canInitiateTrack(RangeBearing2D) false and fix the guide. Apply the same fix to EkfEstimator/UkfEstimator/ParticleFilterEstimator::initiate.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full failing path. (1) ImmEstimator::initiate (core/estimation/ImmEstimator.cpp:448-461) copies z.value(0)/z.value(1) into the ENU position states and z.covariance's top-left 2x2 into position covariance with no switch on z.model; EkfEstimator::initiate (EkfEstimator.cpp:81-98) and UkfEstimator::initiate (UkfEstimator.cpp:122-137) are identical in this respect. (2) For RangeBearing2D, value is [range_m, bearing_rad]: confirmed by predictMeasurementValue (MeasurementModels.cpp:27-31), the wrapAngle residual handling in the update paths (ImmEstimator.cpp:215, UkfEstimator.cpp:86), the scenario builder (core/scenario/Builders.cpp:37-41), and the integration guide table (docs/integration-guide.md:222). (3) canInitiateTrack(RangeBearing2D) returns true (MeasurementModels.hpp:29-31), and every birth site gates only on canInitiateTrack + PSD: Tracker.cpp:175-177 and 312-314 call estimator_.initiate(z) directly; MhtTracker.cpp:349-354 routes through rootFromMeasurement (MhtTracker.cpp:36-58) which calls estimator.initiate(z); PmbmTracker.cpp:441/484 does the same for adaptive birth. (4) Guard search: the only polar-to-ENU conversion in the tree is projectRangeBearingToEnu (core/projection/Projection.cpp), used exclusively at the edges (MeasurementBuilders.cpp:71, adapters/arpa/ArpaAdapter.cpp:133, adapters/eoir/EoIrAdapter.cpp:56, replay loaders) — all of which emit Position2D. Nothing on the initiate path converts. (5) Hand-executed values: z.value=[3000, 2.5], R=diag(75^2, 0.0262^2) (the SensorDefaults.cpp:39 ArpaTtm defaults) births all IMM modes at ENU (3000, 2.5) m with P(1,1)=6.9e-4 m^2, while the true position is (-2404, 1795) m. On the next scan, the predicted measurement from the garbage state is [~3000 m, atan2(2.5,3000)=8.3e-4 rad]; the bearing innovation is ~2.5 rad against S(1,1) ~ 7e-4 rad^2, giving d^2 ~ 8900, far beyond any chi-square gate — so each subsequent return births another phantom and the real vessel is never tracked. (6) Tests do not contradict: tests/estimation/test_imm_estimator.cpp, test_ekf_estimator.cpp, test_ukf_estimator.cpp initiate only from Position2D measurements; buildRangeBearingPassScenario (Builders.cpp:241-252) deliberately emits the first fix as Position2D (evaluation-log.md:5541 confirms 'initial Position2D seed → RangeBearing2D thereafter'), and tests/pipeline/test_tracker_bearing_innovation_emit.cpp also seeds with Position2D before feeding RB. (7) Not documented as intended: the canInitiateTrack docstring says birth paths use it to avoid 'seeding garbage state', yet RB birth seeds exactly that; the integration guide table (line 222 + 225-227) tells consumers RangeBearing2D 'can start a track: yes' with no warning. One correction to the claim's framing: the guide's prose section for range+bearing sensors ('You have range + bearing') directs consumers to makeMeasurementFromRelativeBearing/TrueBearing, which project to Position2D — so a consumer following the recommended builder path is safe, and every in-repo adapter takes that path. The exposure is a consumer who hand-constructs RangeBearing2D measurements, which the model table and SensorDefaults explicitly present as supported.
  - verifier corrected details: All three estimators' initiate() (ImmEstimator.cpp:448-461, EkfEstimator.cpp:81-98, UkfEstimator.cpp:122-137) treat z.value as ENU position regardless of z.model. For MeasurementModel::RangeBearing2D (value=[range_m, bearing_rad]), any unassociated measurement births a track at ENU east=range, north=bearing-in-radians, with the bearing variance (rad^2) installed as the north position variance (m^2). All three tracker birth paths (Tracker.cpp:175/312, MhtTracker.cpp:349+36, PmbmTracker.cpp:441/484) permit this because canInitiateTrack(RangeBearing2D)==true, and the integration guide (line 222) plus SensorDefaults.cpp:39-42 document RangeBearing2D as a supported track-starting model. Result: silent garbage tracks plus a phantom-per-scan cascade (subsequent returns never gate to the mis-seeded track), and the real vessel is never acquired. Severity stays high rather than critical because the canonical consumer path (makeMeasurementFromRelativeBearing/TrueBearing, all in-repo adapters, and the guide's prose instructions) projects to Position2D before the tracker, so only consumers who hand-construct RangeBearing2D measurements — a documented but non-default configuration — hit it. Fix belongs either in initiate() (polar-to-ENU conversion with unscented/linearized covariance transform using z.sensor_position_enu) or in canInitiateTrack/docs (declare RB non-initiating until conversion exists); tests initiate only from Position2D today, so a new test is needed either way.

- **[LOW/REFUTED]** UKF update (canonical config) computes arithmetic mean of sigma-point bearings — catastrophic corruption when predicted bearing straddles +-pi
  - `core/estimation/ImmEstimator.cpp:210` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: In the use_ukf_ update path (the CANONICAL production path — core/benchmark/Config.cpp:97-116 builds the canonical IMM with use_ukf=true, promoted 2026-06-20), z_pred is the weighted arithmetic mean of per-sigma-point measurement values (line 210). predictMeasurementValue returns bearings via atan2 in (-pi, pi]. When the per-mode predicted bearing is near +-pi, sigma points on opposite sides of the -x axis return values differing by ~2*pi, and the arithmetic mean is garbage. With the default ukf_alpha=1e-3, n=5: scale = 5e-6, so Wm(0) ~= -999999 and Wm(i) = +1e5 (SigmaPoints.cpp:45-50). These huge weights cancel exactly only if all sigma bearings share a branch; one sigma point flipped across the cut shifts z_pred by 2*pi*1e5 ~= 6.28e5 rad. The per-sigma deviations zd are then wrap-corrected AFTER subtracting this garbage mean (lines 214-216), yielding arbitrary O(1) wrapped values whose Wc-weighted sum (Wc(0) ~= -1e6) makes Sxx — and hence S — indefinite garbage; y = wrapAngle(z - z_pred) is an arbitrary angle (line 221). K_gain = Pxz*S.inverse() then applies a garbage correction to the mode mean and P_new = P_j - K*S*K' (line 228) corrupts the mode covariance; gaussianScore on the indefinite S (line 259, floored log-det in GaussianScore.hpp:31) produces a huge positive log-likelihood that locks the mode probabilities onto the corrupted mode. Guards: gating happens on the EKF-linearized path (gate(), lines 504-524), which is continuous at +-pi, so the measurement passes the gate and reaches the broken update. Tests: test_imm_estimator.cpp exercises only Position2D with the UKF inner filter (UkfInnerFilterTracksAndShrinksLikeEkfOnLinearMeasurement, line 120) — linear h, no wrap. The doc only lists 'circular-statistics bearing mean when sigma spread is wide' as future work for UkfEstimator (estimation.md:127); the discontinuity blow-up at +-pi occurs at ANY spread and is amplified by the 1e5-magnitude scaled-UKF weights, which that note does not capture. UkfEstimator.cpp:79-91 shares the flaw (out of scope, noted for synthesis).
  - failure_scenario: Canonical IMM (use_ukf=true), EO-IR Bearing2D or radar RangeBearing2D measurement of a vessel almost due WEST of the sensor (true bearing ~ +-pi — e.g. a constant-bearing crossing target, exactly the collision-relevant geometry). Sigma spread in bearing is sqrt(5e-6)*sigma_pos/range ~ 1e-4 rad, so whenever the predicted bearing lands within ~1e-4 rad of pi (expected roughly once per few hundred scans while the geometry holds), one sigma point flips branch: z_pred becomes ~-6.28e5 rad, the residual and S/Pxz are garbage, and the mode state jumps unpredictably (kilometres possible) with a corrupted, possibly indefinite covariance. The moment-matched track.state inherits the jump; the track is silently lost or teleported at the operationally critical moment, and mode probabilities are scrambled.
  - evidence: ImmEstimator.cpp:200-228 (arithmetic mean line 210; wrap applied only to deviations, lines 215-216; non-Joseph P_new line 228); SigmaPoints.cpp:14,45-50 (Wm(0)=lambda/scale = 1-n/(alpha^2*(n+kappa)) ~= -1e6 at alpha=1e-3, n=5); ImmEstimator.hpp:56-58 (default alpha 1e-3); Config.cpp:111-115 (/*use_ukf=*/true on canonical); MeasurementModels.cpp:30-38 (atan2 branch cut).
  - suggested_fix: Compute the bearing component of z_pred with circular statistics (atan2 of weighted sin/cos sums), or re-branch all sigma-point bearings to the chart of the center point (b_i <- b_0 + wrapAngle(b_i - b_0)) before averaging; apply the same to UkfEstimator.
  - verifier: The claimed corruption mechanism is arithmetically wrong for the canonical configuration. With the defaults actually used everywhere (ImmEstimator.hpp:56-58: ukf_alpha=1e-3, ukf_kappa=0.0; no call site in the repo overrides them — grep shows only /*use_ukf=*/true call sites in core/benchmark/Config.cpp and app/mht_fusion_example.cpp) and the fixed 5-d IMM state, the sigma weights are integers: Wm(i)=1/(2·α²·(n+κ))=1/(2·5e-6)=100000 exactly, Wm(0)=λ/scale=1−10⁶ exactly (fp deviation ≲1e-10). A branch flip of any subset of sigma-point bearings therefore shifts the arithmetic mean z_pred by 2π×(integer combination of weights) — an integer multiple of 2π. Every downstream consumer of z_pred wraps the bearing component: zd(1)/zd(0) at ImmEstimator.cpp:215-216 (feeding both Sxx and Pxz) and the residual y via measurementResidual (line 221, MeasurementModels.cpp:93-97, fmod-based wrapAngle exact to fp for 6e5-magnitude inputs). Wrapping removes the 2πk offset exactly, so the claim's key step — "zd are then wrap-corrected AFTER subtracting this garbage mean, yielding arbitrary O(1) wrapped values" — is false: the wrapped deviations equal the correct deviations from the correct circular mean to ~1e-10 rad. I replicated the exact code path numerically (same sigma-point construction from SigmaPoints.cpp, same weights, same wrap placement) with a target due west (state [−3000, 0.02, −2, 0, 0], P=diag(50², 50², 4, 4, 0.01), RangeBearing2D, sensor at origin): one sigma point flipped branch, raw z_pred bearing = −628315.389 (exactly the claimed garbage), yet after the in-code wraps the residual bearing matched the EKF reference to 1.1e-10 rad, Pxz to 1.4e-10 relative, and Sxx stayed positive definite (eigenvalues 2.78e-4, 2.5e3) — no indefinite S, no state jump, no mode-probability scramble. The claimant's static reading correctly identified the huge intermediate mean but failed to account for the fact that with these specific default weights the offset is a multiple of 2π that the existing wrap calls cancel. Residual latent hazard: the rescue is a numerical coincidence of integer weights; my α=0.7 counter-run (w=0.204..., non-integer) shows genuine corruption (wrapped z_pred=1.859 rad instead of ~π). But ukf_alpha/ukf_kappa are constructor-only parameters never passed by any caller, and α=1e-1/1e-2/1e-3 all yield integer weights at n=5, so no reachable configuration hits it. That makes this a hardening suggestion (compute the mean of wrapped-relative bearings, or unwrap Zsp to a common branch before averaging), not a reachable defect at the stated high severity.
  - verifier corrected details: ImmEstimator.cpp:210 (and UkfEstimator.cpp analog) does take an arithmetic mean of atan2 bearings across the ±π cut, but with every shipped configuration (default ukf_alpha=1e-3, ukf_kappa=0, n=5) the scaled-UKF weights are exact integers (1e5 and 1−1e6), so any branch-flip offset in z_pred is an integer multiple of 2π that the wrapAngle calls at lines 215-216 and 221 cancel to ~1e-10 rad — verified by numerically replicating the code path at a straddling geometry (Sxx positive definite, residual/Pxz match EKF reference). The defect is only latent: a consumer constructing ImmEstimator/UkfEstimator with an alpha making 1/(2α²(n+κ)) non-integer (e.g. 0.7) would get real corruption at ±π straddles. No caller in the repo passes a non-default alpha. Severity: low (latent robustness gap, unreachable in all current configs); fix would be to unwrap sigma-point bearings to a common branch (or circular mean) before the weighted average.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** softUpdate assumes one shared R across the gated batch, but per-measurement R is a first-class supported input — asserts don't check it
  - `core/estimation/ImmEstimator.cpp:361` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: softUpdate builds S, the Kalman gain, the per-measurement Gaussian weights f_{m,j} (norm and S_inv, lines 361-384), and the Joseph 'all-correct' covariance arm (line 415) exclusively from z0.covariance — the covariance of whichever gated measurement happens to be FIRST in scan order. The comment block asserts 'All gated measurements share the same measurement model and covariance R ... True for any single-scan JPDA call from Tracker::processBatch' — but that claim is false for the pipeline's own supported input: the integration guide (section 3) explicitly tells consumers 'R is per measurement ... a sensor whose accuracy grows with range just sets a larger R on the far reading', and JpdaAssociator computes the betas with each measurement's OWN R via estimator->logLikelihood (JpdaAssociator.cpp:100-110). The runtime asserts (lines 341-348) check only model and sensor_position_enu equality, not covariance, so a same-sensor heterogeneous-R batch passes silently even in debug builds. The result also depends on which gated measurement is first in the scan (deterministic per log, but an arbitrary weighting choice). EkfEstimator::softUpdate shares the defect (out of scope). No test pins heterogeneous-R softUpdate (test_imm_estimator.cpp soft tests use a single measurement or identical R).
  - failure_scenario: JPDA + IMM pipeline; one radar scan contains two returns gating to the same track: a near return with R = diag(25, 25) m^2 (first in scan) and a far return with R = diag(2500, 2500) m^2, with betas ~ (0.5, 0.5) from the associator. softUpdate computes S, the gain, the mixture weights, and the posterior covariance as if BOTH measurements had the tight 25 m^2 covariance: the far, noisy return pulls the state at 100x its correct weight and the posterior covariance is shrunk as if two precise measurements were fused — an overconfident track whose too-small gate then rejects subsequent legitimate measurements (track loss after a few scans of this pattern). If the far return happens to be first in the scan, the opposite error (severely under-weighted update) occurs instead.
  - evidence: ImmEstimator.cpp:337 (z0 = gated_measurements[0]), 361 (S = H*P_j*H' + z0.covariance), 374-384 (norm/f_sum from z0's S), 415 (K*z0.covariance*K'), 341-348 (asserts omit covariance); docs/integration-guide.md 'R is per measurement' paragraph after the model table; core/association/JpdaAssociator.cpp:100-110 (betas use per-measurement R).
  - suggested_fix: Compute per-measurement S_m = H P_j H' + R_m for the Gaussian weights, and use the beta-weighted effective R (or per-measurement gain contributions) in the PDAF combination; at minimum assert covariance equality across the batch so the violated assumption is loud, and correct the 'True for any single-scan JPDA call' comment.

- **[LOW/unverified]** bearing_range_guard is applied in update() but silently skipped in softUpdate() — JPDA bearing streams lose the LOS-collapse protection the flag promises
  - `core/estimation/ImmEstimator.cpp:417` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: update() clamps the along-LOS position variance after every Bearing2D update when bearing_range_guard_ is set (lines 246-251, per-mode applyBearingRangeGuard). softUpdate() performs the equivalent per-mode Bearing2D covariance updates (Joseph arm line 412-415, PDAF combination lines 417-419) but never applies the guard, and nothing in the header or BearingRangeGuard.hpp documents the guard as hard-update-only (the header's UKF note says softUpdate 'is unchanged — still EKF/Joseph', which is about the inner filter, not the guard). The guard exists precisely because 'a stream of bearings can drive the along-LOS variance below its predicted value' (BearingRangeGuard.hpp:12-15) — the PDAF combination contains the same Joseph term with the same cross-coupling leak, weighted by (1-beta_0), so the pathology reproduces under JPDA at a slightly slower rate. EkfEstimator::softUpdate has the same omission (out of scope). No test covers guard+softUpdate (tests/estimation/test_bearing_range_guard.cpp exercises hard updates).
  - failure_scenario: Consumer wires JpdaAssociator + ImmEstimator(bearing_range_guard=true) with a camera Bearing2D stream (the shipped camera-bearing pipeline) against a distant non-cooperative target. Every scan takes the softUpdate path (Tracker::processBatch, betas present), so a sustained stream of bearing-only updates drives the along-LOS position variance below its predicted value through the kinematic cross-correlations — the filter becomes overconfident in a range it never measured, exactly the documented BOT pathology — despite the operator having enabled the guard that is supposed to prevent it.
  - evidence: ImmEstimator.cpp:246-251 (guard in update), 410-419 (softUpdate covariance write with no guard call); BearingRangeGuard.hpp:8-15 (pathology description); Tracker.cpp:223-250 (JPDA scans route to softUpdate, never update).
  - suggested_fix: In softUpdate, when bearing_range_guard_ && z0.model == Bearing2D, apply applyBearingRangeGuard(P_j, P_combined, x_j, z0.sensor_position_enu) per mode before writing track.imm_covariances[j] (P_j is the pre-update prior, mirroring update()).

- **[LOW/unverified]** IMM overrides of gate()/logLikelihood() (and softUpdate) drop the base-class non-PSD-R guard — a finite indefinite R passes the gate with negative d2 and wins association with an explosive likelihood
  - `core/estimation/ImmEstimator.cpp:496` (input-validation, confidence high)
  - description: IEstimator::gate and IEstimator::logLikelihood (EstimatorDefaults.cpp:28, 45) reject non-PSD measurement covariance (gate fails closed; logLikelihood returns -inf), a guard added deliberately in Phase 8 so 'one bad NMEA frame' cannot poison a track. ImmEstimator's overrides have no such guard. Concrete trace with R = [[1,2],[2,1]] (finite, symmetric, eigenvalues 3 and -1 — passes allFinite, fails the base LDLT check): fast2d gate (lines 503-511) computes S = P_topleft + R; with P_topleft = diag(0.5,0.5), S = [[1.5,2],[2,1.5]], det = -1.75; for y = (1,-1), mahalanobis2x2 = 7/-1.75 = -4, and -4 <= gate_threshold PASSES (GaussianScore.hpp:85 documents the +-inf/NaN singular case but the negative-det case yields a finite negative d2 that fails OPEN). logLikelihood (lines 548-568) on the same S gets mahalanobis = -4 and log_det_safe = log(1e-300) = -690.8, so log_ell ~= +346 — exp() overflows to +inf in JpdaAssociator.cpp:101, concentrating the betas on the malformed measurement. softUpdate (line 334) also lacks the PSD guard that update() has (line 170), so the malformed measurement is then folded in: luInverseDet on the indefinite S returns a finite garbage inverse and the mode states/covariances are silently corrupted. Under any single-Gaussian estimator the identical input is rejected at both the gate and the likelihood, so this is an IMM-only hole in the codebase's own Phase-8 hardening standard. Preconditions are unusual (adapters validate at the edge; a direct-Measurement library consumer must supply a finite-but-indefinite R, e.g. a mis-composed cross-covariance), hence low severity.
  - failure_scenario: A library consumer constructs Measurements directly (the documented primary integration path) and composes R from a heading/GPS covariance combination that goes indefinite (finite entries, negative eigenvalue — the exact case the Phase 8 iter-4 LDLT strengthening cites: 'diagonal-positive / off-diagonal-dominated'). With the IMM + JPDA pipeline: the measurement passes the IMM gate with negative d2, exp(+346) likelihood makes it dominate the betas for whatever track is nearby, and softUpdate writes garbage into every mode's mean and covariance — permanent silent track corruption. The same frame fed to the EKF pipeline is dropped harmlessly.
  - evidence: ImmEstimator.cpp:493-526 (gate override, no PSD check, no isfinite check on d2 unlike EstimatorDefaults.cpp:36), 534-577 (logLikelihood override, no guard), 334 (softUpdate, no guard) vs 170 (update has the guard); EstimatorDefaults.cpp:22-47 (base guards + rationale); GaussianScore.hpp:80-95; MeasurementModels.hpp:69-92 (guard rationale and LDLT strictness).
  - suggested_fix: Mirror the base-class guards in the IMM overrides: early-return false / -inf when !isMeasurementCovariancePsd(z.covariance) in gate()/logLikelihood(), add the same guard at the top of softUpdate() (matching update() line 170), and gate the final d2 on std::isfinite as EstimatorDefaults does.

Coverage notes (estimation-imm): Scope reviewed end-to-end: core/estimation/ImmEstimator.{hpp,cpp}, GaussianScore.hpp, EstimatorDefaults.cpp; supporting reads: MeasurementModels.{hpp,cpp}, SigmaPoints.cpp, CoordinatedTurn.{hpp,cpp}, ConstantVelocity5State.cpp, EkfEstimator.cpp, UkfEstimator.cpp (comparison), BearingRangeGuard.hpp, Tracker.cpp, MhtTracker/PmbmTracker/TrackTree birth+gate call sites, JpdaAssociator likelihood path, benchmark/Config.cpp (canonical wiring: use_ukf=TRUE with default alpha=1e-3), scenario/Builders.cpp, DatumShift.cpp, docs/algorithms/estimation.md section 6, integration-guide model table, tests/estimation/test_imm_estimator.cpp. Checked clean per the hints: (1) mixing c_j==0 division is guarded (identity fallback col, lines 94-100); Sum(c)=1 preserved because transitionFor renormalizes rows; c_j=0 is transient, not absorbing — shipped TPMs are strictly positive and an underflowed-to-zero mode recovers through mixing; log floor max(c,1e-300) handles it. (2) Cross-model state-dimension mixing is a non-issue: unified 5-state everywhere (initiate seeds 5xK; CV5State carries omega as identity+random-walk Q). (3) Missed detections apply no mode-likelihood term (TPM only via predict) — standard, uniform P_D across modes cancels; MHT miss branches copy the predicted ensemble. (4) TPM dt-scaling: code (transitionFor, pi^dt with 1s TPM, dt==1 short-circuit, NaN fallback, clamp+row-renorm) MATCHES estimation.md section 6 and the header; semigroup property verified; tests ModeTransitionIsDtScaled/ComposesAcrossPredicts pin it. (5) predict/update TPM applied exactly once (predict advances mu to the prior; dt<=0 predict no-ops so same-timestamp second update correctly consumes the first update's posterior as prior). (6) EKF-path CT-mode omega unobservability (transitionMatrixAt has zero d/d-omega column, so omega-position cross-covariance never develops and omega stays at 0 under EKF) is DOCUMENTED as a known limitation in estimation.md section 6 with measured resolutions (prescribed-rate IMM-3, UKF backend) — not reported per instructions. (7) Moment-match projection, mixing weight orientation (pi[i][j]=P(j|i), c_j = sum_i pi(i,j)mu_i), PDAF spread term, gate-volume formula (pi*gamma^2*sqrt(det) for d=2, proxy fallback for d>2), log-sum-exp with uniform reset on non-finite/zero sum, and the omitted (2pi)^-d/2 constant in update() log_lambda (cancels, common d) all verified correct. (8) GaussianScore one-LU helpers match the historical determinant/inverse split; mahalanobis2x2 closed form verified; safeLogDet floor semantics preserved. (9) wrapAngle correct at exactly +-pi; measurementResidual wraps both polar models; EKF update path is continuous at +-pi (only the UKF path has the wrap defect reported). (10) SigmaPoints LLT failure falls back to clamped eigendecomposition (no NaN path); asymmetric P is harmless to LLT/SelfAdjointEigenSolver (lower triangle only). (11) Out-of-order timestamps: Tracker reject_stale_ defaults TRUE, so update()'s unconditional last_update = z.time rewind is reachable only via opt-in setRejectStaleMeasurements(false) — latent one-liner. (12) Datum recenter shifts imm_means/imm_covariances (DatumShift.cpp:49-62) — no stale-ensemble hole. Overflow one-liners (not reported as findings): ImmEstimator UKF update lacks UkfEstimator's Phase-8-R4 resymmetrization and LDLT solve (P_new = P_j - K S K', line 228; epsilon-scale drift, no traced failure); ImmEstimator::initiate lacks EkfEstimator's internal empty/non-PSD covariance guard (all in-tree callers guard externally; hazard only for direct estimator->initiate consumers); initiate does not validate mu0_/pi_ dimensions against motions_.size() (constructor misconfiguration -> OOB, all factories consistent); initiate reads z.value(1) without a size check (malformed 1-d Position2D -> OOB, adapters validate); softUpdate ignores the robust noise_ scale that update() applies (documented nowhere, behavioral inconsistency only); estimation.md section 6 still shows the plain (I-KH)P per-mode update and lists 'UKF backend' as future work although code uses Joseph form and the canonical shipped use_ukf=true (doc staleness, not a code defect). Findings 1 and 2 name sibling estimators (Ekf/Ukf/ParticleFilter initiate; UkfEstimator update) sharing the same defects — flagged for the units owning those files.


## Batch B2-assoc-pmbm-pipeline

### unit: association (2 findings)

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** murtyKBest returns an EMPTY result (all-or-nothing) when the seed LSAP contains any forced-infeasible edge, breaking the per-row degradation contract both callers were built against
  - `core/association/Murty.cpp:69` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: hungarianAssignment maps +inf cells to a finite BIG_M so it can always complete, and its documented contract (pinned by tests/association/test_hungarian.cpp:61-77 'DegenerateAllInfRowSurvivesWithoutHang': 'The MHT caller detects this via std::isfinite(cost(t, a[t])) and falls back') is that infeasible rows degrade PER-ROW at the caller. murtyKBest, inserted between Hungarian and both trackers (commit db7dcea), instead rejects the WHOLE seed: feasibleAgainst(seed_assign, C0) fails if ANY assigned cell is +inf in the original matrix, and the function returns zero assignments and zero costs. A forced-infeasible edge occurs whenever an all-+inf row exists with no spare padding column to absorb it (rows >= cols), or an all-+inf COLUMN exists (every column must be assigned when rows >= cols). Both call sites still contain the per-row defensive code that this behavior makes dead: PmbmTracker.cpp:844-856 re-checks isfinite(C(row,col)) per assignment, and MhtTracker.cpp:151-153 comments 'the row is all +inf -> solver will leave it unassigned' — which is false (with cols=M+T > rows=T there are no padding columns for real rows... rows are padded instead, so every real row gets a real column, and one leafless tree empties the entire K-best result).
  - failure_scenario: PMBM path: a consumer wires FixedSensorDetectionModel with clutter_intensity = 0 for AIS ('AIS produces no clutter' — nothing validates lambda_C > 0 anywhere; PmbmTracker's ctor only validates the miss-model combination). At cold start density_.ppp is empty, so for an AIS measurement rho_total = rho_target + lambda_z = 0 + 0 = 0 (PmbmTracker.cpp:271-275). Its new-target diagonal cell stays +inf (line 828-831 guards rho > 0) and, with no gated Bernoulli, its column is all-+inf in the (n+m) x m matrix. Hungarian is forced to place a BIG_M edge on that column, feasibleAgainst(seed) fails, murtyKBest returns EMPTY, updateHypothesis produces ZERO children for every parent, and density_.mbm goes empty — no births for ANY measurement in the scan (including perfectly good radar returns) and all existing hypotheses silently vanish, every scan, for as long as such a measurement recurs. MHT path: any tree that ever reaches the solver with zero leaves (e.g. k_max_leaves configured 0 — pruneKLocal then demotes every unprotected leaf) makes the entire scan's global hypothesis solve return no assignment for ALL trees, not just the degenerate one.
  - evidence: Murty.cpp:39-47 feasibleAgainst rejects any assignment touching a non-finite cell in the ORIGINAL matrix; Murty.cpp:68-69 'if (!feasibleAgainst(seed_assign, C0)) return out;'. Hungarian.cpp:22-26 documents the opposite intent ('the caller can detect this by re-checking the original cost matrix'), and test_hungarian.cpp:61-77 pins that pre-Murty contract naming the MHT caller. MhtTracker.cpp:151-153 states the row 'will be left unassigned' — untrue for the T x (M+T) shape (row-padding, not column-padding, so every real row is assigned a real column). PmbmTracker.cpp:842-856 contains the per-row isfinite re-check that can never fire. Murty.hpp:40-41 only documents the all-+inf-ROW caveat, not the all-+inf-COLUMN case reachable in PMBM. No test covers a partially-infeasible matrix through murtyKBest (test_murty.cpp HonorsForbiddenCells uses a matrix that still has a fully feasible permutation).
  - suggested_fix: On seed (or child) infeasibility, strip the BIG_M edges instead of discarding the result: mark those rows unassigned (-1) and return the remaining partial assignment as the K=1 solution, matching the documented Hungarian degradation contract; the callers' existing isfinite re-checks then handle it. Independently, fail loud on clutter_intensity <= 0 in PmbmTracker's ctor (the project's stated R8.8/R9 philosophy) and fix the stale MhtTracker.cpp:151-153 comment.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** JPDA joint-event enumeration is global over the whole scan, not per gating cluster: event count is the PRODUCT across independent clusters, so ordinary clean multi-target scenes (~20 tracks) trip the 1e6 cap, silently degrading the entire scan to hard GNN and allocating ~100+ MB of transient event storage every scan
  - `core/association/JpdaAssociator.cpp:158` (robustness, confidence high)
  - description: The code comment (JpdaAssociator.cpp:151-157) and header (JpdaAssociator.hpp:49-52) describe the 1e6-event budget as a per-CLUSTER safeguard ('Full-enumeration JPDA is O(M^T) per gating cluster... only pathological real-clutter clusters fall back'). But associate() builds one M x T validation matrix for the whole scan and calls enumerateJointEvents on it once; there is no connected-component decomposition anywhere (Tracker::processBatch passes the full scan directly). Joint events over independent clusters factorize, so the global event count is the product of per-cluster counts — exponential in the number of clusters even when every cluster is trivial. Worse, JointEvents.cpp:19-22 detects overflow only AFTER materializing events (out.push_back(current); return out.size() <= max_events;), so a scan that overflows first allocates up to 1,000,001 std::vector<int> events of M entries each, all discarded on return.
  - failure_scenario: 20 well-separated tracks each cleanly gating exactly one measurement (V is a 20 x 20 diagonal — zero clutter, the most benign scene possible): each measurement independently has 2 options (clutter or its own track), so the enumeration is 2^20 = 1,048,576 > 1,000,000. enumerateJointEvents materializes ~1e6 events of 20 ints each (~100-130 MB including vector headers and allocator overhead), then returns empty; the whole scan falls back to greedy 0/1 hard association (overflow_fallback = true). This repeats EVERY scan while the scene persists: a JPDA deployment silently becomes GNN — losing exactly the soft-association benefit JPDA exists for, in exactly the dense multi-target conditions it targets — plus a recurring ~100 MB allocation spike per scan. With modest clutter it triggers even earlier (13 tracks with 2 gated returns each: 3^13 = 1.59e6). No test contradicts this: tests/association/test_jpda_associator.cpp uses at most 2 tracks and 3 measurements and never exercises the overflow path.
  - evidence: JpdaAssociator.cpp:93-121 builds V and g over the full scan; :158-160 'constexpr std::size_t kMaxJointEvents = 1'000'000; enumerateJointEvents(V, kMaxJointEvents)'; :151-157 comment claims per-cluster capping and 'only pathological real-clutter clusters fall back'. JointEvents.cpp:19-22 pushes each completed event before checking the budget, so the full ~1e6-event vector exists before overflow is signaled. Tracker.cpp:220-221 passes the whole scan with no clustering. Product arithmetic: diagonal V of size n gives exactly 2^n events (each measurement independently clutter-or-own-track).
  - suggested_fix: Decompose the gate graph into connected components (union-find over V) and run enumeration + normalization per component — betas of independent clusters are mathematically independent, so results are identical while the count becomes the SUM of per-cluster counts (40 events for the 20-track scene instead of 2^20). Apply the cap per component. Independently, make enumerateJointEvents count-first or bail before push_back so the overflow signal does not cost max_events allocations.

Coverage notes (association): Scope reviewed end-to-end: Gating.{hpp,cpp}, GnnAssociator.{hpp,cpp}, Hungarian.{hpp,cpp}, JointEvents.{hpp,cpp}, JpdaAssociator.{hpp,cpp}, Murty.{hpp,cpp}, plus their tests (tests/association/*), call sites (PmbmTracker.cpp:740-1200, MhtTracker.cpp:74-330, Tracker.cpp:195-320, Gospa/Ospa/TGospa/Metrics), and supporting code (MeasurementModels.cpp, EstimatorDefaults.cpp, TrackTree.cpp branch/prune paths, ISensorDetectionModel.hpp, ClutterMapDetectionModel.cpp).  Verified CLEAN (hand-traced): Murty partitioning forces/excludes correctly (forbid-edge + lock-row/col loop matches Miller-Stone-Cox); solution spaces are disjoint and complete including rectangular cases with unassigned rows (N>M: the only solution containing all assigned edges is the popped one, so skipping c<0 rows loses nothing and duplicates are impossible); costs evaluated against the ORIGINAL matrix are nondecreasing because each child's space is a subset of its parent's; the 2026-07-06 early-exit commit (45a504d) is bit-identical since children generated after the K-th accept only feed pops that never happen; K>feasible-count terminates (heap drains); test_murty.cpp pins K1==Hungarian (30 random trials), full 3x3 enumeration vs brute force with set-based dedup, forbidden cells, and rectangular surplus-cols. Hungarian: canonical e-maxx JV loop verified line-by-line against the published formulation; hand-executed square, surplus-cols (padding rows) and surplus-rows (padding cols) cases; zero-cost padding never distorts real-row optima (padding rows/cols are indifferent completers); negative costs handled (BIG_M uses abs(max_finite)); delta can never stay infinite (all internal cells finite); empty-matrix and all-inf-row cases exercised by tests.
