Gating/measurement models: bearing residual wrap present and correct (wrapAngle maps to (-pi,pi]); RangeBearing/Bearing Jacobians correct; NaN d2 from near-singular S fails gates closed in all three consumers (GNN 'd2 > thr' NaN->not-continue but NaN cost never beats best; JPDA 'd2 <= thr' NaN->false; IEstimator::gate requires isfinite(d2) and PSD R). JPDA: per-track normalization Sum_j beta_jt + beta_0t = 1 verified structurally (events partition per track); log-sum-exp is max-shifted and the degenerate all-NaN/zero sum falls back to all-miss; clutter-density units consistent per measurement (each j contributes either log lambda_C^s(j) or log P_D + log g in the same measurement-space density units, per ISensorDetectionModel.hpp); per-sensor miss aggregation over distinct (sensor,model,source) tuples matches TrackTree::branch convention exactly (deliberate, tested by PerSensorSingleSensorMatchesScalar / PerSensorOutOfCoverageChargesNoMiss); scalar mode is textbook parametric JPDA; overflow fallback is deterministic per binary and sets the diagnostic flag. JointEvents: enumeration complete (clutter option + injective gated-track options per measurement), empty-return-signals-overflow contract is unambiguous (all-clutter event always exists otherwise), M==0 returns the single empty event.  Overflow candidates / out-of-scope one-liners: (1) Hungarian BIG_M dominance (1+1e3*max|c|+1e9) can theoretically be undercut when rows > ~500 AND |costs| >> 1e6, letting an infeasible solution beat a feasible one (Murty then drops a still-feasible partition) — unreachable at current call sites where costs are log-likelihood scale. (2) lambda_C = 0 also drives MHT hit scores to +inf via -log(0) (TrackTree.cpp:273, no floor unlike JPDA's max(lambda,1e-300)), and the resulting -inf COST cell is mapped by hungarianAssignment to BIG_M-forbidden — inverting 'infinitely good' into 'forbidden' (tracking/ scope, same config edge as finding 1). (3) DetectionParams.probability_of_detection and .clutter_intensity have no default initializers (ports/ISensorDetectionModel.hpp:35-36) — a consumer that default-constructs and partially fills reads indeterminate values (ports scope). (4) JPDA per-sensor mode ignores DetectionParams::gate_threshold per-sensor override honored by MHT/PMBM — header explicitly scopes parity to (P_D, lambda_C) so treated as documented, not a defect. (5) Single chi-square gate shared across 1/2/4-dof measurement models changes effective gate probability per model — config convention with an existing per-sensor override mechanism; not flagged. (6) GnnAssociator re-evaluates estimator gate+logLikelihood for every remaining pair on every greedy commit iteration (O(k*nt*nm) redundant likelihood evals) and Murty copies the full cost matrix per heap node — performance only, correctness unaffected.

### unit: pmbm (7 findings)

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** Misdetected Bernoullis receive spurious SourceTouches: the z.time == b.last_update filter cannot separate misses from detections after predict
  - `core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:1666` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: The source-touch walk (PmbmTracker.cpp:1657-1698) claims "misdetected ones inherit the parent pre-predict timestamp, so an exact-match filter cleanly separates the two". This is false: PmbmTracker::predict() runs estimator_.predict on every Bernoulli (line 226), and every estimator sets track.last_update = to (EkfEstimator.cpp:30, ImmEstimator.cpp:164, UkfEstimator.cpp:55), so after predict(t_max) EVERY Bernoulli — detected or not — has last_update == t_max. Any measurement with time == t_max (in the common uniform-timestamp scan, ALL measurements) passes the filter, and the misdetected Bernoulli is then attributed the NEAREST measurement with no distance limit (lines 1663-1675). The R2-fixed true claim (Bernoulli::last_claimed_meas_index, -1 on miss) is available but unused here. Consequences: (a) every emitted Track's recent_contributions (refreshAggregatedTracks, line 2318-2321) contains touches from measurements the track never claimed — these feed the heading-bias pair extractors per the header's own claim that they are "actual contributions" (PmbmTracker.hpp:938-943), so a coasting radar track paired with another vessel's AIS return produces garbage bias observations; (b) under source_aware_misdetection without identity hints (radar/non-cooperative measurements carry no mmsi, so the vessel_id 'continue' suppression never engages), the false touch adds the scan's source to the track's history, defeating the gate: an AIS-only track near any radar return is charged radar misses on subsequent radar scans — the exact failure the flag documents itself as preventing; (c) idle_halflife_sec decay is muted because the false touch resets last-touch time every scan. Note: tests/pmbm/test_pmbm_sensor_activity.cpp:35-41 explicitly acknowledges the mechanism ("a new SourceTouch is appended ... even for miss-detected Bernoullis"), so part of the identity-gate design compensates for it — but the in-source comment claims the opposite, and consequences (a) and (c) plus the channel-fallback defeat are unmitigated and active in DEFAULT configs (the walk is unconditional).
  - failure_scenario: Default config, uniform-timestamp radar scans at 1 Hz: track T (id 7) is misdetected at scan k while another vessel's return z sits 800 m away at t_max. T.last_update == t_max after predict, so z matches the exact-time filter and is T's nearest measurement; a SourceTouch{sensor=radar, time=t_max, enu=z} is appended to contribution_history_[7]. tracks()[T].recent_contributions now reports a contribution T never claimed; if an AIS return was nearest instead, extractCrossSensorPositionPairs pairs T's radar history with the other vessel's AIS position, feeding a false offset into the bias estimator. With source_aware_misdetection=true, T's history now contains the foreign source and T is existence-penalized on every subsequent scan of a sensor that never observed it.
  - evidence: PmbmTracker.cpp:1659-1662 comment vs EkfEstimator.cpp:30 / ImmEstimator.cpp:164 (predict sets last_update=to); PmbmTracker.cpp:964 (only detected Bernoullis get scan[l].time); tests/pmbm/test_pmbm_sensor_activity.cpp:35-41 documents the false-append; no test exercises 3+ scans of the channel-fallback gate after a false touch (SourceAwareIdentityProtectsAbsentVessels stops at scan 2, before the scan-2 false touch can affect a gate decision).
  - suggested_fix: Record touches from the dominant hypothesis using b.last_claimed_meas_index >= 0 (the true per-assignment claim recorded in enumerateChildren) instead of the nearest-measurement-at-timestamp reconstruction, mirroring MhtTracker which records touches only from committed hits (MhtTracker.cpp:615-651).
  - verifier: Independently traced the full failing path. (1) PmbmTracker::processBatch (PmbmTracker.cpp:1367-1372) calls predict(t_max) BEFORE enumerateChildren; predict (lines 222-228) round-trips every Bernoulli through toTrack/estimator_.predict/fromTrack, and every estimator sets track.last_update = to when dt > 0 (EkfEstimator.cpp:23-30, ImmEstimator.cpp:164, UkfEstimator.cpp:55, ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:73), which fromTrack copies back (PmbmTypes.hpp:459). So after predict, EVERY Bernoulli — detected or not — carries last_update == t_max. The misdetection branch copies the post-predict parent verbatim (PmbmTracker.cpp:1026 `Bernoulli miss = b;`), so the walk's comment at 1659-1662 ("misdetected ones inherit the parent pre-predict timestamp") is factually false. The codebase itself contradicts that comment twice: PmbmTypes.hpp:433-434 ("last_update ... is the filter time, advanced by predict and update alike") and PmbmTracker.cpp:591-593 (idle_decay_for's comment: "last_update can't be used directly because the estimator's predict advances it to the current filter time even when no measurement was applied"). (2) In any uniform-timestamp scan (the harness groups strictly-equal times, HarnessBatchedPmbm.cpp:23-27; a single-measurement AIS batch is the degenerate case), the filter at line 1666 passes for every measurement, and the misdetected Bernoulli is attributed the NEAREST measurement with no distance bound (1663-1675, best_d starts at infinity) — every lone AIS message falsely touches every coasting radar track. (3) The claimed MHT parity is false: MhtTracker records touches only from the committed hit leaf (MhtTracker.cpp:610-651, gated on n.is_hit), never for misses; the true-assignment field Bernoulli::last_claimed_meas_index (-1 on miss) exists but is consumed only by the clutter feed. (4) Consequences verified: (a) refreshAggregatedTracks copies the polluted history into emitted tracks (PmbmTracker.cpp:2318-2321) and Sweep.cpp:501-520 feeds those recent_contributions to SensorBiasEstimator; extractPositionPairs (SensorBiasPairExtractor.cpp:44-75) anchors on ANY AIS touch in the 2 s window, so a foreign vessel's AIS position gets paired with the track's radar touch — a bias observation whose error equals the inter-vessel separation; the Mahalanobis outlier gate (SensorBiasEstimator.cpp:104-109) is weakest at cold start when prior variance is large. (b) With source_aware_misdetection=true, the false touch adds the foreign source_id to history and the channel fallback (PmbmTracker.cpp:584) returns "covered", charging misses from a sensor that never observed the track — the flag's documented purpose (PmbmTracker.hpp:296-305) is defeated; identity suppression (573-582) only protects identity-bearing touches, radar touches carry none. (c) idle-decay muting is real but weaker than claimed (per-scan decays still compound to exp(-ln2*elapsed/halflife)); the substantive effect is that should_misdetect flips to covered so the skip+idle-decay branch stops being taken. (5) Tests do not contradict: tests/pmbm/test_pmbm_sensor_activity.cpp:35-49 explicitly documents that a SourceTouch is appended even for miss-detected Bernoullis (the identity-gate 'continue' was designed around it), and the channel-mode tests (IdleDecayHalvesExistenceAfterHalflife, SourceAwareIdentityLegacyFlagDecaysAbsentVessel) stop at scan 2 — the false touch lands after the asserted scan, so no test exercises a gate decision made after a false touch. Refutation attempts failed: no distance gate exists; the walk is unconditional whenever mbm and scan are non-empty (default config included); the only case where the exact-time filter works is a repeated-timestamp scan where PmbmTracker::predict early-returns on dt<=0 (line 210), not the normal advancing-time case. Severity stays high: default configs emit polluted recent_contributions (provenance + covariance_is_default flag in TrackOutput.cpp:75-80), the supported PMBM bias-estimation wiring silently corrupts registration bias which then rewrites all incoming measurements via applyBiasCorrection (PmbmTracker.cpp:1354), and the source-aware channel gate is functionally negated.
  - verifier corrected details: Confirmed as claimed, with three refinements: (1) the failure is broader than "uniform-timestamp radar scans" — a single-measurement batch (e.g. each real AIS message processed alone) falsely touches EVERY misdetected Bernoulli in the dominant hypothesis with that one measurement, since predict(t_max) stamps all Bernoullis with the message time and there is no distance bound; (2) consequence (c) (idle-decay muting) is weaker than claimed: with a false touch every scan the per-scan decays still compound to exp(-ln2*elapsed/halflife), so decay is reduced from super-exponential to plain half-life rather than fully muted — the substantive damage there is that should_misdetect flips to "covered" and the skip+idle-decay branch stops being taken at all; (3) the claimed MHT-parity is verifiably false in-source: MhtTracker.cpp:610-651 appends touches only for committed hits (n.is_hit + scan_meas_idx), so the PMBM walk diverges from the path PmbmTracker.hpp:936-943 claims to match. Fix direction the code already contains: Bernoulli::last_claimed_meas_index (PmbmTypes.hpp:215) records the true per-scan assignment (-1 on miss) and is already carried through the dominant hypothesis; the walk should key on it instead of the z.time == last_update reconstruction.

- **[MEDIUM/CONFIRMED]** Mixed-timestamp batches double-propagate the [z.time, t_max] interval: predict-to-max then last_update rewind to the claimed measurement's earlier time
  - `core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:964` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: processBatch predicts every Bernoulli to t_max, the LATEST timestamp in the scan (lines 1367-1373); estimators stamp last_update = t_max. A Bernoulli that then claims a measurement l with scan[l].time < t_max is updated against the state-at-t_max (no per-cell re-predict; estimator_.update at line 795 does not predict internally) and its stamp is REWOUND to scan[l].time (estimators set last_update = z.time; line 964 sets it again). On the next batch, per-track dt = t_next - scan[l].time is applied to a state that was already propagated to t_max, so the interval [scan[l].time, t_max] is pushed through F and Q twice, every scan. The batch-ordering contract explicitly supports heterogeneous-timestamp batches (backlog #15 sort at lines 1315-1333; MhtTracker.cpp:208-212 names the "collect everything since the last tick" consumer as canonical), and tests/pipeline/test_batch_ordering.cpp feeds PMBM batches with 0.3 s internal skew — but only checks order-invariance, so both runs carry the identical bias and the test cannot catch it. All bench harnesses group measurements by identical timestamp (HarnessBatchedPmbm.cpp:22-27), so benches never see it either. The result is a systematic position lead of order v x skew per scan on every track updated by a non-latest measurement (e.g., the AIS-updated tracks in a fused AIS+radar tick), plus over-inflated process noise (Q(dt) with dt too large), degrading exactly the multi-sensor fusion the library exists for.
  - failure_scenario: Fixed-rate consumer hands PMBM one batch per second containing an AIS fix at t=k+0.0 and radar returns at t=k+0.5. predict(k+0.5) moves the AIS track's state to k+0.5; it claims the AIS fix, update stamps last_update=k+0.0. Next batch: predict(k+1.5) applies dt=1.5 s to a state physically at k+0.5, so the track is propagated 2.0 s of motion for 1.5 s of elapsed time — for a 5 m/s vessel a 2.5 m per-scan lead the update must fight, biasing velocity and inflating covariance every single scan.
  - evidence: PmbmTracker.cpp:1367-1373 (predict to t_max), :795 (update without re-predict), :964 (last_update = scan[l].time); EkfEstimator.cpp:24-30,64 and ImmEstimator.cpp:78-79,164,278 (predict dt from last_update, update rewinds stamp); tests/pipeline/test_batch_ordering.cpp:60-70 (mixed sub-times k.0/k.3 are contract-supported input); HarnessBatchedPmbm.cpp:22-27 (benches only ever feed uniform-time batches).
  - suggested_fix: After a detection update, restore det.last_update to the batch predict time t_max (the state's physical time) rather than scan[l].time — or predict each cost-matrix cell's track copy to scan[l].time instead of batch-predicting to t_max.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full path with the code open. (1) PmbmTracker::processBatch (core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:1367-1372) predicts every Bernoulli to t_max, the LATEST time in the batch; EkfEstimator::predict (core/estimation/EkfEstimator.cpp:24-30) computes dt from track.last_update and stamps last_update=to, so after predict every Bernoulli carries last_update=t_max (round-tripped via toTrack/fromTrack, PmbmTypes.hpp:438-463). (2) The per-cell update (PmbmTracker.cpp:783-797) calls estimator_.update directly on the predicted state with no re-predict; EkfEstimator::update (line 64) and ImmEstimator::update (ImmEstimator.cpp:278) contain no internal predict and stamp last_update=z.time, and PmbmTracker.cpp:964 re-stamps det.last_update=scan[l].time — so a Bernoulli claiming a non-latest measurement has its stamp rewound below its state's physical time. Adaptive-birth Bernoullis get the same skew (line 1175, PPP was predicted to t_max via toTrack(c, current_time_)). (3) On the next batch, EkfEstimator::predict applies dt = t_next_max − z.time to a state already propagated to t_max: the [z.time, t_max] overlap is pushed through F again for the prediction-inherited part of the posterior and Q over the overlap is added twice. No guard re-stamps Bernoullis to t_max (grepped all last_update writes: 964/1175 write z.time; 2009/2173/2260 are max-merges). (4) Reachability is contract-supported: backlog #15 comments in both trackers and tests/pipeline/test_batch_ordering.cpp:1-7 name 'collect everything since the last tick' as the canonical consumer; the integration guide's RemoteTrackAdapter example (tracker.processBatch(remote.poll())) produces mixed-time batches. MhtTracker avoids the issue differently — TrackTree::branch stamps hit.time = scan_time uniformly (TrackTree.cpp:158-159, 269), so PMBM's rewind is not 'the MhtTracker convention' its own comment claims. (5) No test contradicts: test_batch_ordering.cpp feeds mixed sub-times (k.0/k.3) but only asserts sorted==reversed — both runs carry the identical bias; bench harnesses group same-timestamp scans (core/scenario/HarnessBatched.cpp:22-31), so benches never see it. Also nothing documents the rewind as an approximation — PmbmTypes.hpp:433-434 says last_update is 'the filter time, advanced by predict and update alike', which the rewind violates. One quantitative correction: the claim overstates the magnitude. The KF update pulls the position component toward the measurement-at-z.time with gain K_p, so re-propagating from z.time is EXACT in the K_p→1 limit; the systematic per-scan lead is ≈(1−K_p)·v·skew, not the full v·skew — the '2.5 m per-scan lead' in the failure scenario is the K→0 worst case. The defect (kinematically inconsistent stamp → overlapping F/Q propagation, biased innovations, double-counted Q over the skew window, on the documented canonical consumer path, invisible to all tests and benches) stands.
  - verifier corrected details: Mixed-timestamp batches produce a kinematically inconsistent Bernoulli stamp in PMBM: processBatch predicts all Bernoullis to t_max (PmbmTracker.cpp:1367-1372, estimators stamp last_update=t_max), the per-cell update against an earlier measurement neither re-predicts nor keeps the stamp (estimator update stamps z.time; PmbmTracker.cpp:964 re-stamps scan[l].time), so the next scan's predict applies dt measured from z.time to a state physically at t_max — re-propagating the [z.time, t_max] overlap and double-adding its process noise. Magnitude correction vs the claim: because the update pulls position toward the measurement with gain K_p, the systematic per-scan position lead is ≈(1−K_p)·v·skew (exact/zero when K_p→1), not the full v·skew; for typical AIS-vs-converged-track gains and sub-second intra-tick skews this is decimeters-to-low-meters per scan, partially fought by each update, showing up as biased innovations, a low-biased velocity estimate, and inflated covariance rather than track loss. It grows toward the claimed magnitude for weak/inflated-R measurements (e.g. RemoteTrackAdapter's x3 R-inflation) and for large intra-batch skews (slow pollers, multi-second ticks). Severity medium rather than high: systematic and silent on the documented canonical consumer path (collect-since-last-tick batches; integration-guide processBatch(remote.poll()) example) and invisible to test_batch_ordering (order-invariance only, both orders share the bias) and to benches (HarnessBatched groups same-timestamp scans), but bounded per scan, self-limiting, and zero for the uniform-timestamp batches all current in-repo harnesses feed. Fix direction: either re-predict per-cell to scan[l].time before update (correct OOSM-lite), or keep the Bernoulli stamp at t_max after a claim (MHT's uniform-node-time convention, TrackTree.cpp:269) and document the scan-instant approximation.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Murty cost matrix omits p_D and the (1 - r*p_D) miss ratio, so K-best enumeration order deviates from true posterior order; wrong argmax under K=1 / adaptive-K
  - `core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:821` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: The assignment cost for a detection cell is -(log r + log-lik) (line 821), while the actual child log-weight contribution is log r + log p_D + log-lik for a detection (lines 1015-1017) and log(1 - r*p_D_eff) for a miss (line 1104) — a row left unassigned costs Murty 0. The standard PMBM ranked-assignment cost is -log(r*p_D*l / (1 - r*p_D)) precisely so that assignment-cost order equals posterior-weight order; omitting log(p_D/(1 - r*p_D)) biases Murty against detecting high-r Bernoullis by up to ~2.3 nats (r~1, p_D=0.9). Final child weights ARE computed correctly afterwards, so with K>=2 the mis-ranked children usually all get enumerated and the correct one wins the normalization — but with K=1 (a documented deployment shape: the smart-birth knob is described as "the standard workaround for K=1 deployments") and for every low-weight parent under adaptive_k_best (K_p clamps to 1, lines 1534-1543), the single enumerated child IS the posterior, so the tracker commits to miss+birth/miss+clutter when detection has strictly higher true weight. The design doc (pmbm-design.md section 3.4) documents the same cost but then claims w' ∝ w*exp(-cost), which the code correctly does NOT do — doc and code disagree about which quantity Murty ranks.
  - failure_scenario: K=1, tracked vessel with r=0.999, p_D=0.9, AIS sigma=25 m, lambda_C=1e-4, adaptive birth r*=0.2 (lambda_birth=0.25e-4): a measurement ~1 sigma from the prediction has log-lik ~ -9.3, detection cell cost ~ 9.3; the birth row cost -log(1.25e-4) = 8.99 is cheaper, so Murty's best assignment misdetects the track (r drops to ~0.53 via the miss recursion) and births a duplicate at r=0.2 on the track's own return — even though the detection child's true log-weight (-9.4) beats miss+birth (-11.3) by ~1.9 nats. An ordinary 1-sigma innovation causes an unforced existence sag plus id-flap candidate every time it occurs.
  - evidence: PmbmTracker.cpp:821 (cost = -(log r + ll)), :1015-1017 (true detection weight adds log(pD_l[l])), :1084/:1104 (miss weight log(1-r*pD) never enters C), :1534-1543 (adaptive K floors at 1); docs/algorithms/pmbm-design.md section 3.4 documents cost = -log(l*r) and w' ∝ exp(-cost), contradicting the implemented weight.
  - suggested_fix: Use the ratio cost C(i,l) = -log(r_i * pD_l * l_il / (1 - r_i * pD_miss_i)) so minimizing assignment cost maximizes true child weight; keep the exact log_weight computation as-is.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** clutter_intensity == 0 for a sensor makes an unclaimed measurement's column infeasible, wiping the ENTIRE MBM (all tracks silently lost in one scan)
  - `core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:830` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: The new-target diagonal cell is only written when rho_total > 0 (lines 828-832); rho_total = rho_target + lambda_z. With lambda_z = 0 (nothing validates DetectionParams::clutter_intensity or Config::clutter_intensity > 0; FixedSensorDetectionModel stores raw values) and rho_target = 0 (bearing-only measurement, adaptive birth with birth_existence_target deriving lambda_birth = (r*/(1-r*))*0 = 0, land/obstacle hard-drop, or empty PPP in the legacy path), the measurement's column has no finite cell unless some Bernoulli gates it. hungarianAssignment maps +inf to BIG_M and always returns an assignment (Hungarian.cpp:13-40); murtyKBest rejects the seed as infeasible and returns EMPTY (Murty.cpp:68-69). enumerateChildren then pushes zero children for that parent; when no Bernoulli in ANY parent gates the measurement, every parent produces zero children and density_.mbm = std::move(children) (line 1616) leaves the mixture EMPTY: every track vanishes from tracks() in one scan (onTrackDeleted fires for all), violating the presence-over-suppression principle silently. Even the partial case (one parent infeasible, others not) silently annihilates that parent's probability mass instead of renormalizing it.
  - failure_scenario: A consumer configures AIS with clutter_intensity = 0 ("AIS has no false alarms") in a FixedSensorDetectionModel, adaptive_birth + birth_existence_target = 0.2. A new vessel's first AIS broadcast arrives; no existing Bernoulli gates it (it is new). lambda_birth = 0.25*0 = 0, rho_total = 0, column all-infinite; Murty returns no assignments for every parent; the whole MBM — including ten healthy radar tracks nowhere near the new vessel — is erased in this single scan. No exception, no log; downstream sees a full track-drop.
  - evidence: PmbmTracker.cpp:828-832 (cell unset when rho<=0), :507 (lambda_birth proportional to lambda_z), :842-856 (feasible-check skip), :1616 (mbm replaced by possibly-empty children); Murty.cpp:68-69 (empty result on infeasible seed); Hungarian.cpp:13-40 (BIG_M fallback ensures the seed contains a forbidden cell); no validation of clutter_intensity anywhere in PmbmTracker ctor or SensorDetectionModels.hpp.
  - suggested_fix: Validate/clamp clutter_intensity > 0 at the tracker boundary (ctor fail-loud like the R9 check, or floor lambda_z at a tiny epsilon in the birth builders), and/or fall back to keeping the parent unchanged when murtyKBest returns no feasible assignment instead of dropping it.

- **[LOW/unverified]** predict() with a stale timestamp moves the filter clock BACKWARD, causing double survival decay and rewound-clock side effects
  - `core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:211` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: predict(to) with dt <= 0 executes current_time_ = to and returns (lines 210-213). The docstring says stale calls "advance the clock only"; for to < current_time_ this REWINDS it. Bernoulli/PPP states keep last_update at the old (later) time, so on the next in-order batch the estimator's own dt guard prevents double state propagation — but the tracker-level per-predict-call decays are re-applied: b.existence_probability *= survival_probability (line 224) and c.weight *= survival_probability (line 216) fire again for the re-covered wall-clock interval, so an out-of-order batch pair charges survival twice for the same physical time. While rewound, current_time_ also skews appendTrajectoryPoint times for misses (non-monotonic trajectory timestamps feed rtsSmoothTrajectory with negative dt), cooperative stale-timeout arithmetic, and diagnostic time_s. MhtTracker's convention is a high-water mark that never rewinds (MhtTracker.cpp:227-236), so the claimed parity does not hold.
  - failure_scenario: current_time_ = 100 s after batch A. A delayed sensor delivers a batch whose t_max = 95 s: predict(95) rewinds the clock; the batch's measurements update states that are physically at t=100. Next batch at t_max = 100: predict(100) has dt = 5 > 0, so every Bernoulli's existence and every PPP weight is multiplied by p_S a second time for the already-elapsed [95,100] interval; a track near the r_min or output floor can be pushed under it by the double decay.
  - evidence: PmbmTracker.cpp:209-213 (rewind), :216/:224 (per-call survival decay), estimator dt guards (EkfEstimator.cpp:25) prevent only the state part; MhtTracker.cpp:227-236 (never-rewinding high-water convention the docstring claims to match).
  - suggested_fix: On dt <= 0, return without touching current_time_ (advance-only), matching the docstring and the MhtTracker high-water convention.

- **[LOW/unverified]** alt-birth gate identifies this-scan births by float equality with scan.front().time, missing births from later-timestamped measurements in a mixed-time batch
  - `core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:1608` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: The Phase 9 S3 alt-birth gate strips new-born Bernoullis from weak alt K-children by matching b.birth_time.seconds() == scan.front().time.seconds() (lines 1599-1610). But births set nb.birth_time = scan[l].time (line 1182), the BIRTHING measurement's own timestamp. In a heterogeneous-timestamp batch (the canonical fused AIS+radar tick; batches are stable-sorted, so front is the earliest), every birth from a measurement later than the front escapes the gate — exactly the phantom-birth mass the knob exists to suppress leaks back into the output aggregation. Conversely, if two consecutive batches carry identical timestamps, a Bernoulli born in the PREVIOUS batch has birth_time equal to this scan's front time and is wrongly stripped from weak alt children (a detection/misdetection contribution the gate documents it must keep). Only active when alt_birth_log_gap_threshold > 0 (opt-in bench configs) with K >= 2.
  - failure_scenario: Config with alt_birth_log_gap_threshold = 0.5, K = 3; batch contains an AIS fix at t = 10.0 (front) and radar returns at t = 10.4. A weak alt child (log-gap 0.8 below top) births a phantom Bernoulli from a radar return: birth_time = 10.4 != scan_t = 10.0, so the phantom survives the gate, accumulates Sigma w*r across scans, and emits as a spurious confirmed track — the sc13_anchored regression mechanism the knob was shipped to close.
  - evidence: PmbmTracker.cpp:1600 (scan_t = scan.front().time), :1607-1608 (equality predicate), :1182 (nb.birth_time = scan[l].time); backlog #15 sort at :1315-1333 establishes mixed-time batches as supported input.
  - suggested_fix: Mark new-borns explicitly (e.g., a transient born_this_scan flag on Bernoulli, or compare birth_time >= scan.front().time && id >= first id minted this scan) instead of float equality with the front timestamp.

- **[LOW/unverified]** Empty-scan processBatch never rebuilds the Phase 9 per-track view, leaving density().tracks/tracked_mbm stale under use_per_track_hypotheses
  - `core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:1409` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: With cfg_.use_per_track_hypotheses = true, rebuildPerTrackViewFromFlat is called only on the non-empty-scan path (line 1642-1644). The empty-scan branch (lines 1375-1428) applies misdetections, merges, and pruneAndNormalise — Bernoullis can decay below r_min and be erased, hypothesis weights change — then returns without rebuilding, so the public density().tracks / tracked_mbm views still describe the PREVIOUS scan: erased Bernoullis are still present, weights and hyp_index no longer agree with the flat mbm. This violates the documented invariant that "the two views must agree when both are populated" (PmbmTypes.hpp:358-360). No in-tree consumer reads the view yet (S1 ships the builder only), so the impact today is limited to external consumers of the public density() accessor and the invariant tests never covering the empty-scan transition.
  - failure_scenario: use_per_track_hypotheses = true; a Bernoulli at r = 0.01 receives an empty-scan miss (config P_D 0.9) dropping r below r_min = 1e-3; pruneAndNormalise erases it from mbm. A consumer inspecting density().tracks afterwards still finds the track with its pre-miss hypothesis list and a tracked_mbm whose weights/hyp_index correspond to the pre-scan mixture — a flat-vs-tracked disagreement the type documentation forbids.
  - evidence: PmbmTracker.cpp:1375-1428 (empty-scan path: prune + lifecycle, no rebuild), :1642-1644 (flag-gated rebuild only after the non-empty path); PmbmTypes.hpp:358-360 (agreement invariant); grep shows no non-test consumer of tracks/tracked_mbm.
  - suggested_fix: Call rebuildPerTrackViewFromFlat(density_) after pruneAndNormalise in the empty-scan branch as well (mirroring line 1642).

Coverage notes (pmbm): Read 100% of scope: PmbmTracker.cpp (2464 lines), PmbmTracker.hpp (1098), PmbmTypes.hpp (486), PmbmDiagnostics.hpp (115); cross-checked against docs/algorithms/pmbm-design.md (sections 3.1-3.6), EkfEstimator/ImmEstimator/UkfEstimator predict+update, Murty.cpp, Hungarian.cpp, MhtTracker.cpp (touch recording + stale convention), SensorDetectionModels.hpp, ISensorActivity + DeclaredSensorActivity, HarnessBatchedPmbm, and tests/pmbm/* + tests/pipeline/test_batch_ordering.cpp. CLEAN: log-domain hypothesis normalization (logSumExp with -inf and degenerate all--inf handling); miss recursion r(1-pD)/(1-r*pD) matches doc 3.1; detection existence set to 1; birth existence rho_target/rho_total and adaptive-birth lambda_birth/(lambda_birth+lambda_C) formulas; birth-id caching (per-parent and cross-parent) mints monotonic never-reused ids; pruning/capping has NO dangling-index hazard in the legacy flat path (Bernoullis stored by value; the Phase 9 index view is rebuilt from flat post-prune — except the empty-scan gap reported); mergeBernoulliDuplicates (older-id survivor, max-existence fold, 4-D velocity-aware Bhattacharyya with LDLT PSD guards, claim/identity carry logic all self-consistent); output aggregation Sigma w*r + moment-matched covariance matches doc 3.6 and mass cannot exceed 1 (id unique per hypothesis, verified by construction); output cross-id merge recomputes stats after folds; staged activity/cooperative maps make miss windows parent-order-independent; RTS smoother algebra (LDLT solve-transpose identity valid for symmetric P_filt, resymmetrization, CV-F) correct; trajectory window trim correct; innovation-gate and diagnostics byte-identical-when-off claims hold (guards verified at every site); applyInnovationGate raise-only variance floor + IMM-mode treatment correct; Eigen usage clean (no aliasing hazards; default-constructed updated[i][l] only reachable when C(i,l) finite; empty-mean r_new=0 birth candidates are transient and pruned same scan before any head<2> reader). KNOWN/BY-DESIGN skipped per instructions (lambda_C cancellation, no-birth zone, #25/#11, extraction boundary, Sweep datum, RTS anchored regression). Overflow one-liners not promoted to findings: (1) multi-sensor same-scan asymmetry — detect branch charges only the claimed sensor's p_D and never (1-p_D) for other covering channels while the miss branch aggregates channels (documented Phase-1 single-scan caveat in Config and doc 3.1.1); (2) PPP mass decay uses the Config-scalar P_D even with a detection model wired (documented \"Uniform p_D for Phase 1\"); (3) survival decay is per-predict-call, not dt-scaled (known modeling choice); (4) empty-scan branch leaves stale last_claimed_meas_index/innovation on the carried Bernoullis — diagnostics on empty scans can report a claimed index with n_measurements=0 (feed is skipped on empty scans so no tracking effect); (5) ISensorActivity::evaluate is always passed nullopt mmsi/platform_id though Bernoullis carry identity (sole implementation ignores the params today — latent wiring gap if a per-vessel provider ships); (6) empty scan with a detection model wired charges NO miss (any_coverage=false) while no-model configs charge full config-P_D miss — asymmetric but each defensible; (7) pruned Bernoullis are never recycled into the PPP (standard-PMBM optional step, missing-feature not bug); (8) hypothesis cap uses non-stable partial_sort — deterministic per platform, tie order unspecified across standard libraries (determinism contract is per-log replay, so acceptable). The false-touch finding is partially acknowledged in a test comment (test_pmbm_sensor_activity.cpp:35-49) — reported anyway because the tracker-source comment asserts the opposite, the behavior corrupts consumer-visible recent_contributions in default configs, and the channel-fallback gate defeat is unmitigated; synthesis should weigh intent vs. defect there.

### unit: pipeline (6 findings)

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** Tracker::process() silently mishandles soft (JPDA) association results: no track is ever updated and every measurement births a duplicate track
  - `core/pipeline/Tracker.cpp:144` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: process() reads only AssociationResult::matches. JpdaAssociator (core/association/JpdaAssociator.cpp) never populates matches — it fills only betas/beta_0 (verified: every 'out.' write is betas/beta_0/p_d/gate_threshold/overflow_fallback; even its overflow fallback encodes hard picks as 0/1 betas). So with a JPDA associator wired into Tracker and measurements fed via the canonical single-measurement entry point process(), result.matches is always empty: the soft result is discarded, the else-branch at line 175 initiates a brand-new track for every position-capable measurement, and existing tracks never receive updates (they coast until the miss-timeout deletes them). processBatch() handles the soft path (line 223-275); process() has no equivalent and no guard/assert. The mismatch is acknowledged only in an internal bench comment (core/benchmark/BenchRunner.cpp:36-38), not on the public API: Tracker.hpp's process() doc, CLAUDE.md ('Tracker::process(Measurement) — the entry points'), and the integration guide all present process() as the general entry, and the bench docs name 'JpdaStyle: Tracker + TrackManager (GNN/JPDA/JIPDA)' as a supported pairing.
  - failure_scenario: Consumer wires Tracker(estimator, JpdaAssociator(20.0, 0.9, 1e-4), mgr, 10.0) and calls tracker.process(m) per AIS message (the app/example.cpp pattern). First fix of vessel A at t=0: betas is 0-sized (T=0), matches empty → track 1 initiated. Second fix at t=10s, 50 m away: JPDA gates it to track 1 and returns betas(0,0)≈0.97, but matches is empty → track 1 is NOT updated and track 2 is initiated at the new position. Every subsequent fix repeats this: N fixes yield N tracks, each frozen at its seed state, old ones deleted by the miss timeout. Output is unbounded track churn with zero fusion, no error or diagnostic.
  - evidence: Tracker.cpp:144 `if (!result.matches.empty())` is the only consumer of the association result besides the initiate else-branch at 175; JpdaAssociator.cpp writes only betas/beta_0 (lines 85-86, 166-183, 217-237); BenchRunner.cpp:33-38 states 'Tracker::process only consults AssociationResult::matches (hard path), and JpdaAssociator only populates betas/beta_0'. No test covers process()+JPDA (tests/pipeline/test_jpda_contributing_sources.cpp uses processBatch only; test_tracker.cpp uses GNN).
  - suggested_fix: In process(), when result.betas/beta_0 are non-empty, run the same soft-update path processBatch uses (M=1 degenerates to a trivial beta vs beta_0 split), or reject soft associators explicitly (assert/documented error) so the misuse cannot be silent.
  - verifier: Independently traced the failing path. (1) Tracker.cpp:140-179: process() wraps the measurement in a 1-element batch, calls associate(), and consumes ONLY result.matches (line 144); the else-branch (line 175) initiates a new track for any position-capable, PSD-covariance measurement. betas/beta_0 are never read in process() — grep confirms 'betas' appears only in processBatch (lines 223-250). (2) JpdaAssociator.cpp never writes out.matches: every write to the result is betas/beta_0/p_d/gate_threshold/overflow_fallback (lines 38, 76-86, 166-183, 217-237); even the overflow fallback encodes hard picks as 0/1 betas (lines 178-179). AssociationResult.matches default-constructs empty (ports/IDataAssociator.hpp:22). (3) Concrete trace: Tracker(est, JpdaAssociator(20,0.9,1e-4), mgr, 10.0); process(fix A, t=0): T=0, betas is Mx0, matches empty → initiate track 1 (correct). process(fix A', t=10, 50 m away): JPDA gates to track 1, fills betas(0,0)≈1, matches stays empty → the update branch is skipped, track 1 receives no update/recordHit/noteObservation, and the else-branch initiates track 2. Repeats every fix: N fixes → N tracks each frozen at its seed state; earlier tracks age past miss_timeout (line 184-192) and are deleted. Zero fusion, no error, no diagnostic. (4) No guard exists: process() has no assert on betas.size(), and Tracker.hpp documents process() with no JPDA caveat ('Process a single measurement through the predict-associate-update/initiate cycle') while only processBatch's doc mentions soft dispatch. CLAUDE.md and the integration guide name process() as the entry point; the guide never warns that JPDA requires processBatch (its only processBatch mention is line 353, unrelated). (5) No test contradicts: tests/pipeline/test_jpda_contributing_sources.cpp uses processBatch exclusively; tests/pipeline/test_tracker_bearing_innovation_emit.cpp's JPDA test (line 105-126) calls process() only for the seed against an EMPTY track set (where initiation is correct regardless) and uses processBatch (line 120) for the actual soft update — so it pins nothing about process()+JPDA updates. (6) Strong corroboration that this is a real trap, not a misreading: docs/baselines/README.md lines 274-277 record that BenchRunner itself was once 'using Tracker::process() (hard-match only) instead of processBatch()' with JPDA configs and produced wrong baselines until fixed in commit 7dbe9ae — the fix was applied at the call site (BenchRunner.cpp:33-38 comment), leaving the public-API landmine intact and undocumented on the API surface.
  - verifier corrected details: Confirmed as claimed. Tracker::process() (core/pipeline/Tracker.cpp:144) reads only AssociationResult::matches, which soft associators (JpdaAssociator, and per its header any JIPDA successor) never populate — they fill only betas/beta_0. Wiring a soft associator into Tracker and feeding via process() therefore silently discards every association: existing tracks never update (they coast until the miss-timeout deletes them) and every position-capable measurement births a duplicate track — total, silent fusion failure. The hazard is real, not theoretical: the project's own bench hit exactly this during baseline construction (docs/baselines/README.md item 3, fixed in BenchRunner by switching to processBatch in 7dbe9ae) but the API itself was never guarded. Nuance on severity: no shipped example or guide recipe pairs JPDA with process() (default recipe is GNN; all in-repo JPDA callers use processBatch), so a consumer following documented examples avoids it — but JpdaAssociator is a public, advertised strategy ('pluggable hot path' is an architecture invariant), process() is the documented canonical entry point (Tracker.hpp, CLAUDE.md, integration guide), and the failure gives no diagnostic. High severity for a pre-release library API. Trivial remediations: have process() delegate to processBatch({z}) (processBatch degenerates identically for hard associators per BenchRunner.cpp:38-40), or assert/document that process() is hard-associator-only.

- **[MEDIUM/CONFIRMED]** MHT deferred-commitment leaf protection is inert: flags are always one branch() behind, so all four pruning consumers either never see a protected leaf or keep only a childless zombie chain
  - `core/pipeline/MhtTracker.cpp:531` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: is_protected is set post-solve (MhtTracker.cpp:530-544) on the CURRENT scan's top-K leaves and their ancestor chains. On the next processBatch the very first per-tree step is TrackTree::branch() (line 283), which iterates every current leaf, spawns children (fresh TrackTreeNode structs with is_protected=false) and sets each old leaf's is_leaf=false. Consequently, at the moment any pruning consumer runs, no LEAF is ever protected: (a) pruneKLocal's protected-skip (TrackTree.cpp:451) can never fire — the deferred alternative's children are demoted purely by score; (b) mergeBranches' protected-skip (TrackTree.cpp:484-485) can never fire; (c) the score/existence delete sweep's 'any leaf protected → one more scan' clause (MhtTracker.cpp:413-419) can never fire — a protected tree below threshold is deleted immediately, contradicting the adjacent comment; (d) pruneNScan (TrackTree.cpp:418-419) does keep protected NODES, but when the alternative diverged at/before target_depth (the only case N-scan would prune it, i.e., the exact deferred-commitment case) it keeps only the childless internal chain: the alternative's fresh children are unprotected and outside the winner subtree, so they are removed and the branch is left leafless — functionally dead, cleaned up on the following scan. Net effect: with default k_best=3, the Murty K-best 'protected alternatives carry-over' documented in Config::k_best, score_delta_threshold, TrackTreeNode::is_protected, and commit 6fd1f7b ('turn Murty K>1 from inert to behavioural') changes nothing about which hypotheses survive; the only live piece of the K>1 machinery is the adaptive n_scan extension (protectedAlternativesLastScan>1 → n_eff=n_scan+2). The TrackTree unit tests (tests/tracking/test_track_tree.cpp:223-320) pass because they hand-set flags on current leaves — a state the pipeline ordering can never produce.
  - failure_scenario: Two vessels cross; scans 1-6 are ambiguous. At scan 6 the solve protects the rank-2 identity hypothesis leaf B6 (within score_delta 5.0) and its chain. Scan 7: branch() makes B6 internal; its children B7_hit/B7_miss are unprotected. If B's divergence from the K=1 chain is older than n_eff (5 scans with the extension), pruneNScan's winner is on the A chain: B7_hit/B7_miss are deleted (not protected, not in winner subtree) while the zombie B-chain is retained leafless; the correct-identity alternative can never overtake, forcing the premature commit / id-swap the K-best mechanism exists to prevent. Similarly, a tree whose best score dipped below score_delete_threshold with a protected alternative is deleted the same scan, despite the code comment granting it one more scan.
  - evidence: Ordering: MhtTracker.cpp:282-298 (branch→pruneKLocal→mergeBranches→pruneNScan per tree) then 391-421 (delete sweep) all run before the solve at 515 sets fresh flags at 530-544; TrackTree::branch (TrackTree.cpp:145-306) demotes every current leaf and creates children with default is_protected=false. Commit 6fd1f7b's own benchmark reported cooperative scenarios 'bit-identical' — consistent with the flag pathway having no effect.
  - suggested_fix: Make protection heritable for one scan: in branch(), children of a protected leaf inherit is_protected (cleared post-solve as today), or have pruneKLocal/mergeBranches/the delete sweep walk the parent chain when testing protection; in pruneNScan keep the subtree rooted at protected nodes, not just the nodes themselves.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full flag lifecycle. Flags are set only at MhtTracker.cpp:530-544 (post-solve, on the current scan's top-K leaves and ancestors). On the next processBatch, TrackTree::branch (called first, MhtTracker.cpp:283) demotes every current leaf (TrackTree.cpp:305: nodes_[leaf_idx].is_leaf=false) and creates children with is_protected{false} (TrackTree.hpp:82 default); the miss child is unconditional, so every previously-protected leaf becomes internal. Therefore: (a) pruneKLocal's protected-skip (TrackTree.cpp:451) tests only current leaves — unreachable; (b) mergeBranches' skip (TrackTree.cpp:484-485) — unreachable; (c) the delete sweep's `n.is_leaf && n.is_protected` clause (MhtTracker.cpp:416) — unreachable (newborn roots also default false), so the 'one more scan' comment at 385-390 describes dead code; (d) pruneNScan (TrackTree.cpp:418-419) does keep protected internal nodes, but keep-set = winner chain + winner descendants + protected nodes, so when the alternative diverged at/before target_depth its fresh unprotected children are removed and only a leafless chain survives — behaviorally inert (all consumers operate from leaves: branch, bestLeafIndex, solveGlobalHypothesis, delete sweep, readout, countHitsInWindow), and the zombie is unprotected after the next post-solve clear and removed the following scan. Grep confirms no other writer/reader of is_protected and MhtTracker::processBatch is the only pipeline caller of the prune passes; stale/empty-scan early-returns skip pruning, so no consumer ever runs in the between-batches window where protected leaves exist. Tests don't contradict: test_track_tree.cpp:223-315 hand-set flags on current leaves (a state consumers never observe in the pipeline); MHT-level tests are single-target smoke tests, and the comment in ScoreDeltaTightThresholdDoesNotExplodeTreesOnCleanRun even asserts an unreachable mechanism. The only live piece of the K>1 machinery is protectedAlternativesLastScan → n_eff = n_scan + n_scan_extension_when_protected (MhtTracker.cpp:293-297, 542-543), exactly as the claim concedes. Commit 6fd1f7b's ordering fix moved the clear post-solve but did not account for branch() demoting the flagged leaves before any consumer inspects them; its 'bit-identical cooperative' benchmark note is consistent. Not covered by the known/by-design list (backlog #11 is duplicate-track churn, a different mechanism). Severity reduced to medium: the tree structure still defers commitment within the n_scan window without protection, the live n_eff extension delivers part of the intended benefit, and MHT is the secondary pipeline vs PMBM — so this is an inert advertised default-on mechanism with misleading comments/tests and a bounded behavioral gap (forced commit once ambiguity outlives n_eff; within-Δ alternatives demotable by k_max_leaves=5 score ranking), not corrupted output.
  - verifier corrected details: is_protected is consumed by four sites but the pipeline ordering makes leaf-level protection unobservable: flags are set post-solve on scan-N leaves (MhtTracker.cpp:530-544), and the next processBatch's first per-tree step branch() (MhtTracker.cpp:283; TrackTree.cpp:145-307) demotes every flagged leaf and spawns unprotected children before pruneKLocal/mergeBranches/pruneNScan/delete-sweep run. Consequences verified: pruneKLocal skip (TrackTree.cpp:451), mergeBranches skip (TrackTree.cpp:484-485), and the delete-sweep protected clause (MhtTracker.cpp:413-419) are dead code in pipeline-produced states; pruneNScan's protected-node keep (TrackTree.cpp:418-419) preserves only a leafless zombie chain (children outside the winner subtree are unprotected and removed), cleaned up the following scan — behaviorally equivalent to no protection. The only behavioral effect of k_best>1/score_delta_threshold is the adaptive N-scan extension via protectedAlternativesLastScan (n_eff = n_scan + n_scan_extension_when_protected). Unit tests (tests/tracking/test_track_tree.cpp:223-315) hand-set flags on current leaves — a state no pruning consumer ever observes; MHT-level tests are smoke-only. Severity medium (not high): deferred commitment still partially happens through ordinary tree retention within the n_scan window plus the live n_eff extension, and MHT is the secondary tracker; the real gap is (1) within-Δ alternatives demotable purely by score at k_max_leaves, (2) no survival past the trunk merge once divergence outlives n_eff (default 5 scans), (3) below-threshold trees with protected alternatives deleted immediately contrary to the adjacent comment, plus comments/tests/docs asserting behavior that cannot occur.

- **[LOW/unverified]** RangeBearing2D scans feed raw (range, bearing) values into ScanObservation.positions/clutter_positions, which the port documents as ENU coordinates
  - `core/pipeline/MhtTracker.cpp:822` (contract-violation, confidence high)
  - description: In the post-solve detection-model feed, any measurement passing canInitiateTrack (which includes RangeBearing2D, per core/estimation/MeasurementModels.hpp:29) has (value(0), value(1)) pushed into ScanObservation.positions and clutter_positions. For RangeBearing2D those are (range_m, bearing_rad), but ports/ISensorDetectionModel.hpp:297 documents positions as 'ENU; empty for pure bearings', and downstream consumers written against that contract treat them as tracker-frame ENU points: LiveOccupancyModel::observe calls toAnchorEnu(p)/cellOf(toAnchorEnu(pos[i])) on them (core/static/LiveOccupancyModel.cpp:122,165), and CoverageSector::fromReturns computes sensor footprints from them. Of the models shipped for the MHT wiring today, FixedSensorDetectionModel ignores observe(), ClutterMapSensorDetectionModel explicitly skips RangeBearing2D, and AdaptiveSensorDetectionModel's bounding-box 'area' happens to be dimensionally consistent (m·rad matches the documented (m·rad)^-1 λ_C units) — so the shipped MHT configs do not misbehave — but the field content violates the port contract and any ENU-contract consumer attached to an MhtTracker with a RangeBearing2D sensor silently corrupts. PmbmTracker.cpp:1797-1842 contains the identical pattern including the coverage estimation (out of this review's scope; flagged for the PMBM reviewer).
  - failure_scenario: A consumer wires MhtTracker with a decorator detection model that forwards observe() to a LiveOccupancyModel (the pattern the bench uses for PMBM occupancy configs) and a radar adapter emitting RangeBearing2D. A vessel at range 3000 m, bearing 1.5 rad from own-ship is recorded by the occupancy grid at ENU (3000, 1.5) — a phantom occupancy/structure line hugging the east axis near the datum — while its real cell is decayed as observed-empty; birth suppression then fires at the phantom location.
  - suggested_fix: Project RangeBearing2D returns to ENU (sensor_position_enu + r·(cos b, sin b), as SourceTouchPopulate already does) before filling positions/clutter_positions, or split the port field into measurement-space vs ENU vectors and update the doc.

- **[LOW/unverified]** IPDA hit update with clutter_intensity == 0 collapses the likelihood ratio to 0 instead of infinity, zeroing existence on every detection
  - `core/tracking/TrackTree.cpp:85` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: updateHit computes L = (lambda_c > 0.0) ? (p_d_g / lambda_c) : 0.0. λ_C → 0 means 'no clutter', for which the Bayes ratio L = P_D·g/λ_C → +∞ and the hit posterior should be r' → 1. The guard instead returns L = 0, giving r' = 0: a detection becomes maximal evidence AGAINST existence. DetectionParams places no lower bound on clutter_intensity and FixedSensorDetectionModel accepts whatever the consumer sets, so a 'clean sensor' entry with clutter_density = 0 is representable. The branch score simultaneously becomes +inf (score subtracts log(0) at TrackTree.cpp:273), so the r=0 hit leaf dominates leaf selection.
  - failure_scenario: Consumer configures FixedSensorDetectionModel with {P_D=0.9, clutter_intensity=0.0} for a trusted sensor, IPDA lifecycle on (default). A target detected every scan: each hit leaf gets existence_probability 0 (and score +inf, so it is the reported leaf via the bestLeaf fallback after the solve's isfinite check rejects the -inf cost). The track is emitted Tentative forever (r=0 < ipda_confirm_threshold 0.9) and, once the K-local prune discards the surviving miss-chain leaves, max leaf r < ipda_delete_threshold 0.05 deletes the tree — a perfectly-detected target never confirms and is repeatedly deleted/reborn.
  - suggested_fix: Treat lambda_c <= 0 on the hit branch as r_post = 1 (or clamp lambda_c to a small positive floor at DetectionParams ingestion) and floor the -log(lambda_C) score term consistently.

- **[LOW/unverified]** applyBiasCorrection skips PositionVelocity2D, so a published position bias is applied to only part of a source's measurement stream
  - `core/pipeline/BiasCorrection.hpp:60` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: The correction handles Position2D, Bearing2D, and RangeBearing2D only. PositionVelocity2D measurements — emitted by AisAdapter when SOG/COG are present (adapters/ais/AisAdapter.hpp:39-54), by RemoteTrackAdapter's velocity opt-in (adapters/remote_track/RemoteTrackAdapter.cpp:60-69), and by AisCsvReplayAdapter — fall through untouched: no mean shift, no Schmidt R-inflation, even though their first two components are exactly the ENU position the Position2D branch corrects. Because the same physical source switches models per report (e.g., AisAdapter emits Position2D when SOG is absent/below threshold, PositionVelocity2D otherwise), a published PositionBias for that (sensor, source_id) is applied to some of its reports and not others.
  - failure_scenario: A shore VTS feed (RemoteTrackAdapter, velocity opt-in) has a 40 m registration offset that the bias estimator learns and publishes. Reports carrying velocity arrive as PositionVelocity2D and keep the full 40 m offset while any Position2D reports from the same station are corrected — the per-track filter sees a stream whose position bias steps by 40 m depending on which model each report happened to use, producing zig-zag innovations and inflated velocity estimates instead of the intended uniform correction.
  - suggested_fix: Add a PositionVelocity2D branch mirroring Position2D (shift value(0..1) by the bias, add P_b to covariance block<2,2>(0,0)); decide explicitly whether the velocity fold needs a bias term (likely not).

- **[LOW/unverified]** Innovation-sink emission falls back to a non-chosen best leaf, so one measurement's innovation can be emitted for two different tracks in the same scan
  - `core/pipeline/MhtTracker.cpp:555` (contract-violation, confidence medium)
  - description: The setInnovationSink contract (MhtTracker.hpp:259-266) promises one InnovationEvent per surviving tree 'whose chosen leaf is a HIT' under the global hypothesis, which enforces per-measurement exclusivity. The emission loop, however, substitutes bestLeafIndex() whenever the solver left the tree unassigned (line 553-556). That fallback leaf is outside the global hypothesis and may be a hit on a measurement already consumed by another tree's chosen leaf, so the sink receives two InnovationEvents for the same physical return against two track ids. The Track-view readout uses the same fallback deliberately ('never silently drop a track'), but for the innovation channel it double-counts.
  - failure_scenario: Trees A and B each have only hit leaves on the single scan measurement j (their miss leaves were pruned by K-local/merge). Hungarian gives column j to A; B's row has no finite assignment, chosen_leaf[B]=kNoParent. The emission loop falls back to B's best leaf — a hit on j — and emits innovation events for both A and B from measurement j. A bench NIS aggregation over these events counts the return twice with correlated residuals, biasing the consistency statistics the sink exists to compute.
  - suggested_fix: In the innovation loop, drop the bestLeafIndex() fallback (emit only for solver-chosen hit leaves), matching the documented contract; keep the fallback for the track-view readout only.

Coverage notes (pipeline): SCOPE READ END-TO-END: core/pipeline/Tracker.{hpp,cpp}, MhtTracker.{hpp,cpp}, ReorderBuffer.{hpp,cpp}, BiasCorrection.hpp, SourceTouchPopulate.hpp, core/tracking/TrackTree.{hpp,cpp}. Cross-checked against: MeasurementModels.{hpp,cpp} (canInitiateTrack, predictMeasurement, wrapAngle, PSD guard), EkfEstimator/ImmEstimator predict/update/gate, TrackManager, IDataAssociator + JpdaAssociator output fields, ISensorDetectionModel port + Fixed/Adaptive/ClutterMap models + LiveOccupancyModel consumers, Murty/Hungarian infinity handling, Timestamp, integration guide, git history (6fd1f7b, 9383e03, 6841112), and tests in tests/pipeline + tests/tracking.  VERIFIED CLEAN (hand-executed edge cases): ReorderBuffer — push/drain horizon boundaries (== cutoff accepted then released), equal-timestamp ordering is stable (multimap emplace inserts at upper bound of equal range → deterministic replay), late-beyond-horizon drop is counted and documented, forward clock-skew dragging the cutoff is a documented assumption; no flush API is a documented usage constraint. Tracker stale guard: equal timestamps accepted, high-water only advanced on non-stale input, opt-out path relies on estimator predict dt<=0 no-op (verified in EKF/IMM) and is documented. Miss-timeout sweep collects ids before recordMiss, so TrackManager's erase+reindex (verified correct) cannot invalidate iteration; just-added/just-updated tracks age 0. Track index stability between associate() and mutableTracks()[ti] holds (no add/erase in between). Soft path: emission before softUpdate (pre-update state), betas column/track alignment, T=0 JPDA batch correctly falls through to initiation. BranchParams aggregate init order matches struct. TrackTree::branch: leaf snapshot before push_back (no iterator/index invalidation), per-(sensor,model,source) miss-penalty dedup, coverage-conditioned P_D, dt-scaled IPDA/VIMM Markov prediction (dt=0 identity, negative dt clamped), IPDA hit/miss recursions match Musicki/Brekke forms (P_G omission in hit denominator is benign at default P_G=0.99), last_position_anchor propagation, recapture gate math. pruneNScan ancestor walk/compaction/parent remap correct (protected chains are root-connected so no dangling parent); bestLeafIndex first-element seeding correct; mergeBranches score-desc ordering; bhattacharyyaPosition singular-det guard. MhtTracker: delete sweep guarantees every tree has a leaf before the solve; cross-tree duplicate merge ordering claim (spawn order preserved through all compactions → older id survives) verified, streak erase-on-separation and id-based pruning correct; solveGlobalHypothesis cost construction, private miss slots, isfinite guards, Score-Δ early break (costs non-decreasing) correct; shared-bearing bookkeeping bounds-guarded; per-tree maps (attributes/sources/velocity_observed/history) pruned on tree death; onDatumRecentered shifts nodes + published views and clears the transient history. SourceTouchPopulate RangeBearing→ENU projection and Jacobian match the atan2(dy,dx) convention of predictMeasurement. BiasCorrection Position2D/Bearing2D/RangeBearing2D index/units correct. Both trackers guard initiate() behind isMeasurementCovariancePsd; EkfEstimator::initiate's empty-track defensive return is unreachable from these callers. ImmEstimator::gate falls back to single-Gaussian when the birth-gate Track lacks the IMM ensemble (the MhtTracker birth-gate comment's assumption holds).  OVERFLOW CANDIDATES (not reported as findings): (1) Tracker::processBatch does not sort its batch and uses front().time, unlike MhtTracker/PmbmTracker after backlog #15 — its docstring restricts input to a common-timestamp scan, so this is a contract asymmetry/footgun rather than a defect; the backlog-15 test covers only MHT+PMBM. (2) MhtTracker birth gate tests only each tree's BEST leaf while branch() gates against all leaves, so a measurement can extend a tree (via a non-best chosen leaf) and simultaneously birth a duplicate tree — contributor to the KNOWN #11 duplicate-churn trade-off, so not reported separately. (3) recordMiss fires once per processed measurement after the timeout, so deletion latency couples to the aggregate measurement rate (delete_misses consecutive calls ≈ milliseconds at high rate) — loose but arguably intended semantics. (4) pruneContributions assumes time-ordered history; violated only with reject_stale opted out. (5) Coasting trees' contribution_history_ is only pruned on hits, so Track views can carry >2 s-old touches while coasting (consumers filter by time). (6) TOMHT one-measurement-per-scan structure means a same-timestamp multi-sensor scan forces a tree to forgo the second sensor's hit — explicitly documented in the cross-merge rationale. (7) PmbmTracker.cpp:1797-1842 has the same RangeBearing2D positions-as-ENU defect including CoverageSector::fromReturns — out of scope here, flag to the PMBM reviewer. (8) MhtTracker never populates ScanObservation.coverage (valid=false ⇒ universal occupancy decay) — matches the documented default. NOT COVERED: numerical behavior of Hungarian/Murty internals, estimator internals beyond the interfaces exercised by this scope, and DatumShift.cpp (out of scope).


## Batch B3-tracking-geo-bias

### unit: tracking-types (8 findings)

- **[HIGH/unverified]** Datum-shift axis rotation has the wrong sign: velocity, covariance, IMM means and particles are rotated by +gamma where the true ENU-to-ENU transform is -gamma, making the shift worse than not rotating at all
  - `core/geo/AxisRotation.cpp:17` (math-correctness, confidence high)
  - description: datumAxisRotation(old,new) builds R(+gamma) with gamma = delta_lon*sin(mean_lat), and DatumShift.cpp:39/73 applies v_new = R*v_old (also to the 4x4 covariance block, IMM mode means/covariances, and particle velocities). The correct components transform between two tangent-plane bases is M = R_new_ecef2enu * R_old_ecef2enu^T, whose horizontal block is R(-gamma). Verified numerically by replicating Datum::toEnu (exact R*(x-o) form, Datum.cpp:24) in an independent script: for old=(60N,0E), new=(60N,1E), a due-east old-frame velocity (1,0) has true new-frame components (0.99985, -0.01511); the code produces (+0.01511) — sign flipped, total error 2*gamma. Pole sanity check agrees (at lat 90, old-east must map to due SOUTH in a frame 90 deg east; code gives due north). The unit test RotatesVelocityByConvergenceAngle (tests/tracking/test_datum_shift.cpp:47-65) pins the code's own +gamma convention rather than deriving it from reprojection, so it encodes the bug instead of catching it; the scenario test only asserts positions (which go through exact geodetic reprojection and are unaffected). The same flipped R is used by MhtTracker::onDatumRecentered (MhtTracker.cpp:850/857) for every tree node, and by toGeodeticWithCov (core/output/TrackOutput.cpp:17) for the output covariance rotation. A one-line sign fix in datumAxisRotation corrects all call sites consistently.
  - failure_scenario: Vessel transits >30 km with default auto-recenter (DatumRecenterPolicy.enable_auto_recenter=true). At the recenter, every track's velocity is rotated 2*gamma away from truth instead of 0 (about 0.94 deg at 60N, 3 deg at 80N; larger if a consumer raises recenter_threshold_km). Coasting tracks then propagate with a cross-track velocity error (10 m/s * sin(1 deg) ~ 0.17 m/s), and all tracks emit a simultaneous wrong-direction innovation spike right after each recenter; output COG is biased until the filter washes it out. Covariance ellipses and IMM mode means get the same wrong-direction rotation.
  - evidence: AxisRotation.cpp:15-22 (gamma and R(+gamma)); DatumShift.cpp:14-30,39-46 (v <- R*v, cov <- Rbar*cov*Rbar^T); independent numeric check: true new-frame velocity of old-frame (1,0) is (0.9998477, -0.0151142), code yields (0.9998858, +0.0151144); test_datum_shift.cpp:57 asserts atan2(R(1,0),R(0,0)) == +gamma (pins the flipped convention).
  - suggested_fix: Negate gamma in datumAxisRotation (gamma = -delta_lon_rad*sin(mean_lat_rad)) or return R.transpose(); update the two assertions in tests/tracking/test_datum_shift.cpp to the reprojection-derived sign, and add a test that derives velocity by finite-differencing two positions through both datums.

- **[HIGH/unverified]** recordMiss promotes never-confirmed Tentative tracks to Coasting, which makes one-hit clutter tracks eligible for operator-facing collision-risk events that Tentative status is supposed to gate out
  - `core/tracking/TrackManager.cpp:64` (lifecycle-correctness, confidence high)
  - description: recordMiss unconditionally sets tracks_[i].status = TrackStatus::Coasting for any track below the delete threshold, without checking the prior status. The output contract (docs/output-contract.md:25) defines Coasting as 'was Confirmed, now propagated through a detection gap' — a Tentative track that misses must stay Tentative (or die), never become Coasting. CpaEvaluator (core/collision/CpaEvaluator.cpp:26-30) treats Coasting as CPA-eligible while excluding Tentative by default (evaluate_tentative=false, CpaEvaluator.hpp:23). So the status gate is inverted for unconfirmed tracks: excluded while they are receiving hits, included as soon as they miss. No test covers a Tentative track receiving a miss (tests/tracking/test_track_manager.cpp only exercises the Confirmed->Coasting path).
  - failure_scenario: Tracker(miss_timeout=5s) + TrackManager(confirm_hits=3, delete_misses=3) + CpaEvaluator with defaults. A single clutter radar return at t=0 births Tentative track T (hits=1, TrackManager.cpp:15). T never associates again; at t>5s the stale sweep (Tracker.cpp:192) calls recordMiss(T): misses=1 < 3, status set to Coasting. The next CpaEvaluator::evaluate(t) passes T through the status gate; if own-ship's course passes near the clutter position, probability_below_threshold crosses enter_probability and an Entered collision-risk event fires to the operator sink — a false collision alarm sourced from one unconfirmed clutter blip. T stays CPA-eligible for delete_misses-1 further cycles. Consumers reading TrackOutput.status also see a contract-violating Coasting for a track that was never Confirmed.
  - evidence: TrackManager.cpp:44-65 (no prior-status check before line 64); CpaEvaluator.cpp:26-30 (status_ok includes Coasting, excludes Tentative when evaluate_tentative=false); CpaEvaluatorConfig.evaluate_tentative default false (CpaEvaluator.hpp:23); docs/output-contract.md:25 defines Coasting as 'was Confirmed'.
  - suggested_fix: In recordMiss, only demote to Coasting when the track is currently Confirmed (or Coasting); leave Tentative tracks Tentative: if (tracks_[i].status == TrackStatus::Confirmed) tracks_[i].status = TrackStatus::Coasting;

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** A Coasting (ex-Confirmed) track that re-associates is not restored to Confirmed until confirm_hits consecutive fresh hits, contradicting the documented Coasting semantics, and the eventual re-promotion re-fires onTrackConfirmed despite the port's 'fires once' contract
  - `core/tracking/TrackManager.cpp:36` (lifecycle-correctness, confidence high)
  - description: recordMiss resets hits to 0 (line 48); on recovery each recordHit increments hits but the status stays Coasting until hits >= confirm_hits_ (line 36). During recovery the track IS receiving fresh estimator updates (Tracker calls recordHit only after a successful update), yet its status remains Coasting — the output contract defines Coasting as 'propagated through a detection gap WITHOUT a fresh update' (docs/output-contract.md:25). Consumers that filter output on status==Confirmed (app/example.cpp:141, app/mht_fusion_example.cpp:163, adapters/foxglove/FoxgloveDebugRecorder.cpp:102 is_output, core/benchmark/BenchRunner.cpp:107) drop an actively-updated confirmed vessel from output for confirm_hits-1 update cycles after every single miss event. When re-promotion finally happens, was_unconfirmed is true (Coasting != Confirmed) so onTrackConfirmed fires a second time for the same track, violating ITrackSink.hpp:40-41 ('fires once when Tentative -> Confirmed') — consumers that allocate UI entries or dedup alerts on first confirmation double-fire.
  - failure_scenario: confirm_hits=3, AIS track Confirmed and steady. One dropout longer than miss_timeout: recordMiss -> Coasting, hits=0. AIS resumes at 10 s intervals: for the next 2 reports (20 s) the track is updated every cycle but stays Coasting — a Confirmed-filtered operator display blanks the vessel for 20 s during normal AIS class-B behavior. On the 3rd report the sink receives a duplicate onTrackConfirmed event for a track it already registered.
  - evidence: TrackManager.cpp:30-42 (hits reset by miss at :48, promotion gate at :36, refire via was_unconfirmed at :35-40); ITrackSink.hpp:26-27,40-41 ('fires once when Tentative -> Confirmed'); docs/output-contract.md:25 (Coasting = no fresh update); Confirmed-only filters at FoxgloveDebugRecorder.cpp:102, example.cpp:141, BenchRunner.cpp:107. No test exercises hit-after-miss recovery.
  - suggested_fix: In recordHit, restore Confirmed immediately when the track's status is Coasting and it was previously Confirmed (track the was-confirmed bit or treat Coasting as a Confirmed substate), and fire onTrackConfirmed only on the first Tentative->Confirmed transition.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Documented 'no sensor specs' pattern is a silent no-op for the range/bearing builders: applyDefaultsIfEmpty can never fire on their output, so following the example yields a zero/GPS-only measurement covariance that is silently 100x+ overconfident
  - `app/example.cpp:124` (api-contract, confidence high)
  - description: buildBearingMeasurement always assigns m.covariance = proj.cov (core/types/MeasurementBuilders.cpp:81) — a real 2x2 even when range_std_m and bearing_std_rad are 0 (then cov = sigma_gps^2*I, or exactly zero when position_std_m is also 0). applyDefaultsIfEmpty only fills when covariance.size()==0 (core/types/SensorDefaults.cpp:73), and SensorDefaults has no (ArpaTtm|EoIr, Position2D) entry anyway (SensorDefaults.cpp:31-48) — the arpa_ttm_range_bearing/eoir_range_bearing defaults key on RangeBearing2D, a model the builders never emit (they emit Position2D, MeasurementBuilders.cpp:34). Yet app/example.cpp:124-125 explicitly instructs: 'If your radar didn't report std values, leave them 0 and call applyDefaultsIfEmpty(m, defaults)', and CLAUDE.md:122 states the same generic pattern. The recommended call is a guaranteed no-op, covariance_is_default stays false (no diagnostic), and the degenerate R proceeds.
  - failure_scenario: A consumer with a spec-less radar follows example.cpp: range_std=0, bearing_std=0, GPS sigma 5 m. Every TTM measurement carries R = 25*I m^2 instead of the intended pessimistic defaults (75 m range sigma -> 5625 m^2): 225x overconfident, silently. Tracks initiate with a near-zero position covariance, gating against subsequent honest sensors collapses, and no flag warns (covariance_is_default=false). If GPS sigma is also 0, R is exactly zero: initiation is silently rejected by the strict PSD check (MeasurementModels.hpp:89) so the sensor never births a track, while matched updates to existing tracks apply R=0 and snap tracks onto raw returns.
  - evidence: MeasurementBuilders.cpp:71-81 (covariance always set on the success path); SensorDefaults.cpp:72-78 (empty-only fill) and :31-48 (no Position2D entry for ArpaTtm/EoIr); app/example.cpp:124-125 (the no-op advice); CLAUDE.md:122; adapters/ArpaAdapter.hpp:26-28 has its own nonzero defaults so only direct builder consumers are exposed.
  - suggested_fix: Either have the bearing builders consult a SensorDefaults (or their doc demand nonzero stds and assert/flag zero sigmas), or fix the guidance in example.cpp/CLAUDE.md/integration guide to say: pass the defaults' sigma_range_m/sigma_bearing_rad as builder arguments — and add (sensor, Position2D) awareness or a covariance_is_default marker for this path.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** ClutterMapSensorDetectionModel caches learned clutter cells in ENU grid coordinates but implements no IDatumChangeSink and offers no shift/clear API, so after an auto-datum recenter the learned lambda map silently applies ~30 km off and stale hot cells persist indefinitely
  - `core/tracking/ClutterMapDetectionModel.hpp:194` (state-consistency, confidence high)
  - description: position_maps_ keys cells by floor(ENU/cell_size) in the working datum frame (ClutterMapDetectionModel.cpp:157-161), and paramsFor(z) interpolates at z.value's current-frame ENU (cpp:96-107). The class implements only ISensorDetectionModel; unlike StaticObstacleModel/CoastlineModel/LiveOccupancyModel (which CLAUDE.md's auto-datum section requires registering as datum sinks precisely because they cache ENU state), there is no onDatumRecentered handling and no way to register one. After OwnShipProvider auto-recenters (default policy, 30 km threshold), every learned cell is anchored to the old frame while queries and observe() feeds arrive in the new frame. The class doc itself notes cells unvisited for a long time 'keep their last estimate — persistent map memory', so mis-anchored hot cells (up to max_ratio=64x baseline) are applied at wrong geographic locations forever unless coincidentally overwritten. The bench Sweep's fixed-datum usage is the known exception; a library consumer wiring the decorator into MhtTracker (the shipped imm_cv_ct_mht_cmap wiring pattern) with default auto-recenter hits this.
  - failure_scenario: Consumer wraps their sensor table in ClutterMapSensorDetectionModel for an MhtTracker, auto-recenter on. Ship transits 35 km past a cluttered shoreline; the map learns 64x-baseline cells over the shore. Datum recenters; the tracker's tracks are shifted (MhtTracker::onDatumRecentered) but the clutter cells are not: the 64x lambda region now sits over open water ~30 km from the real shore in the new frame, suppressing legitimate new-target scores there (higher log lambda_C penalty per MHT branch score), while the actual shoreline reverts to baseline. No error, no diagnostic; cells in the phantom region persist until new returns happen to land in those exact cells.
  - evidence: ClutterMapDetectionModel.hpp:169-196 (Cell/PositionMap keyed on int64 ENU indices; class implements only ISensorDetectionModel); grep shows no IDatumChangeSink/onDatumRecentered/clear anywhere in the class; CLAUDE.md auto-datum section lists the three other ENU-caching models as mandatory datum sinks; MhtTracker.cpp:846-860 shifts tracks but detection_model_ is untouched.
  - suggested_fix: Implement IDatumChangeSink on ClutterMapSensorDetectionModel: on recenter, either rebuild cell keys via the old->new reprojection (cell centers through Datum) or, simplest and safe, clear all maps (tau=20 s relearns quickly); document the wiring in the integration guide alongside the other datum sinks.

- **[LOW/unverified]** 5-state (IMM CV/CT mainline) covariance shift rotates only the top-left 4x4 block, leaving the omega row/column cross-covariances in the old frame's axes
  - `core/tracking/DatumShift.cpp:24` (math-correctness, confidence high)
  - description: rotateCovarianceInPlace transforms cov.topLeftCorner<4,4>() with blkdiag(R,R) but the shipped IMM estimator uses 5-state [px,py,vx,vy,omega] tracks with 5x5 covariances (ImmEstimator.cpp:448-467); the CT mode's Jacobian couples omega into vx/vy so P(0:3,4) becomes nonzero in operation. The correct transform is blkdiag(R,R,1)*P*blkdiag(R,R,1)^T, which also rotates the 4x1 cross-covariance column P(0:3,4) by blkdiag(R,R). Leaving it untouched makes the shifted matrix not a similarity transform of the original: cross-correlations between turn rate and position/velocity point ~gamma (~0.5-1.5 deg per recenter) off relative to the rotated block, and in the near-singular high-correlation case the result can lose positive semi-definiteness. Applies identically to each entry of imm_covariances (DatumShift.cpp:65-67) and to the MhtTracker per-node shift.
  - failure_scenario: Turning target tracked by the IMM CT mode develops strong omega-vy correlation; ship transits 30 km, datum recenters. The 4x4 block rotates (currently also with the flipped sign, see the AxisRotation finding) while row/col 4 stays fixed; the resulting P is slightly inconsistent — in the worst case (correlation near 1) non-PSD, which downstream Cholesky/LLT-based likelihood evaluation rejects or turns into NaN d2.
  - evidence: DatumShift.cpp:22-30 (only topLeftCorner<4,4> transformed; comment says 'smaller states skip' but says nothing about larger); ImmEstimator.cpp:448-467 (5-state means/covariances are the mainline carrier); CoordinatedTurn.cpp:12-51 (F couples omega into velocity, producing the cross terms).
  - suggested_fix: In rotateCovarianceInPlace, build an n x n rotation (identity with R in the two 2x2 kinematic slots) sized to cov and apply the full similarity transform so cross terms to any additional states rotate too.

- **[LOW/unverified]** onTrackConfirmed event carries the PREVIOUS observation's timestamp because Tracker calls recordHit before noteObservation
  - `core/tracking/TrackManager.cpp:39` (api-contract, confidence high)
  - description: recordHit fires onTrackConfirmed with last_observation_[i] as the event time (TrackManager.cpp:39), but all three Tracker call sites invoke recordHit BEFORE noteObservation(id, z.time) (Tracker.cpp:172-173, 272-273, 304-305).
