Cross-checked against core/geo/{AxisRotation,Datum}.cpp, core/projection/Projection.cpp, core/own_ship/OwnShipProvider, core/pipeline/Tracker.cpp (caller of TrackManager), core/collision/CpaEvaluator, ports/{ITrackSink,ISensorDetectionModel}.hpp, app examples, docs/output-contract.md, integration guide, and tests in tests/tracking + tests/types. The datum-rotation sign was verified by an independent Python replication of the exact Datum::toEnu math (finite-difference velocity through both frames) — not just by symbolic derivation. Checked the existing 10-bughunt-findings.md from this same review: no overlap (their pipeline batch explicitly lists DatumShift.cpp as out of scope; their TrackManager checks covered only erase+reindex mechanics, which I also verified correct).  VERIFIED CLEAN (hand-executed): TrackManager id allocation — single assignment site, monotonic uint64, caller-supplied ids overwritten, never reused after erase; id_to_index_ erase+reindex correct and pinned by test; determinism preserved (iteration driven by vector, unordered_map is lookup-only). DatumShift position path exact via geodetic round-trip (altitude carried through, curvature ~70 m z at 30 km handled correctly); omega itself correctly frame-invariant; rotateCovarianceInPlace .eval() prevents aliasing; particles/IMM means handled. projectRangeBearingToEnu Jacobian verified analytically (compass convention east=r*sin, J=[[sb,r*cb],[cb,-r*sb]]); heading sigma in quadrature per doc #16; isotropic GPS add is a documented approximation (ignores cross-scan correlation — standard). MeasurementBuilders: no-pose/no-datum empty-value sentinel honored by both in-repo callers (checked m.value.size()>0); bearing wrap irrelevant (sin/cos); heading composition max(pose sigma, floor) as documented; makeMeasurementFromEnuPosition isZero sentinel documented. ClutterMap EWMA math verified (seed=base*area so untouched-cell readback==baseline, w=1-exp(-dt/tau), first-touch prior weight, ratio clamp, bilinear cell centers consistent between cellOf/query/introspection, azimuth wrap incl. negative-index modulo); std::map keeps observe deterministic. CoverageSector::fromReturns traced for n=1, identical bearings, wrap-cut at largest gap, unwrap loop, largest-cluster tie-break — clean. FixedSensorDetectionModel lookup precedence and AdaptiveSensorDetectionModel EWMA/bbox traced. Timestamp: int64 nanos, exact comparisons, secondsSince diffs in integer domain first; no overflow before ~year 2262.  OVERFLOW ONE-LINERS (not reported): (1) Timestamp::fromSeconds loses sub-256 ns precision at Unix-epoch magnitudes (double ULP) and truncates toward zero — below sensor timing resolution. (2) TrackManager::add default first_observation=Timestamp{} (epoch 0) makes a direct-API track instantly stale in Tracker's sweep — pipeline always passes z.time. (3) ClutterMap EWMA gives w=0 for a same-timestamp second observe() on the same (kind,model) map — in-repo producers aggregate one bundle per key per scan so not hit. (4) ClutterMapParams.bearing_cell_rad=0 causes inf/UB size cast, no config validation (nonsensical config). (5) ClutterMap observe seeds new cells from the KIND-WIDE baseline while queries clamp around the SOURCE-keyed baseline — mixed but by-design kind-wide map. (6) TrackStatus::Deleted is never observable via TrackManager (immediate erase) though the output contract describes a final drain — PMBM-only semantics. (7) 'M-of-N' in the header is actually consecutive-counting (hit resets misses and vice versa) — alternating hit/miss never confirms; matches tests, likely intended. (8) SensorDefaults (ArpaTtm,RangeBearing2D)/(EoIr,RangeBearing2D) entries are unreachable via shipped adapters/builders (all emit Position2D) — dead table entries, related to my example.cpp finding.  OUT-OF-SCOPE OBSERVATIONS for other units: (a) core/output/TrackOutput.cpp:21 — toGeodeticWithCov rotates the ENU covariance but never applies the ENU->NED axis swap, while docs/output-contract.md:8 says row0=north/row1=east; for anisotropic covariance [0][0] is actually sigma_east^2 mislabeled as north (worked example is isotropic so no test catches it); it also inherits the AxisRotation sign flip — route to the output reviewer. (b) RangeBearing2D (range,bearing) pushed as ENU into ScanObservation.positions (MhtTracker.cpp:822, PmbmTracker.cpp:1797) — already reported by the pipeline batch. (c) Tracker::process/processBatch per-measurement miss ticking after timeout — already noted as pipeline overflow item. NOT COVERED: TrackTree.* (excluded from unit scope), estimator internals beyond initiate() layout, gitignored fixtures.

### unit: geo-ownship (4 findings)

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** datumAxisRotation does not wrap delta-longitude: datum recenter across the antimeridian rotates every track velocity/covariance by a wildly wrong convergence angle
  - `core/geo/AxisRotation.cpp:15` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: datumAxisRotation computes delta_lon_rad = (n.lon_deg - o.lon_deg) * kDeg2Rad with no normalization to [-180, 180). Longitudes arriving from adapters are in [-180, 180], so when the two datum origins straddle the antimeridian the raw difference is ~±359.7 deg instead of ~±0.3 deg. gamma = delta_lon * sin(mean_lat) then becomes ~-6.28*sin(lat) rad instead of ~+0.003 rad. This feeds (a) shiftStateOnDatumChange / shiftTracksOnDatumChange (core/tracking/DatumShift.cpp:39,73), which rotate every track's velocity, covariance blocks, IMM means/covs and particle velocities on each auto-recenter, and (b) toGeodeticWithCov (core/output/TrackOutput.cpp:17), which rotates the output position covariance into the target's NED frame for targets across the antimeridian from the datum. Positions themselves are shifted exactly via the geodetic round-trip, so the corruption is silent: positions stay right while velocities/covariances are rotated wrong.
  - failure_scenario: Own-ship transits east across the antimeridian at lat 30 N (mid-Pacific; same for Bering Strait at 60 N). Working datum origin lon = +179.90. Ship sails ~31 km east; the next fix at lon = -179.78 exceeds the 30 km threshold and OwnShipProvider auto-recenters. datumAxisRotation(old=+179.90, new=-179.78) computes delta_lon = -359.68 deg, gamma = -6.277 * sin(30) = -3.139 rad (should be +0.0029 rad). R(-3.139) is approximately -I: shiftTracksOnDatumChange reverses the velocity vector of EVERY live track (a 10 kn northbound target becomes 10 kn southbound). All subsequent predictions run backwards, gating fails, tracks fragment or drag. At lat 45 the rotation error is ~105 deg (mod 2pi), corrupting velocity direction and covariance orientation instead of reversing. Independently, toGeodeticWithCov reports output covariance ellipses rotated by ~2*pi*(1-sin(lat)) for any target across the meridian even without a recenter. No test covers longitudes near +/-180 (tests/geo/test_datum.cpp, tests/tracking/test_datum_shift.cpp all use lon 0-8.5; the convergence-angle test uses lon 0->1), so the suite cannot contradict this.
  - evidence: AxisRotation.cpp lines 15-17: `const double delta_lon_rad = (n.lon_deg - o.lon_deg) * kDeg2Rad; ... const double gamma = delta_lon_rad * std::sin(mean_lat_rad);` — no fmod/wrap anywhere. Call sites confirmed at core/tracking/DatumShift.cpp:39,73 and core/output/TrackOutput.cpp:17; MhtTracker::onDatumRecentered (core/pipeline/MhtTracker.cpp:846) routes through the same shiftStateOnDatumChange. OwnShipProvider.cpp:39-44 shows the recenter fires whenever horizontal ENU distance > 30 km, with the new origin taken verbatim from pose.lon_deg.
  - suggested_fix: Normalize the longitude difference before scaling: wrap (n.lon_deg - o.lon_deg) into [-180, 180) (e.g. d = std::remainder(n.lon_deg - o.lon_deg, 360.0)) in datumAxisRotation, and add an antimeridian regression test for both DatumShift and toGeodeticWithCov.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full failing path. (1) core/geo/AxisRotation.cpp:15-17 computes delta_lon_rad = (n.lon_deg - o.lon_deg)*kDeg2Rad and gamma = delta_lon*sin(mean_lat) with no wrap/fmod anywhere in the file. (2) Longitudes reaching it are always wrapped to [-180,180]: ecefToGeodetic (core/geo/Wgs84.cpp:37) uses atan2, adapters validate lon into [-180,180], and Datum stores its origin verbatim (Datum.cpp:11) — so consecutive datum origins straddling the antimeridian genuinely differ by ~±359.7 deg in stored form. (3) The recenter fires across the seam: Datum::toEnu goes through ECEF (Datum.cpp:24-26, globally exact), so the 30 km check at OwnShipProvider.cpp:38-39 works correctly and the new datum takes pose.lon_deg verbatim (line 41); enable_auto_recenter defaults true (OwnShipProvider.hpp:74-75). (4) Hand-executed numbers match the claim: old lon +179.90 → new -179.78 at lat 30 is 30.85 km (fires); delta_lon = -359.68 deg → gamma = -3.1388 rad vs correct +0.00279 rad; R ≈ -I, so shiftTracksOnDatumChange (DatumShift.cpp:73, applied at lines 44/59/87) reverses every live track's velocity, IMM mode velocities, and particle velocities, while positions are shifted exactly via the geodetic round-trip (silent corruption). At lat 45 the rotation error is ~1.84 rad mod 2π — arbitrary wrong rotation of velocity and covariance orientation. (5) Second path confirmed: toGeodeticWithCov (core/output/TrackOutput.cpp:13-21) builds target_datum at the wrapped target lon and calls the same function; output covariance orientation is wrong by -2π·sin(lat) mod 2π for cross-meridian targets (minor nuance: at lat exactly 30 the π error is a near-no-op for the symmetric covariance conjugation, but wrong at general latitudes; the velocity path is wrong at every nonzero latitude). (6) No guard, no documented limitation, no test: repo-wide grep for antimeridian/dateline/lon-wrap handling finds nothing; tests/geo/test_datum.cpp and tests/tracking/test_datum_shift.cpp contain no longitudes near ±180, so the suite cannot contradict this. Not in the known/by-design list.
  - verifier corrected details: Confirmed as claimed. One refinement: in toGeodeticWithCov the covariance conjugation is by R(gamma_err) with gamma_err = -2π·sin(lat) mod 2π, and because covariance conjugation is invariant under a π rotation, the output-covariance corruption vanishes at latitudes where sin(lat) = 0.5 exactly (lat 30) and is worst at mid/high latitudes like 45-60; the DatumShift velocity reversal/rotation, by contrast, is wrong at every latitude with sin(lat) ≠ 0. Trigger requires operating near the antimeridian (mid-Pacific, Bering Strait, Fiji/NZ), so high rather than critical, but when triggered every live track's velocity, covariance, IMM ensemble and particles are silently corrupted on a default-on auto-recenter while positions stay correct.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Maneuver gate is self-defeating: its noise envelope is computed from maneuver-contaminated residuals, so the effective suppression threshold is ~8.8x the configured one and biased own-ship velocity is published during moderate maneuvers
  - `core/own_ship/OwnShipVelocityEstimator.cpp:126` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: The two-halves maneuver gate compares dv against gate = maneuver_dv_threshold_mps + 3*sqrt(2)*sigma_v_half, where sigma_v_half = sigma_pos/sqrt(sxx_half) and sigma_pos is derived from the FULL-window constant-velocity fit residuals (lines 77-79). During a genuine maneuver those residuals contain the maneuver signal itself, so the envelope grows linearly with the very dv the gate is supposed to detect. Hand-execution with zero GPS noise, 1 Hz, window 8 (defaults), velocity step dv at the half boundary (best case for detection): ss_res = 2.619*dv^2, sigma_pos = 0.467*dv, envelope = 0.886*dv, so the gate trips only when dv > 0.5 + 0.886*dv, i.e. dv > 4.4 m/s — 8.8x the configured 0.5 m/s threshold (the coefficient is the same for any axis split; off-boundary maneuvers are detected even less). For any 0.5 < dv < 4.4 the estimator publishes the full-window blended slope (error ~0.405*dv vs the current true velocity) with sigma_v = sigma_pos/sqrt(42) ~ 0.072*dv — about 5.6 sigma overconfident. The design doc (docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-03-adaptive-uere-design.md §4.4) explicitly states the gate must 'suppress publication' during maneuvers and claims 'no chicken-and-egg'; the chicken-and-egg is real. UereEstimator.cpp:112 shares the identical formula, though its failure direction there is only modest sigma inflation.
  - failure_scenario: GGA-only nav feed (no RMC; enable_velocity_estimator defaults true and is the documented fallback, OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:180-184). Own ship at 5 m/s makes a sustained 3 deg/s turn: over the 8 s window the course changes ~24 deg, dv = 2*5*sin(12 deg) ~ 2.1 m/s — 4x the configured gate threshold, yet gate = 0.5 + 0.886*2.1 = 2.36 > 2.1, so publication is NOT suppressed. pose.velocity_enu is published ~0.85 m/s wrong with sigma_v ~ 0.15 m/s (floored at 0.05), velocity_is_valid = true, for the whole duration of the turn. This own-ship velocity feeds CpaOwnShip (core/collision/CpaOwnShip.cpp:15) and hence collision-risk CPA/TCPA — wrong precisely during own-ship maneuvers, when CPA changes matter most. The existing test SuppressesDuringManeuver (tests/own_ship/test_own_ship_velocity_estimator.cpp:40) uses dv = 7.07 m/s, which clears the inflated gate (7.07 > 0.5 + 0.886*7.07 = 6.76) by only 4%, so the suite pins only the extreme case and does not contradict this finding.
  - evidence: Lines 77-79: `var = (fit_x.ss_res + fit_y.ss_res)/(2*(n-2)); sigma_pos = sqrt(var)` — full-window residuals include the maneuver. Lines 123-127: `sigma_v_half = sigma_pos/sqrt(sxx_half); noise_envelope = 3*sqrt(2)*sigma_v_half; gate = cfg_.maneuver_dv_threshold_mps + noise_envelope`. With defaults (1 Hz, n=8): sxx_half = 5, sxx_full = 42; worked numbers above verified by direct computation of the LS fit on x = [0,0,0,0,dv,2dv,3dv,4dv].
  - suggested_fix: Estimate sigma_pos for the envelope from maneuver-robust residuals — e.g. the pooled residuals of the two per-half fits (each half is approximately constant-velocity even mid-maneuver) instead of the full-window fit — or cap the envelope by an a-priori GPS noise bound. Add a test that a dv of 2-3x the threshold with zero noise is suppressed.

- **[LOW/unverified]** approxMeters does not wrap delta-longitude: crossing the antimeridian raises a false position_jump nav-health flag
  - `core/own_ship/NavInputGuard.cpp:17` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: approxMeters computes deast = (lon2 - lon1) * 111320 * cos(mean_lat) with no wrap. For consecutive fixes straddling +/-180 (prev lon +179.999, curr lon -179.999) the raw difference is ~-360 deg, giving a position step of ~2.2e7 m. evaluateNavInput then sets position_jump (step/dt >> 50 m/s) and reports position_step_m ~ 2e7; the derived SOG also becomes huge, which additionally suppresses a legitimate heading_unreliable_low_sog flag for that pair. The guard never rewrites poses, so the damage is confined to one spurious 'degrade visibly' health event per crossing (subsequent pose pairs are on the same side and evaluate correctly).
  - failure_scenario: Vessel crosses the antimeridian westbound at 5 m/s with a 1 Hz GPS feed and a nav-health sink wired (setNavHealthSink). At the crossing pair, onNavHealth fires with position_jump=true and position_step_m ~ 2.2e7 m even though the true step is ~5 m. An operator display or automated degradation logic wired to INavHealthSink reports a GPS glitch that never happened.
  - evidence: NavInputGuard.cpp lines 14-19: `const double deast = (lon2 - lon1) * 111320.0 * std::cos(mean_lat);` — no remainder/wrap, unlike headingDeltaDeg (line 22) which does wrap. tests/own_ship/test_nav_input_guard.cpp exercises only lon 8.0 +/- small deltas, so nothing pins antimeridian behavior.
  - suggested_fix: Wrap the longitude difference: `double dlon = std::remainder(lon2 - lon1, 360.0);` before scaling.

- **[LOW/unverified]** Auto-recenter acts on a pose the nav guard just flagged as a position jump: a single >30 km GPS glitch recenters the datum twice and churns all datum sinks
  - `core/own_ship/OwnShipProvider.cpp:39` (robustness, confidence high)
  - description: update() evaluates the nav guard (which can set position_jump for a physically implausible step) but ignores the result for its own state transitions: the recenter check at lines 35-45 runs unconditionally on the incoming pose. A single glitched fix far from the current origin (>30 km) immediately re-anchors the working datum onto the bogus position and fires every IDatumChangeSink; the next good fix is then >30 km from the glitch origin and recenters again. Each recenter shifts all tracks (numerically near-lossless), but also clears MhtTracker::contribution_history_ (MhtTracker.cpp:846-864, bias-extraction gap by design 'a recenter is rare') and re-anchors the LiveOccupancyModel grid, which is lossy for occupancy content — two spurious re-anchors wipe the suppression map. The provider knows the pose is implausible (its own guard just measured step/dt > max_position_speed_mps) yet re-anchors on it anyway; the guard's flag-only contract covers not rewriting the pose, but recentering is the provider's own state, not the pose.
  - failure_scenario: 1 Hz GPS feed; receiver glitch (cold-start jump / multipath / spoofing) emits one fix 100 km off, then resumes normal fixes. t=k: guard fires position_jump AND the datum recenters onto the glitch (all sinks fire, occupancy grid re-anchors 100 km away, dropping its contents; MHT bias history cleared). t=k+1: good fix is 100 km from the glitch origin — second recenter, second full sink churn, occupancy content lost again. Net effect from one bad sentence: occupancy/suppression state destroyed and every track shifted twice, silently.
  - evidence: OwnShipProvider.cpp lines 28-31 (guard evaluated, result only forwarded to the sink) and 35-45 (recenter decision uses only the ENU distance of the raw pose; no plausibility condition, no consultation of the NavHealth result computed four lines earlier). CLAUDE.md invariant 6 places plausibility validation in adapters, but backlog #18 added the guard here precisely because implausible fixes reach this layer.
  - suggested_fix: When the guard is wired and reports position_jump for the incoming pose, skip (or defer) the recenter for that pose — e.g. require two consecutive far fixes before re-anchoring.

Coverage notes (geo-ownship): Read end-to-end: core/geo/Wgs84.{hpp,cpp}, Datum.{hpp,cpp}, AxisRotation.{hpp,cpp}; core/projection/Projection.{hpp,cpp}; core/own_ship/OwnShipProvider.{hpp,cpp}, NavInputGuard.{hpp,cpp}, OwnShipVelocityEstimator.{hpp,cpp}, UereEstimator.{hpp,cpp}; plus call-site files core/tracking/DatumShift.cpp, core/output/TrackOutput.cpp, core/pipeline/MhtTracker.cpp (recenter path), core/types/MeasurementBuilders.cpp, core/collision/CpaOwnShip.cpp, adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter (estimator feed), and tests (test_wgs84, test_datum, test_datum_shift, test_nav_input_guard, test_own_ship_velocity_estimator, test_uere_estimator). CLEAN: WGS84 constants and Bowring inverse verified against standard formulas (round-trip test passes at 1e-9 deg); only exact-pole input (p=0) yields a wrong altitude — unrealistic for maritime, not reported. Datum ECEF->ENU rotation matrix verified row-by-row; toEnu/toGeodetic are exact 3D transforms (no small-angle error), so the 30 km recenter bound is consistent — no accuracy-vs-distance defect in the transform itself; DatumShift's z=0 round-trip is exact for the 3D point (no horizontal corruption from the ~70 m curvature drop). Projection.cpp polar->Cartesian Jacobian and covariance composition (bearing+heading variance in quadrature, isotropic GPS term) verified correct and PSD by construction. OwnShipProvider: sorted insert / equal-timestamp (most-recent-wins) semantics verified consistent with poseAtOrBefore's reverse walk; measurement-before-first-pose handled gracefully in MeasurementBuilders (empty measurement returned; datum() throw documented and guarded by hasDatum()); recenter fires sinks after the datum swap but before inserting the triggering pose — checked every IDatumChangeSink implementation in-tree (TrackShifter, CoastlineModel, StaticObstacleModel, BearingWedgeModel, LiveOccupancyModel, MhtTracker, FoxgloveDebugRecorder): none reads provider state during the callback, so no half-updated-state observer exists today (latent trap only). NavInputGuard: heading delta wrap correct; dt<=0 / out-of-order / first-pose paths correct and test-pinned; units of all thresholds consistent. LS fit math (fitAxis) in both estimators verified; degenerate windows (sxx=0, window<4, n<=2) return unpublished; Timestamp nanos->double precision adequate (~us). Overflow one-liners, mostly out of scope but relevant to other reviewers: (1) adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:139 equirectangular reference is fixed at the FIRST GGA fix forever — cos(ref_lat) east-scale error grows on long voyages (~2x from 10N to 60N, biasing the published fallback velocity) and a +/-180 lon crossing injects a 2.2e7 m step into both estimators (transient garbage sigma/velocity published for ~1 window); (2) a pure position step (GPS fix-mode shift) aligned with the two-halves boundary evades the maneuver gate entirely (dv~0) and publishes a phantom velocity ~0.19*step m/s — same root family as finding 2; (3) NavInputGuard's derived-SOG-from-step is noise-dominated at high fix rates (anchored ship, 10 Hz, 1 m noise => derived SOG ~10 m/s => documented low-sog anchor case never flags) — accuracy limit of the documented fact-free design, not reported as a defect; (4) both estimators split halves by arrival order, not time order — only an issue if fed out-of-order, which the NMEA adapter does not do.

### unit: bias (9 findings)

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** Closed-loop heading-bias wiring double-subtracts the published bias: estimate converges to half the true gyro bias
  - `core/bias/HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:64` (feedback-loop, confidence high)
  - description: observe(AisArpaPairObservation) treats z = wrap(beta_arpa - beta_ais) as a measurement of the FULL bias b and forms the residual y = wrap(z - b_hat_). But in the documented wiring (integration-guide.md §5: pass the estimator to ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter 'so the estimated bias is removed from their bearings'; same wiring in tests/sim/BusComparisonHelpers.hpp runBusCellInterleaved and test_bus_anchor_loss.cpp), ArpaAdapter.cpp:119 already subtracts the published b_hat from the TTM bearing before projecting to ENU, so the SourceTouch the extractor pairs is ALREADY debiased and z measures only the residual (b_true - b_pub). Subtracting b_hat again gives y = b_true - 2*b_hat once is_published flips true. The KF fixed point of b_hat += k*(b_true - 2*b_hat) is b_hat = b_true/2: the published estimate decays from the correct value to half, and every subsequent ARPA/EO-IR measurement permanently retains half the heading bias while the published variance keeps shrinking below the (0.3 deg)^2 publish threshold (overconfident). Correct closed-loop math with pre-corrected inputs is y = z (or un-correct the touch); y = z - b_hat is only right open-loop.
  - failure_scenario: Guide-§5 wiring, true gyro bias 2 deg, AIS+ARPA target at 1.5 km. Pre-publish the estimator correctly converges to ~2 deg and publishes; the adapter starts subtracting 2 deg; the next pairs give z ~ 0 deg, y = z - b_hat ~ -2 deg (well inside the 5-sigma gate since sigma_v ~ 1.1 deg), dragging b_hat down with time constant of a few pairs to the 1 deg equilibrium. Result: a permanent ~1 deg residual bias (~26 m cross-range at 1.5 km) on every ARPA/EO-IR measurement, with published sigma claiming <0.3 deg. For b_true > ~5.5 deg the post-publish y instead fails the outlier gate: all pairs rejected, last_update freezes, estimator unpublishes 30 s later, correction switches off, raw pairs get re-accepted, it re-publishes — a ~30 s on/off oscillation of the entire correction. No test contradicts: tests/bias unit tests are open-loop (observations built from raw positions), test_bus_anchor_loss.cpp injects bias_deg = 0.0, and test_bus_bias_estimator_sweep.cpp is SUCCEED-only (OSPA printed, never asserts converged bias; half-correction still improves OSPA vs none).
  - evidence: core/bias/HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:46,64 (z and y = z - b_hat); adapters/arpa/ArpaAdapter.cpp:112-119 and adapters/eoir/EoIrAdapter.cpp:38-45 (bearing_corrected = bearing - b_hat when is_published); core/bias/AisArpaPairExtractor.cpp:49-50 (pairs the corrected touch values verbatim); docs/integration-guide.md §5 ('pass it to the sensor adapters ... so the estimated bias is removed from their bearings' alongside 'extract AIS↔ARPA pairs ... feed them to observe'); tests/sim/BusComparisonHelpers.hpp:490-493 documents this exact loop as the intended closed loop.
  - suggested_fix: Pick one convention: either have the extractor un-correct the touch (store/carry the raw bearing, or add back the bias the adapter applied), or drop the '- b_hat_' when the observation comes from already-corrected data (y = z). Cleanest: carry the applied correction in the Measurement/SourceTouch so the estimator can reconstruct the full-bias measurement, and add a closed-loop test asserting b_hat converges to the injected bias (not half) after publish.
  - verifier: I independently traced the full closed-loop path and every link in the claim holds.  1. Mechanism confirmed in code. adapters/arpa/ArpaAdapter.cpp:112-119: for TTM, `b_hat = bias_est.is_published ? bias_est.bias_rad : 0.0` and `bearing_true_rad_corrected = bearing_true_rad - b_hat` is what gets projected into the Measurement value. core/pipeline/SourceTouchPopulate.hpp (Position2D branch) copies that corrected ENU value into Track::SourceTouch.value_enu verbatim; core/bias/AisArpaPairExtractor.cpp:48-50 pairs those touch values with no raw-bearing side channel (SourceTouch has no field carrying the applied correction). So once published, z = wrap(beta_arpa_corrected - beta_ais) ≈ b_true - b_hat. HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:64 then computes y = wrap(z - b_hat_), i.e. y ≈ b_true - 2*b_hat. KF fixed point (y=0) is b_hat = b_true/2.  2. Hand-executed the numbers. b_true = 2 deg, target at 1.5 km: sigma_v ≈ sqrt((1 deg fallback)^2 + (10 m/1500 m)^2) ≈ 1.1 deg, so the 5-sigma gate (line 74-78) is ≈5.5-5.7 deg. Post-publish y ≈ -2 deg passes the gate and drags b_hat toward the 1-deg equilibrium; published sigma stays below the 0.3-deg publish threshold (current(), lines 118-131) while the actual correction error is ~1 deg (≈26 m cross-range at 1.5 km) — overconfident. For b_true above the ~5.5-deg gate width, post-publish pairs are all rejected, last_update_ freezes, stale_seconds=30 unpublishes (line 128), adapters revert to raw, pairs are re-accepted, it republishes — the claimed on/off oscillation. Both regimes check out.  3. This closed loop is the documented, intended wiring, not a misuse. docs/integration-guide.md §5 instructs BOTH: "extract AIS↔ARPA pairs with extractPairs(...) and feed them to observe(...)" AND "pass it to the sensor adapters (ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter take a const IHeadingBiasProvider*) so the estimated bias is removed from their bearings". The design spec (docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-03-heading-bias-estimator-design.md) is internally inconsistent: §4.2 derives z = b + v assuming the RAW bearing (beta_enu_arpa = psi_raw + beta_rel), while §3 composition step 1 has adapters querying the provider and applying b_hat before the tracker sees the measurement, and step 3 extracts pairs from that corrected snapshot. §4.3's y = wrap(z - b_hat) is only correct open-loop. tests/sim/BusComparisonHelpers.hpp (runBusCellInterleaved header comment) explicitly celebrates this as "the closed loop", and sim/ArpaEmitter.cpp emits TTM (the corrected path).  4. No test contradicts. tests/bias/test_heading_bias_estimator.cpp builds pairs from raw positions (makePair: arpa = truth + bias) — open-loop, where line 64 is correct; it asserts convergence there only. tests/sim/test_bus_anchor_loss.cpp:81 sets bias_deg = 0.0 ("anchor-loss is about gating, not bias mag"). tests/sim/test_bus_bias_estimator_sweep.cpp is SUCCEED-only (prints OSPA tables, asserts nothing) and its closed-loop rows never inject a nonzero heading_bias_deg (knobs only set sigma_heading_deg/r_inflation_on), so with b_true = 0 the double-subtraction has fixed point 0 and is invisible. test_bus_heading_bias_drift_probe.cpp injects bias but wires no estimator at all. Grep for closed-loop/double-subtract acknowledgments in docs/ found none — this is not a documented trade-off.  Refutation attempts that failed: no un-correction anywhere between adapter and extractor; SourceTouch carries no applied-bias field; b_pub == b_hat_ exactly when published (current() returns b_hat_); the outlier gate does not save the moderate-bias case (2 deg << 5.5 deg) and actively causes the oscillation in the large-bias case.
  - verifier corrected details: Verified as claimed, with two refinements. (1) The defect originates in the design spec itself: 2026-06-03-heading-bias-estimator-design.md §4.2 models z = b + v from the RAW bearing while §3 step 1 applies the published correction upstream of the snapshot the pairs are extracted from; the code faithfully implements both halves of the contradiction. Fix options: feed observe() the residual form (y = z, no second subtraction) when inputs are corrected, or record the applied correction in the Measurement/SourceTouch and un-correct before differencing. (2) Scope notes: the loop closes only for ARPA TTM (TLL is never bias-corrected, and EO-IR emits SensorKind::EoIr which the pair extractor ignores), but TTM is the standard ARPA path, the sim emitter's path, and the guide-§5 wiring; EO-IR measurements still inherit the halved correction through the shared b_hat. The sibling BearingInnovation path (HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:109, y = wrap(innovation - b_hat)) has the same structural double-count in closed loop and deserves the same audit, though its dynamics differ (innovation is against the track state, itself built from corrected measurements). Severity stays high, not critical: no crash, tracks still form, AIS unaffected; the failure is a silent permanent halving of the advertised heading-bias correction (~26 m cross-range at 1.5 km for a 2-deg gyro bias) with an overconfident published variance (<0.3 deg claimed vs ~1 deg actual error), plus a 30-s publish/unpublish oscillation of the whole correction for biases above the ~5.5-deg gate width.

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** Per-sensor bias loop feeds bias-corrected SourceTouches back into an estimator that subtracts b_hat again: published mounting bias converges to half
  - `core/bias/SensorBiasEstimator.cpp:99` (feedback-loop, confidence high)
  - description: observe(PositionBiasPairObservation) forms r = z_sensor - z_anchor - b_hat (line 99), i.e. it models z_sensor as the RAW biased measurement. But in the shipped item-9 wiring (core/benchmark/Sweep.cpp:318-336 and 500-520; PMBM path identical), the tracker is given the same estimator via setSensorBiasProvider, applyBiasCorrection subtracts the published bias from every incoming measurement (Tracker.cpp:136, MhtTracker.cpp:242-249, PmbmTracker.cpp:1354), and the SourceTouch is populated from the CORRECTED measurement (Tracker.cpp:156-160, MhtTracker.cpp:619+642-649). So once positionBias(key).is_published flips true, the extractor's z_sensor already excludes b_pub and the observation becomes r = (b_true - b_pub) - b_hat = b_true - 2*b_hat; the fixed point is b_hat = b_true/2. Identical defect on the bearing path: applyBiasCorrection subtracts the published bearing bias from Bearing2D value(0) (BiasCorrection.hpp:72), the touch stores the corrected alpha_rad (SourceTouchPopulate.hpp:69), and observe(BearingBiasPairObservation) adds b_hat into alpha_pred (SensorBiasEstimator.cpp:142) — a second subtraction in the residual.
  - failure_scenario: Sweep item-9 wiring (also the guide's 'wire it only if you have mounting misalignment' path): radar with a true 4 m east offset. Estimator converges to ~4 m, publishes when P <= 1 m^2 per axis with an anchored observation; applyBiasCorrection starts shifting radar measurements; next cycle's pair gives r ~ -4 m (0.3 sigma of S ~ P + R_obs with the 10 m fallbacks, so the Mahalanobis gate accepts), and b_hat decays to the 2 m equilibrium. Every corrected radar position permanently retains a 2 m offset while the published covariance claims <= 1 m per axis; there is no staleness gate on positionBias, so this never self-heals. For offsets > ~5 sigma of S the post-publish r is instead rejected forever (rej_outlier climbs, estimate frozen, drift untrackable). Unit tests (PositionConvergesToTrueBias etc.) feed raw synthetic observations open-loop, so they pass; no closed-loop test asserts the converged value through a tracker.
  - evidence: core/bias/SensorBiasEstimator.cpp:98-99 (r = z_sensor - z_anchor - b_hat) and 142-143 (alpha_pred = atan2 + b_hat); core/pipeline/Tracker.cpp:136 + 156-160; core/pipeline/MhtTracker.cpp:242-249 + 619 + 642-649 (touches built from the corrected scan); core/pipeline/BiasCorrection.hpp:60-86; core/benchmark/Sweep.cpp:318 (setSensorBiasProvider(bias_est.get())) + 321-336 (same instance fed by extractPositionPairs/extractBearingPairs post-scan).
  - suggested_fix: Same convention decision as the heading finding: either populate SourceTouches from the PRE-correction measurement (keep the correction filter-internal), or carry the applied bias in the touch so the extractor can reconstruct the raw pair, or drop the '- b_hat' / '+ b_hat' terms when inputs are pre-corrected. Add a closed-loop test (tracker + provider + extractor) asserting the published bias equals the injected offset at steady state.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full closed-loop path with concrete values. (1) Design intent is raw input: docs/algorithms/sensor-bias.md §Math models z_sensor = truth + b + n_sensor and r = z_sensor − z_anchor − b̂; SensorBiasEstimator.cpp:98-99 implements it, and the bearing path adds b_hat into alpha_pred at line 142. (2) All three trackers populate SourceTouch from the bias-CORRECTED measurement: Tracker.cpp:136+152-160; MhtTracker.cpp:241-249 (scan_corrected) + 619+642-649; PmbmTracker.cpp:1351-1358 + 1664-1686. The extractors (SensorBiasPairExtractor.cpp:65-66 position, :110 bearing) copy touch values verbatim with no un-correction. (3) The loop is closed with the SAME estimator instance in the shipped wiring: Sweep.cpp:318 setSensorBiasProvider(bias_est.get()) + 319-336 (MHT) and ~506-517 (PMBM) feed extractPositionPairs/extractBearingPairs back into bias_est; positionBias() returns b_hat itself (line 196), so b_pub ≡ b_hat. (4) Hand-executed dynamics: pre-publish r = b_true − b_hat converges to b_true; publish latches at P ≤ 1 m² per axis with ≥1 anchored obs (lines 207-211); post-publish r = b_true − 2·b_hat ≈ −b_true; for a 4 m offset mahal² ≈ 16/S with S ≈ 50–200 m² per axis — well inside the 5σ²=25 gate — so accepted, and b_hat decays to the b_true/2 fixed point. No unpublish/staleness path exists, so every corrected measurement permanently retains a b_true/2 offset while the published covariance claims ≤1 m per axis; for offsets beyond ~5σ of S the residual is gated out forever instead (frozen estimate, rej_outlier climbs, drift untrackable). Identical structure on the bearing path (BiasCorrection.hpp:72 subtracts, SourceTouchPopulate.hpp:69 stores corrected alpha, estimator line 142 subtracts again). The item-13 cross-sensor fold compounds it (z_anchor = touch − b̂_Y at SensorBiasPairExtractor.cpp:259 double-debiases an already-corrected anchor touch). (5) No test pins the closed loop: tests/bias/test_sensor_bias_estimator.cpp hand-builds RAW observations/touches (open loop); tests/pmbm/test_pmbm_phase8.cpp uses a FixedSensorBiasProvider with no feedback; the doc's 2026-06-17 empirical check was the symmetric ±0.57 m case where GOSPA is bit-identical, insensitive to halving. The doc's math contradicts the implementation, so this is not by design and is not in the known/by-design list.
  - verifier corrected details: Confirmed as claimed, with one refinement: in the large-offset regime (|b_true| > ~5σ of S post-publish), the estimate freezes at b_true — coincidentally the correct value — so the operational harm there is loss of drift tracking plus a permanently climbing rej_outlier, not a wrong correction; the halving-to-b_true/2 equilibrium applies to the common small/medium-offset regime (the gate accepts whenever |b_true| ≲ 5·sqrt(S), S ≈ 50–200 m² per axis with realistic covariances or the 10 m fallbacks). Severity stays high rather than critical because the estimator is strictly opt-in (null provider = bit-identical legacy path; default bench configs do not build it), but when wired as the bench and integration guide direct, the feature silently converges to half the true mounting bias with an overconfident published covariance (≤1 m² per axis) and no self-healing path — defeating its purpose exactly when it activates. Fix direction: either record RAW measurements in SourceTouch (before applyBiasCorrection) or drop the second b_hat subtraction in observe() when the input is corrected — but consistently across Tracker/MhtTracker/PmbmTracker and both position and bearing paths, plus a closed-loop convergence test through a tracker.

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** v1 heading-bias pairs compute bearings about the datum origin, not own-ship: NMEA ArpaAdapter never populates sensor_position_enu
  - `core/bias/AisArpaPairExtractor.cpp:48` (data-contract, confidence high)
  - description: extractPairs sets obs.own_position_enu = arpa->sensor_position_enu (line 48), and HeadingBiasEstimator::observe computes both bearings relative to that point (HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:41-44). But the production NMEA ArpaAdapter never sets Measurement::sensor_position_enu on either TTM (ArpaAdapter.cpp:140-148 — own_xy is computed at line 110 and used for projection but never copied into m) or TLL (lines 77-86) measurements, violating Measurement.hpp:67-71's documented contract ('for a sensor mounted on a moving platform this is the platform's ENU position'); the field stays at its Vector2d::Zero() default, flows into the SourceTouch (Tracker.cpp:157, MhtTracker.cpp:647), and the estimator ends up measuring the angle SUBTENDED AT THE DATUM ORIGIN between the AIS and ARPA target positions instead of the bearing disagreement at own-ship. The bias-induced AIS-ARPA displacement is b*r_ownship-to-target; seen from the origin it subtends ~b*(r_own-to-tgt/r_origin-to-tgt), rotated by the geometry difference. Additionally r_ais (used for the <1 m guard and for sigma_v2 = (sigma_ais/r_ais)^2) and r_arpa (GPS floor) become distances from the origin, so the assumed observation noise is understated by the same ratio — the estimator converges CONFIDENTLY to a wrong value. The replay adapters (PlotCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:116/176, AutoferryJsonReplay.cpp:276/296) and MeasurementBuilders.cpp:82 all set the field, confirming the ArpaAdapter omission. extractPositionPairs' min-range gate (own_position_enu = t.sensor_position_enu, SensorBiasPairExtractor.cpp:72 + SensorBiasEstimator.cpp:89-95) is likewise measured from the origin.
  - failure_scenario: OwnShipProvider auto-datum initializes at the first fix; own-ship transits 20 km (below the 30 km recenter). AIS-equipped target 2 km from own-ship, true gyro bias 2 deg: the 70 m AIS-ARPA displacement subtends only ~0.2 deg at the origin (10x dilution, direction rotated), while sigma_v2 is computed with r_ais ~ 20 km — 10x understated AIS noise. The estimator converges quickly and publishes a bias that is a geometry-dependent fraction of the truth (possibly wrong-signed in component), which the adapters then subtract from every ARPA/EO-IR bearing. Every in-repo sim places own-ship at or within a few hundred meters of the datum origin (test_bus_anchor_loss.cpp: own-ship stationary at the origin), so no test sees it.
  - evidence: core/bias/AisArpaPairExtractor.cpp:48; core/bias/HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:41-62 (ais_rel/arpa_rel/r_ais/r_arpa all relative to obs.own_position_enu); adapters/arpa/ArpaAdapter.cpp:109-110 (own_xy computed) vs 140-148 (m.sensor_position_std_m set, m.sensor_position_enu not set) and 77-86 (TLL never consults own pose); core/types/Measurement.hpp:67-71 (contract); core/types/Track.hpp:88 (zero default).
  - suggested_fix: Set m.sensor_position_enu = own_xy in ArpaAdapter's TTM branch (and resolve own pose for TLL); defensively, extractPairs could refuse pairs whose ARPA touch carries a zero sensor position while own_position_std_m > 0, or the estimator could gate on r_ais vs r_arpa consistency. Add a sim test with own-ship displaced several km from the datum.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full failing path. (1) adapters/arpa/ArpaAdapter.cpp: the TTM branch computes own_xy (line 110) and uses it only inside projectRangeBearingToEnu (Projection.cpp adds own position into the absolute ENU target point), sets m.sensor_position_std_m at line 148 but never m.sensor_position_enu; the TLL branch (lines 65-87) never consults own pose. The field therefore stays at Vector2d::Zero() (Measurement.hpp:71), violating the documented contract at Measurement.hpp:67-70. (2) Tracker.cpp:157 / MhtTracker.cpp:647 / PmbmTracker.cpp:1684 copy z.sensor_position_enu into the SourceTouch; AisArpaPairExtractor.cpp:48 sets obs.own_position_enu = arpa->sensor_position_enu = (0,0); HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:41-62 computes beta_truth, beta_arpa, r_ais (drives sigma_v2 = sigma_ais^2/r_ais^2), and r_arpa (GPS floor) all relative to that zero point. The AisArpaPairObservation doc (HeadingBiasEstimator.hpp:44-49) explicitly requires positions "relative to the same own-ship origin". (3) Hand-executed the numbers: own-ship 20 km from datum, target 2 km away, true bias 2 deg gives a ~70 m AIS-ARPA displacement that subtends 2 deg at own-ship but only ~0.02 deg (geometry-rotated, possibly sign-flipped) at the datum origin, while sigma_v2 is computed with r_ais ~ 20.1 km instead of 2 km (~100x variance understatement); the scalar KF converges confidently to a wrong bias, publishes it, and ArpaAdapter.cpp:119 subtracts it from every subsequent ARPA bearing (EO-IR likewise via bias_provider). The cold-start-exempt outlier gate does not reject the self-consistent diluted observations. (4) This is the documented consumer path: docs/integration-guide.md section 5 (~lines 588-610) wires NMEA ArpaAdapter -> tracker -> extractPairs -> observe -> bias_provider back into ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter, with no own-ship-at-datum caveat. (5) No test contradicts the finding: every test exercising this loop (test_bus_bias_estimator_sweep.cpp:139-141 and 270-272, test_bus_anchor_loss.cpp:101-103, BusComparisonHelpers.hpp:81-83) places own-ship stationary at Vector2d::Zero() — exactly the datum origin, the one geometry where the zero default is accidentally correct. (6) The omission is a bug, not a convention: PlotCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:116/176, AutoferryJsonReplay.cpp:276/296, CameraBearingCsvReader.cpp:103, and MeasurementBuilders.cpp:82 all populate sensor_position_enu. Secondary claim about SensorBiasPairExtractor.cpp:72/108 (position/bearing mounting-bias pairs also inheriting the zero own position from these adapters) also verified. I could find no guard, fix-up after poll(), or documented assumption that refutes any part of the claim.
  - verifier corrected details: Confirmed as claimed. The NMEA ArpaAdapter (both TTM and TLL) never populates Measurement::sensor_position_enu, so the documented v1 heading-bias wiring (integration-guide section 5: ArpaAdapter -> Tracker SourceTouch -> extractPairs -> HeadingBiasEstimator::observe) computes both AIS and ARPA bearings, the r_ais-driven measurement noise, and the r_arpa GPS floor about the DATUM ORIGIN instead of own-ship. When own-ship is displaced from the datum (routine with the auto-datum OwnShipProvider, up to 30 km before recenter), the bias-induced angular disagreement is diluted by roughly r_ownship-to-target / r_origin-to-target and geometry-rotated, while the assumed observation noise is understated by the same ratio; the estimator converges confidently to a wrong bias that is then subtracted from every ARPA and EO-IR bearing (ArpaAdapter.cpp:119, EoIrAdapter via the same IHeadingBiasProvider). All in-repo tests of this loop place own-ship stationary at the origin, masking the defect. Severity high (not critical): only consumers using the navtracker_nmea ArpaAdapter with the v1 AIS-ARPA bias source are affected; the canonical makeMeasurementFromRelativeBearing builder path (MeasurementBuilders.cpp:82) and all replay adapters set the field correctly. Fix is one line in each ArpaAdapter branch (m.sensor_position_enu = own_xy; TLL additionally needs an own-pose lookup) plus a moving-own-ship regression test; the SensorBiasPairExtractor min-range/bearing-pair paths inherit the same fix.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Cross-sensor Schmidt fold debiases the anchor touch a second time when the tracker already applied the published bias
  - `core/bias/SensorBiasPairExtractor.cpp:259` (feedback-loop, confidence high)
  - description: extractCrossSensorPositionPairs sets obs.z_anchor_enu = best_y->value_enu - best_b_anchor (line 259), where best_b_anchor is Y's published bias — designed for RAW touches. In the shipped wiring (Sweep.cpp:318 + 334-336: the same SensorBiasEstimator is both the tracker's setSensorBiasProvider and the extractor's bias_provider), Y's touch value was ALREADY debiased by applyBiasCorrection before the touch was recorded (MhtTracker.cpp:242-249+646, Tracker.cpp:136+156), so the anchor is debiased twice: z_anchor ~ truth + b_y_true - 2*b_pub_y ~ truth - b_y once Y has converged. Every observation for the calibrated key X then carries a systematic error equal to Y's bias, and because is_anchor_source = best_anchor_published = true for exactly these pairs, the corrupted X estimate is allowed to publish and shift all of X's measurements. The test CrossSensorAppliesSchmidtFoldFromProvider builds raw touches by hand, so it validates the extractor in isolation and does not exercise the tracker-corrected-touch composition.
  - failure_scenario: Item-13 wiring with two radars and a lidar (no AIS in window): lidar Y has a 3 m east offset, seeded/refined and published; tracker corrects Y's measurements, touches store corrected values; line 259 subtracts the 3 m again, making the anchor read truth - 3 m east. Radar X, perfectly aligned, receives pair residuals r ~ +3 m every cycle (plus its own double-subtract from the sibling finding) and converges to a phantom ~3 m bias flagged anchor-published — X's measurements are then shifted 3 m off truth by applyBiasCorrection.
  - evidence: core/bias/SensorBiasPairExtractor.cpp:230-259 (fold and z_anchor); core/benchmark/Sweep.cpp:318,334-336 (same estimator as provider and observer); core/pipeline/MhtTracker.cpp:242-249,642-649 (touches from corrected scan); tests/bias/test_sensor_bias_estimator.cpp:559 (fold test uses hand-built raw touches).
  - suggested_fix: Resolve together with the raw-vs-corrected touch convention (previous finding): if touches become raw, line 259 is correct as-is; if touches stay corrected, the fold must NOT subtract the published bias again (and R_anchor should still add P_b_Y). Add a two-sensor closed-loop test with one seeded-published sensor asserting the unbiased sensor stays at zero.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** v2 bearing-innovation outlier gate is centered on zero, not on b_hat: a true bias above ~5x bearing sigma starves the observer before it can publish
  - `core/bias/HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:104` (gating, confidence high)
  - description: observe(BearingInnovation) gates on |obs.innovation_rad| > bi_outlier_sigma * sqrt(S + p_b) — the RAW innovation against zero — while the update residual is y = wrap(r - b_hat) (line 109). Since bearing measurements are never heading-corrected on this path, genuine innovations stay r ~ b_true forever. As p_b shrinks from the accepted updates, the acceptance threshold 5*sqrt(S + p_b) tightens toward 5*sqrt(S); for any true bias b_true > ~5*sqrt(S) the gate permanently closes at p_b ~ (b_true/5sigma)^2 - S, which for realistic S is far ABOVE the (0.3 deg)^2 publish threshold — so the estimator absorbs most of the bias, then rejects every subsequent observation, never publishes (or goes stale and unpublishes within stale_seconds), and the correction never engages despite abundant clean data. This matches the spec formula (2026-06-04-multi-track-bearing-bias-observer-design.md §4 G3), but it is exactly the failure the v1 path's gate was reworked to avoid (HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:66-73 review #14 comment: gating against a reference that excludes the estimate 'would reject any genuinely large uncalibrated bias forever'); v1 and applyScalarUpdate both gate on the residual |y|, v2 alone gates on |r|.
  - failure_scenario: v2-only wiring (Tracker::setBearingInnovationSink, AIS-anchored track feeding a raw-bearing camera), uncalibrated installation with 8 deg gyro bias, bearing sigma 1 deg: cold start accepts (threshold 5*sqrt(1+25 deg^2) ~ 25 deg); after enough updates p_b crosses ~1.6 deg^2 and the threshold drops below 8 deg — every further innovation rejected (rej_outlier climbs), last_update freezes, p_b (1.6 deg^2) never reaches the 0.09 deg^2 publish threshold, and with process noise 9.4e-11 rad^2/s the gate stays closed for days. The estimator holds a good ~7.5 deg internal estimate that is never published and never applied. Unit test OutlierGateRejectsHugeInnovation pins single-shot rejection only; no test runs v2 to convergence with a large bias.
  - evidence: core/bias/HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:102-115 (gate on obs.innovation_rad, update on y = r - b_hat); contrast lines 74-78 (v1 gates on |y|, cold-start exempt) and 141-145 (applyScalarUpdate gates on |y|); docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-04-multi-track-bearing-bias-observer-design.md:84 (G3 as coded).
  - suggested_fix: Gate v2 on the residual |wrap(r - b_hat)| <= N*sqrt(S + p_b) (consistent with v1 and the mhs kinds), or keep the zero-centered gate but only until first acceptance (mirror v1's cold-start exemption logic inverted). Update the spec's G3 row with the rationale.

- **[LOW/unverified]** applyBiasCorrection silently skips PositionVelocity2D, so a published position bias is applied to only part of a source's stream
  - `core/pipeline/BiasCorrection.hpp:60` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: The model dispatch handles Position2D, Bearing2D, and RangeBearing2D only. MeasurementModel::PositionVelocity2D is a first-class model (SourceTouchPopulate.hpp:37-44 handles it; remote-track/velocity-carrying feeds emit it), and its value(0..1) is the same ENU position the Position2D branch shifts — but a published position bias for the same SensorBiasKey is never applied to it and its covariance is never inflated by P_b. A source that mixes the two models (velocity present on some reports only) gets a stream whose position alternates by the full bias magnitude. NOTE: overlaps a LOW finding already recorded in docs/reviews/2026-07-09-prerelease-review (10-bughunt-findings.md:228); re-verified here — the dispatch omission is real.
  - failure_scenario: A shore radar feed with a published 40 m registration bias emits PositionVelocity2D when its tracker reports velocity and Position2D otherwise: corrected reports land on truth, uncorrected ones 40 m off, producing 40 m innovation zig-zag on the same track and biased velocity estimates — the opposite of what the published sub-1-m bias covariance claims.
  - evidence: core/pipeline/BiasCorrection.hpp:60-86 (no PositionVelocity2D branch); core/pipeline/SourceTouchPopulate.hpp:37-44 (model exists on this pipeline path); prior-round finding 10-bughunt-findings.md:228.
  - suggested_fix: Add a PositionVelocity2D branch mirroring Position2D (shift value(0..1), add P_b to covariance block<2,2>(0,0)); decide and document that the velocity components carry no bias term.

- **[LOW/unverified]** No R>0 validation / variance floor in the scalar updates: a zero-sigma observation collapses p_b to exactly 0 and locks the filter onto one noisy sample
  - `core/bias/HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:139` (input-validation, confidence high)
  - description: applyScalarUpdate (and the v1 path via sigma_v2) accepts R = 0: s = p_b, k = 1, b_hat snaps exactly to the measurement and p_b becomes exactly 0. All three v3 observation structs default their sigma fields to 0.0 (HeadingBiasObservations.hpp:20,36,53), so a consumer constructing GyroVsGpsHeadingObservation directly (the guide's 'wire any subset' contract) and forgetting the std gets this by default. After the collapse, sigma = sqrt(q*dt) is ~2e-5 rad per second of elapsed time, so every subsequent genuine observation (noise ~0.5 deg) fails the 5-sigma outlier gate; last_update freezes, the estimator publishes a single-sample bias for stale_seconds and then unpublishes, permanently locked (p_b regrows at 9.4e-11 rad^2/s — ~days to reopen the gate). The in-repo OwnShipNmeaAdapter populates the sigmas from config, so only direct constructors hit it — but these structs are the documented consumer surface and no entry point validates R.
  - failure_scenario: Consumer feeds gyro-vs-GPS-heading observations at 1 Hz without setting gps_true_heading_std_rad: at t=0 the estimator publishes bias = (first sample's noise + bias) with variance 0; for the next 30 s adapters subtract that noisy value; at t=30 it unpublishes; rej_mhs_outlier climbs by one per second forever; no error is ever surfaced.
  - evidence: core/bias/HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:135-150 (no R>0 check; k = p_b/s with s = R + p_b); core/bias/HeadingBiasObservations.hpp:20,36,53 (0.0 sigma defaults); adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:235,260,317 (adapter path sets sigmas from config).
  - suggested_fix: Reject (or floor) observations with non-positive R at each observe() entry point, and/or give the sigma fields non-zero defaults; optionally add a small floor to p_b after update (the estimator currently relies solely on process noise).

- **[LOW/unverified]** Staleness un-publish never triggers unless the consumer keeps calling predictTo: 'now' is last_predict_, which freezes on anchor loss
  - `core/bias/HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:127` (staleness-contract, confidence medium)
  - description: current() computes age_s = deltaSeconds(last_predict_, last_update_). last_predict_ only advances inside observe(...) or an explicit predictTo() call. In a v1-only wiring (guide §5 shows extractPairs -> observe and never mentions predictTo), an AIS dropout stops all observe() calls, so last_predict_ freezes together with last_update_, age stays ~0, and is_published remains true indefinitely with an aging bias — the exact scenario stale_seconds (30 s default) exists to catch. The in-repo closed-loop tests pass only because they explicitly call estimator.predictTo(tick) every truth tick (test_bus_anchor_loss.cpp:200, BusComparisonHelpers.hpp:558); a consumer following the guide gets no such cadence. Wirings that include v3 own-ship observations are immune (each own-ship fix calls predictTo internally), which is why I rate this medium confidence / low severity: it requires a v1-only (or v1+v2-only) wiring plus total source loss.
  - failure_scenario: Consumer wires only the AIS<->ARPA pair path per guide §5. AIS transponder traffic ceases at t=60 s (dropout, jamming, open sea); no observe() calls follow; at t=600 s current().is_published is still true and adapters keep applying the last bias with its frozen 'converged' variance, despite the documented 30 s staleness contract (test_bus_anchor_loss asserts unpublish by t=90 s, but only with external predictTo ticks).
  - evidence: core/bias/HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:118-130 (age from last_predict_); tests/sim/test_bus_anchor_loss.cpp:200 (explicit per-tick predictTo keeps the contract alive); docs/integration-guide.md §5 (wiring shown without any periodic predictTo).
  - suggested_fix: Either document predictTo(now) as a REQUIRED periodic call for the staleness contract (guide + header), or let adapters/tracker drive time into the estimator (e.g. predictTo from each queried current() caller that knows the current data time).

- **[LOW/unverified]** Bearing-bias sign convention documented backwards on the port: 'added to a camera's reported bearing' vs code that subtracts
  - `core/pipeline/BiasCorrection.hpp:72` (doc-contract, confidence high)
  - description: applyBiasCorrection subtracts the published bearing bias (out.value(0) -= bb.bias_rad, line 72; RangeBearing2D line 81), consistent with the estimator's model observed = true + b (SensorBiasEstimator.cpp:142-143: alpha_pred = atan2 + b_hat). But the port struct's doc says the opposite: ports/ISensorBiasProvider.hpp:44 — 'Bearing-bias snapshot (added to a camera's reported bearing, rad)'. A consumer hand-seeding FixedSensorBiasProvider::setBearingBias from an offline calibration and following the port comment will negate the sign, and applyBiasCorrection will then double the camera's bearing error instead of cancelling it. Sign errors here are exactly the 'worse than no correction' hazard: the corrupted bearing feeds association and the track position directly.
  - failure_scenario: Camera reads 2 deg high. Consumer reads the port doc, reasons 'the stored value is added to the reported bearing to correct it' and stores bias_rad = -2 deg via FixedSensorBiasProvider (a documented deployment path, ISensorBiasProvider.hpp:94-106). applyBiasCorrection computes beta - (-2 deg) = beta + 2 deg: every camera bearing is now 4 deg off, silently, with a tight claimed variance (default 1e-8).
  - evidence: core/pipeline/BiasCorrection.hpp:69-85 (subtraction, both Bearing2D and RangeBearing2D); ports/ISensorBiasProvider.hpp:44-49 ('added to'); core/bias/SensorBiasEstimator.cpp:142-143 (estimator convention: measured = true + b, so correction must subtract).
  - suggested_fix: Fix the port comment to state the convention explicitly ('b is the offset the sensor ADDS to truth; applyBiasCorrection subtracts it') and add the same sentence to FixedSensorBiasProvider::setBearingBias and the integration guide's config table row.

Coverage notes (bias): Scope read end-to-end: core/bias/{HeadingBiasEstimator.{hpp,cpp}, HeadingBiasObservations.hpp, AisArpaPairExtractor.{hpp,cpp}, SensorBiasEstimator.{hpp,cpp}, SensorBiasPairExtractor.{hpp,cpp}}, core/pipeline/BiasCorrection.hpp; cross-read for wiring/consumers: Tracker.{hpp,cpp}, MhtTracker.cpp (touch + correction sections), SourceTouchPopulate.hpp, Measurement.hpp, Track.hpp (SourceTouch), MeasurementBuilders.cpp (sensor_position_enu), ports/{IBearingInnovationSink, IHeadingBiasProvider, ISensorBiasProvider}.hpp, adapters/{arpa,eoir,own_ship} bias paths, core/benchmark/Sweep.cpp bias wiring, integration-guide §5, specs 2026-06-03/04/13, all tests in tests/bias plus tests/sim/{BusComparisonHelpers.hpp, test_bus_anchor_loss.cpp, test_bus_bias_estimator_sweep.cpp} and tests/pipeline/test_bias_correction_orthogonality.cpp. Checked CLEAN: (1) angle wrapping — every accepted update wraps its residual before applying (v1 wraps z and y; v2 wraps y; mhs kinds wrap measurement and residual; SensorBias bearing wraps r); downstream EKF residuals wrap bearings (MeasurementModels.cpp:94-96) so the un-rewrapped Bearing2D value after applyBiasCorrection is harmless. (2) Sign convention measured = true + b is consistent across all five heading observation kinds, both SensorBias observation types, and the subtraction in applyBiasCorrection (only the port DOC string contradicts — reported). (3) Random-walk q scaled linearly by dt in both estimators, per-key in SensorBiasEstimator; dt<=0 and out-of-order predicts are no-ops; nanos==0 first-call sentinel is benign even for t=0 streams. (4) Eigen usage: P=(I-K)*P products evaluate into temporaries (no aliasing bug); block<2,2> accesses guarded by rows/cols checks; JPDA weight scaling in Tracker's emitter preserves the G2 ratio as intended; G2's R<=0 harmless-reject documented and correct. (5) NaN containment: SensorBias S.inverse() can go NaN only via caller-misuse zero R at repeated timestamps (extractors always fill R via covWithFallback; P stays PD when R is PSD since P0=25I), and a NaN state can never publish (NaN comparisons fail the publish gates). (6) Cross-sensor extractor determinism (std::map emission order) verified; same-source_id exclusion and one-obs-per-key correlation reasoning are sound. Borderline items NOT reported as findings: AisArpaPairExtractor pairs the OLDEST in-window AIS and ARPA touches (not nearest-in-time), leaving an unmodeled time-misalignment bearing error v_t*dt/r (~1.5 deg with the 1.5 s window used by the anchor-loss test at 12 m/s / 700 m) absent from sigma_v2; Track::SourceTouch.covariance defaults to Identity so a never-populated covariance reads as sigma=1 m instead of triggering the 10 m fallback in sigmaFromCov2D/covWithFallback (reachable only if an empty-covariance measurement survives update); current() can spuriously unpublish if an accepted observation is older than last_predict_ (last_update_ rewinds); wrapToPi boundary conventions differ between the two files ((-pi,pi] vs [-pi,pi]) — immaterial for scalar residuals; v1 path has no bi_min_range_m gate but is self-limited by sigma_v2 growth at short range. Known/by-design items excluded per instructions. Adjacent prior-round findings (PMBM spurious SourceTouches polluting these extractors — B2; RangeBearing2D initiate — B1) were confirmed as distinct and not re-reported; the PositionVelocity2D applyBiasCorrection skip overlaps a prior LOW/unverified entry and is marked as such. Main caveat on the three high findings: they are composition defects (estimator + extractor + tracker/adapter correction all individually defensible; the loop is what is wrong), so the fix owner is a design decision — raw-vs-corrected SourceTouch convention must be picked once and enforced.

NOTE: B3v supersedes section B3 (same findings + verdicts)

## Batch B4-collision-static-adapters

### unit: collision-output (6 findings)

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** position_covariance_m2 is emitted (east,north)-ordered while the contract promises NED (row 0 = north) — axes silently swapped for consumers
  - `core/output/TrackOutput.cpp:21` (contract-mismatch, confidence high)
  - description: toGeodeticWithCov computes out.position_covariance_m2 = R * cov_enu_m2 * R.transpose() where R = geo::datumAxisRotation(...) is a pure 2D meridian-convergence rotation between ENU frames (AxisRotation.cpp builds [[c,-s],[s,c]]). There is no east/north axis permutation anywhere on the path, so the matrix stays (east,north)-ordered exactly like the input ENU covariance. But the consumer contract says otherwise in three places: TrackOutput.hpp:27 comments 'local NED at target, m²'; docs/output-contract.md line 8 states 'row/column 0 = north, row/column 1 = east'; and line 9 tells consumers to extract sigma_north = sqrt(cov[0,0]). The only test that touches ordering (tests/output/test_track_output.cpp CovarianceRotatedAtHighLatitude, lines 129-134) compares against the same swap-free formula R*cov_enu*R^T, i.e. it pins the (east,north)-ordered code behavior and never asserts which index is north; the doc's worked example uses an isotropic 25/25 covariance, which cannot expose the swap. So code and doc contradict each other and nothing arbitrates.
  - failure_scenario: Radar-only track due north of own-ship with down-range sigma = 10 m and cross-range sigma = 100 m: the ENU covariance is diag(10000, 100) (east variance first). A consumer following docs/output-contract.md reads sigma_north = sqrt(cov[0,0]) = 100 m and sigma_east = 10 m — physically the opposite of the truth. Any downstream fusion, alarm-gating, or display-ellipse code consuming the documented NED layout gets a 90-degree-rotated error ellipse for every anisotropic track; the error is silent because magnitudes are plausible.
  - evidence: TrackOutput.cpp:9-23 (no axis swap); core/geo/AxisRotation.cpp:19-21 (pure rotation matrix); TrackOutput.hpp:24-28 and docs/output-contract.md:8-9 (NED north-first claim); tests/output/test_track_output.cpp:129-141 (test expected value computed with identical swap-free formula, so it cannot catch the discrepancy).
  - suggested_fix: Decide the contract: either apply the permutation P=[[0,1],[1,0]] (cov_ned = P*R*cov_enu*R^T*P^T) in toGeodeticWithCov, or fix TrackOutput.hpp + docs/output-contract.md to say the matrix is (east,north)-ordered. Add an anisotropic test (distinct sigma_e/sigma_n) asserting which index is north.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full path. (1) Internal ordering is (east, north): core/geo/Datum.cpp:20 builds ecef_to_enu_ with the east unit vector (-sin lon, cos lon, 0) as row 0, so state/covariance index 0 = east; cross-confirmed by toVelocityOutput's cog = atan2(v.x(), v.y()) (TrackOutput.cpp:38) giving COG=90° (east) for x-only velocity, and by in-test comments labeling cov(0,0) as "east variance". (2) TrackOutput.cpp:21 applies only R*cov*R^T where R (AxisRotation.cpp:19-21) is a pure rotation by the meridian-convergence angle gamma (<0.5 deg within the 30 km horizon); no permutation exists anywhere on the path, so output index 0 remains east. Hand-executed the scenario: target due north (delta_lon=0 so R=I exactly), radar down-range sigma 10 m / cross-range 100 m gives cov_enu=diag(10000,100); output is diag(10000,100); a consumer following docs/output-contract.md:9 reads sigma_north = sqrt(cov[0,0]) = 100 m when the true north sigma is 10 m — axes silently swapped. (3) The contract promises north-first in TrackOutput.hpp:17-27, docs/output-contract.md:8-9, app/example.cpp:144, docs/integration-guide.md:123, and the Option A design spec ("sigma_north reads cleanly", "target's local NED"); NED ordering is unambiguously north-first, so the code is missing the E/N permutation (correct would be P*R*cov*R^T*P^T). (4) The only ordering-sensitive test (tests/output/test_track_output.cpp:129-141) computes its expected value with the identical swap-free formula, so it pins the buggy behavior and cannot arbitrate; the doc worked example is isotropic. (5) Additional evidence beyond the original claim: the in-repo Foxglove adapter (adapters/foxglove/FoxgloveDebugRecorder.cpp:119-122 and 256-259) implements the documented convention (maps LocationFix NN field from matrix(0,0), EE from (1,1), with explicit "NED (0=north,1=east)" comments), so a real in-tree consumer already renders 90-degree-rotated error ellipses for every anisotropic track. No guard, caller-side swap, test, or documented decision reconciles the contradiction.
  - verifier corrected details: Everything in the original claim checks out, with one strengthening addition: the defect is not only latent for external consumers of the documented contract — adapters/foxglove/FoxgloveDebugRecorder.cpp (lines 119-122, 256-259) already implements the documented north-first NED indexing against the actually east-first matrix, so the in-repo debug visualization swaps the uncertainty-ellipse axes for every anisotropic covariance today. The fix is either an E/N permutation in toGeodeticWithCov (making output truly NED, matching TrackOutput.hpp:27, output-contract.md:8-9, example.cpp:144, integration-guide.md:123, and the Foxglove adapter) or correcting all five documentation/consumer sites to (east, north) ordering; the design spec's Option A rationale indicates NED/north-first was the intent. High (not critical): silent 90-degree ellipse rotation for all anisotropic tracks corrupts downstream fusion/gating/display that follows the contract, but internal tracker state, lat/lon, SOG/COG, and track identity are unaffected, and isotropic covariances are unharmed.

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** Sign error in the tcpa Jacobian chain term: sigma_tcpa_seconds is wrong for every converging pair, and sigma_cpa/probability are wrong in the near-zero-CPA (head-on) fallback
  - `core/collision/Cpa.cpp:135` (math-sign-error, confidence high)
  - description: For t_cpa = -(dp.dv)/(dv.dv), the correct gradient is dt/dx = [-(dv^T dDp + dp^T dDv) - 2*t_cpa*(dv^T dDv)] / |dv|^2. Cpa.cpp:135-137 computes chain = +2.0*t_cpa*(dv^T*dDv_dx) and adds it, flipping the sign of the chain term. The upstream spec (docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-03-cpa-uncertainty-design.md, section 4.3, lines 94-96) contains the same '+ 2 t_cpa ...' sign error, so the code faithfully implements a wrong formula. Verified by central finite differences (scratchpad script): for a converging geometry (target 900 m away, t_cpa=91.7 s), max |J_code - J_fd| = 35.85 while max |J_corrected - J_fd| = 2.4e-8. Downstream effects: (a) var_tcpa = J_tcpa*Sigma*J_tcpa^T (line 144) is wrong whenever velocity covariance is nonzero — in the example, published sigma_tcpa = 30.4 s vs correct 10.5 s (~3x); (b) J_p_cpa (line 140) inherits the error through dv*J_tcpa, but the direction-projected sigma_cpa (lines 150-154) is protected because p_cpa is orthogonal to dv at CPA, which annihilates the erroneous term (verified: both give 104.2566695...) — this is exactly why all existing sigma_cpa tests pass; (c) the isotropic fallback for cpa < kEpsCpa = 1 m (line 156) uses the full trace of cov_p_cpa where the error does NOT cancel: 299.3 m vs correct 74.8 m in the example, corrupting sigma_cpa_m and probability_below_threshold for true head-on near-collision geometry. Tests do not pin this: ZeroCovGivesZeroSigma has zero covariance, ParallelVelocities/PastCpa hit the infinity sentinel branch, and HeadOnNearZeroCpaUsesIsotropicFallback uses sigma_vel=0 so the erroneous term (which lives only in the velocity columns) vanishes.
  - failure_scenario: Own-ship (sigma_pos 5 m, sigma_v 0.5 m/s) vs a converging AIS/radar track (sigma_pos 10 m, sigma_v 1 m/s) 900 m away: every CollisionRiskEvent payload carries sigma_tcpa_seconds ~3x too large (30.4 s instead of 10.5 s), corrupting any consumer that uses TCPA confidence for maneuver timing. In an imminent head-on (mean CPA < 1 m — the most safety-critical geometry), sigma_cpa_m is ~4x too large (299 m vs 75 m) and probability_below_threshold at d=500 m drops from ~1.0 to 0.95.
  - evidence: Cpa.cpp:133-137 (chain = +2.0*t_cpa*(dv^T*dDv_dx)); analytic derivation d(-N/D) = (-dN - 2t*dv^T*dDv)/D; finite-difference verification script output: 'max |J_code - J_fd| = 35.85', 'sigma_tcpa code = 30.36 vs correct 10.46', 'isotropic fallback code = 299.33 vs correct 74.83', 'sigma_cpa proj code = correct to 1e-8 (orthogonality)'. Spec section 4.3 carries the identical sign error.
  - suggested_fix: Change line 135-136 to chain = -2.0 * t_cpa * (dv.transpose() * dDv_dx) (equivalently J_tcpa = (num - chain)/dv2), fix spec section 4.3, and add a finite-difference regression test with nonzero velocity covariance pinning sigma_tcpa and the isotropic-fallback sigma_cpa.
  - verifier: Independently re-derived the gradient: for t_cpa = -N/D (N = dp.dv, D = dv.dv), dt/dx = (-dN - 2*t_cpa*(dv^T dDv))/D; the chain term must be subtracted. Cpa.cpp:135-137 computes chain = +2.0*t_cpa*(dv.transpose()*dDv_dx) and adds it — sign flipped. The spec docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-03-cpa-uncertainty-design.md §4.3 contains the same '+ 2 t_cpa' error, so code matches spec but spec is mathematically wrong (verified by quotient rule and by central finite differences in an independent script: max |J_code - J_fd| = 43.9 vs |J_corrected - J_fd| = 1e-9 on a converging geometry with t_cpa=100 s). Downstream effects verified numerically: (a) sigma_tcpa_seconds ~3x inflated (37.06 s vs correct 12.41 s) whenever velocity covariance is nonzero — always true for real KF tracks; (b) projected sigma_cpa (Cpa.cpp:150-154) is exactly protected because p_cpa.dv = 0 at CPA annihilates the dv*J_tcpa term (both versions give 113.0456524003786 — byte-identical), which is precisely why all existing tests pass; (c) the isotropic fallback for cpa < 1 m (Cpa.cpp:156) uses the full trace where the error does NOT cancel: sigma_cpa 326.1 vs correct 79.5 in my head-on example, and probability_below_threshold(d=500) drops from ~1.0 to 0.937 — this value feeds CpaEvaluator.cpp:34's enter/exit hysteresis. Test audit confirms no pin: every test in tests/collision/test_cpa_uncertainty.cpp uses sigma_vel = 0 (makeTrack default), and the erroneous term lives only in the velocity columns of the Jacobian (dDv_dx is zero in position columns), so zero velocity covariance makes it invisible; ParallelVelocities/PastCpa hit the branch-A infinity sentinel and never reach line 135. No guard or caller mitigates: computeCpaWithUncertainty's outputs go straight into CpaPrediction/CollisionRiskEvent payloads. Not a documented decision — it is an unnoticed math error replicated from spec to code.
  - verifier corrected details: core/collision/Cpa.cpp:135-137: the tcpa-Jacobian chain term 2*t_cpa*(dv^T * dDv_dx) is added when it must be subtracted (correct: J_tcpa = (-(dv^T dDp + dp^T dDv) - 2*t_cpa*(dv^T dDv))/|dv|^2). The upstream spec §4.3 (docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-03-cpa-uncertainty-design.md) carries the identical sign error and must be fixed too. Impact: (1) sigma_tcpa_seconds is wrong for every converging pair with nonzero velocity covariance (i.e., all real tracks) — ~3x inflated in realistic covariance regimes (FD-verified: 37.06 s published vs 12.41 s correct); (2) sigma_cpa_m and probability_below_threshold are corrupted in the near-zero-CPA (cpa < kEpsCpa = 1 m) isotropic fallback — the imminent head-on geometry — e.g. 326 m vs 79 m, P(d<500 m) 0.937 vs ~1.0, which feeds CpaEvaluator's enter/exit probability hysteresis and can delay an Entered risk event under a high enter_probability threshold; (3) the direction-projected sigma_cpa path (cpa > 1 m) is exactly immune because p_cpa is orthogonal to dv at CPA, which is why all existing tests (all with sigma_vel = 0) pass. Severity high, not critical: the primary risk-probability path is protected in all cpa > 1 m geometries and the error direction is conservative (inflated uncertainty), but a contract output field is wrong in essentially every event and the fallback corruption coincides with the most safety-critical geometry. Fix is a one-character sign change at Cpa.cpp:135 plus the spec correction and a new test with nonzero velocity covariance (FD-pinned sigma_tcpa, plus a head-on fallback case with sigma_vel > 0).

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Meridian-convergence rotation applied in the transposed (wrong) direction — output covariance frame is 2*gamma off target-local and its induced off-diagonal has flipped sign
  - `core/output/TrackOutput.cpp:17` (math-sign-error, confidence high)
  - description: datumAxisRotation(old,new) (core/geo/AxisRotation.cpp:11-23) returns R(gamma) with gamma = (new_lon - old_lon)*sin(mean_lat), and toGeodeticWithCov applies it as cov_out = R*cov_enu*R^T, i.e. the convention v_target = R*v_datum. Independent WGS84 verification (ECEF->ENU, datum 60N/0E, target 60N/1E): a true-north displacement at the target has datum-ENU components (-1.68, 111.40); mapping to target-local components requires R^T (R^T*v gives (1.3e-5, 111.41)) while the code's R gives (-3.37, ...) — double the convergence error. So the correct datum->target-local map is R(-gamma) and the code rotates the covariance the wrong way: the emitted matrix is expressed in a frame rotated 2*gamma away from the target's local frame, and the off-diagonal it introduces for anisotropic input has the wrong sign, e.g. +(sigma_e^2-sigma_n^2)*sin(g)*cos(g) instead of -(...). The CovarianceRotatedAtHighLatitude test (test_track_output.cpp:126-141) computes its expected value with the same wrong-direction formula and even asserts the flipped-sign off-diagonal (expected_off = +99*s*c), so it pins the bug rather than catching it. Magnitude is bounded (gamma < 0.5 deg inside the 30 km auto-recenter envelope, so ~1 deg frame error), which is why it is medium not high. Note for synthesis: core/tracking/DatumShift.cpp uses the same helper with the same v_new = R*v_old convention for velocity/covariance rotation on datum recenter (out of this unit's scope), so it rotates velocities by +gamma instead of -gamma per recenter.
  - failure_scenario: Track 55 km east of the datum at 60N with ENU covariance diag(100,1): the emitted covariance's off-diagonal is +1.496 m^2 where the true target-local value is -1.496 m^2, and the error-ellipse orientation is off by 2*gamma ~ 1.7 deg; a consumer combining the reported correlation with other data applies the tilt in the wrong direction.
  - evidence: AxisRotation.cpp:15-21; TrackOutput.cpp:17-21; scratchpad WGS84 check: 'R_code @ v_datum: (-3.37, 111.36)' vs 'R_code.T @ v_datum: (1.3e-5, 111.41)' for a true-north displacement at the target; test expected value built from the identical formula so no test contradicts.
  - suggested_fix: Negate gamma in datumAxisRotation (or use R.transpose() at the call sites) so that v_new = R*v_old maps old-datum components to new/target-local components; audit DatumShift with the same ground-truth geodesy test (true-north displacement at target must map to (0,+d)).

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** CPA uses the latest own-ship fix position without extrapolating it from pose.time to t, while target tracks ARE extrapolated — stale GPS silently shifts the whole CPA geometry
  - `core/collision/CpaOwnShip.cpp:10` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: CpaEvaluator::evaluate(t) (CpaEvaluator.cpp:18-20) takes provider_.latest() and calls synthesizeOwnShipTrack(*pose, t, provider_), which stamps tr.last_update = t (CpaOwnShip.cpp:10) around the pose's raw lat/lon. computeCpa/computeCpaWithUncertainty then compute dt_a = t - last_update = 0, so own-ship is treated as being AT the last fix position at time t, while the target track is properly extrapolated from its own last_update to t (Cpa.cpp:24-29). pose.time is entirely ignored, even though the pose carries a valid velocity that could extrapolate it. The result is an own-ship position error of |v_own| * (t - pose.time) meters injected directly into dp, hence into cpa_distance_m, tcpa, and probability_below_threshold. The NavInputGuard (#18) flags stale nav gaps but by design never rewrites data, so nothing downstream compensates. Tests only ever call evaluate() at t == pose.time (test_cpa_evaluator.cpp uses makePoseAtDatum(0.0,...) then evaluate(0.0/0.01/0.02) with 5 m/s, max 10 cm error), so the inconsistency is never exercised.
  - failure_scenario: Own-ship at 8 m/s, GPS quiet for 60 s (receiver reboot / antenna shadowing) while radar keeps updating targets: evaluate(t) computes CPA with own-ship frozen 480 m behind its true position. With d_threshold_m = 500 m, a target actually passing 150 m abeam can evaluate as no-risk (missed Entered), or a safe target as high-risk (false alarm). Even in nominal 1 Hz GPS operation there is a systematic up-to-1 s position lag on the own-ship side of every CPA pair that does not exist on the target side.
  - evidence: CpaEvaluator.cpp:18-20 (latest() + t passed through); CpaOwnShip.cpp:10-15 (last_update = t, position straight from pose lat/lon, pose.time unused); Cpa.cpp:24-29 (targets extrapolated by t - last_update); header CpaOwnShip.hpp documents fields but never justifies ignoring pose.time.
  - suggested_fix: In synthesizeOwnShipTrack, set tr.last_update = pose.time (letting computeCpa extrapolate own-ship with velocity_enu exactly like targets), or extrapolate the ENU position by velocity_enu * (t - pose.time) when velocity_is_valid; add a test with a deliberately stale pose.
