- **[LOW/unverified]** Index-keyed hysteresis state breaks with mutable IStaticObstacleModel implementations (LiveOccupancyModel), and the code's own prescribed mitigation ('clearing inside_') has no API
  - `core/collision/StaticHazardEvaluator.hpp:57` (robustness, confidence high)
  - description: StaticHazardEvaluator keys enter/exit hysteresis by obstacle list index (inside_ map, StaticHazardEvaluator.hpp:57; used at .cpp:28-49). The comment at StaticHazardEvaluator.cpp:19-27 states the precondition (stable-indexed obstacles() for the evaluator's lifetime) and says a mutating model 'must not be paired with this evaluator without clearing inside_' — but inside_ is private and the class exposes no clear/reset method, so the documented mitigation is impossible. Meanwhile LiveOccupancyModel is an in-repo IStaticObstacleModel whose obstacles_ vector is cleared and rebuilt on every occupancy update (LiveOccupancyModel.cpp:349 obstacles_.clear(), :384 push_back), and the port's own docstring advertises obstacles() as feeding 'the hazard output + proximity alarm' (ports/IStaticObstacleModel.hpp:30) — the proximity alarm IS this evaluator. No in-repo wiring pairs them today (the integration guide section 6/7 only shows StaticObstacleModel), which is why this is low, but the interface actively invites the pairing. Two concrete corruptions when paired: (1) index reuse transfers one structure's inside=true to a physically different structure after a rebuild (missed Entered / spurious behavior); (2) when the list shrinks while own-ship is inside obstacle i, the stale inside_[i]=true entry persists forever — no Exited is ever emitted for the vanished hazard, and the stale true suppresses the Entered of whatever obstacle later occupies index i.
  - failure_scenario: Consumer wires LiveOccupancyModel (already implementing IStaticObstacleModel for PMBM birth suppression) into StaticHazardEvaluator for live keep-clear alerts, per the port docstring. Own-ship sits inside live structure S1 (index 3, inside_=true). The next occupancy update evicts S1 and rebuilds the vector so index 3 is now structure S2 two km away: no Exited fires for S1, and when own-ship later approaches S2 no Entered fires because inside_[3] is already true.
  - evidence: StaticHazardEvaluator.hpp:40-57 (public API: ctor/setSink/evaluate only — no reset); StaticHazardEvaluator.cpp:19-35,49; LiveOccupancyModel.hpp:160,175-176 (implements IStaticObstacleModel, returns obstacles_); LiveOccupancyModel.cpp:349/384 (list rebuilt at runtime); ports/IStaticObstacleModel.hpp:30 ('for the hazard output + proximity alarm').
  - suggested_fix: Add a public reset()/clear method (making the comment's mitigation possible), or key hysteresis on hazard_id with an explicit tie-break for colocated records, and state the stable-index requirement in the integration guide next to the StaticHazardEvaluator entry.

- **[LOW/unverified]** CpaEvaluator calls computeCpaWithUncertainty on every eligible track without checking state/covariance dimensions — a 2D-state track causes out-of-bounds Eigen access
  - `core/collision/CpaEvaluator.cpp:33` (robustness, confidence high)
  - description: computeCpaWithUncertainty unconditionally reads b.state(2), b.state(3) (Cpa.cpp:68) and b.covariance.topLeftCorner<4,4>() (Cpa.cpp:78). Cpa.hpp documents 'state.size() >= 4 for both tracks' as an assumption, but CpaEvaluator::evaluate walks all Confirmed/Coasting tracks from TrackManager (CpaEvaluator.cpp:24-33) with no dimension guard. TrackManager::add is a public consumer API accepting any Track, and 2D-state tracks are explicitly considered possible elsewhere in the same output layer: toTrackOutput (TrackOutput.cpp:84-93) defends against state.size() < 4 and covariance smaller than 4x4, and tests/output/test_track_output.cpp TrackOutputFor2DTrackHasInvalidVelocity pins that path. A default-constructed Track even has an EMPTY (0x0) covariance, for which topLeftCorner<4,4> is an Eigen assertion failure in debug and out-of-bounds reads in release. So one drain path (TrackOutput) treats 2D tracks as legal input while the other (CpaEvaluator) crashes on them.
  - failure_scenario: A consumer maintains position-only tracks (e.g. a chart-corroborated static vessel from an external source) via TrackManager::add with state.size()==2, confirms them, and wires CpaEvaluator: the first evaluate(t) call executes b.state(2) on a 2-element vector — assertion abort in debug builds, undefined out-of-bounds read (garbage velocity in the CPA math) in release builds.
  - evidence: CpaEvaluator.cpp:24-33 (no size check before computeCpaWithUncertainty); Cpa.cpp:68/78 (unchecked state(2..3) and topLeftCorner<4,4>); TrackOutput.cpp:84-93 (parallel drain path defends against exactly this input); Track.hpp:51-52 (state is dynamically sized, default empty).
  - suggested_fix: In CpaEvaluator::evaluate, skip (or treat as zero-velocity with inflated covariance) tracks with state.size() < 4 or covariance smaller than 4x4, mirroring toTrackOutput's guard.

Coverage notes (collision-output): Scope read end-to-end: core/collision/{Cpa.hpp,Cpa.cpp,CpaEvaluator.hpp,CpaEvaluator.cpp,CpaOwnShip.hpp,CpaOwnShip.cpp,StaticHazardEvaluator.hpp,StaticHazardEvaluator.cpp}, core/output/{TrackOutput.hpp,TrackOutput.cpp,StaticHazardOutput.hpp,StaticHazardOutput.cpp,BearingWedgeOutput.hpp,BearingWedgeOutput.cpp}; supporting reads: core/geo/AxisRotation.*, core/tracking/DatumShift.cpp, core/own_ship/OwnShipProvider.hpp, core/types/{Track.hpp,Timestamp.hpp}, core/static/{BearingWedgeModel.hpp,LiveOccupancyModel.hpp/.cpp headers+grep}, ports/IStaticObstacleModel.hpp, docs/output-contract.md, spec 2026-06-03-cpa-uncertainty-design.md section 4; tests: tests/collision/{test_cpa,test_cpa_uncertainty,test_cpa_evaluator,test_cpa_synthesize_own_ship,test_static_hazard_evaluator}.cpp, tests/output/test_track_output.cpp. Findings 1-3 verified numerically (finite-difference Jacobian check; independent WGS84 ECEF/ENU convergence check) in the scratchpad, no repo files touched. CHECKED AND CLEAN: negative-variance sqrt guards (std::max(var,0.0) at Cpa.cpp:114/154/162 and TrackOutput.cpp:51/61-62 — the hinted sqrt-of-negative issue does not exist); parallel/near-zero relative-speed tcpa division guarded (kEpsDv2, dv2>0 ternary at Cpa.cpp:92); negative-tcpa clamp policy implemented per header contract; COG = atan2(v_east, v_north) with correct [0,360) normalization (incl. the -1e-14 -> 360.0 -> 0 double-wrap) and the polar Jacobian verified analytically (rows [s,c] and [c/sog,-s/sog] correct for (ve,vn) ordering); documented sigma_cog=0 / isotropic sigma_sog at SOG<0.01; velocity is_valid gating (velocity_observed + finite + 2x2 Sylvester PD) matches doc; CpaEvaluator hysteresis cannot oscillate with valid configs (stay-in tests p>=exit, exit<enter), Exited IS emitted on track deletion/status-regression via the dropped-ids sweep with a zeroed payload, Updated only fires after Entered, id-0 sentinel safe (TrackManager next_id_ starts at 1); StaticHazardEvaluator hysteresis correct for its documented fixed-list model, distance recomputed from geodetic each call (datum-recenter safe); staticHazardId deterministic incl. negative lat/lon cast wrap; toStaticHazardOutput verbatim copy correct; toBearingWedgeOutput verified at its only call site (BearingWedgeModel.cpp:109 passes the model's fixed anchor_, not the current datum), math-to-true bearing conversion and optional max_range carry-through correct. OVERFLOW ONE-LINERS (below reporting bar): (a) computeCpaWithUncertainty's is_diverging can disagree with computeCpa for near-parallel geometries (dv2 in (0,1e-12): t_cpa_raw's meaningless sign decides is_diverging=true while computeCpa reports false) — payload-only, contradicts the 'same semantics' header claim; (b) no validation that enter_probability > exit_probability or exit_hysteresis > 1.0 — inverted configs oscillate Entered/Exited every scan at constant p/d; (c) synthesizeOwnShipTrack uses pose.velocity_enu with ZERO velocity covariance when velocity_is_valid=false (overconfident stationary-own-ship CPA) — documented in the header and pinned by test, so treated as by-design; (d) covariance_is_default reads recent_contributions which consumers must clear per Track.hpp — stale touches can leave the flag stale (documented contract); (e) ADR-0002 wedge-vs-track suppression lives in BearingWedgeModel::drain (core/static, out of scope) — doc says recomputed per drain, never latched; the in-scope output converters themselves suppress nothing. CROSS-UNIT FLAG for synthesis: finding 3's root cause (datumAxisRotation direction transposed for the v_new=R*v_old convention) equally affects core/tracking/DatumShift.cpp velocity/covariance rotation on every datum recenter — outside this unit, should be checked by the tracking reviewer.

### unit: static-land (5 findings)

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** inCoverage measures range/azimuth from the ENU origin, not from own-ship, so coverage is wrong whenever own-ship is away from the datum origin
  - `core/sensor_activity/DeclaredSensorActivity.cpp:12` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: inCoverage computes range = track_pos_enu.norm() and azimuth = atan2(y, x) about the ENU ORIGIN (comment: 'Sensor assumed at the ENU origin'). The ISensorActivity port passes only the track's absolute ENU position (PmbmTracker.cpp:688 and :1046 pass b.mean.head<2>()), and neither the port nor the profile carries an own-ship/sensor pose, so a ship-mounted radar's declared coverage is evaluated about the datum origin instead of the moving sensor. Under the documented auto-datum consumer pattern (CLAUDE.md: OwnShipProvider recenters only when own-ship moves > 30 km) own-ship is routinely 10-30 km from the origin while typical declared radar ranges are 8-20 km (the integration-guide deployment recipe declares max_range 20 km). The integration guide's one-sentence caveat ('the tracker treats the sensor as mounted at the ENU origin, so mount off-centre needs a translated profile') frames this as a static mount offset; a translated profile cannot fix a moving own-ship, and the same guide's 'deployment recipe' wires DeclaredSensorActivity directly into exactly that moving-own-ship deployment. In contrast, the honest detection model (ISensorDetectionModel::missDetectionProbability, ISensorDetectionModel.hpp:131-146) correctly takes sensor_pos_enu per measurement — the two miss models disagree on geometry.
  - failure_scenario: Live deployment per the integration-guide R9 recipe (use_sensor_activity=true, radar Surveillance profile max_range 20 km, AIS/Cooperative profile). Own-ship departs the datum origin and is 25 km out (auto-recenter has not fired at <30 km). (a) A clutter-born ghost Bernoulli 3 km off own-ship's bow sits ~25 km from the origin -> inCoverage returns false every scan -> surveillance_miss never charged -> with idle_halflife_sec=0 (the coverage_land deployment configs, Config.cpp:449) its existence is never decremented by miss math -> permanent phantom track. (b) A real coasting track left 5 km from the origin (20 km behind own-ship, physically far outside radar range) reads 'in coverage' -> one miss with p_D=0.9 charged per 2.5 s duty cycle -> existence collapses and a real, merely-out-of-range vessel's track is deleted within a few sweeps instead of coasting. Every unit test in tests/sensor_activity/test_declared_sensor_activity.cpp places the implicit sensor at the origin, so none contradicts this.
  - evidence: core/sensor_activity/DeclaredSensorActivity.cpp:8-21 (origin-centric geometry); ports/ISensorActivity.hpp:55-59 (no sensor pose in the port); core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:688-690, 1046-1048 (absolute ENU track position passed, nullopt identities); docs/integration-guide.md:957 (mount-offset framing) and :1017-1030 (deployment recipe with 20 km range); CLAUDE.md auto-datum 30 km recenter threshold.
  - suggested_fix: Thread the evaluating sensor's current ENU position (or own-ship pose) through ISensorActivity::evaluate and compute range/azimuth about it; alternatively document DeclaredSensorActivity as valid only for a stationary sensor at the datum origin and refuse wiring it together with an auto-recentering OwnShipProvider.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full failing path. (1) core/sensor_activity/DeclaredSensorActivity.cpp:12-18 gates coverage by track_pos_enu.norm() and atan2 about the ENU origin; the port (ports/ISensorActivity.hpp:55-59) and ChannelProfile carry no sensor/own-ship pose, and PmbmTracker.cpp:688-690/1046-1048 pass the track's absolute ENU position b.mean.head<2>() with no own-ship subtraction — no other ISensorActivity implementation exists in the tree. (2) Both failure directions execute: in the use_sensor_activity path, out-of-coverage means existence UNCHANGED (idle decay bypassed; and makeCoverageLandPmbmConfig sets idle_halflife_sec=0.0), so a phantom the origin-centric model deems uncovered never decays; a real out-of-range track near the origin reads in-coverage and has r <- (1-pD)r/(1-r*pD) with pD=0.9 charged per duty cycle, collapsing existence in a few sweeps. (3) OwnShipProvider.hpp:75 confirms recenter_threshold_km=30.0, so under the documented auto-datum pattern own-ship is routinely farther from the origin than the R9 recipe's 20 km declared radar range — the coverage picture is wrong by more than the whole radar range. (4) ISensorDetectionModel.hpp:131-136 takes sensor_pos_enu (d = track_pos - sensor_pos), confirming the two miss models disagree on geometry. Refutation angles checked and rejected: the assumption IS documented (pmbm-design.md §8.2 #5, integration-guide.md:957) but only as a static mount-offset fixable by a 'translated profile', which cannot represent a moving own-ship, and the port's pure-function contract gives an adapter no per-call sensor pose; the same guide's R9 deployment recipe wires this into a moving ship-mounted deployment with no warning; this item is not on the KNOWN/BY-DESIGN list. Tests (tests/sensor_activity/test_declared_sensor_activity.cpp) all place the implicit sensor at the origin; bench usage runs fixed-datum shore-radar / short-range scenarios where datum ~ sensor site, explaining why benchmarks never exposed it.
  - verifier corrected details: inCoverage (core/sensor_activity/DeclaredSensorActivity.cpp:12) evaluates declared surveillance coverage about the ENU datum origin, but the tracker feeds absolute ENU track positions (PmbmTracker.cpp:688, 1046) and neither the ISensorActivity port nor ChannelProfile carries a sensor/own-ship pose. Under the documented auto-datum pattern (recenter only at >30 km, OwnShipProvider.hpp:75), a ship-mounted radar's coverage is evaluated up to 30 km away from the actual sensor — larger than the R9 recipe's 20 km max_range. Consequences with use_sensor_activity=true (the documented deployment recipe and the coverage_land configs, which also set idle_halflife_sec=0): (a) tracks near own-ship but far from the origin are treated as out of coverage, so misses are never charged and existence never decays — clutter-born phantoms become permanent; (b) tracks near the origin but far behind own-ship (physically out of radar range) are treated as covered and charged pD=0.9 misses per duty cycle, deleting real coasting vessels within a few sweeps. The documented caveat frames the origin assumption as a static mount offset ('translated profile or adapter'), which cannot address a moving own-ship, and the port's pure-function contract provides no way for an adapter to receive the per-call sensor pose. The honest detection model (ISensorDetectionModel::missDetectionProbability, ports/ISensorDetectionModel.hpp:131-136) correctly takes sensor_pos_enu, so the two miss models disagree on geometry. Mitigating factors keeping this at high rather than critical: the feature is opt-in (use_sensor_activity default false, documented as pending broader real-data validation), and deployments whose datum sits at a fixed sensor site (shore radar) or with short transit distances are unaffected.

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** cooperative_overdue is identity-blind, so the cooperative-only retirement path hard-deletes radar-only (non-cooperative) tracks shortly after they leave surveillance coverage
  - `core/sensor_activity/DeclaredSensorActivity.cpp:51` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: The port defines cooperative silence as identity-keyed evidence ('a cooperative source's OWN-identity report was overdue', ISensorActivity.hpp:34-38; mmsi/platform_id are passed for this purpose) and the tracker comments call the consumer branch 'Cooperative-only timeout retirement' (PmbmTracker.cpp:697-698). But DeclaredSensorActivity::evaluate ignores mmsi/platform_id entirely and sets cooperative_overdue=true for ANY track whenever dt > expected_report_interval_sec (line 51), and PmbmTracker passes std::nullopt for both identities at both call sites and applies the retirement with last_report falling back to birth_time for tracks that never had a cooperative touch (PmbmTracker.cpp:699-711, 1055-1064). Net effect: the retirement designed for AIS-only tracks whose feed went quiet fires for every track — including radar-only non-cooperative vessels, the primary reason a fusion tracker exists. The retirement branch is reachable exactly when the track is outside declared surveillance coverage (!surveillance_miss), i.e. exactly when the design says 'Existence UNCHANGED by miss math' / 'out of coverage is not evidence'.
  - failure_scenario: makeCoverageLandPmbmConfig (Config.cpp:447-451: use_sensor_activity=true, cooperative_stale_timeout_sec=120, idle_halflife_sec=0) with a scenario/deployment declaring an AIS Cooperative profile (10 s interval, Sweep.cpp:402-406). A non-AIS vessel is confirmed by radar at t=0 and tracked for 200 s, then sails just past the declared radar max_range (or into the unswept sector, or own-ship turns away). Next scans: inCoverage=false -> no surveillance_miss; dt since its last activity check exceeds 10 s -> cooperative_overdue=true; last_cooperative_touch_ absent -> last_report=birth_time, and now-birth=200s > 120s -> existence forced to 0.0 -> Bernoulli pruned, onTrackDeleted fires. A real vessel that merely left radar coverage is deleted ~10 s later instead of coasting (survival decay would have kept it for minutes) — the ADR-0002 forbidden 'suppressed into nothing'. A vessel fading at the radar range edge is repeatedly killed and re-born with new track IDs. Tests: OverdueLeavesExistenceUnchangedAndFlagsStale (within timeout), CooperativeOnlyRetiredOnlyByTimeout (track HAS cooperative provenance) and FuseOneTrackStableThroughCoopDropout (radar IN coverage suppresses retirement; the retired track had platform_id 7) never exercise a never-cooperative track OUT of coverage, so none contradicts.
  - evidence: DeclaredSensorActivity.cpp:49-52 (identity args ignored, overdue flagged unconditionally); ports/ISensorActivity.hpp:34-38 ('own-identity report'); PmbmTracker.cpp:688-711 and 1046-1066 (nullopt identities; retirement falls back to birth_time with no cooperative-provenance guard); Config.cpp:447-451 (deployment config values).
  - suggested_fix: Gate the retirement on cooperative provenance: either have evaluate() report cooperative_overdue only when the track carries a cooperative identity (requires the tracker to pass the mmsi/platform_id it already stores in contribution_history_), or in the tracker require last_cooperative_touch_ to EXIST (never fall back to birth_time) before retiring.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full failing path. (1) DeclaredSensorActivity.cpp:34-35,51 ignores the mmsi/platform_id identity args and sets cooperative_overdue=true for ANY track whenever dt > expected_report_interval_sec, contradicting the port contract (ISensorActivity.hpp:34-37, 'own-identity report') and spec §3 ('this specific track's own report'). (2) core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp passes std::nullopt for both identities at both call sites (689, 1047-1048) and applies retirement with no cooperative-provenance guard (699-711, 1055-1064): last_cooperative_touch_ is populated only by cooperative-sensor detections (line 1002-1003), so a radar-only track falls back to last_report = birth_time — i.e., any track older than the timeout is treated as 'cooperative-silent since birth'. (3) Hand-executed with makeCoverageLandPmbmConfig (Config.cpp:447-451: use_sensor_activity=true, source_aware_misdetection=false so should_misdetect (PmbmTracker.cpp:567) always passes, timeout=120s) and Sweep-built profiles (Sweep.cpp:383-413, AIS Cooperative 10s + radar Surveillance): a radar-only vessel born t=0, tracked to t=200, exits radar max_range; at ~t=212 dt>10s → cooperative_overdue, surveillance_miss=false (out of coverage), 212-0>120 → existence forced to 0.0 → pruned, onTrackDeleted. Perverse asymmetry confirms it is a fallback bug, not a design: the older the track, the faster it dies after coverage exit (first overdue check), while a fresh track gets the full 120s. (4) Documentation contradicts the behavior: PmbmTracker.hpp:418-421 says the timeout retires 'a cooperative-only track'; spec §4 case 3 and pmbm-design.md §8.1 case 3 say out-of-coverage → r unchanged, 'tracks do not bleed out on a wall-clock timer'; ADR-0002 forbids deleting a persistent object into nothing. The integration guide's 'retire when BOTH channels go silent' describes the fused-track scenario (track with cooperative provenance); a never-cooperative track has no expected report to be silent on. (5) Verified no test pins against it: OutOfCoverageNoPenalty has no Cooperative profile and timeout=0 (branch unreachable); CooperativeOnlyRetiredOnlyByTimeout and AisAsCooperativeFlagsStaleAndRetires use cooperative tracks where birth≈first report; FuseOneTrackStableThroughCoopDropout's no-retirement phase keeps the track IN radar coverage and its retired track has platform_id=7 provenance. Bench scenarios never exposed it (evaluation-log.md:1992-1993: retirement 'unreachable within the scenario horizon', 60s scenarios vs 120s timeout). The AisAsCooperativeFlagsStaleAndRetires test comment even documents this identical birth_time-fallback failure as a previously fixed bug for AIS-touched tracks — the same fallback remains live for never-cooperative tracks. Minor correction: the kill/re-birth cycle at a fading range edge runs at ~120s per reborn ID (new birth_time resets the clock), not ~10s; ~10s applies only to the first kill of an already-aged track.
  - verifier corrected details: In any deployment following the documented cooperative+radar recipe (use_sensor_activity=true, cooperative_stale_timeout_sec>0, a DeclaredSensorActivity with any Cooperative profile — e.g. makeCoverageLandPmbmConfig + Sweep wiring, or the integration-guide §7 recipe), every track with no cooperative provenance whose age exceeds the timeout is hard-deleted (existence forced to 0, Bernoulli pruned, onTrackDeleted) at the first activity check more than expected_report_interval_sec (10s) after it leaves all declared surveillance coverage, instead of coasting with existence unchanged as spec §4 case 3 and pmbm-design.md §8.1 require. Root causes: (a) DeclaredSensorActivity.cpp:51 flags cooperative_overdue identity-blind (mmsi/platform_id args ignored; PmbmTracker passes nullopt anyway); (b) PmbmTracker.cpp:699-711/1055-1064 apply the 'cooperative-only' retirement to any track, with last_report falling back to birth_time when the track never had a cooperative touch. Net effect: non-cooperative (radar-only) vessels — the primary fusion targets — are silently suppressed into nothing (ADR-0002 forbidden mode) upon leaving radar range/sector, with ID churn (kill + re-birth cycle ~timeout cadence) for vessels fading at the coverage edge; older tracks die fastest (~10s after coverage exit). Severity high, not critical: the path is opt-in (use_sensor_activity default false, timeout default 0.0, requires a declared Cooperative profile) and the guide marks the coverage channel as pending real-data validation, but the failing combination is exactly the documented deployment recipe and shipped bench config family (coverage_land). Fix direction: gate the retirement on the track having cooperative provenance (last_cooperative_touch_ entry, or cooperative touches in contribution history) instead of falling back to birth_time, and/or key cooperative_overdue on track identity as the port contract specifies.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** minEdgeDistM silently skips the implicit closing edge of an unclosed ring while pointInRing auto-closes it — and the in-repo synthetic shore builder produces unclosed rings
  - `core/land/CoastlineGeometry.cpp:47` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: minEdgeDistM iterates segments ring[i]..ring[i+1] only (loop 'i + 1 < ring.size()') and relies on the ring being explicitly closed ('Requires the ring to be closed (ring.back() == ring.front()), as GeoJSON mandates'). pointInRing, by contrast, auto-closes (its edge walk starts with j = n-1, the last->first edge). Nothing validates closure, and buildSyntheticShore (core/scenario/Builders.cpp:628-637) constructs an 8-vertex LandPolygon whose ring is NOT closed: last vertex {L,T}, first {L,S}, so the entire west land edge (x = -extent, from y=T to y=S) exists for inside/outside classification but is invisible to the distance computation. The two primitives therefore disagree about the polygon's shape, producing a discontinuous, wrong signed-distance prior along that edge.
  - failure_scenario: SyntheticShore with extent_m=1000, shore_y_m=0, land_depth_m=200, default 50/50 half-widths. Query 10 m WEST of the land block at (x=-1010, y=100): pointInRing says water (correct); nearest true shore is the west edge at 10 m, but minEdgeDistM only sees the top/bottom/pier edges ~100 m away -> d=+100 -> prior clamp((50-100)/100)=0.0 instead of the correct (50-10)/100=0.4 -> shore-clutter suppression silently absent in a 50 m band of water along the west edge. Mirror error just inland (x=-990, y=100): d=-100 -> prior 1.0 (hard-plateau strength) instead of 0.6. Real GeoJSON fixtures are unaffected if RFC-7946-compliant (the loader adapters/land/GeoJsonCoastline.cpp does not verify closure either). tests/land/test_coastline_geometry.cpp uses only explicitly closed rings, so no test contradicts.
  - evidence: CoastlineGeometry.cpp:43-51 (open loop + closure comment) vs :17 (pointInRing j=n-1 auto-close); core/scenario/Builders.cpp:628-637 (ring_enu = 8 vertices, first vertex never repeated).
  - suggested_fix: Auto-close in minEdgeDistM (include the ring.back()->ring.front() segment when they differ), or close the ring at construction/parse time and assert closure in CoastlineGeometry's constructor.

- **[LOW/unverified]** Touched-but-unobservable cells get the EWMA add without the decay, so persistence grows unboundedly past 1.0 and departed objects take longer to forget
  - `core/static/LiveOccupancyModel.cpp:181` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: Step 1 applies the (1-alpha) decay only to cells observable this scan; step 3 then applies 'persistence_[c] += alpha*w' unconditionally to every touched cell. A cell that is touched this scan but NOT inside any estimated coverage sector (or LOS-shadow-frozen) receives p += alpha*w with no decay, so the recursion is p_{k+1} = p_k + alpha*w rather than the documented EWMA (docs/algorithms/live-static-occupancy.md defines the recursion only 'for a touched, observable cell'), and p is no longer bounded by 1. This is realistic on real data: CoverageSector::fromReturns keeps only the LARGEST bearing cluster per bundle (ISensorDetectionModel.hpp fromReturns), so the returns of the smaller clusters — measured on philos at 5-17% of bursts, with 80-169 deg gaps — touch cells that the same bundle's sector does not cover. Each such burst adds up to alpha=0.3 to those cells with no compensating decay.
  - failure_scenario: A pier that repeatedly falls in the discarded (smaller) cluster of multi-cluster bursts: 5 consecutive such bursts push a cell to p=1.5 (>1). Consequences: obstacle_conf is capped (min(1.0,p)) so suppression is unchanged, but (a) once the object departs and the cell re-enters coverage, decay from 1.5-3.0 takes ln(overshoot)/ln(1/0.7) extra scans beyond the documented recovery latency (VacatedCellsRecoverWithinBoundedLatency tests only start from EWMA-bounded values, so they don't contradict); (b) the clutter-adaptive median and peakPersistence() introspection see impossible >1 values. Bounded, safe-direction impact, but a real invariant break versus the documented math.
  - evidence: LiveOccupancyModel.cpp:131-156 (decay only when observable) vs :181 (unconditional add); docs/algorithms/live-static-occupancy.md 'p <- (1-alpha)p + alpha*w_max for a touched, OBSERVABLE cell'; ISensorDetectionModel.hpp fromReturns 'keep the one with the most returns' + doc note that 5-17% of philos bursts are multi-cluster.
  - suggested_fix: In step 3, apply the decay to touched-but-unobservable cells before the add (p <- (1-alpha)p + alpha*w for every touched cell), or clamp p at 1.0 after the add.

- **[LOW/unverified]** Clutter-adaptive bar median includes permanently frozen out-of-coverage cells, cross-contaminating the background estimate between areas (and the frozen set grows without bound over a voyage)
  - `core/static/LiveOccupancyModel.cpp:256` (correctness, confidence medium)
  - description: persistentCells() computes the clutter-background median over ALL live cells (excluding only this scan's LOS-guard-protected set). Under coverage-aware decay, cells that leave every sensor's footprint never decay and are never pruned (erase_floor only removes decayed cells), so they stay in persistence_ forever at whatever value they froze at. On a moving platform the median that is supposed to estimate the CURRENT area's clutter background is therefore polluted by frozen cells from every previously visited area, and the grid grows monotonically (memory + the per-scan decay loop iterates every historical cell).
  - failure_scenario: clutter_adaptive=true detector mode on a vessel that spends hours in harbor A (thousands of cells frozen at 0.5-1.0 as it sails out of range) then works in harbor B where live clutter cells sit near 0.1-0.3. The median over the union is dominated by harbor A's frozen values (e.g. 0.7) -> bar = max(0.5, 1.5*0.7) = 1.05 > any bounded persistence -> no structure in harbor B ever classifies -> pier hazards and their birth suppression silently absent (the presence channel the layer exists for). Currently only reachable in the detector-mode research configs (clutter_adaptive defaults false; the bench runs single-site fixed-datum), so latent for live multi-area deployment.
  - evidence: LiveOccupancyModel.cpp:241-258 (median over all persistence_ cells), :131-156 (out-of-coverage cells never decay), :184-189 (prune only below erase_floor); docs/algorithms/live-static-occupancy.md documents the median as estimating the (current) clutter background from a clutter-dominated feed.
  - suggested_fix: Restrict the median to cells observable (covered) this scan, or to cells touched within a recency window; separately consider bounded retention (e.g. distance-from-own-ship eviction) for the frozen set.

Coverage notes (static-land): CHECKED CLEAN: (1) LiveOccupancyModel cellOf uses std::floor — the hinted negative-coordinate truncation bug is NOT present; cellCenter is consistent for negative indices. (2) Datum re-anchoring: grid/wedge apexes/charted points/vessel fixes are all stored in the fixed anchor frame; onDatumRecentered only swaps the current->anchor transform (no cell shifting needed, no partial copies); toAnchorEnu fast-path double-equality on origins is safe; pinned by DatumRecenterKeepsGeographicSuppression. (3) Decay-vs-dt: per-fed-scan alpha is documented behavior (param comment + algorithm doc), not dt-scaled by design. (4) Clutter weight/position vector alignment: both producers (PmbmTracker.cpp:1815-1822, MhtTracker.cpp:820-828) push position+weight together, so the w[i] indexing under the 'empty means 1.0' contract cannot go out of bounds. (5) EWMA order for observable cells, largest-weight-per-cell order independence, erase-floor pruning, camera-streak pruning, deterministic map-ordered flood fill, membership hysteresis (persistent_prev_ updated once per scan after recompute; eviction pre-pass runs before recompute so both see the same persistence_), conservation invariant of birthSuppression (ramp derived from emitted hazards only; veto only lowers to 0). (6) ShadowMask: bearing wrap through north handled by cut-at-largest-gap + unwrap (hand-executed 350->10 deg case); n==1, all-equal-bearings, at-sensor returns, half-width capped at pi, isShadowed exclusive-at-occluder-range boundary all correct; the range-ignoring bearing clustering (two objects at different ranges merging into one wedge blocked beyond the NEAR one) is the documented safe-direction over-hold, with peakGuardProtectedFraction introspection provided for mis-tuning — not reported. Note (unreported, adjacent): dense uniform clutter with mean bearing gaps < cluster_gap_rad (~6 deg, e.g. 100+ plots/scan) collapses into one whole-circle wedge freezing nearly all decay; visible via the introspection knob, tuning-domain. (7) BearingWedgeModel: angleDelta wrap correct; suspect-remint, stale pruning boundary (strictly >), claim recomputed-never-latched, claim_min_range/max_range gates, mathToTrueDeg conversion (90-alpha, [0,360)) all verified. (8) StaticObstacleModel: ramp math, r_soft=max(keep_clear,r_hard) degenerate handling, soft_max construction cap (composition-root caveat documented in-code). (9) CoastlineModel: trivial datum swap correct. (10) CoastlineGeometry: pointInRing near-vertex behavior is boundary-noise only (prior is continuous ~0.5 at d=0 either way); zero-length segments guarded (len2>0); holes-as-water and nested-polygon logic correct; local-equirectangular scaling uses query-point latitude (fine at these scales). Antimeridian-crossing polygons would break segDistM/pointInRing but RFC 7946 requires splitting there — not reported (unrealistic for the target geographies). (11) DeclaredSensorActivity window semantics: dt<=0 empty, dt<duty_cycle mid-sweep, one-miss-per-call, boundary inclusivity, max-p_D aggregation, undeclared-sensor nullopt fallback all match docs/tests. (12) Vessel-fix veto: prune windows (anchored vs underway), anchor-frame storage, count introspection — consistent; fixes accumulate unboundedly only if observe() is never called (unwired-feed misuse, not reported). NOT COVERED: PmbmTracker internals beyond the sensor-activity/occupancy-feed call sites (another unit's scope); ports/ILiveOccupancyFeed and IStaticObstacleModel consumers on the birth path; FoxgloveDebugRecorder land drawing; gitignored fixtures per instructions. Findings 1 and 2 are anchored in DeclaredSensorActivity but their blast radius runs through PmbmTracker's miss/retirement branches — the synthesis should cross-check with whoever reviewed core/pmbm.

### unit: adapters-sensor (8 findings)

- **[CRITICAL/CONFIRMED]** GGA path validates nothing: no fix-quality check, no lat/lon plausibility — a standard no-fix GGA publishes a (0,0) pose and teleports the datum to Null Island
  - `adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:120` (validation, confidence high)
  - description: The GGA branch parses fields[1..4] with parseDdmm and pushes the pose unconditionally. GGA fix-quality (fields[5], 0 = invalid) is never read, and edge::isPlausibleLatLon is never called anywhere in this adapter (it includes no EdgeValidation at all). parseDdmm("") returns 0.0 (line 15), so the industry-standard no-fix sentence with empty lat/lon fields yields lat=0, lon=0. OwnShipProvider::update (core/own_ship/OwnShipProvider.cpp:33-45) does no validation either: with a datum established near e.g. Hamburg, the (0,0) pose is ~6,000 km away > 30 km, so auto-recenter (default ON) fires, re-anchoring the datum at Null Island and shifting every track through a tangent plane where their real positions are thousands of km off-plane (linearization error is km-scale and not undone by the shift back). The bogus pose also enters the pose history, so ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter poseAtOrBefore lookups project measurements from a false (0,0) own position. The same adapter DOES check RMC status A/V (line 199), confirming the GGA gap is an oversight, not policy. If the FIRST GGA after cold start is a no-fix (very common), the datum AND the equirectangular reference (line 133) initialize at (0,0), permanently mis-scaling the UERE/velocity estimators' east axis by 1/cos(lat) (~1.66 at 53°N). The optional NavInputGuard only notifies a (nullable, default-null) sink and never drops the pose.
  - failure_scenario: GPS antenna shadowed mid-run; receiver emits `$GPGGA,120000.00,,,,,0,00,99.99,,M,,M,,*hh` (fields present but empty, quality 0). Adapter publishes pose lat=0/lon=0 at t; provider auto-recenters the datum to (0,0), fires all datum sinks, tracks are shifted through a 6,000-km-distant frame; TTM/EO-IR measurements stamped near t project from own position (0,0); the next valid fix recenters again. All live tracks are silently corrupted or lost with no error surfaced.
  - evidence: OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:112-192 (no reference to fields[5]; no EdgeValidation include); parseDdmm empty-string return at line 15; provider update/recenter at core/own_ship/OwnShipProvider.cpp:33-45; RMC-only status check at line 199. tests/adapters/own_ship/test_own_ship_nmea.cpp has no no-fix or empty-field GGA case.
  - suggested_fix: In the GGA branch: reject when fields[5] (fix quality) is 0/empty, and require edge::isPlausibleLatLon(lat, lon) plus non-empty lat/lon fields before composing/publishing the pose.
  - verifier: Independently traced the failing path. (1) adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp GGA branch (112-193) never reads fields[5] (fix quality); parseNmea (adapters/util/Nmea.cpp) validates only structure+checksum; parseDdmm("") returns 0.0 at line 15; so the standard no-fix sentence $GPGGA,120000.00,,,,,0,00,99.99,,M,,M,,*hh (14 fields, passes the size>=5 guard at line 119) produces lat=0, lon=0 and provider_.update(pose) at line 191 with no plausibility check — grep confirms edge::isPlausibleLatLon is used in AisAdapter.cpp:23, ArpaAdapter.cpp:74, RemoteTrackAdapter.cpp:16 but never in this adapter. (2) core/own_ship/OwnShipProvider.cpp:24-57 does no validation: the NavInputGuard only notifies a nullable, default-null sink and the comment at line 27 states it "Never rewrites the pose"; enable_auto_recenter defaults true with 30 km threshold (OwnShipProvider.hpp:74-75), so a Hamburg-anchored datum recenters to (0,0) (~6,900 km > 30 km) and fires all datum sinks. (3) The corruption is not undone by the next valid fix: core/tracking/DatumShift.cpp shiftPosition (line 8) round-trips through z=0.0; a Hamburg track in a Null-Island ENU frame has true z about -2,800 km, so forcing z=0 on the shift back displaces the reconstructed 3D point by thousands of km along the (0,0) up-axis — horizontal track positions are destroyed, and mid-interval range/bearing measurements project from own position (0,0) via poseAtOrBefore. The prior review's note that the z=0 round-trip is exact explicitly assumed the ~70 m curvature drop of a 30 km recenter, not this case. (4) Cold-start branch confirmed: enu_ref_set_ (line 133) latches the first GGA forever, so a first no-fix pins cos_ref=1 instead of ~0.60 at 53N, permanently mis-scaling the east axis of the UERE/velocity estimators; the datum also initializes at (0,0). (5) No test pins the behavior: every GGA in tests/adapters/own_ship/test_own_ship_nmea.cpp uses quality=1 with populated lat/lon. One correction: the claim that the gap is "an oversight, not policy" is overstated — docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-31-sensor-adapters.md:1369 documents "quality flag not gated" as an assumption with quality-flag gating listed under ways-to-improve. It is acknowledged debt rather than unnoticed, but it is not in the review's known/by-design list, it predates the auto-recenter datum pattern whose interaction makes the consequence catastrophic, and it violates CLAUDE.md invariant #6 (adapters validate plausibility at the edge).
  - verifier corrected details: GGA branch of OwnShipNmeaAdapter::ingest publishes poses with no fix-quality gate (fields[5] never read) and no lat/lon plausibility check (EdgeValidation not included, unlike AIS/ARPA/RemoteTrack adapters). parseDdmm("") returns 0.0, so a standard no-fix GGA with empty lat/lon fields publishes a (0,0) pose. OwnShipProvider::update performs no validation (NavInputGuard is advisory-only to a default-null sink); with auto-recenter default-on, an established datum >30 km from Null Island is silently re-anchored at (0,0), all datum sinks fire, and shiftTracksOnDatumChange's z=0 round-trip (DatumShift.cpp:8) irreversibly corrupts track positions when the next valid fix recenters back (true z in the (0,0) frame is ~-2,800 km at 6,000 km range, not the ~70 m of a normal 30 km recenter). Measurements timestamped in the bogus interval project from own position (0,0). If the FIRST sentence after cold start is a no-fix (routine GPS behavior at power-on), the datum initializes at (0,0) and the adapter's equirectangular reference (enu_ref_set_, line 133, never reset) permanently mis-scales the UERE/velocity estimators' east axis by 1/cos(lat). No test covers no-fix or empty-field GGA. Caveats vs the original claim: the missing quality gate is documented as an assumption + ways-to-improve item in docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-31-sensor-adapters.md:1369 (acknowledged debt, not a pure oversight), and the NMEA adapters are documented as optional/non-canonical — consumers with their own parsing pipeline are unaffected. Neither caveat mitigates the shipped NMEA path: the trigger is routine, the failure is silent, and it violates CLAUDE.md invariant #6.

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** AisAdapter/ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter/RemoteTrackAdapter hold a fixed private Datum copy with no update path — after an auto-recenter (default ON) they project every measurement into the old frame
  - `adapters/ais/AisAdapter.cpp:24` (architecture-invariant, confidence high)
  - description: All four sensor adapters take `geo::Datum datum` by value at construction (AisAdapter.hpp:100, ArpaAdapter.hpp:76, EoIrAdapter.hpp:64, RemoteTrackAdapter.hpp:116) and use `datum_.toEnu(...)` per ingest. None implements IDatumChangeSink, none has a datum setter, and ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter even hold the OwnShipProvider reference yet still use their frozen copy instead of provider.datum(). DatumRecenterPolicy defaults enable_auto_recenter=true at 30 km. The integration guide (§2 'Register every ENU-caching component as a datum sink') lists StaticObstacleModel/CoastlineModel/LiveOccupancyModel/BearingWedgeModel but omits the sensor adapters — which cannot be registered at all. So a consumer who follows the guide (auto-datum + TrackShifterSink + NMEA adapters) gets a silent frame split the first time own-ship moves 30 km: tracks live in the new frame, all subsequent measurements arrive in the old frame, offset by the full datum shift.
  - failure_scenario: Coastal vessel wires AisAdapter/ArpaAdapter with `provider.datum()` copies and default recenter policy, transits 31 km: provider recenters, shiftTracksOnDatumChange moves all tracks to the new frame; the adapters keep projecting into the old frame, so every AIS/radar measurement lands ~31 km from its true position in the tracker frame — all existing tracks stop updating and phantom tracks are born 31 km off, with zero diagnostics.
  - evidence: No IDatumChangeSink implementation or datum mutator in any of the four adapters (grep confirmed only FoxgloveDebugRecorder implements the sink under adapters/). docs/integration-guide.md §2 sink list omits them; §3/§4 show `RemoteTrackAdapter remote(datum)` style construction with no recenter caveat. app/example.cpp avoids the issue only by building measurements by hand from provider.datum() per call. The bench Sweep fixed-datum exception is documented; these live adapters are not.
  - suggested_fix: Have the adapters read the datum from the OwnShipProvider at ingest time (Arpa/EoIr already hold it), or implement IDatumChangeSink + document mandatory registration; at minimum document that the NMEA/struct adapters require enable_auto_recenter=false.
  - verifier: Independently traced the failing path with concrete code. (1) Frozen datum: AisAdapter.cpp:17 stores `datum_` at construction and AisAdapter.cpp:24 projects every report with it; same pattern in ArpaAdapter.cpp:56/75/109 (which holds `OwnShipProvider& own_ship_` at ArpaAdapter.hpp:77 yet still uses the frozen `datum_` for projection), EoIrAdapter.cpp:19/35, RemoteTrackAdapter.cpp:11/38. None has a datum setter and none implements IDatumChangeSink — grep over adapters/ shows only FoxgloveDebugRecorder implements the sink, and it DOES re-anchor its own datum_ (FoxgloveDebugRecorder.cpp:343), proving the re-anchor pattern exists and was simply not applied to the four sensor adapters. (2) Trigger is default-on: DatumRecenterPolicy{enable_auto_recenter=true, 30 km} (core/own_ship/OwnShipProvider.hpp:73-76); OwnShipProvider.cpp:35-44 replaces the datum and fires sinks when own-ship exceeds 30 km. (3) Hand-executed failure: consumer follows guide §2 (TrackShifterSink registered) + §4 (NMEA adapters constructed from provider.datum() copy). Ship transits 31 km → recenter D0→D1; tracks shift to D1 frame; next AIS report at true position P yields enu = D0.toEnu(P), which the tracker/output interpret in D1 → effective world position P+(D1−D0) ≈ 31 km off. With AIS σ = 10-30 m (AisAdapter defaults), gating can never associate; all live tracks coast to deletion and phantom tracks are born ~31 km from truth, silently (Measurement carries no datum tag, no diagnostic exists). (4) Refutation attempts failed: the canonical §3 builders (MeasurementBuilders.hpp:44-90) take `const OwnShipProvider&` and read the live datum, so they are immune — confirming the defect is specific to the documented NMEA/RemoteTrack path, not the whole library; docs/integration-guide.md §2 sink list (lines 181-197) and the §9 pitfall checklist (line 1156) enumerate StaticObstacleModel/CoastlineModel/LiveOccupancyModel/BearingWedgeModel + MHT but omit the sensor adapters, and §4 (lines 482-516) describes adapter usage with zero recenter caveat; ArpaAdapter.hpp's "in the supplied Datum's ENU frame" docstring mentions the supplied datum but never warns of the auto-recenter interaction and offers no way to keep it current. (5) No test pins the interaction: every adapter test (tests/adapters/*, tests/pipeline/test_bias_correction_orthogonality.cpp, tests/pmbm/test_pmbm_remote_track_fusion.cpp) uses a fixed datum and never triggers a recenter; the bench fixed-datum exception (ReplayScenarioRun.cpp:221, SimMultisensorScenarioRun.cpp:200) is documented for the bench only. This is not in the known/by-design list (that covers the bench Sweep, not the live adapters).
  - verifier corrected details: Confirmed as claimed, with one scope sharpening: the defect affects only consumers on the optional §4 NMEA/RemoteTrack adapter path; the canonical §3 measurement-builder path reads the provider's live datum and is immune. Mitigations available today (set enable_auto_recenter=false, or reconstruct adapters per poll from provider.datum()) are nowhere documented. Failure mode is silent and total for the affected path: after the first 30 km transit under default policy, every subsequent adapter measurement lands offset by the full datum shift (~30+ km), existing tracks stop updating and die, phantom tracks are born offset, with no diagnostic — a direct violation of the presence-over-suppression goal for a documented consumer wiring. Fix surface: either make the four adapters implement IDatumChangeSink (as FoxgloveDebugRecorder already does) or have ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter use own_ship_.datum() live and give AisAdapter/RemoteTrackAdapter a provider reference or setter; plus integration-guide §2/§4/§9 updates. Severity high stands: default-on trigger, realistic coastal transit, zero diagnostics; not critical because the canonical builder path is unaffected and a one-line policy pin avoids it.

- **[MEDIUM/CONFIRMED]** HDT/HDG ingested before the first GGA publishes a default-constructed (0,0) pose, initializing the auto-datum at Null Island
  - `adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:109` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: Every branch starts from `pose = provider_.latest().value_or(OwnShipPose{})`, whose defaults are lat=0, lon=0, and the HDT (lines 269-271, 249-252) and HDG (line 298) branches call provider_.update(pose) unconditionally. When the first sentence after startup is a heading sentence (typical: gyro HDT at 5-10 Hz starts before the GPS acquires), the lazily-initialized datum is anchored at geodetic (0,0) (OwnShipProvider.cpp:33-34). All poses/measurements composed until the first GGA use own position (0,0) in a Null-Island frame; the first real GGA then triggers a 6,000-km 'recenter' during startup, and the bogus (0,0) poses remain in the 16-deep history for poseAtOrBefore lookups by ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter for stale-timestamped detections.
  - failure_scenario: System starts in Hamburg with gyro already running: t=0.0 `$HEHDT,271.3,T` arrives before the first GGA at t=0.8. Datum initializes at (0,0); an ARPA TTM at t=0.5 projects from own_enu = datum.toEnu(0,0) = origin with the target placed in a Null-Island tangent plane; at t=0.8 the datum recenters 6,000 km, firing sinks. Early measurements are garbage and the startup transient is silent.
  - evidence: OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:109 + 249-252/269-271/298; OwnShipProvider.cpp:33-34 initializes the datum from any pose. tests/adapters/own_ship/test_own_ship_nmea_multi_heading.cpp ingests HDT/HDG as the first-ever sentence and asserts a pose IS published (lines 31, 41, 51) but never inspects lat/lon or the datum — it pins the flow without noticing the (0,0) init.
  - suggested_fix: In heading-only branches, skip provider_.update (buffer the heading) until a valid position pose exists, or have the branches require provider_.latest().has_value().
  - verifier: Independently traced the full failing path. (1) OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:109 starts every branch from provider_.latest().value_or(OwnShipPose{}); OwnShipPose defaults lat_deg/lon_deg to 0.0 (core/own_ship/OwnShipProvider.hpp:29-30) — the NaN='not present' convention covers only heading fields, not position. (2) The gyro-HDT branch (lines 269-271), GPS-HDT branch (249-252), and HDG branch (298) call provider_.update(pose) unconditionally, with no has-position or latest().has_value() guard anywhere in the file. (3) OwnShipProvider.cpp:33-34 lazily initializes the datum from any pose with no plausibility check, so a heading sentence arriving before the first GGA anchors the datum at geodetic (0,0); hasDatum() then returns true and datum() stops throwing, silently defeating the documented 'push a pose first' guidance. (4) Downstream, ArpaAdapter.cpp:92-110 (TTM) and MeasurementBuilders.cpp:38-58 resolve poseAtOrBefore(t) to the (0,0) pose and project targets in a Null-Island tangent plane; the measurements pass all validity gates and reach the tracker. (5) The first real GGA (e.g., Hamburg) is ~6,000 km from the datum, exceeding the 30 km default threshold, so a startup recenter fires; the bogus (0,0) poses remain in the 16-deep history for detections stamped before the GGA. Refutation attempts failed: NavInputGuard skips two-pose checks when there is no previous pose, is nullable, and never rewrites a pose, so it cannot prevent this; tests/adapters/own_ship/test_own_ship_nmea_multi_heading.cpp:31/41/51 ingest HDT/HDG as the first-ever sentence but assert only that a pose publishes, never lat/lon or the datum; the canonical integration test (tests/integration/test_full_stack_pipeline.cpp:197-209) even ingests IIHDT before the first GGA and only avoids the bug because its scenario deliberately places own-ship at lat 0, lon~0, where the (0,0) init is coincidentally correct; docs/integration-guide.md documents no GGA-before-heading ordering requirement. However, on the default path this is a bounded, self-healing startup transient: auto-recenter (default on) fixes the provider datum at the first GGA, registered sinks shift tracks, and garbage tracks coast out and die; typical deployments already have GPS lock at software start, making the window seconds. The permanent-damage variants (auto-recenter disabled; ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter freezing a Null-Island datum_ copy — they are not IDatumChangeSinks) require additional consumer wiring choices. Hence medium, not high.
  - verifier corrected details: HDT/HDG (and GPS-routed HDT) sentences ingested before the first GGA publish a default-constructed (0,0) pose (OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:109 + 252/269-271/298), which lazily initializes the auto-datum at Null Island (OwnShipProvider.cpp:33-34) — no position-validity check exists because OwnShipPose lat/lon default to 0.0 rather than NaN. Until the first GGA, hasDatum() is true and datum() returns the Null-Island datum, so range/bearing measurements (ArpaAdapter.cpp:92-110 TTM; MeasurementBuilders.cpp:38-58) are projected in a wrong frame and fed to the tracker; the first GGA then triggers a ~6,000 km startup recenter, and the bogus (0,0) poses remain in the 16-deep history for stale-timestamped detections. NavInputGuard cannot prevent this (skips two-pose checks with no previous pose; flag-only, nullable sink). No test pins the datum after a heading-first ingest; the full-stack integration test ingests HDT before GGA but masks the bug by placing own-ship at ~(0,0). Severity moderated to medium because under default config (auto-recenter on, sinks wired, GPS lock present at startup) the damage is a silent startup transient lasting until the first GGA, after which the provider self-corrects; it escalates (permanent wrong frame) only if auto-recenter is disabled or if ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter — which hold a non-sink datum_ copy — are constructed during the heading-only window. Fix direction: skip provider_.update() (or skip datum init) for poses lacking a real position fix, e.g., gate heading-only publishes on provider_.latest().has_value(), or make datum lazy-init require a position-valid pose.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Empty or garbled heading/COG fields parse to 0.0 and are published as authoritative heading — no finiteness or emptiness validation on any own-ship numeric field
  - `adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:246` (validation, confidence high)
  - description: HDT (line 246), HDG (line 277), and RMC SOG/COG (lines 200-202) use bare strtod with no empty-field or isfinite check. strtod("") returns 0.0, and strtod also accepts "nan"/"inf" tokens. An empty-field HDT (`$GPHDT,,T` — emitted by gyros while settling) publishes pose.heading_true_deg = 0.0 and pushes a 0-rad gyro sample; an empty HDG publishes magnetic_heading_deg = 0.0 (violating the struct's own 'NaN = not present' convention, OwnShipProvider.hpp:25) and feeds a GyroVsMagneticObservation with heading 0; an RMC with empty COG but positive SOG stores velocity (0, sog) = due north. Contrast: the ARPA and EO-IR adapters do validate their numeric fields via EdgeValidation; the own-ship adapter — whose outputs rotate every relative-bearing measurement — validates nothing.
  - failure_scenario: Gyro in settling mode emits `$GPHDT,,T*2F` (valid checksum). Pose heading becomes 0.0 deg. A radar TTM with relative bearing 90 deg while the true heading is 270 deg is projected at bearing 90 instead of 0 — the target is placed on the wrong side of the ship (up to 180 deg azimuth error at full range) and fed to the tracker as a normal-covariance measurement.
  - evidence: OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:246, 277, 200-202; no EdgeValidation include in the file; ArpaAdapter.cpp:103 shows the sibling adapters do gate on isFiniteValue. No test feeds empty heading/COG fields (test_own_ship_nmea*.cpp reviewed).
  - suggested_fix: Reject empty fields and non-finite parses (isFiniteValue) before publishing heading/velocity; treat empty HDT/HDG as 'no update'.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** wrapDegToPi wraps by repeated subtraction — an Inf or astronomically large parsed angle hangs the ingest thread forever
  - `adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:43` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: wrapDegToPi (lines 40-46) and the near-identical loop in gyroRateRadPerSec (lines 101-102) normalize with `while (rad > pi) rad -= 2*pi`. strtod returns HUGE_VAL (=Inf) on overflow (e.g. a corrupted field "1e999") and parses "INF" literally; Inf - 2*pi == Inf, so the loop never terminates. A finite-but-huge value (1e21) needs ~1e19 iterations — an effective hang. Reachable from HDT (pushGyroSample line 270 / wrap at 259), HDG (line 316), and RMC COG (line 234). The NMEA checksum is only an 8-bit XOR, so ~1/256 of randomly corrupted lines still validate; one such line freezes the whole time-driven engine (ingest never returns), which is worse than a wrong value and produces no diagnostic.
  - failure_scenario: Serial-line corruption turns an HDT heading field into "4e387" while the XOR checksum still matches (1/256 chance per corrupted line). parseNmea accepts it, strtod yields Inf, wrapDegToPi(Inf) loops forever inside ingest — the tracking pipeline stalls permanently with no error.
  - evidence: OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:40-46 (wrapDegToPi), 99-102 (gyroRateRadPerSec), callers at 234, 259, 270/66, 316; no finiteness guard on any of these paths (see previous finding); C99 strtod overflow/INF semantics.
  - suggested_fix: Guard with std::isfinite before wrapping and use std::remainder/fmod-based wrapping instead of iterative subtraction.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** RemoteTrackAdapter validates only lat/lon: NaN/Inf or non-PSD stated covariance and NaN velocity pass straight into the Measurement
  - `adapters/remote_track/RemoteTrackAdapter.cpp:48` (validation, confidence high)
  - description: ingest() gates on isPlausibleLatLon(r.lat_deg, r.lon_deg) only. r.position_covariance containing NaN/Inf is not isZero(), so line 48 emits R = NaN*3 on the default Position2D path (no opt-in needed); a non-PSD stated matrix (negative variance from a buggy feed) is likewise multiplied and forwarded. With accept_velocity=true, r.velocity_enu and r.velocity_covariance are also forwarded unchecked (lines 63-76), so a NaN velocity lands in m.value(2..3). The header (lines 81-84) and CLAUDE.md invariant #6 promise 'implausible / NaN' rejection at this edge, and downstream stages explicitly trust adapter output — a NaN R or value silently poisons the associated track's state/covariance (NaN spreads through the KF update; gating comparisons against NaN are all false).
  - failure_scenario: A VTS feed glitch (network decode error) delivers one report with position_covariance = [[NaN,0],[0,NaN]] and valid lat/lon. isZero() is false, so posR becomes NaN; the measurement associates with an existing confirmed track and the estimator update turns the track state/covariance to NaN — the vessel silently disappears from the output with no rejection counter incremented.
  - evidence: RemoteTrackAdapter.cpp:13-19 (only lat/lon check), 42-48, 59-76; rejected_ counter only counts lat/lon drops. tests/adapters/remote_track/test_remote_track_adapter.cpp has no NaN-covariance or NaN-velocity case (test list reviewed).
  - suggested_fix: Reject reports whose covariance entries or velocity components are non-finite (and optionally clamp/reject non-PSD stated covariance), incrementing rejected_.

- **[LOW/unverified]** Equirectangular reference for the UERE/velocity estimators is captured once and never re-anchored — east-axis scale error grows with latitude change over a long run
  - `adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:133` (correctness, confidence medium)
  - description: enu_ref_lat/lon are set on the first GGA and never updated (no reset on datum recenter, which the provider does handle for its own frame). East offsets use cos(ref_lat) (line 138-140), so after the ship changes latitude the east scale is off by cos(ref)/cos(current) — the code comment ('over the timescale of either sliding window the cos(lat) scale change is negligible') addresses within-window change, not the accumulated reference error. Velocity differences inherit the full scale error: a passage from 48N to 58N inflates GGA-derived east velocity by ~26%; combined with finding #1, a garbage first fix at (0,0) fixes cos(ref)=1 and mis-scales east by 1/cos(lat) (~1.66 at 53N) for the whole run.
  - failure_scenario: Multi-day coastal passage 48N to 58N without process restart, RMC feed lost (estimator fallback active): pose.velocity_enu east component reads ~26% high; own-ship velocity feeds CPA prediction, so CPA/TCPA against crossing traffic are computed from a systematically wrong own velocity.
  - evidence: OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:133-148; no writer of enu_ref_set_ = false anywhere (single assignment); provider datum recenter has no hook into the adapter.
  - suggested_fix: Re-anchor the equirectangular reference periodically (e.g. when the offset exceeds a few km) and clear the estimator windows on re-anchor.

- **[LOW/unverified]** AIS SOG accepted anywhere in [0, 1023) knots — the physically impossible 102.3..1022.9 band becomes velocity measurement content instead of being dropped
  - `adapters/ais/AisAdapter.cpp:38` (validation, confidence high)
  - description: has_speed accepts `*r.sog_knots < 1023.0`, but the adapter's own contract (AisAdapter.hpp:33) states valid SOG is [0, 102.2] knots with 1023 as the not-available sentinel. Values in between are neither valid nor the sentinel yet pass the gate and are emitted as PositionVelocity2D content. The most likely producer is the classic integrator bug of passing the raw 0.1-knot AIS field undivided (raw 1023 sentinel = '102.3 knots' would also slip through a correctly-scaled-then-mislabelled path): raw 123 (12.3 kn) becomes 123 kn = 63 m/s velocity content pulling the track hard.
  - failure_scenario: A consumer feeds the raw ITU-1371 SOG field (tenths of knots) as sog_knots: a vessel doing 25.6 kn arrives as 256 kn = 131.7 m/s; the gate passes it, the PV measurement drags the confirmed track's velocity to ~132 m/s, corrupting CPA and downstream kinematics with no edge rejection.
  - evidence: AisAdapter.cpp:37-38 vs the documented range at AisAdapter.hpp:33; tests only exercise 10.0 and 0.2 knots (test_ais_adapter.cpp) — no over-102.2 case.
  - suggested_fix: Tighten the gate to sog_knots <= 102.2 (drop anything above as implausible/sentinel).

Coverage notes (adapters-sensor): Scope fully read end-to-end: adapters/ais/AisAdapter.{hpp,cpp}, adapters/arpa/ArpaAdapter.{hpp,cpp}, adapters/eoir/EoIrAdapter.{hpp,cpp}, adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter.{hpp,cpp} + OwnShipProvider.hpp shim, adapters/remote_track/RemoteTrackAdapter.{hpp,cpp}, adapters/util/Nmea.{hpp,cpp}, adapters/util/EdgeValidation.{hpp,cpp}; plus the in-scope-adjacent code they call: core/own_ship/OwnShipProvider.cpp, core/projection/Projection.cpp, core/estimation/PolarVelocity.hpp, core/types/Timestamp.hpp; tests for all six adapter areas enumerated and key cases read. CLEAN: parseNmea checksum (XOR over chars between $/!, and *, both hex cases, trailing CR tolerated, empty fields preserved, '$GPXXX,*hh' single-empty-field case correct; strict missing-checksum rejection is documented policy); no AIVDM 6-bit/multi-fragment decoder exists anywhere in the tree (grep AIVDM/VDM empty) — the fragment-reassembly / fill-bit / two's-complement hints are N/A, AisAdapter consumes pre-decoded structs; AIS sentinels (lat 91/lon 181, SOG 1023, COG 3600 via <360 gate, heading 511, nav_status 15) all mapped to missing and pinned by tests; NaN in optional AIS fields safely fails comparison gates; sogCogToEnuVelocity Jacobian + iso floor and ENU (sin,cos) convention verified correct; projectRangeBearingToEnu math verified (polar Jacobian, heading-in-quadrature, isotropic GPS term); ArpaAdapter TTM field indices match NMEA TTM (fields[9] units legitimately applies to both distance and speed), K/N/S conversions correct (1852 / 1000 / 1609.344; 0.514444 / /3.6 / 0.44704), courseDeltaDeg wrap correct, TTM speed/course correctly kept out of recurring measurement content (birth prior + swap diagnostic only), strtod-0.0 range/bearing collapse correctly rejected via isPlausibleRange/isFiniteValue; parseDdmm size_t-underflow on short strings is caught by the deg_end>size() guard; GGA/RMC/HDG field indices verified against sentence layouts; RMC status A/V gate present; RMC-fresh-vs-estimator precedence and HDOP*UERE precedence match tests; OwnShipProvider sorted insert / poseAtOrBefore reverse walk / equal-timestamp latest-wins verified; RemoteTrackAdapter thinning per (station,id), inflation-XOR-default logic, circular-AIS guard all correct; Eigen usage clean (small fixed-size temporaries, correct 2x2 corner blocks in 4x4 R, no aliasing). Overflow candidates not promoted to findings: TTM empty/unknown units field silently treated as meters (nonstandard radar → target ~1852x too close, passes isPlausibleRange); parseDdmm accepts minutes >= 60 (garbled-but-in-range positions pass plausibility); ArpaAdapter TLL comment claims parseDdmm-failure 0.0 is caught by isPlausibleLatLon but 0.0 lat with valid lon IS in-range (garbled lat → equator measurement, likely gated out downstream but enters pipeline); pose.heading_true_deg has no validity flag (GGA-only consumer gets TTM/EO-IR relative bearings rotated against heading 0.0 silently — adjacent to finding 4); last_ttm_course_deg_ and last_emit_ maps grow unboundedly under churning remote/target ids (slow leak, bounded in practice for TTM 0-99); RemoteTrackAdapter out-of-order report (older timestamp) is thinned rather than evaluated (minor, safe direction); EoIr CameraDetection per-detection sigmas not validated (caller-supplied 0/negative sigma squares to a degenerate-but-nonnegative R). Known/by-design items from the brief were not re-reported.


## Batch B5-replay-metrics-periphery

### unit: adapters-replay (6 findings)

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** SOG from MarineCadastre/DMA-schema CSVs (knots) is consumed as m/s in the emit_velocity path
  - `adapters/replay/AisCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:168` (units, confidence high)
  - description: detectColumns (line 69) matches a bare `sog` header specifically so the documented external schemas load (the .hpp lists 'MarineCadastre: MMSI,BaseDateTime,LAT,LON,SOG,...' and DMA as auto-detected). MarineCadastre and DMA publish SOG in KNOTS, but line 168 feeds the raw field to sogCogToEnuVelocity, whose contract (core/estimation/PolarVelocity.hpp) is SOG in m/s; the code comment at lines 163-167 asserts 'CSV SOG is already m/s, so no knots conversion'. That is true only for the project-owned fixtures, which use a `sog_mps` header (tests/fixtures/sim_multisensor/generator/writer.py AIS_COLS; tests/fixtures/philos/README.md) — meaning the bare `sog` alias exists solely for the external schemas whose units it then misreads. The gate at line 185 also compares the knots value against kAisSogVelocityMinMps=0.5 m/s, and the AIS not-available sentinel SOG=102.3 (knots) would become a 102.3 m/s velocity measurement. tests/replay/test_ais_csv_replay_adapter.cpp only exercises `sog_mps` fixtures, so nothing pins the alias' units.
  - failure_scenario: loadAisCsv(path_to_marinecadastre.csv, datum, "ais", /*emit_velocity=*/true): a vessel reporting SOG=10.0 (knots, i.e. 5.14 m/s) yields a PositionVelocity2D measurement with |v| = 10.0 m/s — 1.94x the true speed — silently biasing every velocity-updated track; a moored vessel with sentinel SOG 102.3 emits a 102 m/s velocity.
  - evidence: AisCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:69 (`h == "sog"` alias), 166-171 (raw strtod into sog_mps), 185 (m/s threshold applied to the value); AisCsvReplayAdapter.hpp:18-21 (MarineCadastre/DMA schema support claim); PolarVelocity.hpp kAisSogVelocityMinMps and sogCogToEnuVelocity(sog_mps, ...) contract in m/s.
  - suggested_fix: Either treat a bare `sog`/`cog` header (MarineCadastre/DMA) as knots and convert (x0.514444), or restrict velocity emission to explicitly-united headers (`sog_mps`) and ignore bare `sog` for the velocity path; also reject the 102.3 sentinel.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Coastline parser dereferences missing "coordinates" key via const operator[] (assert in debug, UB in release) and lacks the malformed-input hardening its sibling static-obstacle parser got
  - `adapters/land/GeoJsonCoastline.cpp:54` (crash, confidence high)
  - description: Lines 54 and 56 do `geom["coordinates"]` on a const nlohmann::json without checking contains(). nlohmann's const operator[] with a missing key is documented UB: JSON_ASSERT fires in debug builds, and with NDEBUG it dereferences the end() iterator. A Feature `{"geometry":{"type":"Polygon"}}` (no coordinates — e.g. a truncated or tool-mangled chart export) crashes instead of being skipped, contradicting the parser's own tolerance contract ('Other geometry types are silently skipped'; header: rings/null geometries skipped). Additionally, line 43's nlohmann::json::parse is unguarded, so malformed JSON throws nlohmann::json::parse_error — not the std::runtime_error the header documents — and a non-object geometry value (e.g. "geometry": []) makes geom.value("type",...) throw type_error(306). The sibling GeoJsonStaticObstacles.cpp was explicitly hardened for exactly these cases (R7.2: parse wrapped and rethrown as runtime_error, contains() checks, per-feature try/catch); the coastline parser was left out. Sweep.cpp:434-442 catches std::exception so the bench survives the throw cases, but nothing catches for direct library consumers (integration-guide surface) or tests/replay/PhilosLabelReplay.hpp:259, and no catch helps the operator[] UB path. tests/land/test_geojson_coastline.cpp covers only well-formed inputs.
  - failure_scenario: loadCoastlineGeoJson on a chart file containing one feature with geometry {"type":"Polygon"} and no "coordinates": debug build aborts on assert; release build reads through an end() map iterator (UB — typically crash or garbage polygon). A syntactically corrupt file throws json::parse_error past a caller that catches only the documented std::runtime_error.
  - evidence: GeoJsonCoastline.cpp:43 (unguarded parse), 53-57 (geom["coordinates"] without contains()); contrast GeoJsonStaticObstacles.cpp:71-77 (guarded parse), 87-89 (contains("coordinates") check), 83/127 (per-feature try/catch).
  - suggested_fix: Mirror the R7.2 hardening: wrap parse and rethrow as std::runtime_error, and check geom.contains("coordinates") && geom["coordinates"].is_array() (plus geom.is_object()) before access, skipping bad features.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** parseTimeString cannot parse the DMA timestamp format the header claims to support — every row of a DMA CSV is silently dropped
  - `adapters/replay/AisCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:97` (data-loss, confidence medium)
  - description: The .hpp (line 21) lists the DMA schema ('# Timestamp,Type of mobile,MMSI,Latitude,Longitude,...') as auto-detected, and detectColumns indeed matches '# timestamp'. But real DMA (Danish Maritime Authority, aisdk) CSVs stamp that column as 'dd/mm/yyyy hh:mm:ss' (e.g. '23/11/2021 00:00:00'). parseTimeString's unix-float branch rejects it ('/' fails the all_of filter) and the ISO branch's sscanf pattern "%d-%d-%d%*c%d:%d:%d" requires dash separators, so it parses only 1 field and returns false; line 146 then `continue`s. Every row fails identically, so loadAisCsv returns an empty vector — the same result as a missing file, with no diagnostic. Header detection succeeding while every row is dropped makes the advertised DMA support non-functional. No test loads a DMA-format fixture (tests use unix_time headers only).
  - failure_scenario: loadAisCsv("aisdk-2021-11-23.csv", datum, "ais") on a genuine DMA export: header recognized, cols.time=0 found, then parseTimeString("23/11/2021 00:00:00") fails for all rows → returns {} silently; downstream (e.g. a bench scenario) treats it as fixtures-absent and skips.
  - evidence: AisCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:86-99 (both parse branches reject slash-separated dates), 146 (silent row drop); AisCsvReplayAdapter.hpp:21 (DMA schema claim).
  - suggested_fix: Add a dd/mm/yyyy HH:MM:SS branch (or general separator handling) to parseTimeString, or drop the DMA claim from the header; optionally return/report a rows-dropped count so a 100% parse failure is visible.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** loadOwnshipCsv performs no value validation: a blank/corrupt lat-lon field becomes a (0,0) pose that silently poisons every body-frame projection in its time window
  - `adapters/replay/OwnshipCsvReader.cpp:64` (validation, confidence high)
  - description: Rows are accepted whenever they have enough fields (line 61); lat/lon/heading are strtod'd with no finite/range/null-island check (lines 64-66), unlike the AIS loader in the same directory (which rejects |lat|>90, |lon|>180 and 0/0). A row like '1622505600,,,' yields OwnShipPose{lat=0, lon=0, heading=0} at a valid timestamp. feedOwnshipHistory pushes it into OwnShipProvider, whose default DatumRecenterPolicy (enable_auto_recenter=true, 30 km) then recenters the datum to Null Island and back on the next good fix; worse, poseAtOrBefore(t) serves the corrupt pose to loadPlotCsvBodyFrame, loadRadarTruthCsv and loadCameraBearingsCsv for every measurement timestamped between the corrupt fix and the next one, projecting those plots/bearings from geodetic (0,0) — ENU coordinates thousands of km off — which the tracker ingests as valid measurements (core trusts adapters per invariant #6, but this adapter validates nothing). This is the 'validate at the edges' invariant applied to nothing.
  - failure_scenario: ownship.csv with one truncated row mid-file (fields present but empty, e.g. from a partial write): all radar plots in the [corrupt_fix, next_fix) window are placed ~7,000 km away in ENU, spawning garbage tracks / gating chaos, while the run completes without any error; the datum also recenters twice, silently.
  - evidence: OwnshipCsvReader.cpp:58-68 (no isfinite/range checks, no null-island filter); contrast AisCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:149-150; OwnShipProvider.hpp DatumRecenterPolicy defaults (auto-recenter on, 30 km) and poseAtOrBefore contract.
  - suggested_fix: Skip rows whose time/lat/lon fail strtod (endptr check) or fall outside [-90,90]/[-180,180], and drop the (0,0) null-island case, mirroring the AIS loader.

- **[LOW/unverified]** loadPlotCsv keeps '\r' in the last field; on a CRLF plot CSV the station lookup fails for every row and the whole file silently loads as empty
  - `adapters/replay/PlotCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:84` (parsing, confidence high)
  - description: splitLine here (lines 28-42) does not strip '\r' — unlike the splitLine in AisCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:31 and OwnshipCsvReader.cpp:22, which skip it explicitly. The plot schema's LAST column is `station` (header doc line 34: tod,...,amp_max,station), so on a CRLF-terminated file every station value becomes "kattwyk\r", stations.find() misses (loadStations is immune because station is its FIRST column), and line 87 drops every row. loadPlotCsv returns empty; HaxrScenarioRun then produces a Scenario with empty measurements, which Sweep.cpp:270 silently `continue`s — indistinguishable from fixtures-absent. Numeric trailing fields elsewhere are safe (strtod stops at '\r'), so this only bites string-keyed last columns, which is exactly loadPlotCsv. The same non-stripping splitLine is copied into CameraBearingCsvReader, HaxrTruthLoader and RadarTruthCsvReader, but their last-used fields are numeric, so only loadPlotCsv fails this way.
  - failure_scenario: A HAXR/Pohang plot CSV regenerated or re-saved with CRLF line endings (Windows editor / git autocrlf on an untracked data file): every row dropped, bench reports the haxr scenario as skipped with no error, and the gtest path fails only via its 'plot CSV parsed empty' assert if that test is run.
  - evidence: PlotCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:28-42 (no '\r' handling) vs AisCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:31 and OwnshipCsvReader.cpp:22 (explicit '\r' skip); station consumed at line 84-87; schema in PlotCsvReplayAdapter.hpp:33-34; Sweep.cpp:270 silent skip.
  - suggested_fix: Skip '\r' in this splitLine (and the copies in CameraBearingCsvReader/HaxrTruthLoader/RadarTruthCsvReader) to match the AIS/ownship readers.

- **[LOW/unverified]** AIS-as-truth builder merges all MMSI-0/absent-MMSI rows into truth_id 0, creating one interleaved phantom truth target
  - `adapters/benchmark/ReplayScenarioRun.cpp:70` (correctness, confidence medium)
  - description: loadAisCsv only sets hints.mmsi when the parsed MMSI is nonzero (AisCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:208), but keeps the row as a measurement. aisMeasurementToTruth (lines 65-72) leaves TruthSample::truth_id at its default 0 when the hint is absent, so every AIS row with MMSI 0 (a common real-world misconfiguration, present in MarineCadastre/DMA data) or an unparseable MMSI field lands in a single truth trajectory id=0. resampleTruthToClock then treats that as one target and linearly interpolates between positions of physically different vessels (bridging gaps up to 30 s, ReplayScenarioRun.cpp:216), injecting a teleporting phantom into the truth set that distorts GOSPA/cardinality for the philos scoring path. Whether the curated philos fixture currently contains MMSI-0 rows cannot be verified here (fixtures gitignored), so impact on today's numbers is unconfirmed; the code path is unconditional for any AIS CSV with such rows.
  - failure_scenario: PHILOS_CLIP pointed at a clip whose ais.csv contains rows from two different vessels broadcasting MMSI 0: both become truth_id 0; resampling produces a single truth target whose position jumps between the two hulls each tick, charging the tracker phantom misses/false-matches every evaluation step.
  - evidence: ReplayScenarioRun.cpp:65-72 (truth_id only set from hints.mmsi), Truth.hpp truth_id{0} default, AisCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:151-155+208 (mmsi=0 rows kept but hint dropped), TruthResample.cpp interpolation per truth_id.
  - suggested_fix: Skip measurements without an mmsi hint when building AIS-as-truth (or key them by a per-row unique id so they never merge).

Coverage notes (adapters-replay): Scope fully read end-to-end: adapters/replay/{AisCsvReplayAdapter,AutoferryJsonReplay,CameraBearingCsvReader,HaxrTruthLoader,OwnshipCsvReader,PlotCsvReplayAdapter,RadarTruthCsvReader}.{cpp,hpp}, adapters/land/GeoJsonCoastline.*, adapters/static/GeoJsonStaticObstacles.*, adapters/benchmark/{ReplayScenarioRun,SimScenarioRun,SimMultisensorScenarioRun,RbadScenarioRun}.*. Cross-checked against core/projection/Projection.cpp, core/estimation/{PolarVelocity.hpp,MeasurementModels.cpp}, core/scenario/{Truth.hpp,TruthResample.cpp}, core/land/CoastlineGeometry.hpp, core/types/Timestamp.hpp, core/own_ship/OwnShipProvider.hpp, core/benchmark/Sweep.cpp call sites, and tests (test_ais_csv_replay_adapter, test_geojson_coastline, test_haxr_ospa, test_camera_bearing_loader, test_autoferry_json_replay, test_rbad_scenario_run).  Verified CLEAN (checked, no defect): (1) Truth sorting per the fragmentation hint — AutoferryJsonReplay restamps scans to scan-max time, sorts (time,id) and dedups; RadarTruthCsvReader, RbadScenarioRun, loadSimTruthCsv sort; HaxrTruthLoader returns unsorted but BOTH call sites handle it (ReplayScenarioRun.cpp:266 sorts with an explicit comment; test_haxr_ospa scans truth windows order-independently).
