(2) GeoJSON coordinate order — parseRing emits (lon,lat) exactly matching LandPolygon's documented convention; static obstacles read [lon,lat] correctly; CRS ignored silently is true but harmless for the WGS84 sources used. (3) RbadScenarioRun applies no own-ship motion (single fixed station at ENU origin, nominal datum only labels the frame); its (seconds(),id) sort comparator is a valid strict weak ordering (double conversion is monotone in nanos). (4) Marine-bearing→ENU conventions in PlotCsv (station + body-frame), CameraBearingCsvReader (pi/2 − marine, wrapAngle at edge) and RadarTruthCsvReader all agree with Projection.cpp (east=r·sin, north=r·cos); AutoferryJsonReplay's unwrapped pi/2−b_ned bearing values are safe because EKF/UKF/IMM wrap Bearing2D innovations (MeasurementModels.cpp:95-97, ImmEstimator.cpp:215). (5) sogCogToEnuVelocity Jacobian re-derived and correct; loader gates (SOG threshold, COG in [0,360), nav_status 1/5 suppression, sentinel COG 360) correct for m/s inputs. (6) TruthResample cannot divide by zero even with duplicate (time,id) samples from philos Union mode (bracket requires a.time < tick <= b.time so gap > 0); interpolation weight bounded (0,1]. (7) Autoferry hand-rolled JSON parser bounds-safe (u-escape skip caught by loop condition; duplicate keys keep-first; number/bool/null parse guarded); NED→ENU (E,N)←(N,E) swap consistent across measurements, bearings and truth; fd-velocity dt>0 guarded. (8) GeoJsonStaticObstacles fully guarded (R7.2): contains()/type/finite/range checks, per-feature try/catch, parse rethrown as runtime_error, negative radii clamped. (9) Eigen usage: no aliasing hazards, block sizes correct (4x4 R assembly, 2x2 corners), no default-constructed-matrix reads. (10) Timestamp::fromSeconds truncation (~240 ns ulp at 2026 epochs) applies identically to measurements and truth — no cross-frame mismatch. (11) Empty-file/missing-file/fixture-absent paths return empty and callers skip (Sweep.cpp:270).  Overflow one-liners (below reporting bar): parseTimeString silently ignores ISO timezone suffixes (+02:00 treated as UTC) and accepts date-only strings as unix floats ('2026-07-09' → 2026.0 s epoch); presence of a nav_status column adds it to max_col so ragged short rows drop even with emit_velocity=false (slight deviation from the 'OFF is bit-identical' contract on ragged files); HAXR_FEED_AIS truncates the 64-bit FNV uid hash to a 32-bit mmsi hint (small collision risk across many vessels); SimMultisensorScenarioRun::generate ignores with_camera_ — an imazu fixture dir containing camera_bearings.csv would feed EoIr measurements not covered by the descriptor's detection table; splitLine variants have no quoted-field handling (documented for owned fixtures, but a MarineCadastre quoted VesselName containing a comma shifts the Status column into arbitrary numeric fields); OwnshipCsvReader's header detection lacks the keep-first guard the AIS loader has (a file with both 'time' and 'timestamp' columns uses the last); PhilosScenarioRun comment 'no recentering occurs' is inaccurate for >30 km ownship histories (recenters fire during feedOwnshipHistory; final frame remains self-consistent so no defect). Known/by-design items (fixed bench datums, extraction boundary, no-birth zone, PMBM/MHT trade-offs) were excluded per instructions; gitignored fixture/data contents were not reviewed.

### unit: scenario-metrics (8 findings)

- **[MEDIUM/CONFIRMED]** tgospa_smooth_m silently degenerates to all-missed on replay scenarios: smoothed trajectory points matched to steps by exact nanosecond equality
  - `core/benchmark/Metrics.cpp:451` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: computeTGospaSmoothImpl maps smoothed PMBM trajectory points to bench steps via time_to_idx.find(p.time.nanos()) — exact int64 nanosecond equality between the trajectory point's timestamp and the BenchStep time. Trajectory points are stamped with the scan (measurement-batch) time (PmbmTracker.cpp appendTrajectoryPoint uses current_time_, the raw measurement timestamp). But replay scenarios (philos, HAXR — adapters/benchmark/ReplayScenarioRun.cpp:216) resample truth onto a synthetic 1 Hz clock: ticks are Timestamp::fromSeconds(t_min.seconds() + k*1.0), which are not measurement timestamps. Raw radar/AIS timestamps are fractional epoch seconds, so essentially no smoothed point ever matches a step time; every point is dropped as 'off-grid'. The est set fed to tgospa() is then empty (or has empty sample maps), and tgospa_smooth_m equals the pure all-truth-missed cardinality cost. The header comment's justification ('the bench snapshots are at truth ticks' so finer grids 'still align') is false whenever truth ticks are not a subset of scan times — which is every resampled replay, and also unanchored AutoFerry (truth times = max per-scan GT target time, not detection times).
  - failure_scenario: Run the bench with any PMBM config (trajectory_window_scans=50 in makePmbmConfig) on philos or HAXR. Sweep.cpp:596-599 calls the smoothed computeMetrics overload; every smoothed point fails the exact-nanos lookup; tgospa_smooth_m is emitted as a large constant equal to n_steps × per-step missed cost. Anyone comparing tgospa_raw vs tgospa_smooth on that CSV concludes the RTS smoother catastrophically loses every track, when in fact the metric never saw the smoothed trajectories. Conversely a real smoother regression on replays is indistinguishable from this artifact.
  - evidence: core/benchmark/Metrics.cpp:434-455 (time_to_idx built from step.time.nanos(); 'if (it == time_to_idx.end()) continue; // off-grid point'); core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:143-154 (p.time = t = current_time_ = scan time); adapters/benchmark/ReplayScenarioRun.cpp:216 (resampleTruthToClock(period 1.0)); core/scenario/TruthResample.cpp:59-60 (ticks = fromSeconds(t_min.seconds()+k*period), a grid unrelated to measurement times); adapters/replay/AisCsvReplayAdapter.cpp:90/114 (fractional epoch-second measurement timestamps).
  - suggested_fix: Match by nearest step time within a tolerance (e.g. half the median scan interval), or record the step index alongside each snapshot and have the tracker tag trajectory points with a scan counter instead of relying on timestamp identity.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full failing path and found decisive empirical confirmation in checked-in baseline data.  Code path: (1) core/benchmark/Metrics.cpp:436-452 — computeTGospaSmoothImpl builds time_to_idx from result.steps[k].time.nanos() and drops any smoothed point whose timestamp is not an exact int64-nanosecond match ('// off-grid point'). (2) BenchStep::time is the TRUTH-group tick (BenchRunner.cpp:104/249: step.time = g.time), while measurements are processed in scans at their own raw timestamps (flushScansUpTo, BenchRunner.cpp:275-286). (3) PmbmTracker::processBatch predicts to the scan's max MEASUREMENT time (PmbmTracker.cpp:1367-1373, current_time_ = to in predict), and appendTrajectoryPoint stamps p.time = current_time_ (PmbmTracker.cpp:148-149, call sites 675/717/733/743/752/990/1036). So smoothed trajectory points carry measurement times, steps carry truth-tick times. (4) Replay scenarios resample truth onto a synthetic 1 Hz grid: ReplayScenarioRun.cpp:216 resampleTruthToClock(period 1.0); TruthResample.cpp:59-60 ticks = fromSeconds(t_min.seconds()+k) — a grid unrelated to fractional-epoch-second radar/AIS measurement times, so essentially no point matches. (5) With est sample maps empty, tgospa (core/scenario/TGospa.cpp:26,37) charges every truth sample the miss cost c^p/alpha, giving a pure all-missed constant. (6) Sweep.cpp:596-599 calls the smoothed overload for every PMBM config; makePmbmConfig sets trajectory_window_scans=50 (Config.cpp:353), so smoothed maps are non-empty — the mechanism is the time mismatch, not an empty map.  Decisive empirical fingerprint (checked-in baselines): the all-missed value is c*sqrt(N/2) with c=20 (gospa_cutoff_m default, p=2, alpha=2) and integer truth-sample count N. philos tgospa_smooth=213.073 decodes to N=227 exactly (20*sqrt(227/2)=213.0728); autoferry_scenario2=788.416 decodes to N=3108 exactly. philos vs philos_radartruth (different truth POSITIONS, same ids/clock) give different tgospa_raw (721.529 vs 721.51) but bit-identical tgospa_smooth (213.073) — only possible if positions never enter the cost, i.e. zero est contribution. And docs/baselines/pmbm_vs_mht_review_20260624.md shows K=1 vs K=3+xp byte-identical tgospa_smooth on philos and all UNANCHORED autoferry scenarios (constant, config-independent), while anchored autoferry (truth-anchor measurements injected AT truth times, AutoferryJsonReplay.cpp:364-381, so some scan times do equal step times) and synthetics show config-dependent differences — precisely the alignment boundary the claim predicts.  Guards/tests: no test anywhere references tgospa_smooth or the smoothed computeMetrics overload (tests/benchmark/test_metrics.cpp uses the scalar overload only), so nothing pins or contradicts this. The header comment at Metrics.cpp:420-425 asserting alignment ('the bench snapshots are at truth ticks') is false for resampled replays, as claimed.  Severity: I rate this medium rather than high. It is confined to the bench metric tgospa_smooth — no production tracking behavior is affected — and on replays it produces a config-independent constant on both sides of any A/B, so it hides signal rather than flipping winners between configs. However, it has already emitted misleading numbers into decision documents (pmbm_vs_mht_review_20260624.md presents the constants as real smoother scores; autoferry smooth 788 > raw 512 falsely suggests smoothing is catastrophic), and it silently invalidates the entire real-replay arm of any RTS-smoother evaluation, in a project whose eval integrity is treated as load-bearing (D2 external GOSPA cross-check). Note the smoothed metric is additionally window-limited (collectSmoothedTrajectories returns only end-of-run-alive Bernoullis' last 50 scans), so even where times align it covers a small suffix of the run — a further reason smooth-vs-raw comparisons from this column are not meaningful, though that part is arguably by design.
  - verifier corrected details: core/benchmark/Metrics.cpp:451 — computeTGospaSmoothImpl matches smoothed PMBM trajectory points to bench steps by exact nanosecond equality (time_to_idx.find(p.time.nanos())). Trajectory points are stamped with scan (measurement) time (PmbmTracker.cpp:1367-1373 predict(t_max of scan) -> current_time_; appendTrajectoryPoint p.time = current_time_), while BenchStep::time is the truth tick (BenchRunner.cpp:104/185/249). On replay scenarios (philos, HAXR) truth is resampled to a synthetic 1 Hz clock (ReplayScenarioRun.cpp:216, TruthResample.cpp:58-60) whose ticks are not measurement timestamps, so effectively every smoothed point is dropped as 'off-grid'; the est set is empty and tgospa_smooth_m degenerates to the pure all-truth-missed cost, a config-independent constant. Confirmed quantitatively in checked-in baselines: philos 213.073 = 20*sqrt(227/2) and autoferry_scenario2 788.416 = 20*sqrt(3108/2) (exact integer missed-sample counts); philos vs philos_radartruth differ in tgospa_raw but are bit-identical in tgospa_smooth; pmbm_vs_mht_review_20260624.md shows K=1 vs K=3+xp identical smooth on all unanchored replays but differing on synthetics and (partially aligned) anchored autoferry, where truth-anchor measurements share truth timestamps. Unanchored autoferry is also affected (truth time = max per-scan GT label time, not detection time; AutoferryJsonReplay.cpp:332-336). No test covers tgospa_smooth. Scope: bench metric only — no production tracking impact, and as a constant on both A/B arms it hides signal rather than flipping config winners — hence medium, but it has already published misleading smoother numbers on replay rows in baseline docs, and a real smoother regression on replays would be invisible. The justification comment at Metrics.cpp:420-425 is false for resampled replays. Additional context: collectSmoothedTrajectories (PmbmTracker.cpp:2086) only returns end-of-run-alive Bernoullis' last trajectory_window_scans (50) points, so even on aligned scenarios the smooth column covers only a suffix of the run.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Comparator marks worsening signed/target-valued metrics as improvements (card_err_mean, nees_*, nis_coverage, etc. default to lower-is-better)
  - `core/benchmark/Comparator.cpp:59` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: isLowerBetter() returns true for every metric except lifetime_ratio. Sweep emits metrics for which 'lower' is NOT better: card_err_mean is signed (ideal 0; more-negative = worse under-counting), nees_mean/nis_mean have ideal value = dof (2 for NEES; lower means overconservative covariance, and a divergent filter dropping samples can also lower it), nees_coverage_95/nis_coverage_95 have ideal 0.95, nis_trace_ratio and scan_interval_s are direction-free. renderComparison prints an up-triangle 'improvement' indicator whenever such a metric decreases.
  - failure_scenario: Baseline run has card_err_mean = +0.5 (slight over-count); candidate config has card_err_mean = -2.0 (misses two real vessels on average). The comparison table renders '0.5 -> -2 (-2.5 ▲)' — flagged as an improvement — steering an A/B decision toward a config that under-counts targets. Similarly a filter whose NEES coverage drops from 0.95 to 0.60 (badly overconfident) renders as ▲.
  - evidence: core/benchmark/Comparator.cpp:59-63 ('Anything not in this map is treated as lower-is-better'), :98-102 (indicatorFor). Sweep.cpp:128 emits card_err_mean, :163-190 emit nees_*/nis_* rows. tests/benchmark/test_compare.cpp only pins arrows for ospa-style metrics; no test covers signed metrics.
  - suggested_fix: Add a third category (target-valued / direction-free) rendering a neutral indicator, and register card_err_mean (|delta from 0|), coverage (|delta from 0.95|), and nees/nis means (|delta from dof|) explicitly.

- **[LOW/unverified]** Additive builders round-trip scan times through lossy double seconds; on epoch-scale bases injected measurements/truth land on different timestamps than the base scan
  - `core/scenario/Builders.cpp:100` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: distinctScanTimes() extracts scan times as m.time.seconds() (double) and the additive builders (addFixedClutter/addAnchoredBoats/addStopGoBoat/addUniformClutter) re-create Timestamps via Timestamp::fromSeconds(t), which truncates (static_cast<int64>(seconds*1e9)). For nanosecond values beyond 2^53 (epoch-scale timestamps, ~1.7e18 ns), fromSeconds(seconds(N)) != N for ~99.8% of values (empirically verified: errors up to ±316 ns). Injected clutter/boat measurements then carry a timestamp a few hundred ns off the base scan, so BenchRunner/HarnessBatched exact-time scan grouping puts them in a separate scan, and addAnchoredBoats/addStopGoBoat truth samples land on a different tick than co-temporal base truth — exactly the truth-fragmentation failure mode this project hit twice (2026-06-10, 2026-07-02). Currently latent: the only callers (adapters/benchmark/SimScenarioRun.cpp, tests) use small synthetic time bases where the round-trip is exact (verified for 0.1 s steps up to 6000 s).
  - failure_scenario: Someone composes addUniformClutter or addAnchoredBoats onto a replay-derived Scenario (philos/HAXR base with unix-epoch timestamps) — the natural next step for clutter-injection experiments on real data. Injected returns silently form their own one-measurement scans a few hundred ns from the real scan (extra PMBM misdetection cycles, different association), and anchored-boat truth fragments each evaluation step into two truth groups, corrupting cardinality/identity metrics with no error.
  - evidence: core/scenario/Builders.cpp:97-104 (distinctScanTimes via .seconds()), :659-664/:690-699 (fromSeconds(t) on new measurements/truth); core/types/Timestamp.hpp:18-20 (truncating fromSeconds); Python IEEE-double check: 99791/100000 random nanos in [1.7e18,1.8e18] fail fromSeconds(seconds(N))==N.
  - suggested_fix: Have distinctScanTimes return Timestamps (exact nanos) and stamp injected measurements/truth with the original Timestamp, not a re-derived double.

- **[LOW/unverified]** TGospa caps pair cost at c^p, making arbitrarily-far truth-est 'matches' cost-equal to miss+false; recorded assignments at any distance can charge spurious switch penalties
  - `core/scenario/TGospa.cpp:34` (correctness, confidence medium)
  - description: gospaCostAndAssignment uses cost(i,j) = min(d^p, c^p), unlike the validated Gospa.cpp kernel which uses raw d^p. With alpha=2, matching a pair at distance >= c costs exactly c^p — identical to leaving both unmatched (c^p/2 + c^p/2). The per-scan total is unaffected, but the Hungarian tie-break can record truth->est pairs at unbounded distance into assignment_out, and the switch penalty (line 88-96) fires gamma^p whenever that recorded est id changes between scans. Gospa.hpp's documented convention ('a pair is matched only when d^p < 2c^p/alpha') is broken here — the guarantee that matched implies d < c does not hold.
  - failure_scenario: A truth vessel is missed by the tracker for a stretch while short-lived phantom tracks (new ids each time, common in PMBM/MHT clutter runs) exist elsewhere in the scene. At each scan the tie between 'match truth to far phantom' and 'miss + false' is resolved arbitrarily by the solver; if it matches, each phantom id turnover charges an extra switch_penalty^p, inflating tgospa_raw_m for that config by an amount unrelated to any real identity error — a deterministic but spurious penalty that can differ between configs being A/B-compared.
  - evidence: core/scenario/TGospa.cpp:26-35 (cap = pow(cutoff,p); cost = min(pow(d,p), cap)) vs core/scenario/Gospa.cpp:48-50 (uncapped d^p); assignment recorded at :47-49 regardless of distance; switch penalty applied at :88-96 keyed on that assignment.
  - suggested_fix: Use uncapped d^p in the pair block (identical total under alpha=2, since unmatch is then strictly cheaper for d>c) so recorded matches are guaranteed d < c, matching the Gospa.cpp convention.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Ticks clamped to a dropout-gap endpoint get velocity finite-differenced ACROSS the refused gap instead of from the adjacent presence interval
  - `core/scenario/TruthResample.cpp:97` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: When a bracket a->b exceeds max_gap_s, position is correctly clamped to the gap endpoint, but the velocity uses clampVelocity(track, hi-1) for endpoint a, which returns fdVelocity(track[hi-1], track[hi]) — the finite difference across the very gap the function refuses to bridge for position (and likewise for endpoint b when b is the track's last sample, via the i+1==size fallback). The header doc says velocity comes from 'the adjacent segment (toward the interior)'; for a the interior segment is the one BEFORE a. Displacement over a long dropout divided by the gap duration bears no relation to the vessel's speed.
  - failure_scenario: Philos/HAXR replay (resampleTruthToClock(1.0, 30.0)): a vessel doing 5 m/s has a 10-minute AIS dropout during which it loops back near its start; net displacement 30 m. The tick that snaps to the gap's leading sample reports truth velocity 0.05 m/s. If the tracker still holds the (assigned, within 100 m) track there, computeRmse adds a sample with ~5 m/s SOG error and an arbitrary COG error, contaminating sog_rmse_mps / cog_rmse_deg — worst for per-truth breakdowns of sparse targets where a few samples dominate the mean.
  - evidence: core/scenario/TruthResample.cpp:92-103 (gap branch: clampVelocity(track, hi-1) / clampVelocity(track, hi)) and :23-28 (clampVelocity uses fd(track[i], track[i+1]) when i+1 exists — for i=hi-1 that IS the gap segment); TruthResample.hpp:19-21 documents 'velocity from the adjacent segment' intent.
  - suggested_fix: At a gap's leading endpoint use fd(track[hi-2], track[hi-1]) when available (interior segment before a); at a trailing endpoint that is the last sample, use the segment before the gap only if it is itself <= max_gap_s, else fall back to the sample's own stored velocity.

- **[LOW/unverified]** countIdSwitches keys truth by slot index with cardinality frozen from the first step: time-varying truth misattributes tracks across targets and drops late-appearing targets
  - `core/scenario/Metrics.cpp:11` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: countIdSwitches sets k = steps.front().truth.size() and walks per-step truth slots by index i (< k), keeping last[i] across steps. ScenarioStep::truth is a bare position vector built per tick in file order, so if a target is absent at one tick the remaining targets' indices shift and last[i] is compared against a different physical target's track id, manufacturing or hiding switches; any truth slot beyond the first step's count is never scored at all. The benchmark-side computeContinuity was explicitly rewritten to key by truth_id for exactly this reason (its own comment: 'slot keying there counts file layout, not tracker behaviour'), but the scenario-side helper still slot-keys.
  - failure_scenario: A scenario where target 1's truth is absent for a mid-run tick (or a target appears after t0): at that tick slot 0 holds target 2's position; if target 2's track id differs from target 1's, a phantom switch is counted; if a third target enters late, its id churn is invisible. All current callers (tests/scenario/*, tests/sim/*) use constant-cardinality truth, so the defect is latent — but any new scenario test with births/deaths silently gets wrong switch counts.
  - evidence: core/scenario/Metrics.cpp:9-30 (k from front step; last[] indexed by slot; loop bound i < k). Contrast core/benchmark/Metrics.cpp:234-296 (computeContinuity keyed by truth_id, with tests ContinuityKeyedByTruthIdNotSlot and ContinuityTimeVaryingCardinality). tests/scenario/test_metrics.cpp only exercises fixed 1-target steps.
  - suggested_fix: Carry truth_id in ScenarioStep (or reuse the benchmark assignPerStep/computeContinuity pair) and key last-assignment by truth_id.

- **[LOW/unverified]** Sweep CSV writes metric values at default 6-significant-digit precision; round-trip through CsvReader loses bits and CSV-diff 'byte-identical' checks can false-negative
  - `core/benchmark/CsvWriter.cpp:52` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: writeCsv streams r.value with the stream's default precision (6 significant digits), unlike GospaExport and PmbmDiagRecorder which deliberately set max_digits10 for round-trip-exact doubles. All baseline CSVs (bench/baseline_matrix.cpp writes through this path with no precision set) are therefore quantized to ~1e-6 relative. Two consequences: (a) values read back by readCsv/compare differ from the computed metrics in the last ~11 bits; (b) two genuinely different runs whose metrics differ only below 1e-6 relative produce byte-identical CSVs, so the project's routine 'byte-identical / inert knob' verification via CSV diff can pass when the runs actually diverged (the knife-edge / inertness regime this repo repeatedly probes).
  - failure_scenario: A supposedly-inert config knob shifts gospa_mean from 63.10437201 to 63.10437992. The emitted CSV shows '63.1044' for both; a diff-based A/B (or the comparator, whose no-change threshold is |delta|<1e-9 on the truncated values) reports the knob byte-identical/inert, when the tracker output actually changed — masking the first small step of a real divergence.
  - evidence: core/benchmark/CsvWriter.cpp:50-53 (os << r.value, no precision call anywhere in the file); bench/baseline_matrix.cpp:268-273 (plain ofstream, writeCsv); contrast core/benchmark/GospaExport.cpp:19 and PmbmDiagRecorder.hpp:35-36 (max_digits10 with an explicit 'round-trip exact ... determinism check' rationale).
  - suggested_fix: os.precision(std::numeric_limits<double>::max_digits10) before emitting rows (header values too), matching GospaExport.

- **[LOW/unverified]** Label row with t_start set but t_end blank becomes a never-active window (t_end_s=0) instead of open-ended
  - `core/benchmark/ExistenceLabel.cpp:71` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: covers_whole_clip requires BOTH t_start_s and t_end_s blank; a half-blank row falls through to parseDoubleOr(f[6], 0.0), producing window [t_start_s, 0]. activeAtUnix then requires rel >= t_start_s && rel <= 0 — impossible for any t_start_s > 0 — so the label is silently active at no time in the clip. The natural authoring intent of 'starts at 120 s, no end' is 'until clip end'; the parser turns it into 'never', and the header spec only defines the both-blank case, so nothing flags the row.
  - failure_scenario: A label CSV row 'r5,rank9,53.54,9.93,80,120,,KEEP_VESSEL,video,high,appears at 2:00' (vessel enters at 120 s, end blank). The KEEP_VESSEL gate consuming these labels never sees the region active, so a tracker that suppresses that vessel passes the label-aware philos gate that exists precisely to catch it. No parse error, no test covers half-blank rows (test_existence_label.cpp only pins both-set and both-blank).
  - evidence: core/benchmark/ExistenceLabel.cpp:67-71 (covers_whole_clip = blank_start && blank_end; t_end_s = parseDoubleOr(f[6], 0.0)); ExistenceLabel.hpp:60-64 (activeAtUnix: rel >= t_start_s && rel <= t_end_s); tests/benchmark/test_existence_label.cpp has no half-blank case.
  - suggested_fix: Blank t_end -> t_end_s = +infinity (and blank t_start -> -infinity), or reject half-blank rows loudly.

Coverage notes (scenario-metrics): Read every file in scope end-to-end: core/scenario/{Harness,HarnessBatched,HarnessBatchedMht,HarnessBatchedPmbm,Builders,Gospa,TGospa,Ospa,Metrics,Truth,TruthResample} and core/benchmark/{Sweep,BenchRunner,BenchSink,Metrics,Comparator,Consistency,Config,CsvReader,CsvWriter,ExistenceLabel,GospaExport,MarkdownRenderer,PmbmDiagRecorder,ScenarioRun}; cross-checked callers in bench/, adapters/benchmark/SimScenarioRun.cpp, adapters/benchmark/ReplayScenarioRun.cpp, adapters/replay/* loaders, core/pmbm/PmbmTracker trajectory recording, and the tests mirroring each unit. Checked clean: Ospa (rectangular Hungarian, surplus charge, empty-set cases, cutoff clipping); Gospa callers (computeOspa/GospaPerStep, decomposition identity, gospa_rms aggregation, GospaExport writes max_digits10 round-trip-exact and re-scores the exact BenchResult); Consistency NIS/NEES (chi-square dof handling incl. exact m=1/2 one-sided quantiles, Wilson-Hilferty band divided by N which is the correct Bar-Shalom form, Welford mean, LDLT singular/negative-pivot rejection paths, NEES gate reuse); benchmark Metrics continuity/RMSE keyed by truth_id with tests pinning varying cardinality and slot reordering; percentile (q=0/0.5/1 bounds); assignPerStep (infinite-cost forbidden cells double-checked with isfinite); BenchRunner scan grouping + truth grouping preconditions (sortTruthByTime is merged in Builders; replay loaders sort; AutoferryJsonReplay restamps per-scan truth times and dedups); SinkGuard exception safety; Sweep lifetimes (det/asc declaration order, estimator/occupancy/coastline/obstacle shared_ptrs outliving the synchronous run, bias-hook captures) and loop order; CsvReader/MarkdownRenderer/BenchSink/PmbmDiagRecorder; Builders math hand-checked (coordinated-turn position integral, speed-change three-phase kinematics with stop clamp, crossing/convoy/lane geometry, RNG seeding determinism). Empirically verified (IEEE-double emulation) that Timestamp round-trip is exact for sim-scale times but lossy at epoch scale, grounding the Builders finding. Overflow one-liners not promoted to findings: (1) makePmbmConfig comment says phantom-birth gate 0.05 but sets min_new_bernoulli_existence=0.5 (Config.cpp:391-400) — comment/code mismatch only, derived configs override to 0.05; (2) Sweep wires setStaticObstacleModel twice if a config enabled both use_static_obstacle_model and use_live_occupancy_model (last-wins, documented mutually exclusive but not asserted); (3) TGospa does not charge half-switches through unassigned gaps (documented LP-relaxation approximation); (4) TruthResample rescans each track from index 0 per tick — O(ticks×samples), performance only; (5) NisCollector trace-ratio mean divides by all accepted samples though tr_R==0 samples contribute nothing (tiny bias); (6) countIdSwitches ignores tracks with id.value==0 as a sentinel; (7) resampled TruthSample velocity discards loader-provided SOG-derived velocity for multi-sample tracks (documented improve-next); (8) ExistenceLabel splitN shifts fields if evidence/confidence contain commas (documented no-quoting CSV). Not re-reviewed per instructions: the Gospa/Hungarian kernel internals (externally validated), gitignored fixtures, and the known/by-design list.

### unit: periphery (6 findings)

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Canonical example documents the bearing sign convention backwards: 0.5 rad relative bearing is starboard, comment says "to port of bow"
  - `app/example.cpp:114` (consumer-facing-documentation, confidence high)
  - description: example.cpp is the canonical living documentation for wiring navtracker (CLAUDE.md points consumers at it). The radar block passes rel_bearing_rad = 0.5 with the comment "// 28.6° to port of bow". The actual convention is compass/clockwise: makeMeasurementFromRelativeBearing adds own heading and projectRangeBearingToEnu maps bearing b to (east=r*sin b, north=r*cos b) (core/projection/Projection.cpp:14-19), so a positive relative bearing is to STARBOARD of the bow. The one place a consumer is shown the sign convention states it mirrored.
  - failure_scenario: A consumer integrating their own radar reads the example to learn the sign convention, concludes positive = port, and negates their (correctly starboard-positive) relative bearings before calling makeMeasurementFromRelativeBearing / pushRadarTtm. Every radar target is then mirrored across own-ship's heading axis: a contact 28.6° to starboard is tracked 28.6° to port — wrong tracks with no error anywhere in the pipeline.
  - evidence: app/example.cpp:113-114 (`rel_bearing_rad = 0.5; // 28.6° to port of bow`); core/projection/Projection.cpp:14-19 (east = r*sin(bearing), north = r*cos(bearing) ⇒ positive bearing rotates clockwise from north = starboard); sim/ArpaEmitter.cpp:99-104 documents the same compass convention. No test pins example.cpp comments.
  - suggested_fix: Change the comment to "28.6° to starboard of bow" (and state the convention explicitly: relative bearing is clockwise-positive from the bow).

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Detection entity IDs collide for same-source same-timestamp measurements, so the /detections layer shows only the LAST detection of each scan
  - `adapters/foxglove/FoxgloveDebugRecorder.cpp:214` (debug-visualization-correctness, confidence high)
  - description: recordMeasurement builds the SceneUpdate entity id as "det-" + source_id + "-" + to_string(m.time.nanos()), one write per measurement. All detections in one radar/lidar scan share the same timestamp and the same source_id — the autoferry loader stamps every activePoint of a frame with the identical Timestamp and source_id "autoferry_lidar"/"autoferry_radar" (adapters/replay/AutoferryJsonReplay.cpp:258-277), and tools/foxglove_autoferry.cpp:85-105 / tools/foxglove_pmbm_scenario.cpp:142-150 call recordMeasurement per measurement of such a scan. Foxglove SceneUpdate semantics replace an existing entity on the same topic with the same id, so each successive same-scan detection message overwrites the previous one.
  - failure_scenario: Open an mcap produced by foxglove_autoferry on scenario2: a lidar scan with ~dozens of returns at one timestamp renders as a single "det-autoferry_lidar-<t>-cov" ellipse on /detections/autoferry_lidar — the rest are silently replaced. An engineer debugging clutter/birth behavior sees 1 detection where the tracker actually received N, and draws wrong conclusions about extraction density or missed associations.
  - evidence: adapters/foxglove/FoxgloveDebugRecorder.cpp:214 (id = det-<source>-<nanos>), 234-237 (-cov suffix identical for every Position2D at that time), 265-267 (one sceneUpdate write per call, same topic). AutoferryJsonReplay.cpp:265-270 (same m.time and source_id for all points of a frame). tests/adapters/foxglove/test_recorder.cpp only uses distinct times/sources (lines 53-72), so no test pins multi-detection scans.
  - suggested_fix: Append a per-call monotonic sequence number (or an index within the scan) to the entity id, e.g. "det-<source>-<nanos>-<seq>".

- **[LOW/unverified]** Sim TTM sentences have 14 fields instead of 15 (target-name field omitted), shifting status/reference/UTC/acquisition one slot left
  - `sim/ArpaEmitter.cpp:120` (nmea-encoding, confidence high)
  - description: The emitter builds "RATTM,<n>,<rng>,<brg>,R,0.0,0.0,T,0.0,0.0,N,T,,000000.00,A" (same layout for clutter at line 74). NMEA TTM has 15 fields: ...speed/dist units, target NAME, status(T/L/Q), reference, UTC, acquisition. The emitted sentence puts "T" (intended as status) in the name slot and the remaining fields shift left, ending one field short. The repo's own ArpaAdapter tests use the correct 15-field form (tests/adapters/arpa/test_arpa_adapter.cpp:71: "...,N,TARG1,T,R,123456.78,A"). ArpaAdapter today only reads fields[0..9] (ArpaAdapter.cpp:94-104,157-159), so the shift is currently invisible to the pipeline.
  - failure_scenario: Any consumer of the sim's NMEA stream that parses fields beyond index 9 mis-reads the sentence — e.g. if ArpaAdapter is extended to honor the TTM status field (dropping L=lost targets, a natural edge-validation addition), sim sentences report status="" (field 11) while the "T" tracking flag sits in the name slot, so either all sim targets get dropped or the extension silently never triggers in sim tests, masking the new code path.
  - evidence: sim/ArpaEmitter.cpp:74 and 120 vs tests/adapters/arpa/test_arpa_adapter.cpp:71 (canonical 15-field sentences). Field count: 14 after the formatter in the emitter, 15 in the adapter tests.
  - suggested_fix: Insert the empty name field: ",R,0.0,0.0,T,0.0,0.0,N,,T,,000000.00,A".

- **[LOW/unverified]** Negative noisy ranges are clamped to "0.000" NM and then rejected by the adapter, silently truncating the range-noise distribution near min range
  - `sim/ArpaEmitter.cpp:26` (sim-noise-consistency, confidence high)
  - description: formatMilli3 clamps negative values to 0 (line 26: `if (milli < 0) milli = 0;`). r_obs = range + N(0, 50 m) (line 106) can go negative for close targets (min_range default 50 m), producing "0.000" on the wire, which ArpaAdapter rejects via isPlausibleRange (ArpaAdapter.cpp:103). The detection silently vanishes and the surviving range distribution is truncated at 0 while the adapter stamps an unbiased sigma=50 m covariance.
  - failure_scenario: Target at 60 m range with default range_std_m=50: P(r_obs<=0)=Phi(-1.2)~11.5% of detections are dropped, and the surviving ranges have conditional mean ~71 m instead of 60 m — an ~11 m systematic bias plus an effective P_D reduction that no detection model accounts for. Close-range sim scenarios (crossing tests pass within tens of meters of own-ship) get biased range statistics and mis-stated consistency (NEES) without any test failing loudly.
  - evidence: sim/ArpaEmitter.cpp:24-26 (clamp), 106 (unbounded Gaussian range noise), 97 (gate on TRUE range only, not r_obs); adapters/arpa/ArpaAdapter.cpp:99-104 (non-positive range rejected).
  - suggested_fix: Skip emission (or redraw) when r_obs <= 0 instead of encoding 0.000, and document the truncation; alternatively floor at a small positive epsilon and note the residual bias.

- **[LOW/unverified]** std::normal_distribution constructed with stddev == 0 when gps_pos_std_m is 0 — standard-library precondition violation exercised by existing tests
  - `sim/OwnShipEmitter.cpp:21` (undefined-behavior, confidence high)
  - description: OwnShipEmitter's constructor does `noise_(0.0, cfg_.gps_pos_std_m)` with no guard. std::normal_distribution requires 0 < stddev; constructing it with 0 violates the precondition (UB per the standard). Tests routinely configure gps_pos_std_m = 0.0 (tests/sim/test_own_ship_emitter.cpp:29, 92, 122, 198, 235), so the invalid construction happens in the suite today. The distribution is never *sampled* at stddev 0 (draw sites gate on `> 0.0`, lines 37-38), so mainstream libstdc++/libc++ are benign in practice — but AisEmitter (AisEmitter.cpp:15), ArpaEmitter (ArpaEmitter.cpp:43-44) and EoIrEmitter (EoIrEmitter.cpp:27-28) all guard exactly this with `> 0.0 ? std : 1.0`, showing the intended pattern was missed only here.
  - failure_scenario: A standard library that asserts distribution parameter preconditions (e.g. MSVC STL debug checks or a future hardened libstdc++) aborts every noise-free own-ship sim test at emitter construction, turning a valid configuration (deterministic own-ship) into a crash.
  - evidence: sim/OwnShipEmitter.cpp:21 (unguarded), draw guards at 37-38; contrast sim/AisEmitter.cpp:15, sim/ArpaEmitter.cpp:43-44, sim/EoIrEmitter.cpp:27-28; exercised by tests/sim/test_own_ship_emitter.cpp:29.
  - suggested_fix: Mirror the other emitters: `noise_(0.0, cfg_.gps_pos_std_m > 0.0 ? cfg_.gps_pos_std_m : 1.0)`.

- **[LOW/unverified]** CSV provenance total_runs ignores filters and the opt-in scenario batteries, so the recorded run count is wrong for exactly the runs where provenance matters
  - `bench/baseline_matrix.cpp:259` (provenance-correctness, confidence high)
  - description: prov.total_runs = configs.size() * (sim_scenarios.size() * seeds + replay_scenarios.size()) is computed from the PRE-filter sim/replay vectors and never includes the --with-simms / --with-imazu / --with-rbad batteries appended to `all` (lines 184-198). Config/scenario filters (lines 203-230) shrink `configs` before the multiplication but shrink only `all`, not sim_scenarios/replay_scenarios, so any focused re-measurement (--config-eq/--scenario-eq, the documented A/B workflow) writes a total_runs that reflects the full unfiltered scenario matrix, and any simms/imazu/rbad run under-counts.
  - failure_scenario: Run `navtracker_bench_baseline --config-eq imm_cv_ct_pmbm --scenario-eq imazu_15_s0 --with-imazu --seeds 1`: the sweep executes 1 run, but the CSV provenance header records total_runs = 1 * (n_sim * 1 + n_replay) — dozens — and scenario_count=1 disagrees with it. Anyone auditing pinned baselines (the freeze-commit discipline this repo uses) reads a run count that does not match the rows in the file.
  - evidence: bench/baseline_matrix.cpp:259-262 (total_runs formula uses sim_scenarios/replay_scenarios sizes), 184-198 (opt-in batteries go only into `all`), 216-230 (scenario filters applied only to `all`).
  - suggested_fix: Compute total_runs from the post-filter `all` (splitting seeded synthetic vs single-run replay by descriptor kind), or derive it from the actual rows returned by runSweep.

Coverage notes (periphery): SCOPE COVERED (all files read end-to-end): sim/{TruthTrajectory,SensorEmitter,AisEmitter,ArpaEmitter,EoIrEmitter,OwnShipEmitter,NmeaEncode,SkewInjector,SimulatedSensorBus}.{hpp,cpp}; adapters/foxglove/{FoxgloveDebugRecorder,FoxgloveJson,Geometry,McapWriter,Schemas}; app/example.cpp, app/mht_fusion_example.cpp; bench/{baseline_matrix,compare,render_markdown}.cpp; tools/{foxglove_autoferry,foxglove_pmbm_scenario}.cpp. Cross-checked against adapters/ais/AisAdapter, adapters/arpa/ArpaAdapter, adapters/eoir/EoIrAdapter, adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter (RMC/GGA/HDT parsing), core/types/{Timestamp,Ids,Track,MeasurementBuilders}, core/projection/Projection, adapters/replay/AutoferryJsonReplay, and tests/sim + tests/adapters/foxglove + tests/adapters/arpa.  CHECKED AND FOUND CLEAN: (1) TruthTrajectory: CT turn integration is the correct closed form, position/velocity continuous at both leg boundaries; CV integrates exactly. (2) Emitter noise vs stamped covariance: AIS default pos_std 10 m == adapter high-accuracy sigma 10 (entry default high_accuracy=true); ARPA sigma 50 m/1 deg == ArpaAdapterConfig defaults; EO-IR stds ride per-detection and are used verbatim by the adapter; zero-std paths substitute positive sigma on the wire while keeping truth (documented). (3) NMEA encoding: XOR checksum, DDMM.mmmmm/DDDMM.mmmmm with correct 60-minute carry, hemisphere letters, negative coordinates via fabs+hemisphere; RMC/GGA/HDT field layouts match OwnShipNmeaAdapter's parser (RMC [6]/[7], knots conversion consistent both directions); RMC pushed before GGA matches adapter precedence. (4) Bearing conventions: emitter atan2(E,N) compass convention round-trips exactly through the adapters' sin/cos projection; the v1 heading=0 convention is consistent between OwnShipEmitter default and ArpaEmitter/EoIrEmitter, and heading-bias tests are physically consistent (emitted rel-bearing + biased HDT reconstructs truth+bias). (5) SkewInjector: Measurement.time never modified (order-only), stable sort with ingestion-index ties, portable integer jitter ladder, bounds-checked SkewProfile array size 9 == SensorKind enumerator count. (6) SimulatedSensorBus determinism: fixed emitter dispatch order, per-emitter seed derivation, integer step counting, final stable time sort; timestamp arithmetic verified by hand (integer-second cadences are exact under Timestamp::fromSeconds truncation; EoIr's step-count fix eliminates the only non-representable default dt). (7) Foxglove: gate ellipse k=sqrt(gamma) is the correct chi-square boundary; NED->row-major-ENU covariance index mapping in onTracks correct; SourceTouch.alpha_rad NaN sentinel matches Track.hpp default; JSON escaping delegated to nlohmann; McapWriter channel/schema idempotency and per-topic sequence numbers correct. (8) app/mht_fusion_example: member-init order safe, per-sensor detection model wired, datum sink forwards to MhtTracker as CLAUDE.md prescribes. (9) bench compare.cpp / render_markdown.cpp trivial and clean.  OVERFLOW ONE-LINERS (below reporting bar or by-design): OwnShipEmitter default gps_pos_std_m=5 with report_gps_std=false injects own-pose noise the adapters do not budget in R — explicitly documented back-compat opt-in, not reported. ArpaEmitter clutter uses fixed target number \"00\", colliding with ArpaTargetEntry's default arpa_track_num=0 if a real target uses it (no current test does; hint-pollution latent). FoxgloveDebugRecorder::last_S_ never pruned on track deletion (unbounded map growth on long debug runs; IDs never reused so no aliasing). timeJson / McapWriter cast negative (pre-epoch) timestamps to negative nsec / wrapped uint64 — unreachable with current callers. EmitContext truth is frozen per bus tick, so an emitter dt smaller than the bus dt would stamp identical positions at different times (defaults make slots coincide; misconfiguration only); AIS/ARPA catch-up positions use the documented most-recent-truth-sample rule. baseline_matrix argv parsing ignores a flag in the last argv slot and std::stoul on a non-numeric --seeds throws uncaught (CLI-only). SimulatedSensorBus::attachOwnShip dereferences a null ownship_ if called before setOwnShip (misuse; run() itself is guarded). foxglove_pmbm_scenario's demo land ring is not closed (viz demo only). example.cpp does not register the FoxgloveDebugRecorder as a datum sink; the recorder has onDatumRecentered for that, but it only matters past a 30 km recenter in a copied integration.  KNOWN ITEMS HONORED: did not re-report the mcap writer.inl UBSan memcpy (F-BUILD-2), the test_own_ship_nmea dangling optional (F-BUILD-1), bench Sweep fixed-datum design, or any of the listed by-design tracker trade-offs.


## Batch B6-lenses-PARTIAL

### unit: lens-determinism (1 findings)

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Tracker::processBatch never got the backlog-#15 in-tracker time sort: an unsorted fixed-rate batch makes arrival-order front() the scan instant, silently stale-dropping whole batches of fresh data or letting stale members bypass the guard
  - `core/pipeline/Tracker.cpp:197` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: Backlog #15 (docs/algorithms/improvement-backlog.md:561-612) diagnosed this exact footgun — 'front().time is the wrong instant and with reject_stale_measurements on the out-of-order tail is silently dropped' — restated the contract as 'a batch may arrive in any order; the tracker orders it', and shipped the fix as an is_sorted check + stable_sort in MhtTracker::processBatch (MhtTracker.cpp:216-226) and PmbmTracker::processBatch (PmbmTracker.cpp:1323-1333). The third processBatch implementation, the single-hypothesis Tracker::processBatch (Tracker.cpp:195-206), was never updated: it takes t = scan_in.front().time (line 197) from the raw arrival order, gates the WHOLE batch on that one element against high_water_ (lines 198-206, dropping scan_in.size() measurements when the front is stale), calls manager_.predictAll(estimator_, t) with t possibly earlier than in-batch measurements (line 218), and stamps noteObservation(id, t) rather than the matched measurement's own time (lines 273, 305). The backlog entry only says 'Confirmed present in BOTH MhtTracker and PmbmTracker' — plain Tracker was apparently never checked. tests/pipeline/test_batch_ordering.cpp covers only MhtTracker and PmbmTracker (no navtracker::Tracker case), so nothing pins the gap. The integration guide's remote-track recipe (docs/integration-guide.md:353, tracker.processBatch(remote.poll())) hands a poll()-collected batch straight to processBatch with no sort-first warning, and CLAUDE.md's pluggable-hot-path invariant promises the same pipeline works across associator choices — a consumer moving from PmbmTracker/MhtTracker (which tolerate unsorted batches) to Tracker+GNN with identical middleware silently regresses. Tracker.hpp:37 still carries the pre-#15 'share a common timestamp' wording, which is now inconsistent with the restated cross-tracker contract.
  - failure_scenario: Consumer runs the canonical fixed-rate loop (collect everything since the last tick, hand it over — the pattern MhtTracker.cpp:209-211 names as canonical) against Tracker+GNN, fusing ARPA (≈0.05 s latency) with AIS (0.5-1.0 s latency, the repo's own defaultMaritimeSkewProfile numbers). Tick 1 delivers [radar z@t=9.95]; high_water_=9.95. Tick 2 delivers only the delayed AIS fix [z@t=9.60] (arrived after the radar report but timestamped earlier): front=9.60 < high_water_ → with reject_stale_ default ON the ENTIRE batch is dropped and only counted in stale_dropped_ — the AIS stream is repeatedly discarded whenever its stamp lags the last radar stamp, i.e. most of the time, so AIS effectively never fuses. Conversely a mixed tick [radar z@t=10.55, ais z@t=9.90] passes the guard (front fresh), predictAll advances every track to 10.55, then the AIS match updates against the 10.55 state and rewinds track.last_update to 9.90, so the next predict re-propagates the 0.65 s overlap through F and Q a second time — the exact double-propagation failure the stale guard's own doc (Tracker.hpp:74-81) says the guard exists to prevent. Both failure modes are silent (no sink, no error), and neither occurs with MhtTracker/PmbmTracker on the same input.
  - evidence: Tracker.cpp:195-206 (no sort, t = scan_in.front().time, whole-batch stale drop 'stale_dropped_ += scan_in.size()'), 218 (predictAll to front time), 273/305 (noteObservation(id, t)). Contrast MhtTracker.cpp:216-226 and PmbmTracker.cpp:1323-1333 (is_sorted + stable_sort with the comment 'Order it by time here so the caller need not: otherwise scan.front().time is the wrong instant and, with the stale guard on, a front older than the high-water mark drops the whole batch'). Backlog #15 (improvement-backlog.md:569-612) scopes the fix to 'both MhtTracker and PmbmTracker' only. tests/pipeline/test_batch_ordering.cpp instantiates only MhtTracker and PmbmTracker. Integration guide line 353 feeds poll() output to processBatch with no pre-sort.
  - suggested_fix: Add the same is_sorted fast-path + stable_sort-by-time preamble to Tracker::processBatch (bit-identical for already-sorted input, matching the other two trackers), and stamp noteObservation with the matched measurement's time; alternatively, if the same-timestamp contract for plain Tracker is intentional, make it loud (assert/drop-with-diagnostic on mixed timestamps) and fix Tracker.hpp + the integration guide recipe to say batches must be pre-sorted for this tracker only.

Coverage notes (lens-determinism): UNIT lens-determinism, scope core/ adapters/ app/ sim/. Method: grepped the full scope for every determinism hazard class, then read each hit in context and traced whether it can reach output; additionally read the hot-path orchestrators end-to-end. FILES READ END-TO-END: core/pipeline/{Tracker,ReorderBuffer,MhtTracker}.cpp+hpp, core/tracking/{TrackManager,TrackTree}.cpp+hpp, core/association/{GnnAssociator,JpdaAssociator,Murty,Hungarian}.cpp, core/estimation/{ParticleFilterEstimator,Resampling}.cpp+hpp, core/collision/CpaEvaluator.cpp+hpp, core/scenario/{Harness,HarnessBatched,Metrics}.cpp, sim/{AisEmitter,SimulatedSensorBus,SkewInjector}.cpp, core/types/{Track,Timestamp}.hpp; read in relevant part: core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp (processBatch, pruneAndNormalise, mergeBernoulliDuplicates, source-touch/clutter-feed/diag sections), PmbmTypes.hpp, core/benchmark/{MarkdownRenderer,Metrics}.cpp, core/bias/{SensorBiasEstimator.hpp,SensorBiasPairExtractor.cpp}. VERIFIED CLEAN under the invariant-#4 contract (same log, same binary → identical output): (1) unordered_map/unordered_set — every instance is either lookup-only (TrackManager::id_to_index_ with the vector driving iteration; SensorBiasEstimator pos_/brg_; sim emitters' truths/next_emit_ which iterate cfg_.targets vector; McapWriter/FoxgloveDebugRecorder; PlotCsvReplayAdapter StationMap) or paired with an explicit first-seen-order vector (MarkdownRenderer, Comparator) or feeds keyed writes only (PMBM staged maps merge into std::map). (2) RNG — no random_device/rand()/time()/clock anywhere in scope; every engine is fixed-seeded (ParticleFilterEstimator ctor seed with a documented draw-discipline; sim emitters seeded via seed_seq(cfg.seed, emitter-id chars); scenario Builders per-function mt19937(seed); SkewInjector uses an integer jitter ladder specifically for cross-platform reproducibility). steady_clock appears only in bench latency columns (BenchRunner.cpp:67, Sweep.cpp:292/586) — measurement-only, by design (R2), never feeds tracker state or metric selection. (3) sorts — stable_sort used everywhere ties are reachable on the batch path (MhtTracker:224, PmbmTracker:1331, SimulatedSensorBus:142, SkewInjector:54, Builders:109); unstable std::sort sites (replay/bench loaders, TrackTree::pruneKLocal/mergeBranches score sorts, JPDA overflow fallback, PMBM partial_sorts, mergeBernoulliDuplicates id sort) all have strict-weak comparators on int64/id/double keys and are deterministic for identical input; NaN sort keys would require lambda_C=0 && P_D=0 style configs already covered by B2's clutter_intensity==0 finding. (4) no pointer-keyed containers (the two `const X*` maps are pointer-VALUED, keyed by BernoulliId/SensorBiasKey); no static mutable state in scope; ReorderBuffer's multimap preserves insertion order for equal keys (C++11) so drain order is deterministic; Murty priority_queue and Hungarian tie-breaks are first-wins deterministic; GNN greedy strict-< deterministic and NaN-cost-safe (NaN never beats best). (5) uninitialized-read hunt: TrackTreeNode declares uninitialized members (parent/scan_idx/score/is_leaf) but both construction sites (rootFromMeasurement, TrackTree::branch miss+hit) assign every field; Track/Bernoulli/PoissonComponent/SourceTouch fully default-initialized. OVERFLOW ONE-LINERS (not reported): (a) CpaEvaluator.cpp:67 — Exited events for tracks dropped in the same cycle are emitted in unordered_set iteration order: deterministic per binary/input, but relative event order for simultaneous drops is unspecified across STL implementations (cosmetic; contract is same-binary replay). (b) PmbmTracker compares timestamps via double seconds() in three places (t_max selection :1370, stageActivityCheck :1298, birth-time equality :1608) instead of int64 nanos — deterministic but collapses distinctions below ~238 ns at 2026 epochs; :1608 equality is already filed by B2. (c) Timestamp::fromSeconds round-trips in sim (AisEmitter cadence, SimulatedSensorBus ticks) truncate toward zero, drifting emission instants by sub-µs — deterministic, harmless. (d) bench latency columns make bench CSV/markdown outputs non-reproducible by design; freeze/diff workflows must exclude them (already project practice). DEDUP: I independently found Tracker::process()+JPDA silent duplicate-birth before checking prior outputs; it is already CONFIRMED in 10-bughunt-findings.md so not re-reported; also cross-checked my finding list against all five raw unit files (B1-B5) — my single reported finding (Tracker::processBatch missing the #15 sort) appears nowhere there (B2 covered the PMBM-side mixed-timestamp double-propagation and the PMBM float-equality birth gate, not the plain Tracker's missing sort/whole-batch drop). NOT COVERED by me in depth: estimator math internals (B1), PMBM enumerateChildren cost construction (B2), geo/bias math (B3), collision/static/adapter validation (B4), replay loaders/metrics math (B5) — I only re-checked those files' ordering/RNG/uninit surfaces for the determinism lens.

### unit: lens-angles-units (1 findings)

- **[HIGH/unverified]** Heading-bias observation families disagree in sign (marine vs ENU-math frame): v1/v2 sources measure -b while v3 measures +b, and the documented adapter correction DOUBLES the bearing error for v1/v2
  - `core/bias/HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:46` (frame-sign-convention, confidence high)
  - description: The scalar bias state b is consumed by ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter as a MARINE-frame gyro bias: they compose marine bearing = relative + pose.heading_true_deg and then subtract b_hat (ArpaAdapter.cpp:119 'bearing_true_rad_corrected = bearing_true_rad - b_hat'; EoIrAdapter.cpp:45 same). The v3 gyro-vs-X observations feed exactly that quantity: measurement = wrapToPi(gyro_rad - gps_true_heading_rad) = +b_marine (HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:157/177/193). But the v1 AIS-ARPA pair observation computes the disagreement in the ENU MATH frame: z = wrapToPi(beta_arpa - beta_truth) with beta = atan2(y,x) (HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:43-46), and the v2 bearing-innovation is likewise math-frame: r = wrapAngle(beta_obs - beta_pred) (Tracker.cpp:39, model bearing = atan2(dy,dx) per MeasurementModels.cpp:30). Because math angle = pi/2 - marine angle, a physical marine gyro bias +b appears as -b in any math-frame bearing difference: a target at marine bearing theta projected via x=r*sin(theta+b), y=r*cos(theta+b) (Projection.cpp:18-19) has math angle atan2(y,x) = pi/2-(theta+b) = math_true - b, so z = -b and r = -b. All five kinds update the SAME state b (scalar KF), so (1) mixing v1/v2 with v3 — exactly the wiring docs/integration-guide.md section 5 and tests/integration/test_full_stack_pipeline.cpp prescribe (setHeadingBiasEstimator + setBearingInnovationSink on one estimator, then pass it to ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter) — fuses contradictory measurements +b and -b into one state; and (2) with v1/v2 sources alone, b_hat converges to -b and the adapters' subtraction yields theta + b - (-b) = theta + 2b: the 'correction' doubles the bearing error instead of removing it, then closed-loop feedback (z becomes b_hat - b, innovation y = -b every cycle) ratchets b_hat further negative each accepted update, rotating every radar/EO-IR measurement progressively farther from truth. Contrast: the per-sensor SensorBiasEstimator loop is frame-consistent because it both measures AND applies its bearing bias in the math frame on the Bearing2D value (SensorBiasEstimator.cpp:142-143, BiasCorrection.hpp:72). Why tests do not catch it: tests/bias/test_heading_bias_estimator.cpp builds pairs directly in math angles (ARPA at beta_truth + bias, line ~23), i.e. it pins the estimator's internal convention, not the physics of a marine gyro bias flowing through the adapters; tests/scenario/test_bearing_bias_convergence.cpp likewise injects the bias directly on math-frame Bearing2D values; tests/integration/test_full_stack_pipeline.cpp injects the +2deg gyro bias only into the self-consistent v3 sources (target measurements are AIS-style Position2D, so the wired v2 sink never sees a biased bearing); and the only end-to-end closed-loop tests through the real adapters (tests/sim/test_bus_bias_estimator_sweep.cpp) run with knob.bias_deg = 0 and end in SUCCEED() with no assertions.
  - failure_scenario: Own-ship gyro reads 10 deg high (b = +10 deg, HDT-fed pose.heading_true_deg = true + 10). Radar target at true marine bearing 30 deg, range 1500 m. ArpaAdapter composes 40 deg and projects the target ~260 m clockwise of truth. AIS-ARPA pairs give beta_arpa = 50 deg math vs beta_truth = 60 deg math, z = -10 deg; after ~10 pairs p_b < (0.3 deg)^2 and the estimator publishes b_hat ~= -10 deg. From the next TTM on, ArpaAdapter computes corrected bearing = 40 - (-10) = 50 deg: the measurement is now ~520 m from truth — twice the uncorrected error — and every subsequent accepted pair pushes b_hat further negative (innovation stays -b), so radar and EO-IR measurements rotate steadily away from truth until gating/association breaks, all silently. If the operator additionally wires the v3 sources per the integration guide, v3 pushes b_hat toward +10 deg while v1/v2 push toward -10 deg, leaving a wrong, oscillating estimate that corrupts bearings in whichever direction currently dominates.
  - evidence: HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:43-46: 'const double beta_truth = std::atan2(ais_rel.y(), ais_rel.x()); const double beta_arpa = std::atan2(arpa_rel.y(), arpa_rel.x()); const double z = wrapToPi(beta_arpa - beta_truth);' — math-frame difference. ArpaAdapter.cpp:106-119: 'if (bearing_units == "R") bearing_true_deg += own_opt->heading_true_deg; ... const double bearing_true_rad_corrected = bearing_true_rad - b_hat;' — marine-frame subtraction. Projection.cpp:18-19: 'out.pos_enu.x() = own + range_m * sb; out.pos_enu.y() = own + range_m * cb;' — marine bearing convention, so math angle of the projected point = pi/2 - marine. OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:234/259: 'obs.gps_cog_rad = wrapDegToPi(cog_deg)' fed as measurement = wrapToPi(gyro - cog) = +b_marine (HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:177). Worked numbers: marine 30deg -> unit (sin30,cos30)=(0.5,0.866) -> atan2(0.866,0.5)=60deg math; with b=+10: marine 40 -> math 50; z = 50-60 = -10 = -b; corrected = 40-(-10) = 50 vs truth 30 (error doubled).
  - suggested_fix: Pick ONE definition of b (the natural one is the marine gyro bias b = gyro - truth that v3 already measures and the adapters already subtract) and fix the two math-frame sources to it: v1: z = wrapToPi(beta_truth - beta_arpa); v2: feed obs.innovation_rad negated when treated as a measurement of b (or emit r = wrapAngle(beta_pred - beta_obs) for the bias sink specifically, keeping the general IInnovationSink as-is). Then add the missing end-to-end pin: a sim-bus test with own_cfg.heading_bias_deg != 0 that asserts (a) b_hat converges to +bias_deg in radians and (b) corrected ARPA measurement error < uncorrected error, so the frame contract can never silently flip again.

Coverage notes (lens-angles-units): Scope: units/angles/frames lens over ALL of core/, adapters/, app/, sim/ (tests read only to check pinning). I first read docs/reviews/2026-07-09-prerelease-review/10-bughunt-findings.md and excluded everything already reported there (incl. TrackOutput NED ordering + transposed meridian rotation, Cpa tcpa Jacobian sign, datumAxisRotation antimeridian, DatumShift rotation sign, DeclaredSensorActivity coverage-from-origin, AisCsvReplayAdapter knots-as-m/s, UKF sigma-point bearing mean across +-pi, RangeBearing2D-as-ENU initiate bugs, ArpaAdapter missing sensor_position_enu for v1 pairs, closed-loop double-subtract 'half convergence' — note my finding shows that analysis was itself frame-inverted: the loop diverges rather than halving, wrapDegToPi Inf hang, GGA/HDT Null Island, example.cpp port/starboard comment, sim TTM 14-field shift, OwnShipEmitter stddev-0). Verified clean (hand-executed the math): Wgs84 geodetic<->ECEF (Bowring) and deg/rad; Datum ENU rotation matrix rows; Projection.cpp polar->ENU Jacobian (compass convention, J=[[sb,r*cb],[cb,-r*sb]] correct); PolarVelocity sogCogToEnuVelocity (marine COG -> ENU, Jacobian + iso floor); TrackOutput COG = atan2(e,n), [0,360) normalization, SOG/COG polar Jacobian rows, near-zero-SOG fallback; MeasurementModels wrapAngle (fmod-based, returns (-pi,pi], no loop hang) and residual wrapping applied at ALL residual call sites (EkfEstimator:41,154, Gating:11, MhtTracker:580, PF:87, UKF zd:86-87, IMM zd:215-216); ClutterMapDetectionModel azimuth cell indexing/wrap (remainder-based) and bilinear position interpolation; BearingWedgeModel angleDelta + math->true deg output conversion (90-alpha, mod 360); ShadowMask unwrap-at-largest-gap logic; CameraBearingCsvReader marine->math (pi/2 - theta, wrapped); AutoferryJsonReplay NED->ENU bearing (pi/2 - b_ned) and (E,N) assembly; PlotCsvReplayAdapter/HaxrTruthLoader/RadarTruthCsvReader marine sin/cos projections; AisAdapter sentinels (lat 91/lon 181, SOG 1023, COG >=360, heading 511, nav_status 15) and knots factor 0.514444; ArpaAdapter TTM field indexing vs NMEA layout (bearing[2], T/R[3], speed[4], course[5], T/R[6], shared units[9]), distance/speed unit tables (N/K/S), TLL/GGA ddmm parsing incl. size_t underflow guard; OwnShipNmeaAdapter RMC SOG knots->m/s, COG->ENU, HDG deviation/variation signs (E+/W-), gyro-rate wrap; NmeaEncode ddmm formatting with 60-minute carry; sim AisEmitter cadence knots buckets, ArpaEmitter/EoIrEmitter compass atan2(E,N) conventions consistent with heading=0 deferral, OwnShipEmitter RMC/HDT encoding + heading normalization; TruthTrajectory constant-turn closed-form integration; CoordinatedTurn/CV5State F and Q dt-scaling (CT velocity rotation is proper CCW ENU); SourceTouchPopulate RangeBearing2D math-frame (r*cos,r*sin) consistent with its atan2(dy,dx) model; BiasCorrection.hpp per-sensor bearing bias measured AND applied in the math frame (consistent, unlike the heading-bias loop I reported); GeoJSON [lon,lat] ordering in both land and static parsers; CoastlineGeometry equirectangular m-per-deg; SensorDefaults deg->rad; NavInputGuard heading delta wrap [0,180]; OwnShipProvider sorted insert/recenter threshold km->m; RemoteTrackAdapter (velocity already ENU, no conversion); CpaOwnShip synthesis; OwnShipVelocityEstimator LS fit units. Overflow one-liners (below reporting bar): (1) ArpaAdapter.cpp:42 assumes m/s for an unlabelled TTM units field — m/s is not an NMEA TTM unit; a malformed sentence yields ~2x speed error in the birth-velocity hint only; (2) Wgs84.cpp:46 ecefToGeodetic divides by cos(lat) — degenerate exactly at the poles (irrelevant for maritime datums); (3) EoIrAdapter never sets Measurement.sensor_position_enu (stays (0,0)) — same family as the already-reported ArpaAdapter omission; consumed by PMBM range-conditioned paramsForAt (PmbmTracker.cpp:646), so EO-IR coverage conditioning is origin-relative when own-ship is far from the datum; (4) sweep tests test_bus_bias_estimator_sweep.cpp are assertion-free (SUCCEED() after printing) and run with bias_deg=0 — the heading-bias closed loop has no end-to-end pin at all (folded into the main finding's fix). Not audited: tests/ internals beyond pin-checking, gitignored fixtures/data (per brief), docs-only files, core/benchmark CSV/markdown plumbing beyond unit greps (prior batch B5 covered it).


## Batch B6v-lenses-VERIFIED

### unit: lens-determinism (1 findings)

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** Tracker::processBatch never got the backlog-#15 in-tracker time sort: an unsorted fixed-rate batch makes arrival-order front() the scan instant, silently stale-dropping whole batches of fresh data or letting stale members bypass the guard
  - `core/pipeline/Tracker.cpp:197` (correctness, confidence high)
  - description: Backlog #15 (docs/algorithms/improvement-backlog.md:561-612) diagnosed this exact footgun — 'front().time is the wrong instant and with reject_stale_measurements on the out-of-order tail is silently dropped' — restated the contract as 'a batch may arrive in any order; the tracker orders it', and shipped the fix as an is_sorted check + stable_sort in MhtTracker::processBatch (MhtTracker.cpp:216-226) and PmbmTracker::processBatch (PmbmTracker.cpp:1323-1333). The third processBatch implementation, the single-hypothesis Tracker::processBatch (Tracker.cpp:195-206), was never updated: it takes t = scan_in.front().time (line 197) from the raw arrival order, gates the WHOLE batch on that one element against high_water_ (lines 198-206, dropping scan_in.size() measurements when the front is stale), calls manager_.predictAll(estimator_, t) with t possibly earlier than in-batch measurements (line 218), and stamps noteObservation(id, t) rather than the matched measurement's own time (lines 273, 305). The backlog entry only says 'Confirmed present in BOTH MhtTracker and PmbmTracker' — plain Tracker was apparently never checked. tests/pipeline/test_batch_ordering.cpp covers only MhtTracker and PmbmTracker (no navtracker::Tracker case), so nothing pins the gap. The integration guide's remote-track recipe (docs/integration-guide.md:353, tracker.processBatch(remote.poll())) hands a poll()-collected batch straight to processBatch with no sort-first warning, and CLAUDE.md's pluggable-hot-path invariant promises the same pipeline works across associator choices — a consumer moving from PmbmTracker/MhtTracker (which tolerate unsorted batches) to Tracker+GNN with identical middleware silently regresses. Tracker.hpp:37 still carries the pre-#15 'share a common timestamp' wording, which is now inconsistent with the restated cross-tracker contract.
  - failure_scenario: Consumer runs the canonical fixed-rate loop (collect everything since the last tick, hand it over — the pattern MhtTracker.cpp:209-211 names as canonical) against Tracker+GNN, fusing ARPA (≈0.05 s latency) with AIS (0.5-1.0 s latency, the repo's own defaultMaritimeSkewProfile numbers). Tick 1 delivers [radar z@t=9.95]; high_water_=9.95. Tick 2 delivers only the delayed AIS fix [z@t=9.60] (arrived after the radar report but timestamped earlier): front=9.60 < high_water_ → with reject_stale_ default ON the ENTIRE batch is dropped and only counted in stale_dropped_ — the AIS stream is repeatedly discarded whenever its stamp lags the last radar stamp, i.e. most of the time, so AIS effectively never fuses. Conversely a mixed tick [radar z@t=10.55, ais z@t=9.90] passes the guard (front fresh), predictAll advances every track to 10.55, then the AIS match updates against the 10.55 state and rewinds track.last_update to 9.90, so the next predict re-propagates the 0.65 s overlap through F and Q a second time — the exact double-propagation failure the stale guard's own doc (Tracker.hpp:74-81) says the guard exists to prevent. Both failure modes are silent (no sink, no error), and neither occurs with MhtTracker/PmbmTracker on the same input.
  - evidence: Tracker.cpp:195-206 (no sort, t = scan_in.front().time, whole-batch stale drop 'stale_dropped_ += scan_in.size()'), 218 (predictAll to front time), 273/305 (noteObservation(id, t)). Contrast MhtTracker.cpp:216-226 and PmbmTracker.cpp:1323-1333 (is_sorted + stable_sort with the comment 'Order it by time here so the caller need not: otherwise scan.front().time is the wrong instant and, with the stale guard on, a front older than the high-water mark drops the whole batch'). Backlog #15 (improvement-backlog.md:569-612) scopes the fix to 'both MhtTracker and PmbmTracker' only. tests/pipeline/test_batch_ordering.cpp instantiates only MhtTracker and PmbmTracker. Integration guide line 353 feeds poll() output to processBatch with no pre-sort.
  - suggested_fix: Add the same is_sorted fast-path + stable_sort-by-time preamble to Tracker::processBatch (bit-identical for already-sorted input, matching the other two trackers), and stamp noteObservation with the matched measurement's time; alternatively, if the same-timestamp contract for plain Tracker is intentional, make it loud (assert/drop-with-diagnostic on mixed timestamps) and fix Tracker.hpp + the integration guide recipe to say batches must be pre-sorted for this tracker only.

Coverage notes (lens-determinism): UNIT lens-determinism, scope core/ adapters/ app/ sim/. Method: grepped the full scope for every determinism hazard class, then read each hit in context and traced whether it can reach output; additionally read the hot-path orchestrators end-to-end. FILES READ END-TO-END: core/pipeline/{Tracker,ReorderBuffer,MhtTracker}.cpp+hpp, core/tracking/{TrackManager,TrackTree}.cpp+hpp, core/association/{GnnAssociator,JpdaAssociator,Murty,Hungarian}.cpp, core/estimation/{ParticleFilterEstimator,Resampling}.cpp+hpp, core/collision/CpaEvaluator.cpp+hpp, core/scenario/{Harness,HarnessBatched,Metrics}.cpp, sim/{AisEmitter,SimulatedSensorBus,SkewInjector}.cpp, core/types/{Track,Timestamp}.hpp; read in relevant part: core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp (processBatch, pruneAndNormalise, mergeBernoulliDuplicates, source-touch/clutter-feed/diag sections), PmbmTypes.hpp, core/benchmark/{MarkdownRenderer,Metrics}.cpp, core/bias/{SensorBiasEstimator.hpp,SensorBiasPairExtractor.cpp}. VERIFIED CLEAN under the invariant-#4 contract (same log, same binary → identical output): (1) unordered_map/unordered_set — every instance is either lookup-only (TrackManager::id_to_index_ with the vector driving iteration; SensorBiasEstimator pos_/brg_; sim emitters' truths/next_emit_ which iterate cfg_.targets vector; McapWriter/FoxgloveDebugRecorder; PlotCsvReplayAdapter StationMap) or paired with an explicit first-seen-order vector (MarkdownRenderer, Comparator) or feeds keyed writes only (PMBM staged maps merge into std::map). (2) RNG — no random_device/rand()/time()/clock anywhere in scope; every engine is fixed-seeded (ParticleFilterEstimator ctor seed with a documented draw-discipline; sim emitters seeded via seed_seq(cfg.seed, emitter-id chars); scenario Builders per-function mt19937(seed); SkewInjector uses an integer jitter ladder specifically for cross-platform reproducibility). steady_clock appears only in bench latency columns (BenchRunner.cpp:67, Sweep.cpp:292/586) — measurement-only, by design (R2), never feeds tracker state or metric selection. (3) sorts — stable_sort used everywhere ties are reachable on the batch path (MhtTracker:224, PmbmTracker:1331, SimulatedSensorBus:142, SkewInjector:54, Builders:109); unstable std::sort sites (replay/bench loaders, TrackTree::pruneKLocal/mergeBranches score sorts, JPDA overflow fallback, PMBM partial_sorts, mergeBernoulliDuplicates id sort) all have strict-weak comparators on int64/id/double keys and are deterministic for identical input; NaN sort keys would require lambda_C=0 && P_D=0 style configs already covered by B2's clutter_intensity==0 finding. (4) no pointer-keyed containers (the two `const X*` maps are pointer-VALUED, keyed by BernoulliId/SensorBiasKey); no static mutable state in scope; ReorderBuffer's multimap preserves insertion order for equal keys (C++11) so drain order is deterministic; Murty priority_queue and Hungarian tie-breaks are first-wins deterministic; GNN greedy strict-< deterministic and NaN-cost-safe (NaN never beats best). (5) uninitialized-read hunt: TrackTreeNode declares uninitialized members (parent/scan_idx/score/is_leaf) but both construction sites (rootFromMeasurement, TrackTree::branch miss+hit) assign every field; Track/Bernoulli/PoissonComponent/SourceTouch fully default-initialized. OVERFLOW ONE-LINERS (not reported): (a) CpaEvaluator.cpp:67 — Exited events for tracks dropped in the same cycle are emitted in unordered_set iteration order: deterministic per binary/input, but relative event order for simultaneous drops is unspecified across STL implementations (cosmetic; contract is same-binary replay). (b) PmbmTracker compares timestamps via double seconds() in three places (t_max selection :1370, stageActivityCheck :1298, birth-time equality :1608) instead of int64 nanos — deterministic but collapses distinctions below ~238 ns at 2026 epochs; :1608 equality is already filed by B2. (c) Timestamp::fromSeconds round-trips in sim (AisEmitter cadence, SimulatedSensorBus ticks) truncate toward zero, drifting emission instants by sub-µs — deterministic, harmless. (d) bench latency columns make bench CSV/markdown outputs non-reproducible by design; freeze/diff workflows must exclude them (already project practice). DEDUP: I independently found Tracker::process()+JPDA silent duplicate-birth before checking prior outputs; it is already CONFIRMED in 10-bughunt-findings.md so not re-reported; also cross-checked my finding list against all five raw unit files (B1-B5) — my single reported finding (Tracker::processBatch missing the #15 sort) appears nowhere there (B2 covered the PMBM-side mixed-timestamp double-propagation and the PMBM float-equality birth gate, not the plain Tracker's missing sort/whole-batch drop). NOT COVERED by me in depth: estimator math internals (B1), PMBM enumerateChildren cost construction (B2), geo/bias math (B3), collision/static/adapter validation (B4), replay loaders/metrics math (B5) — I only re-checked those files' ordering/RNG/uninit surfaces for the determinism lens.

### unit: lens-time-dt (5 findings)

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** PMBM source-touch loop attributes measurements to MISDETECTED Bernoullis because predict() advances last_update to the scan time
  - `core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:1666` (time-handling, confidence high)
  - description: The contribution-history loop (PmbmTracker.cpp:1651-1698) selects, for every Bernoulli in the dominant hypothesis, the nearest scan measurement whose z.time == b.last_update, relying on the comment's claim that 'misdetected ones inherit the parent pre-predict timestamp, so an exact-match filter cleanly separates the two'. That claim is false: processBatch calls predict(t_max) (line 1372) BEFORE enumerateChildren, and predict round-trips every Bernoulli through estimator.predict + fromTrack (PmbmTracker.cpp:222-229, PmbmTypes.hpp:456-463), which sets b.last_update = t_max whenever dt > 0 (EkfEstimator.cpp:30, ImmEstimator.cpp:164). PmbmTypes.hpp:433-435 even documents that last_update 'is the filter time, advanced by predict and update alike'. So a misdetected Bernoulli carries last_update == t_max, which always equals at least one measurement's time (in the common same-timestamp scan, ALL of them), and the loop appends a SourceTouch from a measurement the Bernoulli never claimed. The R2 fix (lines 1749-1763) replaced exactly this NN-at-timestamp reconstruction with last_claimed_meas_index for the clutter feed because it mis-credited returns, but the touch loop was left on the broken method.
  - failure_scenario: Two vessels A (radar+AIS track) and B. A scan arrives containing only B's AIS report; A is misdetected in the dominant hypothesis. A's last_update == t_max == B's report time, so B's AIS measurement (with B's mmsi as touch.vessel_id) is appended to contribution_history_[A]. Consequences: (1) with source_aware_misdetection + source_aware_identity ON, A is now considered observable whenever B broadcasts, so A takes misdetection penalties while its own AIS is silent — precisely the wrongful decay the feature exists to prevent (pmbm-design.md 3.1.2/3.1.3 define contribution_history as sources the Bernoulli actually contributed from); (2) with idle_halflife_sec > 0, every scan near other traffic refreshes A's last-touch time so a ghost near a shipping lane never idle-decays; (3) on the DEFAULT config the polluted history is copied verbatim into the emitted Track.recent_contributions (refreshAggregatedTracks, line 2318-2321), so extractPositionPairs/extractPairs (Sweep.cpp:509-519 wiring, AisArpaPairExtractor.cpp:35-45) can pair A's genuine radar touch with B's spurious AIS touch, feeding a wrong registration/heading-bias observation that is then applied to all subsequent measurements via setSensorBiasProvider — a feedback loop off cross-vessel geometry.
  - evidence: predict(t_max) at PmbmTracker.cpp:1367-1373 mutates density_ in place via fromTrack (copies last_update, PmbmTypes.hpp:459); EkfEstimator::predict sets track.last_update = to when dt > 0; the misdetection branch copies the post-predict parent ('Bernoulli miss = b;' line 1026) leaving last_update = t_max; the touch filter is 'if (!(z.time == b.last_update)) continue;' (line 1666). Test IdleDecayHalvesExistenceAfterHalflife (tests/pmbm/test_pmbm_tracker_update.cpp:302) does not contradict this: it checks r only immediately after the scan that applies the decay, i.e. before the freshly-polluted history could influence anything; no test asserts absence of touches for misdetected Bernoullis.
  - suggested_fix: Attribute touches from the association result, not timestamps: use b.last_claimed_meas_index >= 0 (already recorded in enumerateChildren for detections and births) to select the claimed measurement, and skip Bernoullis with index -1.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full failing path. (1) processBatch calls predict(t_max) (PmbmTracker.cpp:1372) before enumerateChildren; predict round-trips every Bernoulli through toTrack/estimator.predict/fromTrack (lines 222-228), and both EkfEstimator::predict (EkfEstimator.cpp:30) and ImmEstimator::predict (ImmEstimator.cpp:164) set track.last_update = to when dt > 0, copied back by fromTrack (PmbmTypes.hpp:459). (2) The misdetection branch copies the post-predict parent ("Bernoulli miss = b;" line 1026) leaving last_update == t_max. (3) The touch filter "if (!(z.time == b.last_update)) continue;" (line 1666, exact nanos equality per Timestamp.hpp:35) therefore matches every t_max measurement for misdetected Bernoullis, and the nearest-in-position one (no distance gate) is appended as a SourceTouch. The in-code justification at lines 1659-1662 ("misdetected ones inherit the parent pre-predict timestamp") is false and is contradicted in the SAME file by idle_decay_for's comment (lines 591-593: "the estimator's predict advances it to the current filter time even when no measurement was applied"). Decisive corroboration: tests/pmbm/test_pmbm_sensor_activity.cpp:35-41 explicitly documents that "a new SourceTouch is appended to contribution_history_ even for miss-detected Bernoullis" — the identity-gate tests were written around the pollution; no test asserts the correct (detection-only) behavior. The behavior contradicts the design doc (pmbm-design.md §3.1.2 gate over "contributing source_ids"; §4 vessel_id "set at detection time from the matched measurement") and the claimed MhtTracker parity (MhtTracker.cpp:610-651 appends only for chosen-leaf hits via the true scan_meas_idx). Consequence (1) verified: a polluted touch carrying vessel B's mmsi makes should_misdetect (lines 566-587) return true whenever B broadcasts, wrongfully decaying real track A while its own AIS is silent; source_aware flags are enabled in shipped bench configs (core/benchmark/Config.cpp:360, 443, 1138, 1173). Consequence (3) verified: polluted history is emitted in Track.recent_contributions on the default config (lines 2318-2321) and AisArpaPairExtractor.cpp:36-50 pairs first-AIS + first-ARPA touches per track, enabling a cross-vessel bias observation when the bias wiring is enabled.
