Consequence (2) is overstated (see corrected details). Not on the known/by-design exclusion list; the test-file comment shows the behavior was observed, but the load-bearing code comment claims the opposite and the design doc contradicts it — a defect, not a decision.
  - verifier corrected details: The core defect and consequences (1) and (3) stand as claimed. Correction to consequence (2): a ghost with idle_halflife_sec > 0 does NOT "never idle-decay". The per-scan pollution refreshes last-touch to roughly one scan interval ago, so idle_decay_for applies factor 2^(-s/H) each scan, compounding to 2^(-k*s/H) — i.e., decay at exactly the configured halflife rate (arguably the intended rate; an unpolluted history with per-scan multiplication on cumulative dt would over-decay quadratically). Moreover, with source_aware_misdetection on, the polluted touch typically flips should_misdetect to TRUE on the next scan (the polluting source/vessel is present again), so the FULL misdetection recursion applies instead of idle decay — the practical harm is wrongful decay of real tracks (consequence 1), not ghost immortality. Severity stays high: the pollution silently inverts the documented source-aware protection (real vessel tracks near AIS traffic take misdetection penalties while their own sources are silent — the exact failure §3.1.2/3.1.3 exist to prevent, and those flags are used in shipped bench configs), and on the default config every emitted track's recent_contributions provenance is corrupted by nearest-measurement touches from scans where the track was missed, which the AIS/ARPA and sensor-bias pair extractors consume when wired. Fix direction is already proven in-file: the R2 clutter-feed fix (lines 1749-1763) replaced this same NN-at-timestamp reconstruction with b.last_claimed_meas_index; the touch loop should key on last_claimed_meas_index >= 0 instead of the z.time == last_update filter. Note the identity-gate tests in tests/pmbm/test_pmbm_sensor_activity.cpp were written around the polluted behavior and may need updating with the fix.

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** Mixed-timestamp scans: detected Bernoulli's last_update is rewound to the measurement time while its state sits at t_max, double-propagating the intra-scan interval every scan
  - `core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:964` (time-handling, confidence high)
  - description: processBatch predicts every Bernoulli to t_max = max measurement time in the scan (lines 1363-1373), then enumerateChildren updates the Bernoulli with a measurement at scan[l].time <= t_max and stamps det.last_update = scan[l].time (line 964; estimator update also sets it, EkfEstimator.cpp:64, ImmEstimator.cpp:278). The Bernoulli's state epoch is now t_max but its timestamp says t_l. On the next scan, per-Bernoulli estimator.predict computes dt = t_next - t_l and applies F(dt)/Q(dt) to a state that is already at t_max — over-propagating position by v*(t_max - t_l) and over-inflating Q by the same interval, EVERY scan the track is updated by a non-latest measurement. The backlog-#15 sort comment (lines 1315-1322) explicitly blesses unsorted, mixed-time batches ('callers need not pre-sort'; MhtTracker.cpp:209-211 calls the fixed-rate collect-everything-since-last-tick consumer 'canonical'), so this is supported input, not misuse. Misdetections and births are internally consistent; only the detection branch has the state-epoch/timestamp mismatch. All in-repo drivers (BenchRunner.cpp:143-150, HarnessBatchedPmbm) group scans by exact-equal timestamps, so no bench or test exercises the mixed-time path — which is why this is undetected.
  - failure_scenario: A live consumer ticks at 1 Hz, batching everything since the last tick: an AIS report at t=10.0 and a radar sweep at t=10.8 land in one processBatch. predict(10.8) advances an AIS-tracked vessel to 10.8; the AIS measurement updates it and stamps last_update=10.0. Next tick predict(11.8): dt=1.8 s applied to a state already at 10.8 → the track leads truth by 0.8 s * v (about 4 m at 10 kn) with correspondingly double-counted process noise — a persistent systematic bias plus covariance inflation on every AIS-updated track, degrading gating/association in dense traffic. Additionally, the innovation itself is computed against the state at t_max rather than t_l, biasing the update by the same v*dt.
  - evidence: Traced end-to-end: predict-to-t_max (1367-1373) -> toTrack(b) with last_update=t_max -> estimator_.update sets last_update=z.time -> fromTrack copies it (PmbmTypes.hpp:459) -> explicit det.last_update = scan[l].time (964) -> next predict uses to.secondsSince(track.last_update) (EkfEstimator.cpp:24). BenchRunner/harness scans are exact-same-time groups, so existing green suites cannot pin this.
  - suggested_fix: After updating with scan[l], set det.last_update = t_max (the epoch the state actually corresponds to), or predict each Bernoulli only to its claimed measurement's time; document the chosen intra-scan convention alongside MhtTracker's earliest-instant convention.
  - verifier: Independently traced end-to-end; every load-bearing step of the claim checks out.  1. Predict-to-t_max: PmbmTracker::processBatch computes t_max over the batch and calls predict(t_max) (PmbmTracker.cpp:1367-1372). predict() round-trips each Bernoulli through toTrack/estimator_.predict/fromTrack (lines 222-229); EkfEstimator::predict sets track.last_update = to (EkfEstimator.cpp:30), and fromTrack copies it back (PmbmTypes.hpp:459). So after predict, every Bernoulli has state epoch = t_max AND last_update = t_max — consistent.  2. No re-predict per measurement: enumerateChildren builds the per-cell updated Bernoulli from `Track t = toTrack(b)` (line 783, the post-predict-to-t_max state) and calls estimator_.update(t_upd, scan[l]) directly (line 795). EkfEstimator::update applies a plain KF update (no time propagation) and stamps track.last_update = z.time (EkfEstimator.cpp:64); ImmEstimator does the same (ImmEstimator.cpp:278). Line 964 (`det.last_update = scan[l].time`) reasserts it. Result: detected Bernoulli has state epoch t_max but last_update = t_l < t_max whenever the claiming measurement is not the latest in the batch. The misdetection branch keeps last_update = t_max (consistent), so the mismatch is detection-branch-only, as claimed.  3. Double propagation next scan: EkfEstimator::predict computes dt = to.secondsSince(track.last_update) (EkfEstimator.cpp:24; ImmEstimator.cpp:78 same). Concrete run: track updated by AIS@10.0 in a batch whose radar sweep is @10.8 → state epoch 10.8, stamp 10.0. Next tick predict(11.8): dt = 1.8 s of F/Q applied to a state already at 10.8 — 0.8 s of extra transport (≈4 m at 10 kn) plus Q over an interval 1.8 s instead of 1.0 s, recurring every scan. The global dt guard at PmbmTracker.cpp:209-213 only gates on current_time_ (= previous t_max) and does not prevent the per-Bernoulli over-propagation. Steady state is a persistent position lead of order v·Δ·(1-g)/g plus systematically inflated covariance. The secondary point also holds: the innovation itself is computed against the t_max state (no re-predict), biasing the update by v·(t_max - t_l).  4. Supported input, not misuse: the backlog-#15 comments (PmbmTracker.cpp:1316-1322; MhtTracker.cpp:209-215) and the header of tests/pipeline/test_batch_ordering.cpp explicitly bless the "collect everything since the last tick" consumer producing mixed-time batches as canonical. The contract comment PmbmTypes.hpp:433 ("last_update ... is the filter time, advanced by predict and update alike") confirms last_update is supposed to be the state epoch — the rewind violates the stated invariant.  5. No test pins correct behavior: the only mixed-time-batch test, BatchOrdering.PmbmUnsortedBatchMatchesSorted (tests/pipeline/test_batch_ordering.cpp:92), feeds sub-times 0.3 s apart but only asserts sorted-vs-reversed equality — both runs contain the identical bug, and there is no accuracy-vs-truth assertion, so it stays green. BenchRunner.cpp:143-150 groups scans by exact-equal timestamps (meas[mi].time == scan_t), so no bench/replay exercises the mixed-time path.  6. Not shared with MHT (so not "the documented scan approximation"): TrackTree::branch predicts from nodes_[leaf].time to scan_time (the earliest instant) and stamps hit.time = scan_time uniformly (TrackTree.cpp:158-159, 269), so MHT's epoch bookkeeping is self-consistent across scans; only PMBM has the compounding stamp/epoch mismatch. The detected-stamp-equals-measurement-time behavior is load-bearing for the source-touch matching at PmbmTracker.cpp:1658-1666, which was designed under the single-timestamp-scan assumption — it does not fix the epoch mismatch.  Severity: high is fair. It is a silent, per-scan-compounding systematic bias plus covariance inflation on the explicitly-blessed live consumption pattern (multi-sensor batches at a fixed tick — the normal deployment shape), degrading gating/association exactly where fusion matters; it is invisible to every in-repo bench and test. It is not critical because it does not crash, kill tracks outright, or corrupt any existing benchmark result, and consumers who batch per-timestamp are unaffected.
  - verifier corrected details: Confirmed as claimed, with one clarification worth adding: the defect exists even without PmbmTracker.cpp:964 — EkfEstimator::update (EkfEstimator.cpp:64) and ImmEstimator (ImmEstimator.cpp:278) already stamp last_update = z.time and fromTrack (PmbmTypes.hpp:459) round-trips it, so line 964 merely reasserts the mismatch. Any fix must address the epoch bookkeeping (e.g., stamp detected Bernoullis at t_max, or predict per-Bernoulli to the claiming measurement's time before update), not just delete line 964. Note also the source-touch history matcher (PmbmTracker.cpp:1658-1666) keys on b.last_update == z.time, so naively re-stamping t_max breaks that diagnostic feed for mixed-time scans — the fix has a second consumer to reconcile. Adaptive-birth Bernoullis (nb.last_update = scan[l].time, PmbmTracker.cpp:1175) are built from PPP components at epoch current_time_ = t_max folded with a measurement at t_l, so births carry a smaller version of the same epoch ambiguity; misdetections are consistent as claimed.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** PmbmTracker has no stale-scan guard: an out-of-order batch is applied against newer states and rewinds both the filter clock and Bernoulli last_update
  - `core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:210` (time-handling, confidence high)
  - description: Tracker (Tracker.hpp:82, default on) and MhtTracker (MhtTracker.hpp:73, default true) both reject batches older than the high-water mark, documenting the harm ('rewind track.last_update, inflating the next predict's dt'). PmbmTracker::processBatch has no such guard: predict(t_old) with dt <= 0 sets current_time_ backwards and returns without propagating (lines 209-213), then the update path runs anyway — measurements at t_old are gated/scored against states predicted to t_new (position offset v*(t_new - t_old) biases association), the winning update stamps last_update = t_old, and the following predict over-propagates the overlap exactly as in the mixed-time finding. The header (PmbmTracker.hpp:639-641) claims this 'matches the MhtTracker stale-input convention', but MHT's convention is to DROP the stale batch; PMBM silently processes it.
  - failure_scenario: A consumer feeds AIS and radar streams directly (no ReorderBuffer). Radar scan at t=100 is processed; a delayed AIS batch stamped t=98 arrives next. PMBM rewinds current_time_ to 98, compares the AIS fix against states 2 s ahead (20 m off at 10 m/s — may fall outside the gate, or drags the track backward), stamps the updated Bernoulli last_update=98, then predict(101) advances 3 s from a state at t=100, overshooting 20 m. The same input to Tracker or MhtTracker is dropped and counted (staleDropped); PMBM corrupts state with no counter or signal.
  - evidence: Full read of processBatch (lines 1315-1882): only the within-batch sort exists; no high-water check. predict() dt<=0 branch at 209-213 moves current_time_ backwards. Compare MhtTracker.cpp:227-236 and Tracker.cpp:126-134.
  - suggested_fix: Add the same high-water reject (with a dropped counter) to PmbmTracker::processBatch, or at minimum refuse to move current_time_ backwards and skip the update for scans older than current_time_.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** HDT/HDG sentence arriving before the first GGA initializes the auto-datum at lat/lon (0,0) and inserts a bogus (0,0) pose into the history
  - `adapters/own_ship/OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:109` (edge-validation, confidence high)
  - description: ingest() starts from provider_.latest().value_or(OwnShipPose{}) whose defaults are lat_deg=0, lon_deg=0 (OwnShipProvider.hpp:29-30). The HDT branch (line 268-272) and HDG branch (line 298) call provider_.update(pose) unconditionally even when no GGA has ever been seen, so the first heading sentence on a live stream pushes a pose at (0°,0°) — off the coast of West Africa. OwnShipProvider::update then lazily initializes the working datum from that pose (OwnShipProvider.cpp:33-34) and stores the bogus fix in history_. On real NMEA streams HDT is typically 10 Hz vs GGA 1 Hz, so heading-before-position is the NORMAL startup ordering, not an exotic one. With auto-recenter on (default), the first real GGA (>30 km away) forces an immediate datum recenter — tolerable if every ENU-caching component is registered as a datum sink, but any measurement composed in the window (EoIrAdapter/ArpaAdapter call poseAtOrBefore(d.time), which returns the (0,0) pose for timestamps before the first GGA) projects the target thousands of km away. With auto-recenter disabled and no explicit datum, the datum permanently stays at (0,0).
  - failure_scenario: Live startup: stream begins HDT, HDT, GGA... First HDT at t0 initializes the datum at (0,0) and stores pose{lat=0, lon=0, t0}. A camera detection timestamped between t0 and the first GGA is projected from that pose into ENU — an absurd position that seeds a garbage track (Position2D always passes canInitiateTrack); the subsequent forced recenter then shifts all tracks by ~6000 km through shiftTracksOnDatumChange. No test covers heading-before-GGA ordering (grep over tests/adapters/own_ship shows GGA always fed first).
  - evidence: OwnShipNmeaAdapter.cpp:109-110 (default pose + time stamp), 268-272 (HDT provider_.update), 298 (HDG); OwnShipProvider.cpp:33-34 (lazy datum init from first update), 52-56 (pose inserted into history unconditionally); OwnShipPose defaults at OwnShipProvider.hpp:29-30.
  - suggested_fix: In the HDT/HDG (and RMC) branches, skip provider_.update() until a position fix has been ingested (e.g., only update when provider_.latest() exists or track a has_position_ flag), or have OwnShipProvider refuse datum initialization from a pose that never carried a real fix.

- **[LOW/unverified]** Alt-birth gate only strips births whose birth_time equals scan.front().time, so births from later-in-batch measurements escape it on mixed-time scans
  - `core/pmbm/PmbmTracker.cpp:1608` (time-handling, confidence high)
  - description: The S3 alt-birth gate identifies this scan's new-born Bernoullis by b.birth_time.seconds() == scan.front().time.seconds() (line 1600/1608), but births are stamped birth_time = scan[l].time (line 1182), which differs from scan.front().time for any measurement that is not the earliest in the batch. On a mixed-timestamp batch (the input regime the backlog-#15 sort explicitly supports), phantom births in weak alternative children created from later-in-batch measurements are not stripped, silently disabling the gate for exactly those births. Knob-gated (alt_birth_log_gap_threshold > 0, default 0) and inert on same-timestamp bench scans, which is why no test catches it.
  - failure_scenario: Consumer enables alt_birth_log_gap_threshold and feeds 1 Hz collect-since-last-tick batches (AIS t=10.0, radar t=10.8). A weak K-child births a phantom Bernoulli from the radar return at 10.8; the strip predicate compares against 10.0 and keeps it, so the phantom leaks into the aggregated output mass — the exact leak the gate was added to stop (Diagnostic A).
  - evidence: Birth stamping at line 1182 (nb.birth_time = scan[l].time) vs gate reference at line 1600 (scan.front().time). Batches with heterogeneous times are legal per lines 1315-1322.
  - suggested_fix: Mark this-scan births directly (e.g., a transient born_this_scan flag or compare birth_time against the full set of scan times / >= scan.front().time) instead of equality with the front timestamp.

Coverage notes (lens-time-dt): LENS: time/dt handling across ALL of core/, adapters/, app/, sim/. Read end-to-end: Timestamp.hpp; pipeline (Tracker, MhtTracker, ReorderBuffer, TrackManager, TrackTree); pmbm (PmbmTracker 2465 lines fully, PmbmTypes); estimation (Ekf/Ukf/Imm/ParticleFilter estimators, CV2D/CV5/CT/PrescribedTurn motion models, MeasurementModels, SigmaPoints usage); own_ship (OwnShipProvider, NavInputGuard, OwnShipVelocityEstimator, OwnShipNmeaAdapter); bias (HeadingBiasEstimator, SensorBiasEstimator time paths, AisArpaPairExtractor, SensorBiasPairExtractor windows); collision (Cpa, CpaEvaluator, CpaOwnShip); sensor_activity (DeclaredSensorActivity); sim (SimulatedSensorBus, SkewInjector, AisEmitter, OwnShipEmitter cadence loops); adapters (ais/arpa/eoir/remote_track/own_ship, benchmark ReplayScenarioRun + SimMultisensorScenarioRun + RbadScenarioRun batching, AutoferryJsonReplay velocity differencing); core/benchmark BenchRunner; core/scenario Harness/HarnessBatchedPmbm grouping. CLEAN: all four estimators clamp dt<=0 in predict and never rewind last_update on predict; CV/CT Q blocks are correctly dt-scaled (q*dt^3/3, dt^2/2, dt); IMM TPM is dt-scaled via matrix fractional power with row-stochastic sanitation and a dt==1 fast path; TrackTree IPDA/VIMM persistence is correctly raised to dt (per-second rates), and MHT's batch-at-earliest-instant convention is self-consistent (node.time == state epoch) and documented; ReorderBuffer window arithmetic and push/drain boundaries are consistent; Tracker and MhtTracker stale guards default-on; contribution pruning windows use int64 nanos; NavInputGuard skips dt<=0; ClutterMapDetectionModel clamps dt>=0 in the EWMA; sim emitters' catch-up loops are bounded and the bus uses integer step counting; SkewInjector sorts by arrival deterministically; NMEA adapters stamp caller-supplied receive time (no NMEA-sentence time parsing, so no midnight-rollover surface); replay loaders sort measurements; BenchRunner/Harness group scans by exact-equal timestamps (which is also why the two PMBM mixed-time findings are invisible to every bench/test). OVERFLOW one-liners (below finding bar or contract-covered): (a) CpaEvaluator/synthesizeOwnShipTrack stamps own track last_update=t without extrapolating from pose.time, so own position is stale by up to one nav period (~5 m at 10 kn / 1 Hz) — small vs 500 m CPA thresholds; (b) ImmEstimator::initiate (ImmEstimator.cpp:458) and ParticleFilterEstimator::initiate (line 137) read z.covariance(0,0..1,1) without EkfEstimator's empty/PSD guard — all in-repo call sites guard first and 'internal stages trust their inputs' is the documented invariant, but direct IEstimator port users can hit Eigen OOB; likewise gate()/logLikelihood() would Eigen-assert on the documented empty-covariance sentinel if applyDefaultsIfEmpty is skipped; (c) NMEA adapters (ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter/RemoteTrackAdapter) hold geo::Datum BY VALUE and are not IDatumChangeSinks, so under auto-recenter their projections go silently stale — integration-surface hazard, possibly documented, flagged for the datum/geo reviewer; (d) HeadingBiasEstimator freshness (last_predict - last_update) only grows while observations keep arriving; if all observation streams stop, is_published stays true forever unless the consumer calls predictTo() per cycle (Sweep does); (e) seconds()-based sort comparators (SimMultisensorScenarioRun.cpp:94, RbadScenarioRun.cpp:92) are strictly-weak-order-unsafe only for timestamps within ~238 ns at 2026-scale epochs — unreachable with fixture data; same sub-µs collapse applies to double-seconds comparisons inside PmbmTracker (stageActivityCheck, t_max scan max at line 1370); (f) Timestamp::fromSeconds truncates rather than rounds, so independently-computed 'same instant' values can differ by 1 ns and split an exact-equality scan group in bench tooling — not observed with current generators; (g) PMBM empty-scan processBatch does not advance the clock, so duty-cycle miss charging on empty scans is inert unless the consumer calls predict(t) first — arguably under-documented API contract rather than a defect.

### unit: lens-angles-units (6 findings)

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** Heading-bias sign convention is inconsistent across observation kinds and inverted vs. the adapter correction
  - `core/bias/HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:46` (angle-sign-convention, confidence high)
  - description: The five observation kinds feed the same scalar bias state b with contradictory signs. The gyro-vs-reference kinds (HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:157, :177, :193) measure b = gyro - reference in the compass frame: a gyro reading HIGH by b yields +b. But the AIS/ARPA pair observation (line 46: z = wrapToPi(beta_arpa - beta_truth)) and the BearingInnovation observation (Tracker.cpp:39: r = wrapAngle(beta_obs - beta_pred)) are computed in the MATH frame (atan2(N,E)), where the same physical gyro bias +b rotates the projected bearing by -b (math = pi/2 - compass, so math differences negate compass differences). Concretely: own-ship heading true 0, gyro bias +5 deg, target due north at 1 km; ArpaAdapter projects the target at compass 5 deg -> ENU (87.2, 996.2); pair extractor gives beta_arpa = 85 deg, beta_truth = 90 deg (math), z = -5 deg = -b. The consumers of the published estimate, ArpaAdapter.cpp:119 and EoIrAdapter.cpp:45, subtract b_hat from a COMPASS bearing (corrected = bearing_true_rad - b_hat), which is only correct for b_hat = +b. With the v1 AIS-ARPA wiring (documented in integration-guide.md section 5 as a primary calibration source and mirrored in tests/sim/BusComparisonHelpers.hpp row_c), b_hat converges to -b and the 'correction' becomes bearing = true + 2b, doubling the physical error; because the corrected measurements feed back into the next pairs, each subsequent accepted pair shifts b_hat further negative (innovation y stays -b), a positive-feedback runaway that progressively rotates all ARPA/EO-IR positions until they stop gating with the AIS tracks. Mixed wiring (all five kinds, as the guide shows) makes v1/v2 and v3 sources fight over the same state. No test catches this: tests/bias/test_heading_bias_estimator.cpp constructs pairs directly in the math frame (self-consistent), tests/scenario/test_bearing_bias_convergence.cpp injects the bias as a math-frame offset, tests/integration/test_full_stack_pipeline.cpp exercises ONLY the three gyro-vs-reference kinds (asserts b_hat = +b), and every sim sweep that wires the closed loop (test_bus_bias_estimator_sweep, test_bus_anchor_loss) runs with heading_bias_deg = 0.0, where a sign flip is invisible.
  - failure_scenario: Deployment wires HeadingBiasEstimator per the integration guide: extractPairs() -> observe(AisArpaPairObservation), estimator passed as IHeadingBiasProvider to ArpaAdapter/EoIrAdapter. Gyro has a +2 deg bias. Estimator converges to b_hat = -2 deg and publishes; ArpaAdapter then projects targets at compass_true + 4 deg (cross-range error doubles from 35 m to 70 m at 1 km), subsequent pairs push b_hat further negative each cycle, radar returns drift out of the AIS tracks' gates, and radar/AIS fusion silently breaks - the exact failure the estimator exists to prevent. If GPS-heading observations are also wired, the two source families pull b_hat in opposite directions and the estimate oscillates with |error| >= b either way.
  - evidence: HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:41-46 (math-frame atan2 on ENU positions), Tracker.cpp:37-39 (math-frame innovation), HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:157/177/193 (compass-frame gyro minus reference), ArpaAdapter.cpp:119 and EoIrAdapter.cpp:45 (compass-frame subtraction), docs/learning/17-multi-sensor-and-bias.md table ('b = gyro - gps_hdg' and pair = 'direct b measurement' - impossible simultaneously), ArpaEmitter.cpp:99-108 + OwnShipEmitter.cpp:134 (sim loop is physical, so the closed-loop bench would expose it, but BusComparisonHelpers.hpp:200 defaults bias_deg=0 and the sweep never sets it nonzero).
  - suggested_fix: Define b once (compass frame, gyro minus truth). Negate the two math-frame sources: z = wrapToPi(beta_truth - beta_arpa) in observe(AisArpaPairObservation), and negate the bearing innovation before the KF update in observe(BearingInnovation) (or emit r = beta_pred - beta_obs). Fix the math-frame unit tests to inject a physical compass bias, and add one closed-loop sim test with heading_bias_deg != 0 asserting post-publish ARPA residuals shrink.
  - verifier: Independently traced the failing path with concrete values. (1) Frame mismatch is real: HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:43-46 computes beta = atan2(N, E) (math frame), while projectRangeBearingToEnu (Projection.cpp:14-19) and ArpaAdapter.cpp:106/119, EoIrAdapter.cpp:33/45 work in the compass frame (E = r·sin β, N = r·cos β; correction = compass_bearing − b_hat). Since math = 90° − compass, math-frame bearing differences negate compass differences. Hand trace: true heading 0, gyro bias +5° compass, target at compass 30°/1000 m → ARPA projected at compass 35° → beta_arpa = 55° math vs beta_truth = 60° math → z = −5° = −b, yet HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:64/80 treats z as a direct measurement of +b. The design spec (docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-03-heading-bias-estimator-design.md) itself contains the error: §4.4 defines b compass-frame (ψ_corrected = ψ_raw − b, ψ_raw = pose.heading_true_deg) while §4.2 claims z = β_enu_arpa − β_truth = b + v; both cannot hold, and the code implements both. (2) The runaway is real: after b_hat converges to −b and publishes, ArpaAdapter.cpp:119 yields corrected = (β_c + b) − (−b) = β_c + 2b (error doubles); the next pair gives z = b_hat − b so the innovation y = z − b_hat = −b is CONSTANT — no fixed point, b_hat drifts without bound, and the 5σ outlier gate (σ_v ≥ 1° fallback → threshold ≥5°) never fires for realistic 1-3° biases. (3) The v3 gyro kinds (lines 157/177/193, gyro − reference) measure +b compass — the sign the consumers need — so v1/v2 and v3 feed the same scalar state with opposite signs, exactly as the learning-doc table (17-multi-sensor-and-bias.md:209-211) and guide (integration-guide.md:622-626) jointly (impossibly) assert. v2 confirmed flipped too: CameraBearingCsvReader.cpp:85-96 converts via π/2 − (heading + rel), so a gyro-high bias shifts β_obs by −b and Tracker.cpp:39 emits −b against an AIS-anchored track. (4) No test contradicts: test_heading_bias_estimator.cpp:16-29 builds pairs directly in the math frame (self-consistent, frame-blind); test_bearing_bias_convergence.cpp:42-44 injects a math-frame offset; test_full_stack_pipeline.cpp feeds Position2D targets only (no BearingInnovation fires, no ARPA wired → no pairs) so only the v3 gyro kinds are asserted (+2° compass); the only closed-loop adapter↔estimator wiring (test_bus_bias_estimator_sweep.cpp row_c via BusComparisonHelpers.hpp:556-557) leaves HeadingSweepKnob::bias_deg at its 0.0 default and is SUCCEED-only with no assertions; the 3° drift probe (test_bus_heading_bias_drift_probe.cpp) wires no estimator; test_bus_anchor_loss.cpp:81 explicitly uses bias 0. The sim loop itself is physical (OwnShipEmitter.cpp:134 adds bias to HDT; ArpaEmitter emits relative bearings that ArpaAdapter re-references with the biased heading), so a closed-loop run with nonzero bias would expose the flip — none exists.
  - verifier corrected details: Defect exactly as claimed: the v1 AIS↔ARPA pair observation (HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:46) and the v2 bearing-innovation observation measure −b (math frame) while the v3 gyro-vs-reference kinds measure +b (compass frame) into the same scalar state, and the consumers (ArpaAdapter.cpp:119, EoIrAdapter.cpp:45) require +b compass. With the documented v1 wiring and a real gyro bias b, the estimator converges to −b, the "correction" doubles the physical bearing error to 2b, and the innovation thereafter stays constant at −b — an unbounded negative-drift feedback loop (limit-cycled only by association breakdown and the 30 s staleness gate), silently rotating all ARPA/EO-IR measurements out of the AIS tracks' gates. The root cause is in the original spec (2026-06-03 design §4.2 asserts z = b + v while §4.4 defines b compass-frame); code, learning doc, and integration guide all inherited it. Fix is a one-line negation of z at HeadingBiasEstimator.cpp:46 (and matching negation for the BearingInnovation path, Tracker.cpp:39 consumer side or at observe()), plus a closed-loop regression test with nonzero heading_bias_deg asserting compass-frame convergence sign. Rated high rather than critical because the subsystem is opt-in (bias_provider is nullable; default wiring and v3-only wirings are unaffected) — but it is critical-in-effect for any consumer who wires v1/v2 per integration-guide §5, since it inverts the feature's purpose under exactly the condition (a biased gyro) the feature exists to handle.

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** position_covariance_m2 is returned in (east, north) order while the output contract, example, and Foxglove consumer read it as (north, east)
  - `core/output/TrackOutput.cpp:21` (frame-convention-contract, confidence high)
  - description: toGeodeticWithCov computes R * cov_enu * R^T where R is only the tiny (<0.5 deg) convergence-angle rotation from geo::datumAxisRotation - it never swaps axes. Track state and covariance are (east, north) ordered (state(0)=east), so the returned matrix keeps (0,0)=var_east, (1,1)=var_north. But the declared contract says the opposite: TrackOutput.hpp:27 ('local NED at target'), docs/output-contract.md line 8-9 ('row/column 0 = north, row/column 1 = east; extract sigma_north = sqrt([0,0])'), app/example.cpp:144 ('(north, east)'), and adapters/foxglove/FoxgloveDebugRecorder.cpp:256-259 which maps (1,1)->LocationFix east and (0,0)->north. For any anisotropic covariance the consumer gets sigma_north and sigma_east swapped, i.e. the uncertainty ellipse rotated 90 degrees.
  - failure_scenario: A radar-only track at 5 km due east of own-ship has cross-range-dominated covariance: var_east ~ 100 m2 (range), var_north ~ 7600 m2 (cross-range at 1 deg bearing sigma). A consumer following docs/output-contract.md reads sigma_north = sqrt([0,0]) = 10 m and sigma_east = 87 m - exactly swapped. A COLREGS/CPA display draws the safety ellipse elongated along the line of sight instead of across it; the Foxglove map ellipse is likewise rotated 90 degrees. Tests cannot catch it: tests/output/test_track_output.cpp uses an isotropic covariance at the datum (lines 64-79) and the anisotropic high-latitude test (lines 98-142) computes its expected value as R*cov*R^T, mirroring the implementation.
  - evidence: TrackOutput.cpp:9-23 (no axis swap), docs/output-contract.md:8-9, TrackOutput.hpp:24-28, FoxgloveDebugRecorder.cpp:121-122 and 256-259, app/example.cpp:144; test mirrors implementation at tests/output/test_track_output.cpp:129.
  - suggested_fix: Apply the axis swap S = [[0,1],[1,0]]: position_covariance_m2 = S * (R * cov_enu * R^T) * S^T (equivalently swap the diagonal entries and keep off-diagonals), or change the contract/doc/consumers to ENU ordering; either way add a test with anisotropic covariance asserting [0,0] equals the north variance.
  - verifier: Independently traced the failing path. (1) Track/ENU state is (east, north)-ordered: TrackOutput.cpp:38 computes COG as atan2(v.x(), v.y()) and tests/output/test_track_output.cpp:148-164 pin v=(10,0) -> COG=90 deg (east); the high-latitude test's own comment (lines 107-109) labels cov(0,0) "east variance"; TrackOutputFor4DTrack round-trips state(0)=10000 to 10 km east. (2) toGeodeticWithCov (TrackOutput.cpp:21) applies only R*cov*R^T where R = geo::datumAxisRotation (AxisRotation.cpp:19-21) is a pure small-angle (<0.5 deg) rotation [[c,-s],[s,c]] — no [[0,1],[1,0]] permutation, so the output keeps (0,0)=var_east, (1,1)=var_north. The design doc (2026-06-04-output-interface-design.md section 4.1) specifies exactly this swap-free math while simultaneously labeling the result NED — the contradiction is baked into the spec itself. (3) The declared contract and consumers read the opposite ordering: docs/output-contract.md:8-9 ("row/column 0 = north ... sigma_north = sqrt([0,0])"), TrackOutput.hpp:27 ("local NED"), app/example.cpp:144 "(north, east)", and FoxgloveDebugRecorder.cpp (~121-122 and ~257-259) maps cov[0](EE)=geo(1,1), cov[4](NN)=geo(0,0). Hand-executed scenario: track due east with var_east=100 m2, var_north=7600 m2, gamma~0 -> output (0,0)~100; a contract-following consumer reads sigma_north=10 m and sigma_east=87 m — exactly swapped, ellipse rotated 90 deg on the Foxglove map and any operator display. (4) Tests cannot catch it: the at-datum test uses identity (isotropic) covariance, and CovarianceRotatedAtHighLatitude computes its expected value with the same swap-free R*cov*R^T, mirroring the implementation rather than the documented NED ordering (test lines 126-134). Not on the known/by-design list. Whichever side is declared canonical (code emits east-first vs contract says north-first), at least one shipped consumer is wrong today, and any external consumer following docs/output-contract.md gets swapped sigmas for every anisotropic covariance.
  - verifier corrected details: Producer/contract axis-order mismatch: toGeodeticWithCov (core/output/TrackOutput.cpp:21) returns position_covariance_m2 in the input's (east, north) ordering — datumAxisRotation is a tiny convergence rotation with no ENU->NED axis permutation — while TrackOutput.hpp:27, docs/output-contract.md:8-9, app/example.cpp:144, and adapters/foxglove/FoxgloveDebugRecorder.cpp (two LocationFix mappings) all declare/consume it as (north, east). For any anisotropic covariance (the normal case for radar tracks: cross-range >> range variance), sigma_north and sigma_east are exchanged, i.e. the uncertainty ellipse is rotated 90 degrees in every contract-following consumer and in the Foxglove map layer. Fusion math is unaffected (output-only defect). Tests do not pin the documented ordering: the isotropic at-datum test is swap-invisible and the anisotropic high-latitude test computes its expectation with the identical swap-free formula. Fix is one of: add the [[0,1],[1,0]] permutation in toGeodeticWithCov (making code match the NED contract, and then fixing Foxglove is unnecessary since it already assumes NED), or re-declare the contract as (east, north) and fix the two Foxglove mappings plus example/doc text; a regression test with anisotropic covariance asserting sigma_north per the contract recipe is needed either way.

- **[HIGH/CONFIRMED]** Track initiation copies RangeBearing2D polar values (range, bearing) directly into ENU position state
  - `core/estimation/EkfEstimator.cpp:82` (polar-vs-cartesian, confidence high)
  - description: canInitiateTrack (core/estimation/MeasurementModels.hpp:30) returns true for RangeBearing2D, and all birth paths - Tracker.cpp:175-178 and :312-315, MhtTracker.cpp:349-354 (rootFromMeasurement), PmbmTracker.cpp:441/484 and :1494 - call estimator.initiate(z). Every initiate implementation (EkfEstimator.cpp:82-83, UkfEstimator.cpp:123-124, ImmEstimator.cpp:449-450, ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:128-129) does x(0)=z.value(0), x(1)=z.value(1) and copies z.covariance(0..1,0..1) into the position block. For a RangeBearing2D measurement, value = (range_m, bearing_rad) and covariance = diag(sigma_r^2 m2, sigma_b^2 rad2), so the track is born at ENU (range, bearing) - e.g. (5000, 1.2) meters - with an absurdly tight north variance (sigma_b^2 ~ 3e-4 'm2'). Updates and gating handle RangeBearing2D correctly via predictMeasurement/measurementResidual, so once born the wrong track is confidently pinned near y ~ +-pi meters of the origin while its bearing innovation churns.
  - failure_scenario: A consumer feeds native polar radar contacts as RangeBearing2D (the model is public in core/types/Ids.hpp:48 and is the documented way to get bearing-corrected innovations); the first contact of a new vessel (or any contact that fails to gate, e.g. after a maneuver) births a phantom track at ENU (r, beta) instead of the true position - wrong track output, and in PMBM the false Bernoulli additionally distorts the assignment costs for real measurements. The bench builder core/scenario/Builders.cpp:245-252 hits the same path whenever an RB measurement misses the gate (only the first sample is Position2D). No test pins this: the RB scenario always seeds with a Position2D so initiate-from-RB is never exercised.
  - evidence: canInitiateTrack excludes only Bearing2D (MeasurementModels.hpp:29-31); EkfEstimator.cpp:81-98 uses z.value/z.covariance verbatim; PmbmTracker.cpp:484 'Track t = estimator_.initiate(z)'; SourceTouchPopulate.hpp:45-60 shows the codebase already has the correct polar->ENU projection for RB touches, confirming the intended semantics.
  - suggested_fix: Either project (r, beta) -> sensor_position_enu + r*(cos b, sin b) with the polar Jacobian inside initiate (mirroring fillSourceTouchEnu), or make canInitiateTrack return false for RangeBearing2D until initiate supports it; add a test that an unassociated RangeBearing2D measurement births a track at the projected ENU position.
  - verifier: Independently traced the full failing path. (1) RangeBearing2D value is (range_m, bearing_rad): documented in docs/integration-guide.md:222, and confirmed by predictMeasurement (core/estimation/MeasurementModels.cpp:27-31) and by fillSourceTouchEnu (core/pipeline/SourceTouchPopulate.hpp:45-62), which performs the correct polar-to-ENU projection with the J*R*J^T covariance transform — proving the codebase's intended semantics. (2) canInitiateTrack (MeasurementModels.hpp:29-31) returns true for RangeBearing2D, and the integration guide table explicitly tells consumers RB "can start a track: yes". (3) All four estimator initiate() implementations copy z.value(0), z.value(1) verbatim into the ENU position state and z.covariance(0..1,0..1) — units (m^2, rad^2) — into the position covariance block: EkfEstimator.cpp:82-83 and 94-98, UkfEstimator.cpp:~121-124, ImmEstimator.cpp:~449-450, ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:~127-130. None switches on z.model. (4) No birth path converts: Tracker.cpp:175-178 and 311-315, PmbmTracker.cpp:441/484 and 1452/1494, MhtTracker.cpp:318/349 all guard only on canInitiateTrack + isMeasurementCovariancePsd (a diag(75^2, 7e-4) R trivially passes PSD) and then call estimator_.initiate(z) with the raw measurement. (5) No test pins the behavior: tests/estimation/test_ekf_estimator.cpp exercises RB only via update() on a pre-seeded track; the initiate tests use Position2D only; buildRangeBearingPassScenario (core/scenario/Builders.cpp:241-252) seeds sample 0 as Position2D so scenario tests never birth from RB. Hand-executed example: RB contact r=5000 m, beta=1.2 rad that gates to no track births a Tentative track at ENU (5000, 1.2) m with north variance ~7e-4 "m^2" — position wrong by kilometers and absurdly overconfident; in PMBM the false Bernoulli also enters the assignment problem. One mitigating fact tempers severity but does not refute: no in-repo adapter emits RangeBearing2D (AIS/ARPA/EOIR/replay adapters all emit Position2D/PositionVelocity2D/Bearing2D, and makeMeasurementFromRelativeBearing projects to ENU Position2D), so the shipped adapter pipelines never hit this path. Exposure is (a) external consumers following the documented contract for native polar sensors — a first-class, advertised use case (SensorDefaults.cpp:39-42 ships ArpaTtm/EoIr + RangeBearing2D noise defaults specifically for it), and (b) the bench RB scenario whenever an RB measurement misses the gate.
  - verifier corrected details: Track initiation treats RangeBearing2D measurement values as ENU coordinates. All four estimators' initiate() (EkfEstimator.cpp:82-83/94-98, UkfEstimator.cpp:~121, ImmEstimator.cpp:~449, ParticleFilterEstimator.cpp:~127) copy value(0..1)=(range_m, bearing_rad) into the ENU position state and the polar R (m^2, rad^2 units) into the position covariance block. Every birth path (Tracker.cpp:175/312, MhtTracker.cpp:318/349, PmbmTracker.cpp:484/1494) passes RB measurements through unconverted, guarded only by canInitiateTrack (which admits RB) and a PSD check. The integration guide (docs/integration-guide.md:220-227) explicitly promises consumers that RangeBearing2D can start a track, and SensorDefaults ships ArpaTtm/EoIr+RangeBearing2D defaults, so feeding native polar contacts is a documented first-class use — yet the first non-gating RB contact of a vessel births a phantom track at ENU (r, beta) meters with near-zero (rad^2-as-m^2) north variance. Correct projection code already exists in fillSourceTouchEnu (SourceTouchPopulate.hpp:45-62) and should be applied (with the Jacobian covariance transform) in initiate, or canInitiateTrack should exclude RB until it is. Not critical because no in-repo adapter emits RangeBearing2D, so shipped pipelines and current benchmarks (whose RB scenario seeds birth with a Position2D sample) do not hit it in normal operation; no existing test pins initiate-from-RB.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** datumAxisRotation returns the transpose of the correct old-to-new ENU axis rotation (convergence angle applied with inverted sign)
  - `core/geo/AxisRotation.cpp:20` (frame-rotation-sign, confidence high)
  - description: Numerically verified against exact ECEF/ENU geodesy: for old datum (60N, 0E) and new datum (60N, 1E), re-expressing an old-frame east unit vector in the new frame gives (0.99985, -0.01511) (north component NEGATIVE), computed as E_new * E_old^T. The code builds R = [[c,-s],[s,c]] with gamma = dlon*sin(mean_lat), and consumers apply v_new = R*v_old (DatumShift.cpp:17, cov: DatumShift.cpp:28-29) which yields (+0.01511) - the transpose/inverse of the correct rotation. Every datum recenter therefore rotates all track velocities, IMM mode means, particle velocities, and covariance orientations by -gamma instead of +gamma, a 2*gamma directional error (~0.9-1.9 deg per 30-60 km eastward recenter at 60N, growing with latitude). toGeodeticWithCov (TrackOutput.cpp:17) uses the same matrix in the same direction, so the NED covariance rotation is also inverted (small, <1 deg, but systematic). The test (tests/tracking/test_datum_shift.cpp:47-64) asserts the velocity rotates by atan2(R(1,0),R(0,0)) - it mirrors the implementation's own gamma rather than checking against exact geodesy, so it pins the wrong direction.
  - failure_scenario: Vessel transiting at 60N with auto-recenter (30 km threshold): each recenter injects a ~1 deg heading error into every live track's velocity (and rotates every covariance ellipse the wrong way), momentarily degrading gating and CPA bearing for all tracks simultaneously until measurements wash it out; on sparse tracks (coasting, AIS 3-min class-B cadence) the error persists for the full gap. Effect doubles at each successive same-direction recenter boundary crossing.
  - evidence: Python replication of Wgs84.cpp/Datum.cpp math: exact E_new*(E_old^T*e_east) = (0.9998, -0.015114, ...) vs code R*e_east = (0.9999, +0.015114). Consumers: core/tracking/DatumShift.cpp:39-46 (v and cov via R), core/output/TrackOutput.cpp:17-21.
  - suggested_fix: Flip the sign: return [[c, s], [-s, c]] for (old, new) (equivalently negate gamma), and strengthen the test to compare the shifted velocity against the exact E_new*E_old^T rotation of a known vector rather than against the implementation's own gamma.

- **[MEDIUM/unverified]** UKF measurement update takes the arithmetic mean of sigma-point bearings, which breaks when the predicted bearing straddles +-pi (target due west)
  - `core/estimation/UkfEstimator.cpp:80` (angle-wrap, confidence high)
  - description: z_pred is computed as sum(Wm(i) * Zsp.col(i)) where for Bearing2D / RangeBearing2D each Zsp column contains an atan2 in (-pi, pi]. The per-sigma-point deviations zd ARE wrapped afterwards (lines 86-87), but the mean itself is not circular: for a track due west of the sensor (math bearing +-pi), sigma points spread across the discontinuity produce bearings like {+3.11, -3.11, ...} whose weighted arithmetic mean is ~0 (due east) instead of ~pi. Then every wrapped zd is ~+-3.11, so the innovation covariance S inflates to ~pi^2 ~ 9.9 rad2 (vs a realistic 1e-4), the Kalman gain collapses, y = wrapAngle(z - z_pred) ~ +-pi, and the measurement is effectively discarded while the per-mode likelihood (ImmEstimator.cpp:259, gaussianScore(y, S)) collapses, corrupting the IMM mode probabilities and the PMBM/MHT association scores for that track. The identical pattern exists in the IMM's inner-UKF path at ImmEstimator.cpp:209-216, which is live in the canonical bench configs (Config.cpp builds ImmEstimator with use_ukf=true) fed with Bearing2D camera measurements (autoferry replay include_bearings, CameraBearingCsvReader).
  - failure_scenario: Canonical imm_cv_ct config, camera bearing stream: a target bears 179 deg math (just south of due west) at 300 m with ~50 m position sigma; sigma-point bearings span [pi - 0.3, -pi + 0.2], the arithmetic mean lands near 0, the bearing update is silently nulled (S ~ 10 rad2) and the likelihood tanks for exactly as long as the target stays in the wedge around due west - bearing-only corroboration and heading-bias innovations (which reuse the same z_pred path) both go dark or emit garbage there, direction-dependently.
  - evidence: UkfEstimator.cpp:79-92 (mean at 80, wrap only of deviations at 86-87), ImmEstimator.cpp:209-216 (same), MeasurementModels.cpp:30/36 (bearings from atan2, range (-pi, pi]). Hand-executed with points {+3.11, -3.11}: mean 0, wrapped zd +-3.11, S ~ 9.7 rad2.
  - suggested_fix: Compute the bearing component of z_pred as a circular mean: z_pred_b = atan2(sum Wm*sin(b_i), sum Wm*cos(b_i)) (or rebase all sigma-point bearings to the first point via wrapAngle before averaging), in both UkfEstimator::update and the ImmEstimator UKF branch; add a test with a target at bearing pi.

- **[LOW/unverified]** Canonical example comment inverts the relative-bearing sign convention ('to port of bow' for a positive bearing)
  - `app/example.cpp:114` (doc-convention, confidence high)
  - description: buildBearingMeasurement composes bearing_true = relative + heading and projects with the compass convention (east = r*sin, north = r*cos), so a POSITIVE relative bearing is clockwise from the bow, i.e. to STARBOARD. The canonical consumer example annotates rel_bearing_rad = 0.5 as '28.6 deg to port of bow'. A consumer calibrating their radar feed against this comment will negate their relative bearings.
  - failure_scenario: Integrator reads app/example.cpp (the documented starting point per CLAUDE.md), concludes the library wants port-positive bearings, and negates their sensor's starboard-positive bearings; every projected radar/EO-IR target is then mirrored across the bow axis (e.g. a contact 30 deg to starboard is tracked 30 deg to port), which is self-consistent enough to pass a casual smoke test with a dead-ahead target.
  - evidence: core/types/MeasurementBuilders.cpp:51-54 (relative + heading, compass) with core/projection/Projection.cpp:18-19 (E = r*sin b); heading 0, rel +0.5 rad puts the target at ENU (sin 0.5, cos 0.5) = east of the bow = starboard.
  - suggested_fix: Change the comment to '28.6 deg to starboard of bow' (and state the clockwise-positive convention explicitly in the makeMeasurementFromRelativeBearing doc block).

Coverage notes (lens-angles-units): Scope: all of core/, adapters/, app/, sim/ read with focus on units/frames/angles; every atan2/M_PI/deg/knots/fmod/wrap site enumerated by grep was visited. Checked clean: geo (Wgs84 Bowring closed-form, Datum ECEF-ENU matrix, round-trips), Projection.cpp compass-convention Jacobian (correct), MeasurementModels (math-angle convention, atan2 argument order, residual wrap incl. wrapAngle boundary at exactly +-pi, Jacobians for RB/Bearing), Gating/EKF/PF (all use wrapped measurementResidual), CoordinatedTurn F/Q, ConstantVelocity models, ManeuveringTrajectory turn integrals, Cpa/CpaOwnShip/CpaEvaluator math and Jacobians, TrackOutput velocity polar Jacobian + COG [0,360) normalization + low-SOG singularity handling, benchmark Metrics COG error (wrapped), scenario Metrics, ArpaAdapter (TTM/TLL, K/N/S unit codes incl. TTM speed via shared field 9, ddmm parse, relative+heading composition, TTM course->ENU birth velocity via compass sin/cos, course-jump wrap), EoIrAdapter, AisAdapter (knots 0.514444, sentinels 1023 SOG / 360 COG / 511 heading / nav-status 15, PolarVelocity shared helper Jacobian), OwnShipNmeaAdapter (ddmm, RMC COG->ENU, magnetic deviation/variation E/W signs, gyro-rate wrap, HDG true=mag+var convention), NavInputGuard (heading delta wrap), OwnShipProvider (no angle interpolation; sorted-insert history), Own-ship velocity/UERE estimators (linear LS, no angles), replay loaders (AisCsv m/s COG gate + nav-status suppression, CameraBearingCsv marine->math with wrap, AutoferryJson NED->ENU for positions and bearings, PlotCsv/RadarTruth/HAXR marine-convention projections, OwnshipCsv), sim emitters (ArpaEmitter compass atan2(E,N), EoIrEmitter FOV wrapSignedDeg, OwnShipEmitter HDT/RMC encoding incl. 360.000 wire artefact guard, AisEmitter knots constant), NmeaEncode ddmm, ShadowMask/BearingWedgeModel/ClutterMapDetectionModel circular grids and gap-cut unwrapping (all wrap-aware), LiveOccupancyModel bearing usage, DeclaredSensorActivity (sensor-at-origin is documented assumption), foxglove yaw conversions (90-hdg correct; its covariance consumption is folded into finding 2), RemoteTrackAdapter (ENU velocity passthrough), DatumShift position path (exact re-projection; rotation direction is finding 4), GeoJSON loaders lat/lon range validation, JPDA/IMM Gaussian normalizations ((2pi)^d, unit-ball c_d fallback documented), ImmEstimator state mixing (no angular states in [px,py,vx,vy,omega], so linear mixing is fine), IMM TPM non-dt-scaling already a known backlog item (not reported). Bias sign chain (finding 1) verified end-to-end: extractor -> estimator -> both adapters -> sim loop -> all bias tests + integration guide + eval-log sweeps (all sweeps run bias_deg=0). Finding 4 verified numerically against exact ECEF/ENU math in Python (scratchpad). Overflow one-liners not promoted to findings: ArpaAdapter passes cfg_.position_std_m as the TTM range sigma (documented in ArpaAdapterConfig comment, so treated as intended); projectRangeBearingToEnu uses compass convention while the internal RangeBearing2D model uses math convention - each path is self-consistent but the dual convention is a consumer trap worth a doc note; UkfEstimator::initiate would read z.value(1)/z.covariance(0,1) out of bounds for a 1-D Bearing2D measurement but every birth path guards via canInitiateTrack (latent only); AIS SOG sentinel is compared as 1023.0 knots which assumes the decoder passes the raw sentinel through unscaled (documented contract in AisAdapter.hpp). Not reviewed per instructions: tests/ internals except to check pinning, gitignored fixtures/data, and the known/by-design list (lambda_C cancellation, no-birth zone, PMBM CPA loss, extraction boundary, bench fixed datum, RTS anchored regression).

## F2 Rider-B channel-conflation correction (2026-07-15)

The T5 "spurious SourceTouch" finding (and the T2T review's Rider B that quoted
it) said the bug made **`contributing_sources` lie**. That wording **conflated
two sibling channels**. F2 fixed `Track::recent_contributions` (the `SourceTouch`
vector consumed by the source-aware-misdetection gate / idle-halflife / AIS-ARPA
bias loop). `Track::contributing_sources` — the string list the T2T self-adapter
reads for pedigree — is a **separate** channel that PMBM leaves **empty** (flat/MHT
populate it genuinely). The finding's real target was `recent_contributions`; the
`contributing_sources` framing was imprecise. The T2T live-pedigree caveat (gates
doc §10 Rider B) was lifted on this corrected rationale, resting on an E2E pin, and
pedigree remains diagnostics-only in fusion math. See
`docs/baselines/2026-07-15_f2_provenance_cycle.md` and design-spec §14.11 (a
backlog item to populate PMBM `contributing_sources` from the now-truthful channel).

## Unverified medium/low findings

The 31 unverified MEDIUM findings are triaged in the next section (dated
2026-07-15); the 41 LOW findings are swept there for duplicates/obsolete with the
remainder kept as a grouped backlog note. Neither set was adversarially verified
by the original review.
